001 # Tech Stack Selection (2025)
002 
003 > Default and alternative technology choices for web applications.
004 
005 ## Default Stack (Web App - 2025)
006 
007 ```yaml
008 Frontend:
009   framework: Next.js 16 (Stable)
010   language: TypeScript 5.7+
011   styling: Tailwind CSS v4
012   state: React 19 Actions / Server Components
013   bundler: Turbopack (Stable for Dev)
014 
015 Backend:
016   runtime: Node.js 23
017   framework: Next.js API Routes / Hono (for Edge)
018   validation: Zod / TypeBox
019 
020 Database:
021   primary: PostgreSQL
022   orm: Prisma / Drizzle
023   hosting: Supabase / Neon
024 
025 Auth:
026   provider: Auth.js (v5) / Clerk
027 
028 Monorepo:
029   tool: Turborepo 2.0
030 ```
031 
032 ## Alternative Options
033 
034 | Need | Default | Alternative |
035 |------|---------|-------------|
036 | Real-time | - | Supabase Realtime, Socket.io |
037 | File storage | - | Cloudinary, S3 |
038 | Payment | Stripe | LemonSqueezy, Paddle |
039 | Email | - | Resend, SendGrid |
040 | Search | - | Algolia, Typesense |

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F43 path:skills/app-builder/templates/cli-tool/TEMPLATE.md hash:89c0e5940c9fc79e664981d2826f9d5b2c4855a343d6b179ed0087032d3a323d lines:88 ===
001 ---
002 name: cli-tool
003 description: Node.js CLI tool template principles. Commander.js, interactive prompts.
004 ---
005 
006 # CLI Tool Template
007 
008 ## Tech Stack
009 
010 | Component | Technology |
011 |-----------|------------|
012 | Runtime | Node.js 20+ |
013 | Language | TypeScript |
014 | CLI Framework | Commander.js |
015 | Prompts | Inquirer.js |
016 | Output | chalk + ora |
017 | Config | cosmiconfig |
018 
019 ---
020 
021 ## Directory Structure
022 
023 ```
024 project-name/
025 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ src/
026 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ index.ts         # Entry point
027 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ cli.ts           # CLI setup
028 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ commands/        # Command handlers
029 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ lib/
030 ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ config.ts    # Config loader
031 ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ logger.ts    # Styled output
032 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ types/
033 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ bin/
034 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ cli.js           # Executable
035 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ package.json
036 ```
037 
038 ---
039 
040 ## CLI Design Principles
041 
042 | Principle | Description |
043 |-----------|-------------|
044 | Subcommands | Group related actions |
045 | Options | Flags with defaults |
046 | Interactive | Prompts when needed |
047 | Non-interactive | Support --yes flags |
048 
049 ---
050 
051 ## Key Components
052 
053 | Component | Purpose |
054 |-----------|---------|
055 | Commander | Command parsing |
056 | Inquirer | Interactive prompts |
057 | Chalk | Colored output |
058 | Ora | Spinners/loading |
059 | Cosmiconfig | Config file discovery |
060 
061 ---
062 
063 ## Setup Steps
064 
065 1. Create project directory
066 2. `npm init -y`
067 3. Install deps: `npm install commander @inquirer/prompts chalk ora cosmiconfig`
068 4. Configure bin in package.json
069 5. `npm link` for local testing
070 
071 ---
072 
073 ## Publishing
074 
075 ```bash
076 npm login
077 npm publish
078 ```
079 
080 ---
081 
082 ## Best Practices
083 
084 - Provide helpful error messages
085 - Support both interactive and non-interactive modes
086 - Use consistent output styling
087 - Validate inputs with Zod
088 - Exit with proper codes (0 success, 1 error)

006 # Electron Desktop App Template
007 
008 ## Tech Stack
009 
010 | Component | Technology |
011 |-----------|------------|
012 | Framework | Electron 28+ |
013 | UI | React 18 |
014 | Language | TypeScript |
015 | Styling | Tailwind CSS |
016 | Bundler | Vite + electron-builder |
017 | IPC | Type-safe communication |
018 
019 ---
020 
021 ## Directory Structure
022 
023 ```
024 project-name/
025 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ electron/
026 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ main.ts          # Main process
027 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ preload.ts       # Preload script
028 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ ipc/             # IPC handlers
029 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ src/
030 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ App.tsx
031 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ components/
032 ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ TitleBar.tsx # Custom title bar
033 ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ ...
034 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ hooks/
035 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ public/
036 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ package.json
037 ```
038 
039 ---
040 
041 ## Process Model
042 
043 | Process | Role |
044 |---------|------|
045 | Main | Node.js, system access |
046 | Renderer | Chromium, React UI |
047 | Preload | Bridge, context isolation |
048 
049 ---
050 
051 ## Key Concepts
052 
053 | Concept | Purpose |
054 |---------|---------|
055 | contextBridge | Safe API exposure |
056 | ipcMain/ipcRenderer | Process communication |
057 | nodeIntegration: false | Security |
058 | contextIsolation: true | Security |
059 
060 ---
061 
062 ## Setup Steps
063 
064 1. `npm create vite {{name}} -- --template react-ts`
065 2. Install: `npm install -D electron electron-builder vite-plugin-electron`
066 3. Create electron/ directory
067 4. Configure main process
068 5. `npm run electron:dev`
069 
070 ---
071 
072 ## Build Targets
073 
074 | Platform | Output |
075 |----------|--------|
076 | Windows | NSIS, Portable |
077 | macOS | DMG, ZIP |
078 | Linux | AppImage, DEB |
079 
080 ---
081 
082 ## Best Practices
083 
084 - Use preload script for main/renderer bridge
085 - Type-safe IPC with typed handlers
086 - Custom title bar for native feel
087 - Handle window state (maximize, minimize)
088 - Auto-updates with electron-updater

006 # Express.js API Template

008 ## Tech Stack

014 | Language | TypeScript |
015 | Database | PostgreSQL + Prisma |
016 | Validation | Zod |
017 | Auth | JWT + bcrypt |
018 
019 ---
020 
021 ## Directory Structure
022 
023 ```
024 project-name/
025 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ prisma/
026 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ schema.prisma
027 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ src/
028 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ app.ts           # Express setup
029 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ config/          # Environment
030 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ routes/          # Route handlers
031 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ controllers/     # Business logic
032 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ services/        # Data access
033 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ middleware/
034 ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ auth.ts      # JWT verify
035 ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ error.ts     # Error handler

039 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ package.json
040 ```
041 
042 ---
043 
044 ## Middleware Stack
045 
046 | Order | Middleware |
047 |-------|------------|
048 | 1 | helmet (security) |
049 | 2 | cors |
050 | 3 | morgan (logging) |
051 | 4 | body parsing |
052 | 5 | routes |
053 | 6 | error handler |
054 
055 ---
056 
057 ## API Response Format
058 
059 | Type | Structure |
060 |------|-----------|
061 | Success | `{ success: true, data: {...} }` |
062 | Error | `{ error: "message", details: [...] }` |
063 
064 ---
065 
066 ## Setup Steps
067 
068 1. Create project directory
069 2. `npm init -y`
070 3. Install deps: `npm install express prisma zod bcrypt jsonwebtoken`
071 4. Configure Prisma
072 5. `npm run db:push`
073 6. `npm run dev`
074 
075 ---
076 
077 ## Best Practices
078 
079 - Layer architecture (routes ‚Üí controllers ‚Üí services)
080 - Validate all inputs with Zod
081 - Centralized error handling
082 - Environment-based config
083 - Use Prisma for type-safe DB access

001 ---
002 name: monorepo-turborepo
003 description: Turborepo monorepo template principles. pnpm workspaces, shared packages.
004 ---
005 
006 # Turborepo Monorepo Template
007 
008 ## Tech Stack
009 
010 | Component | Technology |
011 |-----------|------------|
012 | Build System | Turborepo |
013 | Package Manager | pnpm |
014 | Apps | Next.js, Express |
015 | Packages | Shared UI, Config, Types |
016 | Language | TypeScript |
017 
018 ---
019 
020 ## Directory Structure
021 
022 ```
023 project-name/
024 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ apps/
025 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ web/             # Next.js app
026 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ api/             # Express API
027 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ docs/            # Documentation
028 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ packages/
029 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ ui/              # Shared components
030 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ config/          # ESLint, TS, Tailwind
031 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ types/           # Shared types
032 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ utils/           # Shared utilities
033 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ turbo.json
034 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ pnpm-workspace.yaml
035 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ package.json
036 ```
037 
038 ---
039 
040 ## Key Concepts
041 
042 | Concept | Description |
043 |---------|-------------|
044 | Workspaces | pnpm-workspace.yaml |
045 | Pipeline | turbo.json task graph |
046 | Caching | Remote/local task caching |
047 | Dependencies | `workspace:*` protocol |
048 
049 ---
050 
051 ## Turbo Pipeline
052 
053 | Task | Depends On |
054 |------|------------|
055 | build | ^build (dependencies first) |
056 | dev | cache: false, persistent |
057 | lint | ^build |
058 | test | ^build |
059 
060 ---
061 
062 ## Setup Steps
063 
064 1. Create root directory
065 2. `pnpm init`
066 3. Create pnpm-workspace.yaml
067 4. Create turbo.json
068 5. Add apps and packages
069 6. `pnpm install`
070 7. `pnpm dev`
071 
072 ---
073 
074 ## Common Commands
075 
076 | Command | Description |
077 |---------|-------------|
078 | `pnpm dev` | Run all apps |
079 | `pnpm build` | Build all |
080 | `pnpm --filter @name/web dev` | Run specific app |
081 | `pnpm --filter @name/web add axios` | Add dep to app |
082 
083 ---
084 
085 ## Best Practices
086 
087 - Shared configs in packages/config
088 - Shared types in packages/types
089 - Internal packages with `workspace:*`
090 - Use Turbo remote caching for CI

008 ## Tech Stack

010 | Component | Technology |
011 |-----------|------------|
012 | Framework | Nuxt 3 |
013 | Language | TypeScript |
014 | UI | Vue 3 (Composition API) |
015 | State | Pinia |
016 | Database | PostgreSQL + Prisma |
017 | Styling | Tailwind CSS |
018 | Validation | Zod |
019 
020 ---
021 
022 ## Directory Structure
023 
024 ```
025 project-name/
026 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ prisma/
027 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ schema.prisma
028 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ server/
029 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ api/
030 ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ [resource]/
031 ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ index.ts
032 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ utils/
033 ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ db.ts         # Prisma client
034 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ composables/
035 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ useAuth.ts
036 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ stores/
037 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ user.ts           # Pinia store
038 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ components/
039 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ ui/

050 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ package.json
051 ```
052 
053 ---
054 
055 ## Key Concepts
056 
057 | Concept | Description |
058 |---------|-------------|
059 | Auto-imports | Components, composables, utils |
060 | File-based routing | pages/ ‚Üí routes |
061 | Server Routes | server/api/ ‚Üí API endpoints |
062 | Composables | Reusable reactive logic |
063 | Pinia | State management |
064 
065 ---
066 
067 ## Environment Variables
068 
069 | Variable | Purpose |
070 |----------|---------|
071 | DATABASE_URL | Prisma connection |
072 | NUXT_PUBLIC_APP_URL | Public URL |
073 
074 ---
075 
076 ## Setup Steps
077 
078 1. `npx nuxi@latest init {{name}}`
079 2. `cd {{name}}`
080 3. `npm install @pinia/nuxt @prisma/client prisma zod`
081 4. `npm install -D @nuxtjs/tailwindcss`
082 5. Add modules to `nuxt.config.ts`:
083    ```ts
084    modules: ['@pinia/nuxt', '@nuxtjs/tailwindcss']
085    ```
086 6. `npx prisma init`
087 7. Configure schema
088 8. `npx prisma db push`
089 9. `npm run dev`
090 
091 ---
092 
093 ## Best Practices
094 
095 - Use `<script setup>` for components
096 - Composables for reusable logic
097 - Pinia stores in `stores/` folder
098 - Server routes for API logic
099 - Auto-import for clean code
100 - TypeScript for type safety
101 - See `@[skills/vue-expert]` for Vue patterns

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F55 path:skills/architecture/context-discovery.md hash:0698e38a37669c36c819bac70c51213bb955e99125ca96b690c840c317595a17 lines:43 ===
001 # Context Discovery
002 
003 > Before suggesting any architecture, gather context.
004 
005 ## Question Hierarchy (Ask User FIRST)
006 
007 1. **Scale**
008    - How many users? (10, 1K, 100K, 1M+)
009    - Data volume? (MB, GB, TB)
010    - Transaction rate? (per second/minute)
011 
012 2. **Team**
013    - Solo developer or team?
014    - Team size and expertise?
015    - Distributed or co-located?
016 
017 3. **Timeline**
018    - MVP/Prototype or long-term product?
019    - Time to market pressure?
020 
021 4. **Domain**
022    - CRUD-heavy or business logic complex?
023    - Real-time requirements?
024    - Compliance/regulations?
025 
026 5. **Constraints**
027    - Budget limitations?
028    - Legacy systems to integrate?
029    - Technology stack preferences?
030 
031 ## Project Classification Matrix
032 
033 ```
034                     MVP              SaaS           Enterprise
035 ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
036 ‚îÇ Scale        ‚îÇ <1K           ‚îÇ 1K-100K      ‚îÇ 100K+        ‚îÇ
037 ‚îÇ Team         ‚îÇ Solo          ‚îÇ 2-10         ‚îÇ 10+          ‚îÇ
038 ‚îÇ Timeline     ‚îÇ Fast (weeks)  ‚îÇ Medium (months)‚îÇ Long (years)‚îÇ
039 ‚îÇ Architecture ‚îÇ Simple        ‚îÇ Modular      ‚îÇ Distributed  ‚îÇ
040 ‚îÇ Patterns     ‚îÇ Minimal       ‚îÇ Selective    ‚îÇ Comprehensive‚îÇ
041 ‚îÇ Example      ‚îÇ Next.js API   ‚îÇ NestJS       ‚îÇ Microservices‚îÇ
042 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
043 ```
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F55 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F56 path:skills/architecture/examples.md hash:5bdd281a7409189049af4c55fbf8c8f562c250cd3e34cd60741be113110843a5 lines:94 ===
001 # Architecture Examples
002 
003 > Real-world architecture decisions by project type.
004 
005 ---
006 
007 ## Example 1: MVP E-commerce (Solo Developer)
008 
009 ```yaml
010 Requirements:
011   - <1000 users initially
012   - Solo developer
013   - Fast to market (8 weeks)
014   - Budget-conscious
015 
016 Architecture Decisions:
017   App Structure: Monolith (simpler for solo)
018   Framework: Next.js (full-stack, fast)
019   Data Layer: Prisma direct (no over-abstraction)
020   Authentication: JWT (simpler than OAuth)
021   Payment: Stripe (hosted solution)
022   Database: PostgreSQL (ACID for orders)
023 
024 Trade-offs Accepted:
025   - Monolith ‚Üí Can't scale independently (team doesn't justify it)
026   - No Repository ‚Üí Less testable (simple CRUD doesn't need it)
027   - JWT ‚Üí No social login initially (can add later)
028 
029 Future Migration Path:
030   - Users > 10K ‚Üí Extract payment service
031   - Team > 3 ‚Üí Add Repository pattern
032   - Social login requested ‚Üí Add OAuth
033 ```
034 
035 ---
036 
037 ## Example 2: SaaS Product (5-10 Developers)
038 
039 ```yaml
040 Requirements:
041   - 1K-100K users
042   - 5-10 developers
043   - Long-term (12+ months)
044   - Multiple domains (billing, users, core)
045 
046 Architecture Decisions:
047   App Structure: Modular Monolith (team size optimal)
048   Framework: NestJS (modular by design)
049   Data Layer: Repository pattern (testing, flexibility)
050   Domain Model: Partial DDD (rich entities)
051   Authentication: OAuth + JWT
052   Caching: Redis
053   Database: PostgreSQL
054 
055 Trade-offs Accepted:
056   - Modular Monolith ‚Üí Some module coupling (microservices not justified)
057   - Partial DDD ‚Üí No full aggregates (no domain experts)
058   - RabbitMQ later ‚Üí Initial synchronous (add when proven needed)
059 
060 Migration Path:
061   - Team > 10 ‚Üí Consider microservices
062   - Domains conflict ‚Üí Extract bounded contexts
063   - Read performance issues ‚Üí Add CQRS
064 ```
065 
066 ---
067 
068 ## Example 3: Enterprise (100K+ Users)
069 
070 ```yaml
071 Requirements:
072   - 100K+ users
073   - 10+ developers
074   - Multiple business domains
075   - Different scaling needs
076   - 24/7 availability
077 
078 Architecture Decisions:
079   App Structure: Microservices (independent scale)
080   API Gateway: Kong/AWS API GW
081   Domain Model: Full DDD
082   Consistency: Event-driven (eventual OK)
083   Message Bus: Kafka
084   Authentication: OAuth + SAML (enterprise SSO)
085   Database: Polyglot (right tool per job)
086   CQRS: Selected services
087 
088 Operational Requirements:
089   - Service mesh (Istio/Linkerd)
090   - Distributed tracing (Jaeger/Tempo)
091   - Centralized logging (ELK/Loki)
092   - Circuit breakers (Resilience4j)
093   - Kubernetes/Helm
094 ```
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F56 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F57 path:skills/architecture/pattern-selection.md hash:6bdc74d7900a0574057d7c03b79afa3bf35b9efc4bc719cf6e198575373b879d lines:68 ===
001 # Pattern Selection Guidelines
002 
003 > Decision trees for choosing architectural patterns.
004 
005 ## Main Decision Tree
006 
007 ```
008 START: What's your MAIN concern?
009 
010 ‚îå‚îÄ Data Access Complexity?
011 ‚îÇ  ‚îú‚îÄ HIGH (complex queries, testing needed)
012 ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  ‚Üí Repository Pattern + Unit of Work
013 ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  VALIDATE: Will data source change frequently?
014 ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ     ‚îú‚îÄ YES ‚Üí Repository worth the indirection
015 ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ     ‚îî‚îÄ NO  ‚Üí Consider simpler ORM direct access
016 ‚îÇ  ‚îî‚îÄ LOW (simple CRUD, single database)
017 ‚îÇ     ‚Üí ORM directly (Prisma, Drizzle)
018 ‚îÇ     Simpler = Better, Faster
019 ‚îÇ
020 ‚îú‚îÄ Business Rules Complexity?
021 ‚îÇ  ‚îú‚îÄ HIGH (domain logic, rules vary by context)
022 ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  ‚Üí Domain-Driven Design
023 ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  VALIDATE: Do you have domain experts on team?
024 ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ     ‚îú‚îÄ YES ‚Üí Full DDD (Aggregates, Value Objects)
025 ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ     ‚îî‚îÄ NO  ‚Üí Partial DDD (rich entities, clear boundaries)
026 ‚îÇ  ‚îî‚îÄ LOW (mostly CRUD, simple validation)
027 ‚îÇ     ‚Üí Transaction Script pattern
028 ‚îÇ     Simpler = Better, Faster
029 ‚îÇ
030 ‚îú‚îÄ Independent Scaling Needed?
031 ‚îÇ  ‚îú‚îÄ YES (different components scale differently)
032 ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  ‚Üí Microservices WORTH the complexity
033 ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  REQUIREMENTS (ALL must be true):
034 ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ    - Clear domain boundaries
035 ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ    - Team > 10 developers
036 ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ    - Different scaling needs per service
037 ‚îÇ  ‚îÇ  IF NOT ALL MET ‚Üí Modular Monolith instead
038 ‚îÇ  ‚îî‚îÄ NO (everything scales together)
039 ‚îÇ     ‚Üí Modular Monolith
040 ‚îÇ     Can extract services later when proven needed
041 ‚îÇ
042 ‚îî‚îÄ Real-time Requirements?
043    ‚îú‚îÄ HIGH (immediate updates, multi-user sync)
044    ‚îÇ  ‚Üí Event-Driven Architecture
045    ‚îÇ  ‚Üí Message Queue (RabbitMQ, Redis, Kafka)
046    ‚îÇ  VALIDATE: Can you handle eventual consistency?
047    ‚îÇ     ‚îú‚îÄ YES ‚Üí Event-driven valid
048    ‚îÇ     ‚îî‚îÄ NO  ‚Üí Synchronous with polling
049    ‚îî‚îÄ LOW (eventual consistency acceptable)
050       ‚Üí Synchronous (REST/GraphQL)
051       Simpler = Better, Faster
052 ```
053 
054 ## The 3 Questions (Before ANY Pattern)
055 
056 1. **Problem Solved**: What SPECIFIC problem does this pattern solve?
057 2. **Simpler Alternative**: Is there a simpler solution?
058 3. **Deferred Complexity**: Can we add this LATER when needed?
059 
060 ## Red Flags (Anti-patterns)
061 
062 | Pattern | Anti-pattern | Simpler Alternative |
063 |---------|-------------|-------------------|
064 | Microservices | Premature splitting | Start monolith, extract later |
065 | Clean/Hexagonal | Over-abstraction | Concrete first, interfaces later |
066 | Event Sourcing | Over-engineering | Append-only audit log |
067 | CQRS | Unnecessary complexity | Single model |
068 | Repository | YAGNI for simple CRUD | ORM direct access |
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F57 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F58 path:skills/architecture/patterns-reference.md hash:264d0c372a6b5d2a7bba506a4dd4d74855f69298d4dabf1ae046d51f2f49bd9d lines:50 ===
001 # Architecture Patterns Reference
002 
003 > Quick reference for common patterns with usage guidance.
004 
005 ## Data Access Patterns
006 
007 | Pattern | When to Use | When NOT to Use | Complexity |
008 |---------|-------------|-----------------|------------|
009 | **Active Record** | Simple CRUD, rapid prototyping | Complex queries, multiple sources | Low |
010 | **Repository** | Testing needed, multiple sources | Simple CRUD, single database | Medium |
011 | **Unit of Work** | Complex transactions | Simple operations | High |
012 | **Data Mapper** | Complex domain, performance | Simple CRUD, rapid dev | High |
013 
014 ## Domain Logic Patterns
015 
016 | Pattern | When to Use | When NOT to Use | Complexity |
017 |---------|-------------|-----------------|------------|
018 | **Transaction Script** | Simple CRUD, procedural | Complex business rules | Low |
019 | **Table Module** | Record-based logic | Rich behavior needed | Low |
020 | **Domain Model** | Complex business logic | Simple CRUD | Medium |
021 | **DDD (Full)** | Complex domain, domain experts | Simple domain, no experts | High |
022 
023 ## Distributed System Patterns
024 
025 | Pattern | When to Use | When NOT to Use | Complexity |
026 |---------|-------------|-----------------|------------|
027 | **Modular Monolith** | Small teams, unclear boundaries | Clear contexts, different scales | Medium |
028 | **Microservices** | Different scales, large teams | Small teams, simple domain | Very High |
029 | **Event-Driven** | Real-time, loose coupling | Simple workflows, strong consistency | High |
030 | **CQRS** | Read/write performance diverges | Simple CRUD, same model | High |
031 | **Saga** | Distributed transactions | Single database, simple ACID | High |
032 
033 ## API Patterns
034 
035 | Pattern | When to Use | When NOT to Use | Complexity |
036 |---------|-------------|-----------------|------------|
037 | **REST** | Standard CRUD, resources | Real-time, complex queries | Low |
038 | **GraphQL** | Flexible queries, multiple clients | Simple CRUD, caching needs | Medium |
039 | **gRPC** | Internal services, performance | Public APIs, browser clients | Medium |
040 | **WebSocket** | Real-time updates | Simple request/response | Medium |
041 
042 ---
043 
044 ## Simplicity Principle
045 
046 **"Start simple, add complexity only when proven necessary."**
047 
048 - You can always add patterns later
049 - Removing complexity is MUCH harder than adding it
050 - When in doubt, choose simpler option
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F58 ===

001 ---

006 
007 # Architecture Decision Framework
008 
009 > "Requirements drive architecture. Trade-offs inform decisions. ADRs capture rationale."
010 
011 ## üéØ Selective Reading Rule
012 
013 **Read ONLY files relevant to the request!** Check the content map, find what you need.
014 
015 | File | Description | When to Read |
016 |------|-------------|--------------|
017 | `context-discovery.md` | Questions to ask, project classification | Starting architecture design |
018 | `trade-off-analysis.md` | ADR templates, trade-off framework | Documenting decisions |
019 | `pattern-selection.md` | Decision trees, anti-patterns | Choosing patterns |
020 | `examples.md` | MVP, SaaS, Enterprise examples | Reference implementations |
021 | `patterns-reference.md` | Quick lookup for patterns | Pattern comparison |
022 
023 ---
024 
025 ## üîó Related Skills
026 
027 | Skill | Use For |
028 |-------|---------|
029 | `@[skills/database-design]` | Database schema design |
030 | `@[skills/api-patterns]` | API design patterns |
031 | `@[skills/deployment-procedures]` | Deployment architecture |
032 
033 ---
034 
035 ## Core Principle
036 
037 **"Simplicity is the ultimate sophistication."**
038 
039 - Start simple
040 - Add complexity ONLY when proven necessary
041 - You can always add patterns later
042 - Removing complexity is MUCH harder than adding it
043 
044 ---
045 
046 ## Validation Checklist
047 
048 Before finalizing architecture:
049 
050 - [ ] Requirements clearly understood
051 - [ ] Constraints identified
052 - [ ] Each decision has trade-off analysis
053 - [ ] Simpler alternatives considered
054 - [ ] ADRs written for significant decisions
055 - [ ] Team expertise matches chosen patterns

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F60 path:skills/architecture/trade-off-analysis.md hash:14a0ceb22e88af2d39b24f06a9095312aa04bc72e8980f244bf2b42f8260abaa lines:77 ===
001 # Trade-off Analysis & ADR
002 
003 > Document every architectural decision with trade-offs.
004 
005 ## Decision Framework
006 
007 For EACH architectural component, document:
008 
009 ```markdown
010 ## Architecture Decision Record
011 
012 ### Context
013 - **Problem**: [What problem are we solving?]
014 - **Constraints**: [Team size, scale, timeline, budget]
015 
016 ### Options Considered
017 
018 | Option | Pros | Cons | Complexity | When Valid |
019 |--------|------|------|------------|-----------|
020 | Option A | Benefit 1 | Cost 1 | Low | [Conditions] |
021 | Option B | Benefit 2 | Cost 2 | High | [Conditions] |
022 
023 ### Decision
024 **Chosen**: [Option B]
025 
026 ### Rationale
027 1. [Reason 1 - tied to constraints]
028 2. [Reason 2 - tied to requirements]
029 
030 ### Trade-offs Accepted
031 - [What we're giving up]
032 - [Why this is acceptable]
033 
034 ### Consequences
035 - **Positive**: [Benefits we gain]
036 - **Negative**: [Costs/risks we accept]
037 - **Mitigation**: [How we'll address negatives]
038 
039 ### Revisit Trigger
040 - [When to reconsider this decision]
041 ```
042 
043 ## ADR Template
044 
045 ```markdown
046 # ADR-[XXX]: [Decision Title]
047 
048 ## Status
049 Proposed | Accepted | Deprecated | Superseded by [ADR-YYY]
050 
051 ## Context
052 [What problem? What constraints?]
053 
054 ## Decision
055 [What we chose - be specific]
056 
057 ## Rationale
058 [Why - tie to requirements and constraints]
059 
060 ## Trade-offs
061 [What we're giving up - be honest]
062 
063 ## Consequences
064 - **Positive**: [Benefits]
065 - **Negative**: [Costs]
066 - **Mitigation**: [How to address]
067 ```
068 
069 ## ADR Storage
070 
071 ```
072 docs/
073 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ architecture/
074     ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ adr-001-use-nextjs.md
075     ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ adr-002-postgresql-over-mongodb.md
076     ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ adr-003-adopt-repository-pattern.md
077 ```

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F61 path:skills/bash-linux/SKILL.md hash:17c0a0d75bf28f0f639c983299a5e3c0f7fa829d50d6e147f553b3d26ffcb13c lines:199 ===
001 ---
002 name: bash-linux
003 description: Bash/Linux terminal patterns. Critical commands, piping, error handling, scripting. Use when working on macOS or Linux systems.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Write, Edit, Glob, Grep, Bash
005 ---
006 
007 # Bash Linux Patterns
008 
009 > Essential patterns for Bash on Linux/macOS.
010 
011 ---
012 
013 ## 1. Operator Syntax
014 
015 ### Chaining Commands
016 
017 | Operator | Meaning | Example |
018 |----------|---------|---------|
019 | `;` | Run sequentially | `cmd1; cmd2` |
020 | `&&` | Run if previous succeeded | `npm install && npm run dev` |
021 | `\|\|` | Run if previous failed | `npm test \|\| echo "Tests failed"` |
022 | `\|` | Pipe output | `ls \| grep ".js"` |
023 
024 ---
025 
026 ## 2. File Operations
027 
028 ### Essential Commands
029 
030 | Task | Command |
031 |------|---------|
032 | List all | `ls -la` |
033 | Find files | `find . -name "*.js" -type f` |
034 | File content | `cat file.txt` |
035 | First N lines | `head -n 20 file.txt` |
036 | Last N lines | `tail -n 20 file.txt` |
037 | Follow log | `tail -f log.txt` |
038 | Search in files | `grep -r "pattern" --include="*.js"` |
039 | File size | `du -sh *` |
040 | Disk usage | `df -h` |
041 
042 ---
043 
044 ## 3. Process Management
045 
046 | Task | Command |
047 |------|---------|
048 | List processes | `ps aux` |
049 | Find by name | `ps aux \| grep node` |
050 | Kill by PID | `kill -9 <PID>` |
051 | Find port user | `lsof -i :3000` |
052 | Kill port | `kill -9 $(lsof -t -i :3000)` |
053 | Background | `npm run dev &` |
054 | Jobs | `jobs -l` |
055 | Bring to front | `fg %1` |
056 
057 ---
058 
059 ## 4. Text Processing
060 
061 ### Core Tools
062 
063 | Tool | Purpose | Example |
064 |------|---------|---------|
065 | `grep` | Search | `grep -rn "TODO" src/` |
066 | `sed` | Replace | `sed -i 's/old/new/g' file.txt` |
067 | `awk` | Extract columns | `awk '{print $1}' file.txt` |
068 | `cut` | Cut fields | `cut -d',' -f1 data.csv` |
069 | `sort` | Sort lines | `sort -u file.txt` |
070 | `uniq` | Unique lines | `sort file.txt \| uniq -c` |
071 | `wc` | Count | `wc -l file.txt` |
072 
073 ---
074 
075 ## 5. Environment Variables
076 
077 | Task | Command |
078 |------|---------|
079 | View all | `env` or `printenv` |
080 | View one | `echo $PATH` |
081 | Set temporary | `export VAR="value"` |
082 | Set in script | `VAR="value" command` |
083 | Add to PATH | `export PATH="$PATH:/new/path"` |
084 
085 ---
086 
087 ## 6. Network
088 
089 | Task | Command |
090 |------|---------|
091 | Download | `curl -O https://example.com/file` |
092 | API request | `curl -X GET https://api.example.com` |
093 | POST JSON | `curl -X POST -H "Content-Type: application/json" -d '{"key":"value"}' URL` |
094 | Check port | `nc -zv localhost 3000` |
095 | Network info | `ifconfig` or `ip addr` |
096 
097 ---
098 
099 ## 7. Script Template
100 
101 ```bash
102 #!/bin/bash
103 set -euo pipefail  # Exit on error, undefined var, pipe fail
104 
105 # Colors (optional)
106 RED='\033[0;31m'
107 GREEN='\033[0;32m'
108 NC='\033[0m'
109 
110 # Script directory
111 SCRIPT_DIR="$(cd "$(dirname "${BASH_SOURCE[0]}")" && pwd)"
112 
113 # Functions
114 log_info() { echo -e "${GREEN}[INFO]${NC} $1"; }
115 log_error() { echo -e "${RED}[ERROR]${NC} $1" >&2; }
116 
117 # Main
118 main() {
119     log_info "Starting..."
120     # Your logic here
121     log_info "Done!"
122 }
123 
124 main "$@"
125 ```
126 
127 ---
128 
129 ## 8. Common Patterns
130 
131 ### Check if command exists
132 
133 ```bash
134 if command -v node &> /dev/null; then
135     echo "Node is installed"
136 fi
137 ```
138 
139 ### Default variable value
140 
141 ```bash
142 NAME=${1:-"default_value"}
143 ```
144 
145 ### Read file line by line
146 
147 ```bash
148 while IFS= read -r line; do
149     echo "$line"
150 done < file.txt
151 ```
152 
153 ### Loop over files
154 
155 ```bash
156 for file in *.js; do
157     echo "Processing $file"
158 done
159 ```
160 
161 ---
162 
163 ## 9. Differences from PowerShell
164 
165 | Task | PowerShell | Bash |
166 |------|------------|------|
167 | List files | `Get-ChildItem` | `ls -la` |
168 | Find files | `Get-ChildItem -Recurse` | `find . -type f` |
169 | Environment | `$env:VAR` | `$VAR` |
170 | String concat | `"$a$b"` | `"$a$b"` (same) |
171 | Null check | `if ($x)` | `if [ -n "$x" ]` |
172 | Pipeline | Object-based | Text-based |
173 
174 ---
175 
176 ## 10. Error Handling
177 
178 ### Set options
179 
180 ```bash
181 set -e          # Exit on error
182 set -u          # Exit on undefined variable
183 set -o pipefail # Exit on pipe failure
184 set -x          # Debug: print commands
185 ```
186 
187 ### Trap for cleanup
188 
189 ```bash
190 cleanup() {
191     echo "Cleaning up..."
192     rm -f /tmp/tempfile
193 }
194 trap cleanup EXIT
195 ```
196 
197 ---
198 
199 > **Remember:** Bash is text-based. Use `&&` for success chains, `set -e` for safety, and quote your variables!

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F62 path:skills/behavioral-modes/SKILL.md hash:1bfdf106d23c51a425b687677638d88472ea5bcdd3bcd76ca13783df77f6eb13 lines:242 ===
001 ---
002 name: behavioral-modes
003 description: AI operational modes (brainstorm, implement, debug, review, teach, ship, orchestrate). Use to adapt behavior based on task type.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Glob, Grep
005 ---
006 
007 # Behavioral Modes - Adaptive AI Operating Modes
008 
009 ## Purpose
010 This skill defines distinct behavioral modes that optimize AI performance for specific tasks. Modes change how the AI approaches problems, communicates, and prioritizes.
011 
012 ---
013 
014 ## Available Modes
015 
016 ### 1. üß† BRAINSTORM Mode
017 
018 **When to use:** Early project planning, feature ideation, architecture decisions
019 
020 **Behavior:**
021 - Ask clarifying questions before assumptions
022 - Offer multiple alternatives (at least 3)
023 - Think divergently - explore unconventional solutions
024 - No code yet - focus on ideas and options
025 - Use visual diagrams (mermaid) to explain concepts
026 
027 **Output style:**
028 ```
029 "Let's explore this together. Here are some approaches:
030 
031 Option A: [description]
032   ‚úÖ Pros: ...
033   ‚ùå Cons: ...
034 
035 Option B: [description]
036   ‚úÖ Pros: ...
037   ‚ùå Cons: ...
038 
039 What resonates with you? Or should we explore a different direction?"
040 ```
041 
042 ---
043 
044 ### 2. ‚ö° IMPLEMENT Mode
045 
046 **When to use:** Writing code, building features, executing plans
047 
048 **Behavior:**
049 - **CRITICAL: Use `clean-code` skill standards** - concise, direct, no verbose explanations
050 - Fast execution - minimize questions
051 - Use established patterns and best practices
052 - Write complete, production-ready code
053 - Include error handling and edge cases
054 - **NO tutorial-style explanations** - just code
055 - **NO unnecessary comments** - let code self-document
056 - **NO over-engineering** - solve the problem directly
057 - **NO RUSHING** - Quality > Speed. Read ALL references before coding.
058 
059 **Output style:**
060 ```
061 [Code block]
062 
063 [Brief summary, max 1-2 sentences]
064 ```
065 
066 **NOT:**
067 ```
068 "Building [feature]...
069 
070 ‚úì Created [file1]
071 ‚úì Created [file2]
072 ‚úì Updated [file3]
073 
074 [long explanation]
075 
076 Run `npm run dev` to test."
077 ```
078 
079 ---
080 
081 ### 3. üîç DEBUG Mode
082 
083 **When to use:** Fixing bugs, troubleshooting errors, investigating issues
084 
085 **Behavior:**
086 - Ask for error messages and reproduction steps
087 - Think systematically - check logs, trace data flow
088 - Form hypothesis ‚Üí test ‚Üí verify
089 - Explain the root cause, not just the fix
090 - Prevent future occurrences
091 
092 **Output style:**
093 ```
094 "Investigating...
095 
096 üîç Symptom: [what's happening]
097 üéØ Root cause: [why it's happening]
098 ‚úÖ Fix: [the solution]
099 üõ°Ô∏è Prevention: [how to avoid in future]
100 ```
101 
102 ---
103 
104 ### 4. üìã REVIEW Mode
105 
106 **When to use:** Code review, architecture review, security audit
107 
108 **Behavior:**
109 - Be thorough but constructive
110 - Categorize by severity (Critical/High/Medium/Low)
111 - Explain the "why" behind suggestions
112 - Offer improved code examples
113 - Acknowledge what's done well
114 
115 **Output style:**
116 ```
117 ## Code Review: [file/feature]
118 
119 ### üî¥ Critical
120 - [issue with explanation]
121 
122 ### üü† Improvements
123 - [suggestion with example]
124 
125 ### üü¢ Good
126 - [positive observation]
127 ```
128 
129 ---
130 
131 ### 5. üìö TEACH Mode
132 
133 **When to use:** Explaining concepts, documentation, onboarding
134 
135 **Behavior:**
136 - Explain from fundamentals
137 - Use analogies and examples
138 - Progress from simple to complex
139 - Include practical exercises
140 - Check understanding
141 
142 **Output style:**
143 ```
144 ## Understanding [Concept]
145 
146 ### What is it?
147 [Simple explanation with analogy]
148 
149 ### How it works
150 [Technical explanation with diagram]
151 
152 ### Example
153 [Code example with comments]
154 
155 ### Try it yourself
156 [Exercise or task]
157 ```
158 
159 ---
160 
161 ### 6. üöÄ SHIP Mode
162 
163 **When to use:** Production deployment, final polish, release preparation
164 
165 **Behavior:**
166 - Focus on stability over features
167 - Check for missing error handling
168 - Verify environment configs
169 - Run all tests
170 - Create deployment checklist
171 
172 **Output style:**
173 ```
174 ## Pre-Ship Checklist
175 
176 ### ‚úÖ Code Quality
177 - [ ] No TypeScript errors
178 - [ ] ESLint passing
179 - [ ] All tests passing
180 
181 ### ‚úÖ Security
182 - [ ] No exposed secrets
183 - [ ] Input validation complete
184 
185 ### ‚úÖ Performance
186 - [ ] Bundle size acceptable
187 - [ ] No console.logs
188 
189 ### üöÄ Ready to deploy
190 ```
191 
192 ---
193 
194 ## Mode Detection
195 
196 The AI should automatically detect the appropriate mode based on:
197 
198 | Trigger | Mode |
199 |---------|------|
200 | "what if", "ideas", "options" | BRAINSTORM |
201 | "build", "create", "add" | IMPLEMENT |
202 | "not working", "error", "bug" | DEBUG |
203 | "review", "check", "audit" | REVIEW |
204 | "explain", "how does", "learn" | TEACH |
205 | "deploy", "release", "production" | SHIP |
206 
207 ---
208 
209 ## Multi-Agent Collaboration Patterns (2025)
210 
211 Modern architectures optimized for agent-to-agent collaboration:
212 
213 ### 1. üî≠ EXPLORE Mode
214 **Role:** Discovery and Analysis (Explorer Agent)
215 **Behavior:** Socratic questioning, deep-dive code reading, dependency mapping.
216 **Output:** `discovery-report.json`, architectural visualization.
217 
218 ### 2. üó∫Ô∏è PLAN-EXECUTE-CRITIC (PEC)
219 Cyclic mode transitions for high-complexity tasks:
220 1. **Planner:** Decomposes the task into atomic steps (`task.md`).
221 2. **Executor:** Performs the actual coding (`IMPLEMENT`).
222 3. **Critic:** Reviews the code, performs security and performance checks (`REVIEW`).
223 
224 ### 3. üß† MENTAL MODEL SYNC
225 Behavior for creating and loading "Mental Model" summaries to preserve context between sessions.
226 
227 ---
228 
229 ## Combining Modes
230 
231 ---
232 
233 ## Manual Mode Switching
234 
235 Users can explicitly request a mode:
236 
237 ```
238 /brainstorm new feature ideas
239 /implement the user profile page
240 /debug why login fails
241 /review this pull request
242 ```

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F63 path:skills/brainstorming/dynamic-questioning.md hash:b8ee14ed26f4ebffd4d6e63959eab94646dea87c5c3cfb15e9f036bd9a6a7c61 lines:350 ===
001 # Dynamic Question Generation
002 
003 > **PRINCIPLE:** Questions are not about gathering data‚Äîthey are about **revealing architectural consequences**.
004 >
005 > Every question must connect to a concrete implementation decision that affects cost, complexity, or timeline.
006 
007 ---
008 
009 ## üß† Core Principles
010 
011 ### 1. Questions Reveal Consequences
012 
013 A good question is not "What color do you want?" but:
014 
015 ```markdown
016 ‚ùå BAD: "What authentication method?"
017 ‚úÖ GOOD: "Should users sign up with email/password or social login?
018 
019    Impact:
020    - Email/Pass ‚Üí Need password reset, hashing, 2FA infrastructure
021    - Social ‚Üí OAuth providers, user profile mapping, less control
022 
023    Trade-off: Security vs. Development time vs. User friction"
024 ```
025 
026 ### 2. Context Before Content
027 
028 First understand **where** this request fits:
029 
030 | Context | Question Focus |
031 |---------|----------------|
032 | **Greenfield** (new project) | Foundation decisions: stack, hosting, scale |
033 | **Feature Addition** | Integration points, existing patterns, breaking changes |
034 | **Refactor** | Why refactor? Performance? Maintainability? What's broken? |
035 | **Debug** | Symptoms ‚Üí Root cause ‚Üí Reproduction path |
036 
037 ### 3. Minimum Viable Questions
038 
039 **PRINCIPLE:** Each question must eliminate a fork in the implementation road.
040 
041 ```
042 Before Question:
043 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Path A: Do X (5 min)
044 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Path B: Do Y (15 min)
045 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Path C: Do Z (1 hour)
046 
047 After Question:
048 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Path Confirmed: Do X (5 min)
049 ```
050 
051 If a question doesn't reduce implementation paths ‚Üí **DELETE IT**.
052 
053 ### 4. Questions Generate Data, Not Assumptions
054 
055 ```markdown
056 ‚ùå ASSUMPTION: "User probably wants Stripe for payments"
057 ‚úÖ QUESTION: "Which payment provider fits your needs?
058 
059    Stripe ‚Üí Best documentation, 2.9% + $0.30, US-centric
060    LemonSqueezy ‚Üí Merchant of Record, 5% + $0.50, global taxes
061    Paddle ‚Üí Complex pricing, handles EU VAT, enterprise focus"
062 ```
063 
064 ---
065 
066 ## üìã Question Generation Algorithm
067 
068 ```
069 INPUT: User request + Context (greenfield/feature/refactor/debug)
070 ‚îÇ
071 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ STEP 1: Parse Request
072 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Extract domain (ecommerce, auth, realtime, cms, etc.)
073 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Extract features (explicit and implied)
074 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Extract scale indicators (users, data volume, frequency)
075 ‚îÇ
076 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ STEP 2: Identify Decision Points
077 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ What MUST be decided before coding? (blocking)
078 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ What COULD be decided later? (deferable)
079 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ What has ARCHITECTURAL impact? (high-leverage)
080 ‚îÇ
081 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ STEP 3: Generate Questions (Priority Order)
082 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ P0: Blocking decisions (cannot proceed without answer)
083 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ P1: High-leverage (affects >30% of implementation)
084 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ P2: Medium-leverage (affects specific features)
085 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ P3: Nice-to-have (edge cases, optimization)
086 ‚îÇ
087 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ STEP 4: Format Each Question
088     ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ What: Clear question
089     ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Why: Impact on implementation
090     ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Options: Trade-offs (not just A vs B)
091     ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Default: What happens if user doesn't answer
092 ```
093 
094 ---
095 
096 ## üéØ Domain-Specific Question Banks
097 
098 ### E-Commerce
099 
100 | Question | Why It Matters | Trade-offs |
101 |----------|----------------|------------|
102 | **Single or Multi-vendor?** | Multi-vendor ‚Üí Commission logic, vendor dashboards, split payments | +Revenue, -Complexity |
103 | **Inventory Tracking?** | Needs stock tables, reservation logic, low-stock alerts | +Accuracy, -Development time |
104 | **Digital or Physical Products?** | Digital ‚Üí Download links, no shipping | Physical ‚Üí Shipping APIs, tracking |
105 | **Subscription or One-time?** | Subscription ‚Üí Recurring billing, dunning, proration | +Revenue, -Complexity |
106 
107 ### Authentication
108 
109 | Question | Why It Matters | Trade-offs |
110 |----------|----------------|------------|
111 | **Social Login Needed?** | OAuth providers vs. password reset infrastructure | +UX, -Control |
112 | **Role-Based Permissions?** | RBAC tables, policy enforcement, admin UI | +Security, -Development time |
113 | **2FA Required?** | TOTP/SMI infrastructure, backup codes, recovery flow | +Security, -UX friction |
114 | **Email Verification?** | Verification tokens, email service, resend logic | +Security, -Sign-up friction |
115 
116 ### Real-time
117 
118 | Question | Why It Matters | Trade-offs |
119 |----------|----------------|------------|
120 | **WebSocket or Polling?** | WS ‚Üí Server scaling, connection management | Polling ‚Üí Simpler, higher latency |
121 | **Expected Concurrent Users?** | <100 ‚Üí Single server, >1000 ‚Üí Redis pub/sub, >10k ‚Üí specialized infra | +Scale, -Complexity |
122 | **Message Persistence?** | History tables, storage costs, pagination | +UX, -Storage |
123 | **Ephemeral or Durable?** | Ephemeral ‚Üí In-memory, Durable ‚Üí Database write before emit | +Reliability, -Latency |
124 
125 ### Content/CMS
126 
127 | Question | Why It Matters | Trade-offs |
128 |----------|----------------|------------|
129 | **Rich Text or Markdown?** | Rich Text ‚Üí Sanitization, XSS risks | Markdown ‚Üí Simple, no WYSIWYG |
130 | **Draft/Publish Workflow?** | Status field, scheduled jobs, versioning | +Control, -Complexity |
131 | **Media Handling?** | Upload endpoints, storage, optimization | +Features, -Development time |
132 | **Multi-language?** | i18n tables, translation UI, fallback logic | +Reach, -Complexity |
133 
134 ---
135 
136 ## üìê Dynamic Question Template
137 
138 ```markdown
139 Based on your request for [DOMAIN] [FEATURE]:
140 
141 ## üî¥ CRITICAL (Blocking Decisions)
142 
143 ### 1. **[DECISION POINT]**
144 
145 **Question:** [Clear, specific question]
146 
147 **Why This Matters:**
148 - [Explain architectural consequence]
149 - [Affects: cost / complexity / timeline / scale]
150 
151 **Options:**
152 | Option | Pros | Cons | Best For |
153 |--------|------|------|----------|
154 | A | [Advantage] | [Disadvantage] | [Use case] |
155 | B | [Advantage] | [Disadvantage] | [Use case] |
156 
157 **If Not Specified:** [Default choice + rationale]
158 
159 ---
160 
161 ## üü° HIGH-LEVERAGE (Affects Implementation)
162 
163 ### 2. **[DECISION POINT]**
164 [Same format]
165 
166 ---
167 
168 ## üü¢ NICE-TO-HAVE (Edge Cases)
169 
170 ### 3. **[DECISION POINT]**
171 [Same format]
172 ```
173 
174 ---
175 
176 ## üîÑ Iterative Questioning
177 
178 ### First Pass (3-5 Questions)
179 Focus on **blocking decisions**. Don't proceed without answers.
180 
181 ### Second Pass (After Initial Implementation)
182 As patterns emerge, ask:
183 - "This feature implies [X]. Should we handle [edge case] now or defer?"
184 - "We're using [Pattern A]. Should [Feature B] follow the same pattern?"
185 
186 ### Third Pass (Optimization)
187 When functionality works:
188 - "Performance bottleneck at [X]. Optimize now or acceptable for now?"
189 - "Refactor [Y] for maintainability or ship as-is?"
190 
191 ---
192 
193 ## üé≠ Example: Full Question Generation
194 
195 ```
196 USER REQUEST: "Build an Instagram clone"
197 
198 STEP 1: Parse
199 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Domain: Social Media
200 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Features: Photo sharing, engagement (likes/comments), user profiles
201 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Implied: Feed, following, authentication
202 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Scale: Potentially high (social apps go viral)
203 
204 STEP 2: Decision Points
205 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Blocking: Storage strategy, authentication method, feed type
206 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ High-leverage: Real-time notifications, data model complexity
207 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Deferable: Analytics, advanced search, reels/video
208 
209 STEP 3: Generate Questions (Priority)
210 
211 P0 (Blocking):
212 1. Storage Strategy ‚Üí Affects architecture, cost, speed
213 2. Feed Algorithm ‚Üí Affects database queries, complexity
214 3. Auth Method ‚Üí Affects dev time, UX, security
215 
216 P1 (High-leverage):
217 4. Real-time Notifications ‚Üí WebSocket vs polling
218 5. Media Processing ‚Üí Client-side vs server-side optimization
219 
220 P2 (Deferable):
221 6. Story/Reels ‚Üí Major feature creep, defer to v2
222 7. DM/Chat ‚Üí Separate subsystem, defer to v2
223 
224 STEP 4: Format Output
225 ```
226 
227 ---
228 
229 ## üìä Generated Output (Example)
230 
231 ```
232 Based on your Instagram clone request:
233 
234 ## üî¥ CRITICAL DECISIONS (Cannot Proceed Without Answers)
235 
236 ### 1. **Photo Storage Strategy**
237 
238 **Question:** Where will user photos be stored and served?
239 
240 **Why This Matters:**
241 - Affects: Monthly hosting costs, page load speed, CDN complexity
242 - High-volume social apps: 1000 users √ó 10 photos √ó 2MB = 20GB storage
243 
244 **Options:**
245 | Option | Cost | Speed | Complexity | Best For |
246 |--------|------|-------|------------|----------|
247 | **Cloudinary** | $89/mo (25GB) | Fast (CDN) | Low | MVP, rapid launch |
248 | **AWS S3 + CloudFront** | $0.023/GB | Fast (CDN) | Medium | Production, cost-optimized |
249 | **Supabase Storage** | Free tier 1GB | Medium | Low | Small scale, simple |
250 | **Local Storage** | Server cost | Slow | Low | Development only |
251 
252 **If Not Specified:** Cloudinary (balanced for MVP)
253 
254 ---
255 
256 ### 2. **Feed Algorithm Choice**
257 
258 **Question:** How should the main feed work?
259 
260 **Why This Matters:**
261 - Affects: Database query complexity, caching strategy, development time
262 - Algorithmic feeds require ML infrastructure, ranking signals
263 
264 **Options:**
265 | Option | Complexity | Database Impact | Best For |
266 |--------|------------|-----------------|----------|
267 | **Chronological** | Low | Simple query | Early stage, transparency |
268 | **Follow-Only** | Medium | JOIN with pagination | Most social apps |
269 | **Algorithmic** | High | Pre-computed feed tables | Instagram competitor |
270 
271 **If Not Specified:** Follow-Only (balanced for social app)
272 
273 ---
274 
275 ### 3. **Authentication Approach**
276 
277 **Question:** How do users sign up and login?
278 
279 **Why This Matters:**
280 - Affects: Development time (2-5 hours), security posture, UX friction
281 
282 **Options:**
283 | Option | Dev Time | Security | UX | Best For |
284 |--------|----------|----------|-----|----------|
285 | **Email/Password** | 4-5 hrs | High (if 2FA) | Medium | Full control needed |
286 | **Social Only** | 1-2 hrs | Provider-dependent | Smooth | B2C, rapid launch |
287 | **Magic Link** | 2-3 hrs | Medium | Very smooth | Security-focused |
288 | **Clerk/Auth0** | 1 hr | High | Smooth | Fastest to market |
289 
290 **If Not Specified:** Clerk (fastest for MVP)
291 
292 ---
293 
294 ## üü° HIGH-LEVERAGE (Affects Architecture)
295 
296 ### 4. **Real-time Notifications**
297 
298 **Question:** Do users need instant notifications for likes/comments?
299 
300 **Why This Matters:**
301 - WebSocket adds infrastructure complexity (Redis pub/sub for scaling)
302 - Polling is simpler but higher latency
303 
304 **Options:**
305 | Option | Complexity | Scale Cost | Best For |
306 |--------|------------|------------|----------|
307 | **WebSocket + Redis** | High | $10+/mo | >1000 concurrent users |
308 | **Polling (30s)** | Low | DB queries | <1000 users |
309 | **No Real-time** | None | None | MVP, validate first |
310 
311 **If Not Specified:** Polling for MVP (defer WebSocket until validated)
312 
313 ---
314 
315 ## üü¢ NICE-TO-HAVE (Defer to v2)
316 
317 ### 5. **Video/Reels Support**
318 - Major complexity (video processing, streaming infrastructure)
319 - Recommendation: Launch with photos only, add video after validation
320 
321 ### 6. **Direct Messaging**
322 - Separate subsystem (chat infrastructure different from feed)
323 - Recommendation: Use Pusher/Stream for real-time or defer entirely
324 
325 ---
326 
327 ## üìã Summary
328 
329 | Decision | Recommendation | If Changed |
330 |----------|----------------|------------|
331 | Storage | Cloudinary | +3 hrs setup |
332 | Feed | Follow-only | +2 hrs query optimization |
333 | Auth | Clerk | -3 hrs dev time |
334 | Real-time | Polling | +5 hrs WebSocket setup |
335 | Video | Defer to v2 | N/A |
336 | DM | Defer to v2 | N/A |
337 
338 **Total Estimated MVP Time:** 15-20 hours with recommendations above
339 ```
340 
341 ---
342 
343 ## üéØ Principles Recap
344 
345 1. **Every question = Architectural decision** ‚Üí Not data gathering
346 2. **Show trade-offs** ‚Üí User understands consequences
347 3. **Prioritize blocking decisions** ‚Üí Cannot proceed without
348 4. **Provide defaults** ‚Üí If user doesn't answer, we proceed anyway
349 5. **Domain-aware** ‚Üí Ecommerce questions ‚â† Auth questions ‚â† Real-time questions
350 6. **Iterative** ‚Üí More questions as patterns emerge during implementation

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F64 path:skills/brainstorming/SKILL.md hash:1a501a9fea86ec58121206b5c73d34bdaddd595be3da4d12761b6c1ac37f8fa4 lines:163 ===
001 ---
002 name: brainstorming
003 description: Socratic questioning protocol + user communication. MANDATORY for complex requests, new features, or unclear requirements. Includes progress reporting and error handling.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Glob, Grep
005 ---
006 
007 # Brainstorming & Communication Protocol
008 
009 > **MANDATORY:** Use for complex/vague requests, new features, updates.
010 
011 ---
012 
013 ## üõë SOCRATIC GATE (ENFORCEMENT)
014 
015 ### When to Trigger
016 
017 | Pattern | Action |
018 |---------|--------|
019 | "Build/Create/Make [thing]" without details | üõë ASK 3 questions |
020 | Complex feature or architecture | üõë Clarify before implementing |
021 | Update/change request | üõë Confirm scope |
022 | Vague requirements | üõë Ask purpose, users, constraints |
023 
024 ### üö´ MANDATORY: 3 Questions Before Implementation
025 
026 1. **STOP** - Do NOT start coding
027 2. **ASK** - Minimum 3 questions:
028    - üéØ Purpose: What problem are you solving?
029    - üë• Users: Who will use this?
030    - üì¶ Scope: Must-have vs nice-to-have?
031 3. **WAIT** - Get response before proceeding
032 
033 ---
034 
035 ## üß† Dynamic Question Generation
036 
037 **‚õî NEVER use static templates.** Read `dynamic-questioning.md` for principles.
038 
039 ### Core Principles
040 
041 | Principle | Meaning |
042 |-----------|---------|
043 | **Questions Reveal Consequences** | Each question connects to an architectural decision |
044 | **Context Before Content** | Understand greenfield/feature/refactor/debug context first |
045 | **Minimum Viable Questions** | Each question must eliminate implementation paths |
046 | **Generate Data, Not Assumptions** | Don't guess‚Äîask with trade-offs |
047 
048 ### Question Generation Process
049 
050 ```
051 1. Parse request ‚Üí Extract domain, features, scale indicators
052 2. Identify decision points ‚Üí Blocking vs. deferable
053 3. Generate questions ‚Üí Priority: P0 (blocking) > P1 (high-leverage) > P2 (nice-to-have)
054 4. Format with trade-offs ‚Üí What, Why, Options, Default
055 ```
056 
057 ### Question Format (MANDATORY)
058 
059 ```markdown
060 ### [PRIORITY] **[DECISION POINT]**
061 
062 **Question:** [Clear question]
063 
064 **Why This Matters:**
065 - [Architectural consequence]
066 - [Affects: cost/complexity/timeline/scale]
067 
068 **Options:**
069 | Option | Pros | Cons | Best For |
070 |--------|------|------|----------|
071 | A | [+] | [-] | [Use case] |
072 
073 **If Not Specified:** [Default + rationale]
074 ```
075 
076 **For detailed domain-specific question banks and algorithms**, see: `dynamic-questioning.md`
077 
078 ---
079 
080 ## Progress Reporting (PRINCIPLE-BASED)
081 
082 **PRINCIPLE:** Transparency builds trust. Status must be visible and actionable.
083 
084 ### Status Board Format
085 
086 | Agent | Status | Current Task | Progress |
087 |-------|--------|--------------|----------|
088 | [Agent Name] | ‚úÖüîÑ‚è≥‚ùå‚ö†Ô∏è | [Task description] | [% or count] |
089 
090 ### Status Icons
091 
092 | Icon | Meaning | Usage |
093 |------|---------|-------|
094 | ‚úÖ | Completed | Task finished successfully |
095 | üîÑ | Running | Currently executing |
096 | ‚è≥ | Waiting | Blocked, waiting for dependency |
097 | ‚ùå | Error | Failed, needs attention |
098 | ‚ö†Ô∏è | Warning | Potential issue, not blocking |
099 
100 ---
101 
102 ## Error Handling (PRINCIPLE-BASED)
103 
104 **PRINCIPLE:** Errors are opportunities for clear communication.
105 
106 ### Error Response Pattern
107 
108 ```
109 1. Acknowledge the error
110 2. Explain what happened (user-friendly)
111 3. Offer specific solutions with trade-offs
112 4. Ask user to choose or provide alternative
113 ```
114 
115 ### Error Categories
116 
117 | Category | Response Strategy |
118 |----------|-------------------|
119 | **Port Conflict** | Offer alternative port or close existing |
120 | **Dependency Missing** | Auto-install or ask permission |
121 | **Build Failure** | Show specific error + suggested fix |
122 | **Unclear Error** | Ask for specifics: screenshot, console output |
123 
124 ---
125 
126 ## Completion Message (PRINCIPLE-BASED)
127 
128 **PRINCIPLE:** Celebrate success, guide next steps.
129 
130 ### Completion Structure
131 
132 ```
133 1. Success confirmation (celebrate briefly)
134 2. Summary of what was done (concrete)
135 3. How to verify/test (actionable)
136 4. Next steps suggestion (proactive)
137 ```
138 
139 ---
140 
141 ## Communication Principles
142 
143 | Principle | Implementation |
144 |-----------|----------------|
145 | **Concise** | No unnecessary details, get to point |
146 | **Visual** | Use emojis (‚úÖüîÑ‚è≥‚ùå) for quick scanning |
147 | **Specific** | "~2 minutes" not "wait a bit" |
148 | **Alternatives** | Offer multiple paths when stuck |
149 | **Proactive** | Suggest next step after completion |
150 
151 ---
152 
153 ## Anti-Patterns (AVOID)
154 
155 | Anti-Pattern | Why |
156 |--------------|-----|
157 | Jumping to solutions before understanding | Wastes time on wrong problem |
158 | Assuming requirements without asking | Creates wrong output |
159 | Over-engineering first version | Delays value delivery |
160 | Ignoring constraints | Creates unusable solutions |
161 | "I think" phrases | Uncertainty ‚Üí Ask instead |
162 
163 ---

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F65 path:skills/clean-code/SKILL.md hash:ac3bae08f75a0076511f1084e6b94ca5b6e2bf014f50c613a2ce16fcd5cfbcd4 lines:201 ===
001 ---
002 name: clean-code
003 description: Pragmatic coding standards - concise, direct, no over-engineering, no unnecessary comments
004 allowed-tools: Read, Write, Edit
005 version: 2.0
006 priority: CRITICAL
007 ---
008 
009 # Clean Code - Pragmatic AI Coding Standards
010 
011 > **CRITICAL SKILL** - Be **concise, direct, and solution-focused**.
012 
013 ---
014 
015 ## Core Principles
016 
017 | Principle | Rule |
018 |-----------|------|
019 | **SRP** | Single Responsibility - each function/class does ONE thing |
020 | **DRY** | Don't Repeat Yourself - extract duplicates, reuse |
021 | **KISS** | Keep It Simple - simplest solution that works |
022 | **YAGNI** | You Aren't Gonna Need It - don't build unused features |
023 | **Boy Scout** | Leave code cleaner than you found it |
024 
025 ---
026 
027 ## Naming Rules
028 
029 | Element | Convention |
030 |---------|------------|
031 | **Variables** | Reveal intent: `userCount` not `n` |
032 | **Functions** | Verb + noun: `getUserById()` not `user()` |
033 | **Booleans** | Question form: `isActive`, `hasPermission`, `canEdit` |
034 | **Constants** | SCREAMING_SNAKE: `MAX_RETRY_COUNT` |
035 
036 > **Rule:** If you need a comment to explain a name, rename it.
037 
038 ---
039 
040 ## Function Rules
041 
042 | Rule | Description |
043 |------|-------------|
044 | **Small** | Max 20 lines, ideally 5-10 |
045 | **One Thing** | Does one thing, does it well |
046 | **One Level** | One level of abstraction per function |
047 | **Few Args** | Max 3 arguments, prefer 0-2 |
048 | **No Side Effects** | Don't mutate inputs unexpectedly |
049 
050 ---
051 
052 ## Code Structure
053 
054 | Pattern | Apply |
055 |---------|-------|
056 | **Guard Clauses** | Early returns for edge cases |
057 | **Flat > Nested** | Avoid deep nesting (max 2 levels) |
058 | **Composition** | Small functions composed together |
059 | **Colocation** | Keep related code close |
060 
061 ---
062 
063 ## AI Coding Style
064 
065 | Situation | Action |
066 |-----------|--------|
067 | User asks for feature | Write it directly |
068 | User reports bug | Fix it, don't explain |
069 | No clear requirement | Ask, don't assume |
070 
071 ---
072 
073 ## Anti-Patterns (DON'T)
074 
075 | ‚ùå Pattern | ‚úÖ Fix |
076 |-----------|-------|
077 | Comment every line | Delete obvious comments |
078 | Helper for one-liner | Inline the code |
079 | Factory for 2 objects | Direct instantiation |
080 | utils.ts with 1 function | Put code where used |
081 | "First we import..." | Just write code |
082 | Deep nesting | Guard clauses |
083 | Magic numbers | Named constants |
084 | God functions | Split by responsibility |
085 
086 ---
087 
088 ## üî¥ Before Editing ANY File (THINK FIRST!)
089 
090 **Before changing a file, ask yourself:**
091 
092 | Question | Why |
093 |----------|-----|
094 | **What imports this file?** | They might break |
095 | **What does this file import?** | Interface changes |
096 | **What tests cover this?** | Tests might fail |
097 | **Is this a shared component?** | Multiple places affected |
098 
099 **Quick Check:**
100 ```
101 File to edit: UserService.ts
102 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Who imports this? ‚Üí UserController.ts, AuthController.ts
103 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Do they need changes too? ‚Üí Check function signatures
104 ```
105 
106 > üî¥ **Rule:** Edit the file + all dependent files in the SAME task.
107 > üî¥ **Never leave broken imports or missing updates.**
108 
109 ---
110 
111 ## Summary
112 
113 | Do | Don't |
114 |----|-------|
115 | Write code directly | Write tutorials |
116 | Let code self-document | Add obvious comments |
117 | Fix bugs immediately | Explain the fix first |
118 | Inline small things | Create unnecessary files |
119 | Name things clearly | Use abbreviations |
120 | Keep functions small | Write 100+ line functions |
121 
122 > **Remember: The user wants working code, not a programming lesson.**
123 
124 ---
125 
126 ## üî¥ Self-Check Before Completing (MANDATORY)
127 
128 **Before saying "task complete", verify:**
129 
130 | Check | Question |
131 |-------|----------|
132 | ‚úÖ **Goal met?** | Did I do exactly what user asked? |
133 | ‚úÖ **Files edited?** | Did I modify all necessary files? |
134 | ‚úÖ **Code works?** | Did I test/verify the change? |
135 | ‚úÖ **No errors?** | Lint and TypeScript pass? |
136 | ‚úÖ **Nothing forgotten?** | Any edge cases missed? |
137 
138 > üî¥ **Rule:** If ANY check fails, fix it before completing.
139 
140 ---
141 
142 ## Verification Scripts (MANDATORY)
143 
144 > üî¥ **CRITICAL:** Each agent runs ONLY their own skill's scripts after completing work.
145 
146 ### Agent ‚Üí Script Mapping
147 
148 | Agent | Script | Command |
149 |-------|--------|---------|
150 | **frontend-specialist** | UX Audit | `python .agent/skills/frontend-design/scripts/ux_audit.py .` |
151 | **frontend-specialist** | A11y Check | `python .agent/skills/frontend-design/scripts/accessibility_checker.py .` |
152 | **backend-specialist** | API Validator | `python .agent/skills/api-patterns/scripts/api_validator.py .` |
153 | **mobile-developer** | Mobile Audit | `python .agent/skills/mobile-design/scripts/mobile_audit.py .` |
154 | **database-architect** | Schema Validate | `python .agent/skills/database-design/scripts/schema_validator.py .` |
155 | **security-auditor** | Security Scan | `python .agent/skills/vulnerability-scanner/scripts/security_scan.py .` |
156 | **seo-specialist** | SEO Check | `python .agent/skills/seo-fundamentals/scripts/seo_checker.py .` |
157 | **seo-specialist** | GEO Check | `python .agent/skills/geo-fundamentals/scripts/geo_checker.py .` |
158 | **performance-optimizer** | Lighthouse | `python .agent/skills/performance-profiling/scripts/lighthouse_audit.py <url>` |

169 
170 ### üî¥ Script Output Handling (READ ‚Üí SUMMARIZE ‚Üí ASK)
171 
172 **When running a validation script, you MUST:**
173 
174 1. **Run the script** and capture ALL output
175 2. **Parse the output** - identify errors, warnings, and passes
176 3. **Summarize to user** in this format:
177 
178 ```markdown
179 ## Script Results: [script_name.py]
180 
181 ### ‚ùå Errors Found (X items)
182 - [File:Line] Error description 1
183 - [File:Line] Error description 2
184 
185 ### ‚ö†Ô∏è Warnings (Y items)
186 - [File:Line] Warning description
187 
188 ### ‚úÖ Passed (Z items)
189 - Check 1 passed
190 - Check 2 passed
191 
192 **Should I fix the X errors?**
193 ```
194 
195 4. **Wait for user confirmation** before fixing
196 5. **After fixing** ‚Üí Re-run script to confirm
197 
198 > üî¥ **VIOLATION:** Running script and ignoring output = FAILED task.
199 > üî¥ **VIOLATION:** Auto-fixing without asking = Not allowed.
200 > üî¥ **Rule:** Always READ output ‚Üí SUMMARIZE ‚Üí ASK ‚Üí then fix.

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F66 path:skills/code-review-checklist/SKILL.md hash:905ec9820ad5ac6f04de94a26921c1c7e363b3d5449853c1ffa2150f0c9e8caf lines:109 ===
001 ---
002 name: code-review-checklist
003 description: Code review guidelines covering code quality, security, and best practices.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Glob, Grep
005 ---
006 
007 # Code Review Checklist
008 
009 ## Quick Review Checklist
010 
011 ### Correctness
012 - [ ] Code does what it's supposed to do
013 - [ ] Edge cases handled
014 - [ ] Error handling in place
015 - [ ] No obvious bugs
016 
017 ### Security
018 - [ ] Input validated and sanitized
019 - [ ] No SQL/NoSQL injection vulnerabilities
020 - [ ] No XSS or CSRF vulnerabilities
021 - [ ] No hardcoded secrets or sensitive credentials
022 - [ ] **AI-Specific:** Protection against Prompt Injection (if applicable)
023 - [ ] **AI-Specific:** Outputs are sanitized before being used in critical sinks
024 
025 ### Performance
026 - [ ] No N+1 queries
027 - [ ] No unnecessary loops
028 - [ ] Appropriate caching
029 - [ ] Bundle size impact considered
030 
031 ### Code Quality
032 - [ ] Clear naming
033 - [ ] DRY - no duplicate code
034 - [ ] SOLID principles followed
035 - [ ] Appropriate abstraction level
036 
037 ### Testing
038 - [ ] Unit tests for new code
039 - [ ] Edge cases tested
040 - [ ] Tests readable and maintainable
041 
042 ### Documentation
043 - [ ] Complex logic commented
044 - [ ] Public APIs documented
045 - [ ] README updated if needed
046 
047 ## AI & LLM Review Patterns (2025)
048 
049 ### Logic & Hallucinations
050 - [ ] **Chain of Thought:** Does the logic follow a verifiable path?
051 - [ ] **Edge Cases:** Did the AI account for empty states, timeouts, and partial failures?
052 - [ ] **External State:** Is the code making safe assumptions about file systems or networks?
053 
054 ### Prompt Engineering Review
055 ```markdown
056 // ‚ùå Vague prompt in code
057 const response = await ai.generate(userInput);
058 
059 // ‚úÖ Structured & Safe prompt
060 const response = await ai.generate({
061   system: "You are a specialized parser...",
062   input: sanitize(userInput),
063   schema: ResponseSchema
064 });
065 ```
066 
067 ## Anti-Patterns to Flag
068 
069 ```typescript
070 // ‚ùå Magic numbers
071 if (status === 3) { ... }
072 
073 // ‚úÖ Named constants
074 if (status === Status.ACTIVE) { ... }
075 
076 // ‚ùå Deep nesting
077 if (a) { if (b) { if (c) { ... } } }
078 
079 // ‚úÖ Early returns
080 if (!a) return;
081 if (!b) return;
082 if (!c) return;
083 // do work
084 
085 // ‚ùå Long functions (100+ lines)
086 // ‚úÖ Small, focused functions
087 
088 // ‚ùå any type
089 const data: any = ...
090 
091 // ‚úÖ Proper types
092 const data: UserData = ...
093 ```
094 
095 ## Review Comments Guide
096 
097 ```
098 // Blocking issues use üî¥
099 üî¥ BLOCKING: SQL injection vulnerability here
100 
101 // Important suggestions use üü°
102 üü° SUGGESTION: Consider using useMemo for performance
103 
104 // Minor nits use üü¢
105 üü¢ NIT: Prefer const over let for immutable variable
106 
107 // Questions use ‚ùì
108 ‚ùì QUESTION: What happens if user is null here?
109 ```

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F67 path:skills/database-design/database-selection.md hash:3655cdd3a38a9ca1ae8408be8057ea628b08bf9ab22460b1bc571228dd2ba6c6 lines:43 ===
001 # Database Selection (2025)
002 
003 > Choose database based on context, not default.
004 
005 ## Decision Tree
006 
007 ```
008 What are your requirements?
009 ‚îÇ
010 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Full relational features needed
011 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Self-hosted ‚Üí PostgreSQL
012 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Serverless ‚Üí Neon, Supabase
013 ‚îÇ
014 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Edge deployment / Ultra-low latency
015 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Turso (edge SQLite)
016 ‚îÇ
017 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ AI / Vector search
018 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ PostgreSQL + pgvector
019 ‚îÇ
020 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Simple / Embedded / Local
021 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ SQLite
022 ‚îÇ
023 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Global distribution
024     ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ PlanetScale, CockroachDB, Turso
025 ```
026 
027 ## Comparison
028 
029 | Database | Best For | Trade-offs |
030 |----------|----------|------------|
031 | **PostgreSQL** | Full features, complex queries | Needs hosting |
032 | **Neon** | Serverless PG, branching | PG complexity |
033 | **Turso** | Edge, low latency | SQLite limitations |
034 | **SQLite** | Simple, embedded, local | Single-writer |
035 | **PlanetScale** | MySQL, global scale | No foreign keys |
036 
037 ## Questions to Ask
038 
039 1. What's the deployment environment?
040 2. How complex are the queries?
041 3. Is edge/serverless important?
042 4. Vector search needed?
043 5. Global distribution required?
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F67 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F68 path:skills/database-design/indexing.md hash:eec8ce01e7c1c8ec2aed7a96d260a52b12d90c2996288e32814a8d9cf29cc22a lines:39 ===
001 # Indexing Principles
002 
003 > When and how to create indexes effectively.
004 
005 ## When to Create Indexes
006 
007 ```
008 Index these:
009 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Columns in WHERE clauses
010 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Columns in JOIN conditions
011 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Columns in ORDER BY
012 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Foreign key columns
013 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Unique constraints
014 
015 Don't over-index:
016 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Write-heavy tables (slower inserts)
017 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Low-cardinality columns
018 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Columns rarely queried
019 ```
020 
021 ## Index Type Selection
022 
023 | Type | Use For |
024 |------|---------|
025 | **B-tree** | General purpose, equality & range |
026 | **Hash** | Equality only, faster |
027 | **GIN** | JSONB, arrays, full-text |
028 | **GiST** | Geometric, range types |
029 | **HNSW/IVFFlat** | Vector similarity (pgvector) |
030 
031 ## Composite Index Principles
032 
033 ```
034 Order matters for composite indexes:
035 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Equality columns first
036 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Range columns last
037 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Most selective first
038 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Match query pattern
039 ```
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F68 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F69 path:skills/database-design/migrations.md hash:b5b9e518f18264cdd946f4914d73c2355065ba712cb61db01ba59bacb95423a2 lines:48 ===
001 # Migration Principles
002 
003 > Safe migration strategy for zero-downtime changes.
004 
005 ## Safe Migration Strategy
006 
007 ```
008 For zero-downtime changes:
009 ‚îÇ
010 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Adding column
011 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Add as nullable ‚Üí backfill ‚Üí add NOT NULL
012 ‚îÇ
013 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Removing column
014 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Stop using ‚Üí deploy ‚Üí remove column
015 ‚îÇ
016 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Adding index
017 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ CREATE INDEX CONCURRENTLY (non-blocking)
018 ‚îÇ
019 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Renaming column
020     ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Add new ‚Üí migrate data ‚Üí deploy ‚Üí drop old
021 ```
022 
023 ## Migration Philosophy
024 
025 - Never make breaking changes in one step
026 - Test migrations on data copy first
027 - Have rollback plan
028 - Run in transaction when possible
029 
030 ## Serverless Databases
031 
032 ### Neon (Serverless PostgreSQL)
033 
034 | Feature | Benefit |
035 |---------|---------|
036 | Scale to zero | Cost savings |
037 | Instant branching | Dev/preview |
038 | Full PostgreSQL | Compatibility |
039 | Autoscaling | Traffic handling |
040 
041 ### Turso (Edge SQLite)
042 
043 | Feature | Benefit |
044 |---------|---------|
045 | Edge locations | Ultra-low latency |
046 | SQLite compatible | Simple |
047 | Generous free tier | Cost |
048 | Global distribution | Performance |
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F69 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F70 path:skills/database-design/optimization.md hash:10a6f484fdae9973957030d8ef47bad4ffba9f7709e9c824883a97f92925a722 lines:36 ===
001 # Query Optimization
002 
003 > N+1 problem, EXPLAIN ANALYZE, optimization priorities.
004 
005 ## N+1 Problem
006 
007 ```
008 What is N+1?
009 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ 1 query to get parent records
010 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ N queries to get related records
011 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Very slow!
012 
013 Solutions:
014 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ JOIN ‚Üí Single query with all data
015 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Eager loading ‚Üí ORM handles JOIN
016 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ DataLoader ‚Üí Batch and cache (GraphQL)
017 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Subquery ‚Üí Fetch related in one query
018 ```
019 
020 ## Query Analysis Mindset
021 
022 ```
023 Before optimizing:
024 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ EXPLAIN ANALYZE the query
025 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Look for Seq Scan (full table scan)
026 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Check actual vs estimated rows
027 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Identify missing indexes
028 ```
029 
030 ## Optimization Priorities
031 
032 1. **Add missing indexes** (most common issue)
033 2. **Select only needed columns** (not SELECT *)
034 3. **Use proper JOINs** (avoid subqueries when possible)
035 4. **Limit early** (pagination at database level)
036 5. **Cache** (when appropriate)
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F70 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F71 path:skills/database-design/orm-selection.md hash:11ece2e816949e26a7019b84004e240a9f9ab0b38c4f454bd522dd251c5dac97 lines:30 ===
001 # ORM Selection (2025)
002 
003 > Choose ORM based on deployment and DX needs.
004 
005 ## Decision Tree
006 
007 ```
008 What's the context?
009 ‚îÇ
010 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Edge deployment / Bundle size matters
011 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Drizzle (smallest, SQL-like)
012 ‚îÇ
013 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Best DX / Schema-first
014 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Prisma (migrations, studio)
015 ‚îÇ
016 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Maximum control
017 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Raw SQL with query builder
018 ‚îÇ
019 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Python ecosystem
020     ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ SQLAlchemy 2.0 (async support)
021 ```
022 
023 ## Comparison
024 
025 | ORM | Best For | Trade-offs |
026 |-----|----------|------------|
027 | **Drizzle** | Edge, TypeScript | Newer, less examples |
028 | **Prisma** | DX, schema management | Heavier, not edge-ready |
029 | **Kysely** | Type-safe SQL builder | Manual migrations |
030 | **Raw SQL** | Complex queries, control | Manual type safety |
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F71 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F72 path:skills/database-design/schema-design.md hash:0a83addd1e9963e3d958eb00474d7dc72881c4290a97bac03bf09553607e3f6f lines:56 ===
001 # Schema Design Principles
002 
003 > Normalization, primary keys, timestamps, relationships.
004 
005 ## Normalization Decision
006 
007 ```
008 When to normalize (separate tables):
009 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Data is repeated across rows
010 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Updates would need multiple changes
011 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Relationships are clear
012 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Query patterns benefit
013 
014 When to denormalize (embed/duplicate):
015 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Read performance critical
016 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Data rarely changes
017 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Always fetched together
018 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Simpler queries needed
019 ```
020 
021 ## Primary Key Selection
022 
023 | Type | Use When |
024 |------|----------|
025 | **UUID** | Distributed systems, security |
026 | **ULID** | UUID + sortable by time |
027 | **Auto-increment** | Simple apps, single database |
028 | **Natural key** | Rarely (business meaning) |
029 
030 ## Timestamp Strategy
031 
032 ```
033 For every table:
034 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ created_at ‚Üí When created
035 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ updated_at ‚Üí Last modified
036 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ deleted_at ‚Üí Soft delete (if needed)
037 
038 Use TIMESTAMPTZ (with timezone) not TIMESTAMP
039 ```
040 
041 ## Relationship Types
042 
043 | Type | When | Implementation |
044 |------|------|----------------|
045 | **One-to-One** | Extension data | Separate table with FK |
046 | **One-to-Many** | Parent-children | FK on child table |
047 | **Many-to-Many** | Both sides have many | Junction table |
048 
049 ## Foreign Key ON DELETE
050 
051 ```
052 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ CASCADE ‚Üí Delete children with parent
053 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ SET NULL ‚Üí Children become orphans
054 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ RESTRICT ‚Üí Prevent delete if children exist
055 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ SET DEFAULT ‚Üí Children get default value
056 ```
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F72 ===
