=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F74 path:skills/deployment-procedures/SKILL.md hash:61e5f86dfbacfcc76604917d49cc5c9e80d53a0fddf48933ede81005549abb17 lines:241 ===
001 ---
002 name: deployment-procedures
003 description: Production deployment principles and decision-making. Safe deployment workflows, rollback strategies, and verification. Teaches thinking, not scripts.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Glob, Grep, Bash
005 ---
006 
007 # Deployment Procedures
008 
009 > Deployment principles and decision-making for safe production releases.
010 > **Learn to THINK, not memorize scripts.**
011 
012 ---
013 
014 ## ‚ö†Ô∏è How to Use This Skill
015 
016 This skill teaches **deployment principles**, not bash scripts to copy.
017 
018 - Every deployment is unique
019 - Understand the WHY behind each step
020 - Adapt procedures to your platform
021 
022 ---
023 
024 ## 1. Platform Selection
025 
026 ### Decision Tree
027 
028 ```
029 What are you deploying?
030 ‚îÇ
031 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Static site / JAMstack
032 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Vercel, Netlify, Cloudflare Pages
033 ‚îÇ
034 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Simple web app
035 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Managed ‚Üí Railway, Render, Fly.io
036 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Control ‚Üí VPS + PM2/Docker
037 ‚îÇ
038 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Microservices
039 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Container orchestration
040 ‚îÇ
041 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Serverless
042     ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Edge functions, Lambda
043 ```
044 
045 ### Each Platform Has Different Procedures
046 
047 | Platform | Deployment Method |
048 |----------|------------------|
049 | **Vercel/Netlify** | Git push, auto-deploy |
050 | **Railway/Render** | Git push or CLI |
051 | **VPS + PM2** | SSH + manual steps |
052 | **Docker** | Image push + orchestration |
053 | **Kubernetes** | kubectl apply |
054 
055 ---
056 
057 ## 2. Pre-Deployment Principles
058 
059 ### The 4 Verification Categories
060 
061 | Category | What to Check |
062 |----------|--------------|
063 | **Code Quality** | Tests passing, linting clean, reviewed |
064 | **Build** | Production build works, no warnings |
065 | **Environment** | Env vars set, secrets current |
066 | **Safety** | Backup done, rollback plan ready |
067 
068 ### Pre-Deployment Checklist
069 
070 - [ ] All tests passing
071 - [ ] Code reviewed and approved
072 - [ ] Production build successful
073 - [ ] Environment variables verified
074 - [ ] Database migrations ready (if any)
075 - [ ] Rollback plan documented
076 - [ ] Team notified
077 - [ ] Monitoring ready
078 
079 ---
080 
081 ## 3. Deployment Workflow Principles
082 
083 ### The 5-Phase Process
084 
085 ```
086 1. PREPARE
087    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Verify code, build, env vars
088 
089 2. BACKUP
090    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Save current state before changing
091 
092 3. DEPLOY
093    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Execute with monitoring open
094 
095 4. VERIFY
096    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Health check, logs, key flows
097 
098 5. CONFIRM or ROLLBACK
099    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ All good? Confirm. Issues? Rollback.
100 ```
101 
102 ### Phase Principles
103 
104 | Phase | Principle |
105 |-------|-----------|
106 | **Prepare** | Never deploy untested code |
107 | **Backup** | Can't rollback without backup |
108 | **Deploy** | Watch it happen, don't walk away |
109 | **Verify** | Trust but verify |
110 | **Confirm** | Have rollback trigger ready |
111 
112 ---
113 
114 ## 4. Post-Deployment Verification
115 
116 ### What to Verify
117 
118 | Check | Why |
119 |-------|-----|
120 | **Health endpoint** | Service is running |
121 | **Error logs** | No new errors |
122 | **Key user flows** | Critical features work |
123 | **Performance** | Response times acceptable |
124 
125 ### Verification Window
126 
127 - **First 5 minutes**: Active monitoring
128 - **15 minutes**: Confirm stable
129 - **1 hour**: Final verification
130 - **Next day**: Review metrics
131 
132 ---
133 
134 ## 5. Rollback Principles
135 
136 ### When to Rollback
137 
138 | Symptom | Action |
139 |---------|--------|
140 | Service down | Rollback immediately |
141 | Critical errors | Rollback |
142 | Performance >50% degraded | Consider rollback |
143 | Minor issues | Fix forward if quick |
144 
145 ### Rollback Strategy by Platform
146 
147 | Platform | Rollback Method |
148 |----------|----------------|
149 | **Vercel/Netlify** | Redeploy previous commit |
150 | **Railway/Render** | Rollback in dashboard |
151 | **VPS + PM2** | Restore backup, restart |
152 | **Docker** | Previous image tag |
153 | **K8s** | kubectl rollout undo |
154 
155 ### Rollback Principles
156 
157 1. **Speed over perfection**: Rollback first, debug later
158 2. **Don't compound errors**: One rollback, not multiple changes
159 3. **Communicate**: Tell team what happened
160 4. **Post-mortem**: Understand why after stable
161 
162 ---
163 
164 ## 6. Zero-Downtime Deployment
165 
166 ### Strategies
167 
168 | Strategy | How It Works |
169 |----------|--------------|
170 | **Rolling** | Replace instances one by one |
171 | **Blue-Green** | Switch traffic between environments |
172 | **Canary** | Gradual traffic shift |
173 
174 ### Selection Principles
175 
176 | Scenario | Strategy |
177 |----------|----------|
178 | Standard release | Rolling |
179 | High-risk change | Blue-green (easy rollback) |
180 | Need validation | Canary (test with real traffic) |
181 
182 ---
183 
184 ## 7. Emergency Procedures
185 
186 ### Service Down Priority
187 
188 1. **Assess**: What's the symptom?
189 2. **Quick fix**: Restart if unclear
190 3. **Rollback**: If restart doesn't help
191 4. **Investigate**: After stable
192 
193 ### Investigation Order
194 
195 | Check | Common Issues |
196 |-------|--------------|
197 | **Logs** | Errors, exceptions |
198 | **Resources** | Disk full, memory |
199 | **Network** | DNS, firewall |
200 | **Dependencies** | Database, APIs |
201 
202 ---
203 
204 ## 8. Anti-Patterns
205 
206 | ‚ùå Don't | ‚úÖ Do |
207 |----------|-------|
208 | Deploy on Friday | Deploy early in week |
209 | Rush deployment | Follow the process |
210 | Skip staging | Always test first |
211 | Deploy without backup | Backup before deploy |
212 | Walk away after deploy | Monitor for 15+ min |
213 | Multiple changes at once | One change at a time |
214 
215 ---
216 
217 ## 9. Decision Checklist
218 
219 Before deploying:
220 
221 - [ ] **Platform-appropriate procedure?**
222 - [ ] **Backup strategy ready?**
223 - [ ] **Rollback plan documented?**
224 - [ ] **Monitoring configured?**
225 - [ ] **Team notified?**
226 - [ ] **Time to monitor after?**
227 
228 ---
229 
230 ## 10. Best Practices
231 
232 1. **Small, frequent deploys** over big releases
233 2. **Feature flags** for risky changes
234 3. **Automate** repetitive steps
235 4. **Document** every deployment
236 5. **Review** what went wrong after issues
237 6. **Test rollback** before you need it
238 
239 ---
240 
241 > **Remember:** Every deployment is a risk. Minimize risk through preparation, not speed.
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F74 ===

090         # Calculate tax
091         tax = i['price'] * 0.1
092         total = total + i['price'] + tax
093         time.sleep(0.1)  # Simulate slow network call
094     return total
095 
096 def run_batch():
097     users = [{'id': 1, 'name': 'Alice'}, {'id': 2, 'name': 'Bob'}]
098     items = [{'price': 10}, {'price': 20}, {'price': 100}]
099 
100     u = get_user_data(users, 3)
101     print("User found: " + u['name'])  # Will crash if None
102 
103     print("Total: " + str(process_payments(items)))
104 
105 if __name__ == "__main__":
106     run_batch()
107 ```
108 
109 **Prompt**: `review the @demo_bad_code.py file`
110 
111 Agent s·∫Ω t·ª± ƒë·ªông x√°c ƒë·ªãnh k·ªπ nƒÉng `code-review`, t·∫£i th√¥ng tin v√† th·ª±c hi·ªán theo h∆∞·ªõng d·∫´n.
112 
113 ---
114

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F76 path:skills/documentation-templates/SKILL.md hash:463a55ff6ded0e84d0f0eb1454c9635b7b8695ea5ee4a308f0cd810f27060dba lines:194 ===
001 ---
002 name: documentation-templates
003 description: Documentation templates and structure guidelines. README, API docs, code comments, and AI-friendly documentation.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Glob, Grep
005 ---
006 
007 # Documentation Templates
008 
009 > Templates and structure guidelines for common documentation types.
010 
011 ---
012 
013 ## 1. README Structure
014 
015 ### Essential Sections (Priority Order)
016 
017 | Section | Purpose |
018 |---------|---------|
019 | **Title + One-liner** | What is this? |
020 | **Quick Start** | Running in <5 min |
021 | **Features** | What can I do? |
022 | **Configuration** | How to customize |
023 | **API Reference** | Link to detailed docs |
024 | **Contributing** | How to help |
025 | **License** | Legal |
026 
027 ### README Template
028 
029 ```markdown
030 # Project Name
031 
032 Brief one-line description.
033 
034 ## Quick Start
035 
036 [Minimum steps to run]
037 
038 ## Features
039 
040 - Feature 1
041 - Feature 2
042 
043 ## Configuration
044 
045 | Variable | Description | Default |
046 |----------|-------------|---------|
047 | PORT | Server port | 3000 |
048 
049 ## Documentation
050 
051 - [API Reference](./docs/api.md)
052 - [Architecture](./docs/architecture.md)
053 
054 ## License
055 
056 MIT
057 ```
058 
059 ---
060 
061 ## 2. API Documentation Structure
062 
063 ### Per-Endpoint Template
064 
065 ```markdown
066 ## GET /users/:id
067 
068 Get a user by ID.
069 
070 **Parameters:**
071 | Name | Type | Required | Description |
072 |------|------|----------|-------------|
073 | id | string | Yes | User ID |
074 
075 **Response:**
076 - 200: User object
077 - 404: User not found
078 
079 **Example:**
080 [Request and response example]
081 ```
082 
083 ---
084 
085 ## 3. Code Comment Guidelines
086 
087 ### JSDoc/TSDoc Template
088 
089 ```typescript
090 /**
091  * Brief description of what the function does.
092  *
093  * @param paramName - Description of parameter
094  * @returns Description of return value
095  * @throws ErrorType - When this error occurs
096  *
097  * @example
098  * const result = functionName(input);
099  */
100 ```
101 
102 ### When to Comment
103 
104 | ‚úÖ Comment | ‚ùå Don't Comment |
105 |-----------|-----------------|
106 | Why (business logic) | What (obvious) |
107 | Complex algorithms | Every line |
108 | Non-obvious behavior | Self-explanatory code |
109 | API contracts | Implementation details |
110 
111 ---
112 
113 ## 4. Changelog Template (Keep a Changelog)
114 
115 ```markdown
116 # Changelog
117 
118 ## [Unreleased]
119 ### Added
120 - New feature
121 
122 ## [1.0.0] - 2025-01-01
123 ### Added
124 - Initial release
125 ### Changed
126 - Updated dependency
127 ### Fixed
128 - Bug fix
129 ```
130 
131 ---
132 
133 ## 5. Architecture Decision Record (ADR)
134 
135 ```markdown
136 # ADR-001: [Title]
137 
138 ## Status
139 Accepted / Deprecated / Superseded
140 
141 ## Context
142 Why are we making this decision?
143 
144 ## Decision
145 What did we decide?
146 
147 ## Consequences
148 What are the trade-offs?
149 ```
150 
151 ---
152 
153 ## 6. AI-Friendly Documentation (2025)
154 
155 ### llms.txt Template
156 
157 For AI crawlers and agents:
158 
159 ```markdown
160 # Project Name
161 > One-line objective.
162 
163 ## Core Files
164 - [src/index.ts]: Main entry
165 - [src/api/]: API routes
166 - [docs/]: Documentation
167 
168 ## Key Concepts
169 - Concept 1: Brief explanation
170 - Concept 2: Brief explanation
171 ```
172 
173 ### MCP-Ready Documentation
174 
175 For RAG indexing:
176 - Clear H1-H3 hierarchy
177 - JSON/YAML examples for data structures
178 - Mermaid diagrams for flows
179 - Self-contained sections
180 
181 ---
182 
183 ## 7. Structure Principles
184 
185 | Principle | Why |
186 |-----------|-----|
187 | **Scannable** | Headers, lists, tables |
188 | **Examples first** | Show, don't just tell |
189 | **Progressive detail** | Simple ‚Üí Complex |
190 | **Up to date** | Outdated = misleading |
191 
192 ---
193 
194 > **Remember:** Templates are starting points. Adapt to your project's needs.

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F77 path:skills/frontend-design/animation-guide.md hash:50b6c57bd21dd545befc48038ed92dc5e1ada7d65489a6fc833f68857a461317 lines:331 ===
001 # Animation Guidelines Reference
002 
003 > Animation principles and timing psychology - learn to decide, not copy.
004 > **No fixed durations to memorize - understand what affects timing.**
005 
006 ---
007 
008 ## 1. Duration Principles
009 
010 ### What Affects Timing
011 
012 ```
013 Factors that determine animation speed:
014 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ DISTANCE: Further travel = longer duration
015 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ SIZE: Larger elements = slower animations
016 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ COMPLEXITY: Complex = slower to process
017 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ IMPORTANCE: Critical actions = clear feedback
018 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ CONTEXT: Urgent = fast, luxurious = slow
019 ```
020 
021 ### Duration Ranges by Purpose
022 
023 | Purpose | Range | Why |
024 |---------|-------|-----|
025 | Instant feedback | 50-100ms | Below perception threshold |
026 | Micro-interactions | 100-200ms | Quick but noticeable |
027 | Standard transitions | 200-300ms | Comfortable pace |
028 | Complex animations | 300-500ms | Time to follow |
029 | Page transitions | 400-600ms | Smooth handoff |
030 | **Wow/Premium Effects** | 800ms+ | Dramatic, organic spring-based, layered |
031 
032 ### Choosing Duration
033 
034 Ask yourself:
035 1. How far is the element moving?
036 2. How important is it to notice this change?
037 3. Is the user waiting, or is this background?
038 
039 ---
040 
041 ## 2. Easing Principles
042 
043 ### What Easing Does
044 
045 ```
046 Easing = how speed changes over time
047 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Linear: constant speed (mechanical, robotic)
048 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Ease-out: fast start, slow end (natural entry)
049 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Ease-in: slow start, fast end (natural exit)
050 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Ease-in-out: slow both ends (smooth, deliberate)
051 ```
052 
053 ### When to Use Each
054 
055 | Easing | Best For | Feels Like |
056 |--------|----------|------------|
057 | **Ease-out** | Elements entering | Arriving, settling |
058 | **Ease-in** | Elements leaving | Departing, exiting |
059 | **Ease-in-out** | Emphasis, loops | Deliberate, smooth |
060 | **Linear** | Continuous motion | Mechanical, constant |
061 | **Bounce/Elastic** | Playful UI | Fun, energetic |
062 
063 ### The Pattern
064 
065 ```css
066 /* Entering view = ease-out (decelerate) */
067 .enter {
068   animation-timing-function: ease-out;
069 }
070 
071 /* Leaving view = ease-in (accelerate) */
072 .exit {
073   animation-timing-function: ease-in;
074 }
075 
076 /* Continuous = ease-in-out */
077 .continuous {
078   animation-timing-function: ease-in-out;
079 }
080 ```
081 
082 ---
083 
084 ## 3. Micro-Interaction Principles
085 
086 ### What Makes Good Micro-Interactions
087 
088 ```
089 Purpose of micro-interactions:
090 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ FEEDBACK: Confirm the action happened
091 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ GUIDANCE: Show what's possible
092 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ STATUS: Indicate current state
093 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ DELIGHT: Small moments of joy
094 ```
095 
096 ### Button States
097 
098 ```
099 Hover ‚Üí slight visual change (lift, color, scale)
100 Active ‚Üí pressed feeling (scale down, shadow change)
101 Focus ‚Üí clear indicator (outline, ring)
102 Loading ‚Üí progress indicator (spinner, skeleton)
103 Success ‚Üí confirmation (check, color)
104 ```
105 
106 ### Principles
107 
108 1. **Respond immediately** (under 100ms perception)
109 2. **Match the action** (press = `scale(0.95)`, hover = `translateY(-4px) + glow`)
110 3. **Be bold but smooth** (Usta i≈üi hissettir)
111 4. **Be consistent** (same actions = same feedback)
112 
113 ---
114 
115 ## 4. Loading States Principles
116 
117 ### Types by Context
118 
119 | Situation | Approach |
120 |-----------|----------|
121 | Quick load (<1s) | No indicator needed |
122 | Medium (1-3s) | Spinner or simple animation |
123 | Long (3s+) | Progress bar or skeleton |
124 | Unknown duration | Indeterminate indicator |
125 
126 ### Skeleton Screens
127 
128 ```
129 Purpose: Reduce perceived wait time
130 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Show layout shape immediately
131 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Animate subtly (shimmer, pulse)
132 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Replace with content when ready
133 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Feels faster than spinner
134 ```
135 
136 ### Progress Indicators
137 
138 ```
139 When to show progress:
140 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ User-initiated action
141 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ File uploads/downloads
142 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Multi-step processes
143 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Long operations
144 
145 When NOT needed:
146 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Very quick operations
147 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Background tasks
148 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Initial page loads (skeleton better)
149 ```
150 
151 ---
152 
153 ## 5. Page Transitions Principles
154 
155 ### Transition Strategy
156 
157 ```
158 Simple rule: exit fast, enter slower
159 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Outgoing content fades quickly
160 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Incoming content animates in
161 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Avoids "everything moving at once"
162 ```
163 
164 ### Common Patterns
165 
166 | Pattern | When to Use |
167 |---------|-------------|
168 | **Fade** | Safe default, works everywhere |
169 | **Slide** | Sequential navigation (prev/next) |
170 | **Scale** | Opening/closing modals |
171 | **Shared element** | Maintaining visual continuity |
172 
173 ### Direction Matching
174 
175 ```
176 Navigation direction = animation direction
177 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Forward ‚Üí slide from right
178 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Backward ‚Üí slide from left
179 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Deeper ‚Üí scale up from center
180 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Back up ‚Üí scale down
181 ```
182 
183 ---
184 
185 ## 6. Scroll Animation Principles
186 
187 ### Progressive Reveal
188 
189 ```
190 Content appears as user scrolls:
191 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Reduces initial cognitive load
192 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Rewards exploration
193 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Must not feel sluggish
194 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Option to disable (accessibility)
195 ```
196 
197 ### Trigger Points
198 
199 | When to Trigger | Effect |
200 |-----------------|--------|
201 | Just entering viewport | Standard reveal |
202 | Centered in viewport | For emphasis |
203 | Partially visible | Earlier reveal |
204 | Fully visible | Late trigger |
205 
206 ### Animation Properties
207 
208 - Fade in (opacity)
209 - Slide up (transform)
210 - Scale (transform)
211 - Combination of above
212 
213 ### Performance
214 
215 - Use Intersection Observer
216 - Animate only transform/opacity
217 - Reduce on mobile if needed
218 
219 ---
220 
221 ## 7. Hover Effects Principles
222 
223 ### Matching Effect to Action
224 
225 | Element | Effect | Intent |
226 |---------|--------|--------|
227 | **Clickable card** | Lift + shadow | "This is interactive" |
228 | **Button** | Color/brightness change | "Press me" |
229 | **Image** | Zoom/scale | "View closer" |
230 | **Link** | Underline/color | "Navigate here" |
231 
232 ### Principles
233 
234 1. **Signal interactivity** - hover shows it's clickable
235 2. **Don't overdo it** - subtle changes work
236 3. **Match importance** - bigger change = more important
237 4. **Touch alternatives** - hover doesn't work on mobile
238 
239 ---
240 
241 ## 8. Feedback Animation Principles
242 
243 ### Success States
244 
245 ```
246 Celebrate appropriately:
247 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Minor action ‚Üí subtle check/color
248 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Major action ‚Üí more pronounced animation
249 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Completion ‚Üí satisfying animation
250 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Match brand personality
251 ```
252 
253 ### Error States
254 
255 ```
256 Draw attention without panic:
257 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Color change (semantic red)
258 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Shake animation (brief!)
259 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Focus on error field
260 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Clear messaging
261 ```
262 
263 ### Timing
264 
265 - Success: slightly longer (enjoy the moment)
266 - Error: quick (don't delay action)
267 - Loading: continuous until complete
268 
269 ---
270 
271 ## 9. Performance Principles
272 
273 ### What's Cheap to Animate
274 
275 ```
276 GPU-accelerated (FAST):
277 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ transform: translate, scale, rotate
278 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ opacity: 0 to 1
279 
280 CPU-intensive (SLOW):
281 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ width, height
282 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ top, left, right, bottom
283 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ margin, padding
284 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ border-radius changes
285 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ box-shadow changes
286 ```
287 
288 ### Optimization Strategies
289 
290 1. **Animate transform/opacity** whenever possible
291 2. **Avoid layout triggers** (size/position changes)
292 3. **Use will-change sparingly** (hints to browser)
293 4. **Test on low-end devices** (not just dev machine)
294 
295 ### Respecting User Preferences
296 
297 ```css
298 @media (prefers-reduced-motion: reduce) {
299   /* Honor this preference */
300   /* Essential animations only */
301   /* Reduce or remove decorative motion */
302 }
303 ```
304 
305 ---
306 
307 ## 10. Animation Decision Checklist
308 
309 Before adding animation:
310 
311 - [ ] **Is there a purpose?** (feedback/guidance/delight)
312 - [ ] **Is timing appropriate?** (not too fast/slow)
313 - [ ] **Did you pick correct easing?** (enter/exit/emphasis)
314 - [ ] **Is it performant?** (transform/opacity only)
315 - [ ] **Tested reduced motion?** (accessibility)
316 - [ ] **Consistent with other animations?** (same timing feel)
317 - [ ] **Not your default settings?** (variety check)
318 - [ ] **Asked user about style if unclear?**
319 
320 ### Anti-Patterns
321 
322 - ‚ùå Same timing values every project
323 - ‚ùå Animation for animation's sake
324 - ‚ùå Ignoring reduced-motion preference
325 - ‚ùå Animating expensive properties
326 - ‚ùå Too many things animating at once
327 - ‚ùå Delays that frustrate users
328 
329 ---
330 
331 > **Remember**: Animation is communication. Every motion should have meaning and serve the user experience.
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F77 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F78 path:skills/frontend-design/color-system.md hash:31a6b50a4263591f68725461e1af85bc4334e5807bf6dac8b6342657118d0857 lines:311 ===
001 # Color System Reference
002 
003 > Color theory principles, selection process, and decision-making guidelines.
004 > **No memorized hex codes - learn to THINK about color.**
005 
006 ---
007 
008 ## 1. Color Theory Fundamentals
009 
010 ### The Color Wheel
011 
012 ```
013                     YELLOW
014                       ‚îÇ
015            Yellow-    ‚îÇ    Yellow-
016            Green      ‚îÇ    Orange
017               ‚ï≤       ‚îÇ       ‚ï±
018                ‚ï≤      ‚îÇ      ‚ï±
019     GREEN ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ ‚óè ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ ORANGE
020                ‚ï±      ‚îÇ      ‚ï≤
021               ‚ï±       ‚îÇ       ‚ï≤
022            Blue-      ‚îÇ    Red-
023            Green      ‚îÇ    Orange
024                       ‚îÇ
025                      RED
026                       ‚îÇ
027                    PURPLE
028                   ‚ï±       ‚ï≤
029              Blue-         Red-
030              Purple        Purple
031                   ‚ï≤       ‚ï±
032                     BLUE
033 ```
034 
035 ### Color Relationships
036 
037 | Scheme | How to Create | When to Use |
038 |--------|---------------|-------------|
039 | **Monochromatic** | Pick ONE hue, vary only lightness/saturation | Minimal, professional, cohesive |
040 | **Analogous** | Pick 2-3 ADJACENT hues on wheel | Harmonious, calm, nature-inspired |
041 | **Complementary** | Pick OPPOSITE hues on wheel | High contrast, vibrant, attention |
042 | **Split-Complementary** | Base + 2 colors adjacent to complement | Dynamic but balanced |
043 | **Triadic** | 3 hues EQUIDISTANT on wheel | Vibrant, playful, creative |
044 
045 ### How to Choose a Scheme:
046 1. **What's the project mood?** Calm ‚Üí Analogous. Bold ‚Üí Complementary.
047 2. **How many colors needed?** Minimal ‚Üí Monochromatic. Complex ‚Üí Triadic.
048 3. **Who's the audience?** Conservative ‚Üí Monochromatic. Young ‚Üí Triadic.
049 
050 ---
051 
052 ## 2. The 60-30-10 Rule
053 
054 ### Distribution Principle
055 ```
056 ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
057 ‚îÇ                                                 ‚îÇ
058 ‚îÇ     60% PRIMARY (Background, large areas)       ‚îÇ
059 ‚îÇ     ‚Üí Should be neutral or calming              ‚îÇ
060 ‚îÇ     ‚Üí Carries the overall tone                  ‚îÇ
061 ‚îÇ                                                 ‚îÇ
062 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
063 ‚îÇ                                    ‚îÇ            ‚îÇ
064 ‚îÇ   30% SECONDARY                    ‚îÇ 10% ACCENT ‚îÇ
065 ‚îÇ   (Cards, sections, headers)       ‚îÇ (CTAs,     ‚îÇ
066 ‚îÇ   ‚Üí Supports without dominating    ‚îÇ highlights)‚îÇ
067 ‚îÇ                                    ‚îÇ ‚Üí Draws    ‚îÇ
068 ‚îÇ                                    ‚îÇ   attention‚îÇ
069 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¥‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
070 ```
071 
072 ### Implementation Pattern
073 ```css
074 :root {
075   /* 60% - Pick based on light/dark mode and mood */
076   --color-bg: /* neutral: white, off-white, or dark gray */
077   --color-surface: /* slightly different from bg */
078 
079   /* 30% - Pick based on brand or context */
080   --color-secondary: /* muted version of primary or neutral */
081 
082   /* 10% - Pick based on desired action/emotion */
083   --color-accent: /* vibrant, attention-grabbing */
084 }
085 ```
086 
087 ---
088 
089 ## 3. Color Psychology - Meaning & Selection
090 
091 ### How to Choose Based on Context
092 
093 | If Project Is... | Consider These Hues | Why |
094 |------------------|---------------------|-----|
095 | **Finance, Tech, Healthcare** | Blues, Teals | Trust, stability, calm |
096 | **Eco, Wellness, Nature** | Greens, Earth tones | Growth, health, organic |
097 | **Food, Energy, Youth** | Orange, Yellow, Warm | Appetite, excitement, warmth |
098 | **Luxury, Beauty, Creative** | Deep Teal, Gold, Black | Sophistication, premium |
099 | **Urgency, Sales, Alerts** | Red, Orange | Action, attention, passion |
100 
101 ### Emotional Associations (For Decision Making)
102 
103 | Hue Family | Positive Associations | Cautions |
104 |------------|----------------------|----------|
105 | **Blue** | Trust, calm, professional | Can feel cold, corporate |
106 | **Green** | Growth, nature, success | Can feel boring if overused |
107 | **Red** | Passion, urgency, energy | High arousal, use sparingly |
108 | **Orange** | Warmth, friendly, creative | Can feel cheap if saturated |
109 | **Purple** | ‚ö†Ô∏è **BANNED** - AI overuses this! | Use Deep Teal/Maroon/Emerald instead |
110 | **Yellow** | Optimism, attention, happy | Hard to read, use as accent |
111 | **Black** | Elegance, power, modern | Can feel heavy |
112 | **White** | Clean, minimal, open | Can feel sterile |
113 
114 ### Selection Process:
115 1. **What industry?** ‚Üí Narrow to 2-3 hue families
116 2. **What emotion?** ‚Üí Pick primary hue
117 3. **What contrast?** ‚Üí Decide light vs dark mode
118 4. **ASK USER** ‚Üí Confirm before proceeding
119 
120 ---
121 
122 ## 4. Palette Generation Principles
123 
124 ### From a Single Color (HSL Method)
125 
126 Instead of memorizing hex codes, learn to **manipulate HSL**:
127 
128 ```
129 HSL = Hue, Saturation, Lightness
130 
131 Hue (0-360): The color family
132   0/360 = Red
133   60 = Yellow
134   120 = Green
135   180 = Cyan
136   240 = Blue
137   300 = Purple
138 
139 Saturation (0-100%): Color intensity
140   Low = Muted, sophisticated
141   High = Vibrant, energetic
142 
143 Lightness (0-100%): Brightness
144   0% = Black
145   50% = Pure color
146   100% = White
147 ```
148 
149 ### Generating a Full Palette
150 
151 Given ANY base color, create a scale:
152 
153 ```
154 Lightness Scale:
155   50  (lightest) ‚Üí L: 97%
156   100            ‚Üí L: 94%
157   200            ‚Üí L: 86%
158   300            ‚Üí L: 74%
159   400            ‚Üí L: 66%
160   500 (base)     ‚Üí L: 50-60%
161   600            ‚Üí L: 48%
162   700            ‚Üí L: 38%
163   800            ‚Üí L: 30%
164   900 (darkest)  ‚Üí L: 20%
165 ```
166 
167 ### Saturation Adjustments
168 
169 | Context | Saturation Level |
170 |---------|-----------------|
171 | **Professional/Corporate** | Lower (40-60%) |
172 | **Playful/Youth** | Higher (70-90%) |
173 | **Dark Mode** | Reduce by 10-20% |
174 | **Accessibility** | Ensure contrast, may need adjustment |
175 
176 ---
177 
178 ## 5. Context-Based Selection Guide
179 
180 ### Instead of Copying Palettes, Follow This Process:
181 
182 **Step 1: Identify the Context**
183 ```
184 What type of project?
185 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ E-commerce ‚Üí Need trust + urgency balance
186 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ SaaS/Dashboard ‚Üí Need low-fatigue, data focus
187 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Health/Wellness ‚Üí Need calming, natural feel
188 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Luxury/Premium ‚Üí Need understated elegance
189 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Creative/Portfolio ‚Üí Need personality, memorable
190 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Other ‚Üí ASK the user
191 ```
192 
193 **Step 2: Select Primary Hue Family**
194 ```
195 Based on context, pick ONE:
196 - Blue family (trust)
197 - Green family (growth)
198 - Warm family (energy)
199 - Neutral family (elegant)
200 - OR ask user preference
201 ```
202 
203 **Step 3: Decide Light/Dark Mode**
204 ```
205 Consider:
206 - User preference?
207 - Industry standard?
208 - Content type? (text-heavy = light preferred)
209 - Time of use? (evening app = dark option)
210 ```
211 
212 **Step 4: Generate Palette Using Principles**
213 - Use HSL manipulation
214 - Follow 60-30-10 rule
215 - Check contrast (WCAG)
216 - Test with actual content
217 
218 ---
219 
220 ## 6. Dark Mode Principles
221 
222 ### Key Rules (No Fixed Codes)
223 
224 1. **Never pure black** ‚Üí Use very dark gray with slight hue
225 2. **Never pure white text** ‚Üí Use 87-92% lightness
226 3. **Reduce saturation** ‚Üí Vibrant colors strain eyes in dark mode
227 4. **Elevation = brightness** ‚Üí Higher elements slightly lighter
228 
229 ### Contrast in Dark Mode
230 
231 ```
232 Background layers (darker ‚Üí lighter as elevation increases):
233 Layer 0 (base)    ‚Üí Darkest
234 Layer 1 (cards)   ‚Üí Slightly lighter
235 Layer 2 (modals)  ‚Üí Even lighter
236 Layer 3 (popups)  ‚Üí Lightest dark
237 ```
238 
239 ### Adapting Colors for Dark Mode
240 
241 | Light Mode | Dark Mode Adjustment |
242 |------------|---------------------|
243 | High saturation accent | Reduce saturation 10-20% |
244 | Pure white background | Dark gray with brand hue tint |
245 | Black text | Light gray (not pure white) |
246 | Colorful backgrounds | Desaturated, darker versions |
247 
248 ---
249 
250 ## 7. Accessibility Guidelines
251 
252 ### Contrast Requirements (WCAG)
253 
254 | Level | Normal Text | Large Text |
255 |-------|-------------|------------|
256 | AA (minimum) | 4.5:1 | 3:1 |
257 | AAA (enhanced) | 7:1 | 4.5:1 |
258 
259 ### How to Check Contrast
260 
261 1. **Convert colors to luminance**
262 2. **Calculate ratio**: (lighter + 0.05) / (darker + 0.05)
263 3. **Adjust until ratio meets requirement**
264 
265 ### Safe Patterns
266 
267 | Use Case | Guideline |
268 |----------|-----------|
269 | **Text on light bg** | Use lightness 35% or less |
270 | **Text on dark bg** | Use lightness 85% or more |
271 | **Primary on white** | Ensure dark enough variant |
272 | **Buttons** | High contrast between bg and text |
273 
274 ---
275 
276 ## 8. Color Selection Checklist
277 
278 Before finalizing any color choice, verify:
279 
280 - [ ] **Asked user preference?** (if not specified)
281 - [ ] **Matches project context?** (industry, audience)
282 - [ ] **Follows 60-30-10?** (proper distribution)
283 - [ ] **WCAG compliant?** (contrast checked)
284 - [ ] **Works in both modes?** (if dark mode needed)
285 - [ ] **NOT your default/favorite?** (variety check)
286 - [ ] **Different from last project?** (avoid repetition)
287 
288 ---
289 
290 ## 9. Anti-Patterns to Avoid
291 
292 ### ‚ùå DON'T:
293 - Copy the same hex codes every project
294 - Default to purple/violet (AI tendency)
295 - Default to dark mode + neon (AI tendency)
296 - Use pure black (#000000) backgrounds
297 - Use pure white (#FFFFFF) text on dark
298 - Ignore user's industry context
299 - Skip asking user preference
300 
301 ### ‚úÖ DO:
302 - Generate fresh palette per project
303 - Ask user about color preferences
304 - Consider industry and audience
305 - Use HSL for flexible manipulation
306 - Test contrast and accessibility
307 - Offer light AND dark options
308 
309 ---
310 
311 > **Remember**: Colors are decisions, not defaults. Every project deserves thoughtful selection based on its unique context.

047 ### Who is your target user?
048 
049 ```
050 TARGET AUDIENCE
051       ‚îÇ

053       ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Colors: Bold, vibrant, unexpected combinations
054       ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Type: Large, expressive, variable
055       ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Layout: Mobile-first, vertical, snackable

058       ‚îÇ

062       ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Layout: Responsive, card-based, organized
063       ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Effects: Subtle, purposeful only
064       ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Approach: Value-driven, transparent, sustainable
065       ‚îÇ
066       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Gen X (42-57)
067       ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Colors: Professional, trusted, conservative
068       ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Type: Familiar, clear, no-nonsense
069       ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Layout: Traditional hierarchy, predictable
070       ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Effects: Minimal, functional feedback
071       ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Approach: Direct, efficient, reliable
072       ‚îÇ

084           ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Effects: Professional, subtle
085           ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Approach: Expert, solution-focused, ROI-driven

090 ## 3. Color Selection Decision Tree
091 
092 ### Instead of fixed hex codes, use this process:
093 
094 ```
095 WHAT EMOTION/ACTION DO YOU WANT?
096             ‚îÇ
097             ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Trust & Security
098             ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Consider: Blue family, professional neutrals
099             ‚îÇ       ‚Üí ASK user for specific shade preference
100             ‚îÇ
101             ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Growth & Health
102             ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Consider: Green family, natural tones
103             ‚îÇ       ‚Üí ASK user if eco/nature/wellness focus
104             ‚îÇ
105             ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Urgency & Action
106             ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Consider: Warm colors (orange/red) as ACCENTS
107             ‚îÇ       ‚Üí Use sparingly, ASK if appropriate
108             ‚îÇ
109             ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Luxury & Premium
110             ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Consider: Deep darks, metallics, restrained palette
111             ‚îÇ       ‚Üí ASK about brand positioning
112             ‚îÇ
113             ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Creative & Playful
114             ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Consider: Multi-color, unexpected combinations
115             ‚îÇ       ‚Üí ASK about brand personality
116             ‚îÇ
117             ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Calm & Minimal
118                 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Consider: Neutrals with single accent
119                     ‚Üí ASK what accent color fits brand
120 ```
121 
122 ### The Process:
123 1. Identify the emotion needed
124 2. Narrow to color FAMILY
125 3. ASK user for preference within family
126 4. Generate fresh palette using HSL principles

130 ## 4. Typography Decision Tree
131 
132 ```
133 WHAT'S THE CONTENT TYPE?
134           ‚îÇ
135           ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Data-Heavy (Dashboard, SaaS)
136           ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Style: Sans-serif, clear, compact
137           ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Scale: Tighter ratio (1.125-1.2)
138           ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Priority: Scannability, density
139           ‚îÇ
140           ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Editorial (Blog, Magazine)
141           ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Style: Serif heading + Sans body works well
142           ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Scale: More dramatic (1.333+)
143           ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Priority: Reading comfort, hierarchy
144           ‚îÇ
145           ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Modern Tech (Startup, SaaS Marketing)
146           ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Style: Geometric or humanist sans
147           ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Scale: Balanced (1.25)
148           ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Priority: Modern feel, clarity
149           ‚îÇ
150           ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Luxury (Fashion, Premium)
151           ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Style: Elegant serif or thin sans
152           ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Scale: Dramatic (1.5-1.618)
153           ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Priority: Sophistication, whitespace
154           ‚îÇ
155           ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Playful (Kids, Games, Casual)
156               ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Style: Rounded, friendly fonts
157               ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Scale: Varied, expressive
158               ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Priority: Fun, approachable, readable
159 ```
160 
161 ### Selection Process:
162 1. Identify content type
163 2. Choose style DIRECTION
164 3. ASK user if they have brand fonts
165 4. Select fonts that match direction
166

168 
169 ## 5. E-commerce Guidelines {#e-commerce}
170 
171 ### Key Principles (Not Fixed Rules)
172 - **Trust first:** How will you show security?
173 - **Action-oriented:** Where are the CTAs?
174 - **Scannable:** Can users compare quickly?
175 
176 ### Color Thinking:
177 ```
178 E-commerce typically needs:
179 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Trust color (often blue family) ‚Üí ASK preference
180 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Clean background (white/neutral) ‚Üí depends on brand
181 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Action accent (for CTAs, sales) ‚Üí depends on urgency level
182 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Success/error semantics ‚Üí standard conventions work
183 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Brand integration ‚Üí ASK about existing colors
184 ```
185 
186 ### Layout Principles:
187 ```
188 ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
189 ‚îÇ  HEADER: Brand + Search + Cart                      ‚îÇ
190 ‚îÇ  (Keep essential actions visible)                   ‚îÇ
191 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
192 ‚îÇ  TRUST ZONE: Why trust this site?                   ‚îÇ
193 ‚îÇ  (Shipping, returns, security - if applicable)      ‚îÇ
194 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
195 ‚îÇ  HERO: Primary message or offer                     ‚îÇ
196 ‚îÇ  (Clear CTA, single focus)                          ‚îÇ
197 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
198 ‚îÇ  CATEGORIES: Easy navigation                        ‚îÇ
199 ‚îÇ  (Visual, filterable, scannable)                    ‚îÇ
200 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
201 ‚îÇ  PRODUCTS: Easy comparison                          ‚îÇ
202 ‚îÇ  (Price, rating, quick actions visible)             ‚îÇ
203 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
204 ‚îÇ  SOCIAL PROOF: Why others trust                     ‚îÇ
205 ‚îÇ  (Reviews, testimonials - if available)             ‚îÇ
206 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
207 ‚îÇ  FOOTER: All the details                            ‚îÇ
208 ‚îÇ  (Policies, contact, trust badges)                  ‚îÇ
209 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
210 ```
211 
212 ### Psychology to Apply:
213 - Hick's Law: Limit navigation choices
214 - Fitts' Law: Size CTAs appropriately
215 - Social proof: Show where relevant
216 - Scarcity: Use honestly if at all
217 
218 ---
219 
220 ## 6. SaaS Dashboard Guidelines {#saas}
221 
222 ### Key Principles
223 - **Functional first:** Data clarity over decoration
224 - **Calm UI:** Reduce cognitive load
225 - **Consistent:** Predictable patterns
226 
227 ### Color Thinking:
228 ```
229 Dashboard typically needs:
230 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Background: Light OR dark (ASK preference)
231 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Surface: Slight contrast from background
232 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Primary accent: For key actions
233 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Data colors: Success/warning/danger semantics
234 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Muted: For secondary information
235 ```
236 
237 ### Layout Principles:
238 ```
239 Consider these patterns (not mandated):
240 
241 OPTION A: Sidebar + Content
242 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Fixed sidebar for navigation
243 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Main area for content
244 
245 OPTION B: Top nav + Content
246 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Horizontal navigation
247 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ More horizontal content space
248 
249 OPTION C: Collapsed + Expandable
250 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Icon-only sidebar expands
251 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Maximum content area
252 
253 ‚Üí ASK user about their navigation preference
254 ```
255 
256 ### Psychology to Apply:
257 - Hick's Law: Group navigation items
258 - Miller's Law: Chunk information
259 - Cognitive Load: Whitespace, consistency
260 
261 ---
262 
263 ## 7. Landing Page Guidelines {#landing-page}
264 
265 ### Key Principles
266 - **Hero-centric:** First impression matters most
267 - **Single focus:** One primary CTA
268 - **Emotional:** Connect before selling
269 
270 ### Color Thinking:
271 ```
272 Landing page typically needs:
273 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Brand primary: Hero background or accent
274 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Clean secondary: Most of page
275 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ CTA color: Stands out from everything
276 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Supporting: For sections, testimonials
277 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ ASK about brand colors first!
278 ```
279 
280 ### Structure Principles:
281 ```
282 ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
283 ‚îÇ  Navigation: Minimal, CTA visible                   ‚îÇ
284 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
285 ‚îÇ  HERO: Hook + Value + CTA                          ‚îÇ
286 ‚îÇ  (Most important section, biggest impact)           ‚îÇ
287 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
288 ‚îÇ  PROBLEM: What pain do they have?                   ‚îÇ
289 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
290 ‚îÇ  SOLUTION: How you solve it                         ‚îÇ
291 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
292 ‚îÇ  PROOF: Why believe you?                            ‚îÇ
293 ‚îÇ  (Testimonials, logos, stats)                       ‚îÇ
294 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
295 ‚îÇ  HOW: Simple explanation of process                 ‚îÇ
296 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§

298 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
299 ‚îÇ  FAQ: Address objections                            ‚îÇ
300 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
301 ‚îÇ  FINAL CTA: Repeat main action                      ‚îÇ
302 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
303 ```
304 
305 ### Psychology to Apply:
306 - Visceral: Beautiful hero impression
307 - Serial Position: Key info top/bottom

355 ## 9. Pre-Design Checklists
356 
357 ### Before Starting ANY Design
358 
359 - [ ] **Audience defined?** (who exactly)
360 - [ ] **Primary goal identified?** (what action)
361 - [ ] **Constraints known?** (time, brand, tech)
362 - [ ] **Content available?** (or placeholders needed)
363 - [ ] **User preferences asked?** (colors, style, layout)
364 
365 ### Before Choosing Colors
366 
367 - [ ] **Asked user preference?**
368 - [ ] **Considered context?** (industry, emotion)
369 - [ ] **Different from your default?**
370 - [ ] **Checked accessibility?**
371 
372 ### Before Finalizing Layout
373 
374 - [ ] **Hierarchy clear?**
375 - [ ] **Primary CTA obvious?**
376 - [ ] **Mobile considered?**
377 - [ ] **Content fits structure?**
378 
379 ### Before Delivery
380 
381 - [ ] **Looks premium, not generic?**
382 - [ ] **Would you be proud of this?**
383 - [ ] **Different from last project?**
384

387 ## 10. Complexity Estimation
388 
389 ### Quick Projects (Hours)
390 ```
391 Simple landing page
392 Small portfolio
393 Basic form
394 Single component
395 ```
396 ‚Üí Approach: Minimal decisions, focused execution
397 
398 ### Medium Projects (Days)
399 ```
400 Multi-page site
401 Dashboard with modules
402 E-commerce category
403 Complex forms
404 ```
405 ‚Üí Approach: Establish tokens, custom components
406 
407 ### Large Projects (Weeks)
408 ```
409 Full SaaS application
410 E-commerce platform
411 Custom design system
412 Complex workflows
413 ```
414 ‚Üí Approach: Full design system, documentation, testing

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F80 path:skills/frontend-design/motion-graphics.md hash:0351bd1a0a5ec2759c4cea6874e6a8bc2d2ada557e39b96c9345c6498f9ed96e lines:306 ===
001 # Motion Graphics Reference
002 
003 > Advanced animation techniques for premium web experiences - Lottie, GSAP, SVG, 3D, Particles.
004 > **Learn the principles, create WOW effects.**
005 
006 ---
007 
008 ## 1. Lottie Animations
009 
010 ### What is Lottie?
011 
012 ```
013 JSON-based vector animations:
014 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Exported from After Effects via Bodymovin
015 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Lightweight (smaller than GIF/video)
016 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Scalable (vector-based, no pixelation)
017 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Interactive (control playback, segments)
018 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Cross-platform (web, iOS, Android, React Native)
019 ```
020 
021 ### When to Use Lottie
022 
023 | Use Case | Why Lottie? |
024 |----------|-------------|
025 | **Loading animations** | Branded, smooth, lightweight |
026 | **Empty states** | Engaging illustrations |
027 | **Onboarding flows** | Complex multi-step animations |
028 | **Success/Error feedback** | Delightful micro-interactions |
029 | **Animated icons** | Consistent cross-platform |
030 
031 ### Principles
032 
033 - Keep file size under 100KB for performance
034 - Use loop sparingly (avoid distraction)
035 - Provide static fallback for reduced-motion
036 - Lazy load animation files when possible
037 
038 ### Sources
039 
040 - LottieFiles.com (free library)
041 - After Effects + Bodymovin (custom)
042 - Figma plugins (export from design)
043 
044 ---
045 
046 ## 2. GSAP (GreenSock)
047 
048 ### What Makes GSAP Different
049 
050 ```
051 Professional timeline-based animation:
052 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Precise control over sequences
053 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ ScrollTrigger for scroll-driven animations
054 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ MorphSVG for shape transitions
055 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Physics-based easing
056 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Works with any DOM element
057 ```
058 
059 ### Core Concepts
060 
061 | Concept | Purpose |
062 |---------|---------|
063 | **Tween** | Single A‚ÜíB animation |
064 | **Timeline** | Sequenced/overlapping animations |
065 | **ScrollTrigger** | Scroll position controls playback |
066 | **Stagger** | Cascade effect across elements |
067 
068 ### When to Use GSAP
069 
070 - ‚úÖ Complex sequenced animations
071 - ‚úÖ Scroll-triggered reveals
072 - ‚úÖ Precise timing control needed
073 - ‚úÖ SVG morphing effects
074 - ‚ùå Simple hover/focus effects (use CSS)
075 - ‚ùå Performance-critical mobile (heavier)
076 
077 ### Principles
078 
079 - Use timeline for orchestration (not individual tweens)
080 - Stagger delay: 0.05-0.15s between items
081 - ScrollTrigger: start at 70-80% viewport entry
082 - Kill animations on unmount (prevent memory leaks)
083 
084 ---
085 
086 ## 3. SVG Animations
087 
088 ### Types of SVG Animation
089 
090 | Type | Technique | Use Case |
091 |------|-----------|----------|
092 | **Line Drawing** | stroke-dashoffset | Logo reveals, signatures |
093 | **Morph** | Path interpolation | Icon transitions |
094 | **Transform** | rotate, scale, translate | Interactive icons |
095 | **Color** | fill/stroke transition | State changes |
096 
097 ### Line Drawing Principles
098 
099 ```
100 How stroke-dashoffset drawing works:
101 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Set dasharray to path length
102 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Set dashoffset equal to dasharray (hidden)
103 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Animate dashoffset to 0 (revealed)
104 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Create "drawing" effect
105 ```
106 
107 ### When to Use SVG Animations
108 
109 - ‚úÖ Logo reveals, brand moments
110 - ‚úÖ Icon state transitions (hamburger ‚Üî X)
111 - ‚úÖ Infographics, data visualization
112 - ‚úÖ Interactive illustrations
113 - ‚ùå Photo-realistic content (use video)
114 - ‚ùå Very complex scenes (performance)
115 
116 ### Principles
117 
118 - Get path length dynamically for accuracy
119 - Duration: 1-3s for full drawings
120 - Easing: ease-out for natural feel
121 - Simple fills complement, don't compete
122 
123 ---
124 
125 ## 4. 3D CSS Transforms
126 
127 ### Core Properties
128 
129 ```
130 CSS 3D Space:
131 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ perspective: depth of 3D field (500-1500px typical)
132 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ transform-style: preserve-3d (enable children 3D)
133 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ rotateX/Y/Z: rotation per axis
134 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ translateZ: move toward/away from viewer
135 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ backface-visibility: show/hide back side
136 ```
137 
138 ### Common 3D Patterns
139 
140 | Pattern | Use Case |
141 |---------|----------|
142 | **Card flip** | Reveals, flashcards, product views |
143 | **Tilt on hover** | Interactive cards, 3D depth |
144 | **Parallax layers** | Hero sections, immersive scrolling |
145 | **3D carousel** | Image galleries, sliders |
146 
147 ### Principles
148 
149 - Perspective: 800-1200px for subtle, 400-600px for dramatic
150 - Keep transforms simple (rotate + translate)
151 - Ensure backface-visibility: hidden for flips
152 - Test on Safari (different rendering)
153 
154 ---
155 
156 ## 5. Particle Effects
157 
158 ### Types of Particle Systems
159 
160 | Type | Feel | Use Case |
161 |------|------|----------|
162 | **Geometric** | Tech, network | SaaS, tech sites |
163 | **Confetti** | Celebration | Success moments |
164 | **Snow/Rain** | Atmospheric | Seasonal, mood |
165 | **Dust/Bokeh** | Dreamy | Photography, luxury |
166 | **Fireflies** | Magical | Games, fantasy |
167 
168 ### Libraries
169 
170 | Library | Best For |
171 |---------|----------|
172 | **tsParticles** | Configurable, lightweight |
173 | **particles.js** | Simple backgrounds |
174 | **Canvas API** | Custom, maximum control |
175 | **Three.js** | Complex 3D particles |
176 
177 ### Principles
178 
179 - Default: 30-50 particles (not overwhelming)
180 - Movement: slow, organic (speed 0.5-2)
181 - Opacity: 0.3-0.6 (don't compete with content)
182 - Connections: subtle lines for "network" feel
183 - ‚ö†Ô∏è Disable or reduce on mobile
184 
185 ### When to Use
186 
187 - ‚úÖ Hero backgrounds (atmospheric)
188 - ‚úÖ Success celebrations (confetti burst)
189 - ‚úÖ Tech visualization (connected nodes)
190 - ‚ùå Content-heavy pages (distraction)
191 - ‚ùå Low-powered devices (battery drain)
192 
193 ---
194 
195 ## 6. Scroll-Driven Animations
196 
197 ### Native CSS (Modern)
198 
199 ```
200 CSS Scroll Timelines:
201 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ animation-timeline: scroll() - document scroll
202 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ animation-timeline: view() - element in viewport
203 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ animation-range: entry/exit thresholds
204 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ No JavaScript required
205 ```
206 
207 ### Principles
208 
209 | Trigger Point | Use Case |
210 |---------------|----------|
211 | **Entry 0%** | When element starts entering |
212 | **Entry 50%** | When half visible |
213 | **Cover 50%** | When centered in viewport |
214 | **Exit 100%** | When fully exited |
215 
216 ### Best Practices
217 
218 - Reveal animations: start at ~25% entry
219 - Parallax: continuous scroll progress
220 - Sticky elements: use cover range
221 - Always test scroll performance
222 
223 ---
224 
225 ## 7. Performance Principles
226 
227 ### GPU vs CPU Animation
228 
229 ```
230 CHEAP (GPU-accelerated):
231 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ transform (translate, scale, rotate)
232 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ opacity
233 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ filter (use sparingly)
234 
235 EXPENSIVE (triggers reflow):
236 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ width, height
237 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ top, left, right, bottom
238 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ padding, margin
239 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ complex box-shadow
240 ```
241 
242 ### Optimization Checklist
243 
244 - [ ] Animate only transform/opacity
245 - [ ] Use `will-change` before heavy animations (remove after)
246 - [ ] Test on low-end devices
247 - [ ] Implement `prefers-reduced-motion`
248 - [ ] Lazy load animation libraries
249 - [ ] Throttle scroll-based calculations
250 
251 ---
252 
253 ## 8. Motion Graphics Decision Tree
254 
255 ```
256 What animation do you need?
257 ‚îÇ
258 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Complex branded animation?
259 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Lottie (After Effects export)
260 ‚îÇ
261 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Sequenced scroll-triggered?
262 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ GSAP + ScrollTrigger
263 ‚îÇ
264 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Logo/icon animation?
265 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ SVG animation (stroke or morph)
266 ‚îÇ
267 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Interactive 3D effect?
268 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ CSS 3D Transforms (simple) or Three.js (complex)
269 ‚îÇ
270 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Atmospheric background?
271 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ tsParticles or Canvas
272 ‚îÇ
273 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Simple entrance/hover?
274     ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ CSS @keyframes or Framer Motion
275 ```
276 
277 ---
278 
279 ## 9. Anti-Patterns
280 
281 | ‚ùå Don't | ‚úÖ Do |
282 |----------|-------|
283 | Animate everything at once | Stagger and sequence |
284 | Use heavy libraries for simple effects | Start with CSS |
285 | Ignore reduced-motion | Always provide fallback |
286 | Block main thread | Optimize for 60fps |
287 | Same particles every project | Match brand/context |
288 | Complex effects on mobile | Feature detection |
289 
290 ---
291 
292 ## 10. Quick Reference
293 
294 | Effect | Tool | Performance |
295 |--------|------|-------------|
296 | Loading spinner | CSS/Lottie | Light |
297 | Staggered reveal | GSAP/Framer | Medium |
298 | SVG path draw | CSS stroke | Light |
299 | 3D card flip | CSS transforms | Light |
300 | Particle background | tsParticles | Heavy |
301 | Scroll parallax | GSAP ScrollTrigger | Medium |
302 | Shape morphing | GSAP MorphSVG | Medium |
303 
304 ---
305 
306 > **Remember**: Motion graphics should enhance, not distract. Every animation must serve a PURPOSE‚Äîfeedback, guidance, delight, or storytelling.

007 # Frontend Design System
008 
009 > **Philosophy:** Every pixel has purpose. Restraint is luxury. User psychology drives decisions.
010 > **Core Principle:** THINK, don't memorize. ASK, don't assume.

042 ## ‚ö†Ô∏è CRITICAL: ASK BEFORE ASSUMING (MANDATORY)
043 
044 > **STOP! If the user's request is open-ended, DO NOT default to your favorites.**
045 
046 ### When User Prompt is Vague, ASK:
047 
048 **Color not specified?** Ask:
049 > "What color palette do you prefer? (blue/green/orange/neutral/other?)"
050 
051 **Style not specified?** Ask:
052 > "What style are you going for? (minimal/bold/retro/futuristic/organic?)"
053 
054 **Layout not specified?** Ask:
055 > "Do you have a layout preference? (single column/grid/asymmetric/full-width?)"
056 
057 ### ‚õî DEFAULT TENDENCIES TO AVOID (ANTI-SAFE HARBOR):
058 
059 | AI Default Tendency | Why It's Bad | Think Instead |
060 |---------------------|--------------|---------------|
061 | **Bento Grids (Modern Clich√©)** | Used in every AI design | Why does this content NEED a grid? |
062 | **Hero Split (Left/Right)** | Predictable & Boring | How about Massive Typography or Vertical Narrative? |
063 | **Mesh/Aurora Gradients** | The "new" lazy background | What's a radical color pairing? |
064 | **Glassmorphism** | AI's idea of "premium" | How about solid, high-contrast flat? |
065 | **Deep Cyan / Fintech Blue** | Safe harbor from purple ban | Why not Red, Black, or Neon Green? |
066 | **"Orchestrate / Empower"** | AI-generated copywriting | How would a human say this? |
067 | Dark background + neon glow | Overused, "AI look" | What does the BRAND actually need? |
068 | **Rounded everything** | Generic/Safe | Where can I use sharp, brutalist edges? |
069 
070 > üî¥ **"Every 'safe' structure you choose brings you one step closer to a generic template. TAKE RISKS."**
071

073 
074 ## 1. Constraint Analysis (ALWAYS FIRST)
075 
076 Before any design work, ANSWER THESE or ASK USER:
077 
078 | Constraint | Question | Why It Matters |
079 |------------|----------|----------------|
080 | **Timeline** | How much time? | Determines complexity |
081 | **Content** | Ready or placeholder? | Affects layout flexibility |
082 | **Brand** | Existing guidelines? | May dictate colors/fonts |
083 | **Tech** | What stack? | Affects capabilities |
084 | **Audience** | Who exactly? | Drives all visual decisions |
085 
086 ### Audience ‚Üí Design Approach
087 
088 | Audience | Think About |
089 |----------|-------------|
090 | **Gen Z** | Bold, fast, mobile-first, authentic |
091 | **Millennials** | Clean, minimal, value-driven |
092 | **Gen X** | Familiar, trustworthy, clear |
093 | **Boomers** | Readable, high contrast, simple |
094 | **B2B** | Professional, data-focused, trust |
095 | **Luxury** | Restrained elegance, whitespace |
096 
097 ---
098 
099 ## 2. UX Psychology Principles
100 
101 ### Core Laws (Internalize These)
102 
103 | Law | Principle | Application |
104 |-----|-----------|-------------|
105 | **Hick's Law** | More choices = slower decisions | Limit options, use progressive disclosure |
106 | **Fitts' Law** | Bigger + closer = easier to click | Size CTAs appropriately |
107 | **Miller's Law** | ~7 items in working memory | Chunk content into groups |
108 | **Von Restorff** | Different = memorable | Make CTAs visually distinct |
109 | **Serial Position** | First/last remembered most | Key info at start/end |
110 
111 ### Emotional Design Levels
112 
113 ```
114 VISCERAL (instant)  ‚Üí First impression: colors, imagery, overall feel
115 BEHAVIORAL (use)    ‚Üí Using it: speed, feedback, efficiency
116 REFLECTIVE (memory) ‚Üí After: "I like what this says about me"
117 ```
118 
119 ### Trust Building
120 
121 - Security indicators on sensitive actions
122 - Social proof where relevant
123 - Clear contact/support access
124 - Consistent, professional design
125 - Transparent policies
126 
127 ---
128 
129 ## 3. Layout Principles
130 
131 ### Golden Ratio (œÜ = 1.618)
132 
133 ```
134 Use for proportional harmony:
135 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Content : Sidebar = roughly 62% : 38%
136 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Each heading size = previous √ó 1.618 (for dramatic scale)
137 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Spacing can follow: sm ‚Üí md ‚Üí lg (each √ó 1.618)
138 ```
139 
140 ### 8-Point Grid Concept
141 
142 ```
143 All spacing and sizing in multiples of 8:
144 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Tight: 4px (half-step for micro)
145 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Small: 8px
146 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Medium: 16px
147 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Large: 24px, 32px
148 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ XL: 48px, 64px, 80px
149 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Adjust based on content density
150 ```
151 
152 ### Key Sizing Principles
153 
154 | Element | Consideration |
155 |---------|---------------|
156 | **Touch targets** | Minimum comfortable tap size |
157 | **Buttons** | Height based on importance hierarchy |
158 | **Inputs** | Match button height for alignment |
159 | **Cards** | Consistent padding, breathable |
160 | **Reading width** | 45-75 characters optimal |
161 
162 ---
163 
164 ## 4. Color Principles
165 
166 ### 60-30-10 Rule
167 
168 ```
169 60% ‚Üí Primary/Background (calm, neutral base)
170 30% ‚Üí Secondary (supporting areas)
171 10% ‚Üí Accent (CTAs, highlights, attention)
172 ```
173 
174 ### Color Psychology (For Decision Making)
175 
176 | If You Need... | Consider Hues | Avoid |
177 |----------------|---------------|-------|
178 | Trust, calm | Blue family | Aggressive reds |
179 | Growth, nature | Green family | Industrial grays |
180 | Energy, urgency | Orange, red | Passive blues |
181 | Luxury, creativity | Deep Teal, Gold, Emerald | Cheap-feeling brights |
182 | Clean, minimal | Neutrals | Overwhelming color |
183 
184 ### Selection Process
185 
186 1. **What's the industry?** (narrows options)
187 2. **What's the emotion?** (picks primary)
188 3. **Light or dark mode?** (sets foundation)
189 4. **ASK USER** if not specified
190 
191 For detailed color theory: [color-system.md](color-system.md)
192 
193 ---
194 
195 ## 5. Typography Principles
196 
197 ### Scale Selection
198 
199 | Content Type | Scale Ratio | Feel |
200 |--------------|-------------|------|
201 | Dense UI | 1.125-1.2 | Compact, efficient |
202 | General web | 1.25 | Balanced (most common) |
203 | Editorial | 1.333 | Readable, spacious |
204 | Hero/display | 1.5-1.618 | Dramatic impact |
205 
206 ### Pairing Concept
207 
208 ```
209 Contrast + Harmony:
210 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ DIFFERENT enough for hierarchy
211 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ SIMILAR enough for cohesion
212 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Usually: display + neutral, or serif + sans
213 ```
214 
215 ### Readability Rules
216 
217 - **Line length**: 45-75 characters optimal
218 - **Line height**: 1.4-1.6 for body text
219 - **Contrast**: Check WCAG requirements
220 - **Size**: 16px+ for body on web
221 
222 For detailed typography: [typography-system.md](typography-system.md)
223 
224 ---
225 
226 ## 6. Visual Effects Principles
227 
228 ### Glassmorphism (When Appropriate)
229 
230 ```
231 Key properties:
232 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Semi-transparent background
233 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Backdrop blur
234 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Subtle border for definition
235 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ ‚ö†Ô∏è **WARNING:** Standard blue/white glassmorphism is a modern clich√©. Use it radically or not at all.
236 ```
237 
238 ### Shadow Hierarchy
239 
240 ```
241 Elevation concept:
242 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Higher elements = larger shadows
243 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Y-offset > X-offset (light from above)
244 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Multiple layers = more realistic
245 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Dark mode: may need glow instead
246 ```
247 
248 ### Gradient Usage
249 
250 ```
251 Harmonious gradients:
252 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Adjacent colors on wheel (analogous)
253 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ OR same hue, different lightness
254 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Avoid harsh complementary pairs
255 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ üö´ **NO Mesh/Aurora Gradients** (floating blobs)
256 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ VARY from project to project radically
257 ```
258 
259 For complete effects guide: [visual-effects.md](visual-effects.md)
260

262 
263 ## 7. Animation Principles
264 
265 ### Timing Concept
266 
267 ```
268 Duration based on:
269 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Distance (further = longer)
270 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Size (larger = slower)
271 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Importance (critical = clear)
272 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Context (urgent = fast, luxury = slow)
273 ```
274 
275 ### Easing Selection
276 
277 | Action | Easing | Why |
278 |--------|--------|-----|
279 | Entering | Ease-out | Decelerate, settle in |
280 | Leaving | Ease-in | Accelerate, exit |
281 | Emphasis | Ease-in-out | Smooth, deliberate |
282 | Playful | Bounce | Fun, energetic |
283 
284 ### Performance
285 
286 - Animate only transform and opacity
287 - Respect reduced-motion preference
288 - Test on low-end devices
289 
290 For animation patterns: [animation-guide.md](animation-guide.md), for advanced: [motion-graphics.md](motion-graphics.md)
291

294 ## 8. "Wow Factor" Checklist
295 
296 ### Premium Indicators
297 
298 - [ ] Generous whitespace (luxury = breathing room)
299 - [ ] Subtle depth and dimension
300 - [ ] Smooth, purposeful animations
301 - [ ] Attention to detail (alignment, consistency)
302 - [ ] Cohesive visual rhythm
303 - [ ] Custom elements (not all defaults)
304 
305 ### Trust Builders
306 
307 - [ ] Security cues where appropriate
308 - [ ] Social proof / testimonials
309 - [ ] Clear value proposition
310 - [ ] Professional imagery
311 - [ ] Consistent design language
312 
313 ### Emotional Triggers
314 
315 - [ ] Hero that evokes intended emotion
316 - [ ] Human elements (faces, stories)
317 - [ ] Progress/achievement indicators
318 - [ ] Moments of delight

322 ## 9. Anti-Patterns (What NOT to Do)
323 
324 ### ‚ùå Lazy Design Indicators
325 
326 - Default system fonts without consideration
327 - Stock imagery that doesn't match
328 - Inconsistent spacing
329 - Too many competing colors
330 - Walls of text without hierarchy
331 - Inaccessible contrast
332 
333 ### ‚ùå AI Tendency Patterns (AVOID!)
334 
335 - **Same colors every project**
336 - **Dark + neon as default**
337 - **Purple/violet everything (PURPLE BAN ‚úÖ)**
338 - **Bento grids for simple landing pages**
339 - **Mesh Gradients & Glow Effects**
340 - **Same layout structure / Vercel clone**
341 - **Not asking user preferences**
342 
343 ### ‚ùå Dark Patterns (Unethical)
344 
345 - Hidden costs
346 - Fake urgency
347 - Forced actions
348 - Deceptive UI
349 - Confirmshaming
350

353 ## 10. Decision Process Summary
354 
355 ```
356 For EVERY design task:
357 
358 1. CONSTRAINTS
359    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ What's the timeline, brand, tech, audience?
360    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ If unclear ‚Üí ASK
361 
362 2. CONTENT
363    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ What content exists?
364    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ What's the hierarchy?
365 
366 3. STYLE DIRECTION
367    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ What's appropriate for context?
368    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ If unclear ‚Üí ASK (don't default!)
369 
370 4. EXECUTION
371    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Apply principles above
372    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Check against anti-patterns
373 
374 5. REVIEW
375    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ "Does this serve the user?"
376    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ "Is this different from my defaults?"
377    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ "Would I be proud of this?"
378 ```
