=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F82 path:skills/frontend-design/typography-system.md hash:79c82e26c31d28087c8528ba280ad7810e85d101ae2661abd2f94dd3277a648a lines:345 ===
001 # Typography System Reference
002 
003 > Typography principles and decision-making - learn to think, not memorize.
004 > **No fixed font names or sizes - understand the system.**
005 
006 ---
007 
008 ## 1. Modular Scale Principles
009 
010 ### What is a Modular Scale?
011 
012 ```
013 A mathematical relationship between font sizes:
014 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Pick a BASE size (usually body text)
015 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Pick a RATIO (multiplier)
016 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Generate all sizes using: base √ó ratio^n
017 ```
018 
019 ### Common Ratios and When to Use
020 
021 | Ratio | Value | Feeling | Best For |
022 |-------|-------|---------|----------|
023 | Minor Second | 1.067 | Very subtle | Dense UI, small screens |
024 | Major Second | 1.125 | Subtle | Compact interfaces |
025 | Minor Third | 1.2 | Comfortable | Mobile apps, cards |
026 | Major Third | 1.25 | Balanced | General web (most common) |
027 | Perfect Fourth | 1.333 | Noticeable | Editorial, blogs |
028 | Perfect Fifth | 1.5 | Dramatic | Headlines, marketing |
029 | Golden Ratio | 1.618 | Maximum impact | Hero sections, display |
030 
031 ### Generate Your Scale
032 
033 ```
034 Given: base = YOUR_BASE_SIZE, ratio = YOUR_RATIO
035 
036 Scale:
037 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ xs:  base √∑ ratio¬≤
038 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ sm:  base √∑ ratio
039 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ base: YOUR_BASE_SIZE
040 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ lg:  base √ó ratio
041 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ xl:  base √ó ratio¬≤
042 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ 2xl: base √ó ratio¬≥
043 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ 3xl: base √ó ratio‚Å¥
044 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ ... continue as needed
045 ```
046 
047 ### Choosing Base Size
048 
049 | Context | Base Size Range | Why |
050 |---------|-----------------|-----|
051 | Mobile-first | 16-18px | Readability on small screens |
052 | Desktop app | 14-16px | Information density |
053 | Editorial | 18-21px | Long-form reading comfort |
054 | Accessibility focus | 18px+ | Easier to read |
055 
056 ---
057 
058 ## 2. Font Pairing Principles
059 
060 ### What Makes Fonts Work Together
061 
062 ```
063 Contrast + Harmony:
064 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Different ENOUGH to create hierarchy
065 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Similar ENOUGH to feel cohesive
066 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Usually: serif + sans, or display + neutral
067 ```
068 
069 ### Pairing Strategies
070 
071 | Strategy | How | Result |
072 |----------|-----|--------|
073 | **Contrast** | Serif heading + Sans body | Classic, editorial feel |
074 | **Same Family** | One variable font, different weights | Cohesive, modern |
075 | **Same Designer** | Fonts by same foundry | Often harmonious proportions |
076 | **Era Match** | Fonts from same time period | Historical consistency |
077 
078 ### What to Look For
079 
080 ```
081 When pairing, compare:
082 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ x-height (height of lowercase letters)
083 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Letter width (narrow vs wide)
084 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Stroke contrast (thin/thick variation)
085 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Overall mood (formal vs casual)
086 ```
087 
088 ### Safe Pairing Patterns
089 
090 | Heading Style | Body Style | Mood |
091 |---------------|------------|------|
092 | Geometric sans | Humanist sans | Modern, friendly |
093 | Display serif | Clean sans | Editorial, sophisticated |
094 | Neutral sans | Same sans | Minimal, tech |
095 | Bold geometric | Light geometric | Contemporary |
096 
097 ### Avoid
098 
099 - ‚ùå Two decorative fonts together
100 - ‚ùå Similar fonts that conflict
101 - ‚ùå More than 2-3 font families
102 - ‚ùå Fonts with very different x-heights
103 
104 ---
105 
106 ## 3. Line Height Principles
107 
108 ### The Relationship
109 
110 ```
111 Line height depends on:
112 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Font size (larger text = less line height needed)
113 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Line length (longer lines = more line height)
114 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Font design (some fonts need more space)
115 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Content type (headings vs body)
116 ```
117 
118 ### Guidelines by Context
119 
120 | Content Type | Line Height Range | Why |
121 |--------------|-------------------|-----|
122 | **Headings** | 1.1 - 1.3 | Short lines, want compact |
123 | **Body text** | 1.4 - 1.6 | Comfortable reading |
124 | **Long-form** | 1.6 - 1.8 | Maximum readability |
125 | **UI elements** | 1.2 - 1.4 | Space efficiency |
126 
127 ### Adjustment Factors
128 
129 - **Longer line length** ‚Üí Increase line height
130 - **Larger font size** ‚Üí Decrease line height ratio
131 - **All caps** ‚Üí May need more line height
132 - **Tight tracking** ‚Üí May need more line height
133 
134 ---
135 
136 ## 4. Line Length Principles
137 
138 ### Optimal Reading Width
139 
140 ```
141 The sweet spot: 45-75 characters per line
142 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ < 45: Too choppy, breaks flow
143 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ 45-75: Comfortable reading
144 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ > 75: Eye tracking strain
145 ```
146 
147 ### How to Measure
148 
149 ```css
150 /* Character-based (recommended) */
151 max-width: 65ch; /* ch = width of "0" character */
152 
153 /* This adapts to font size automatically */
154 ```
155 
156 ### Context Adjustments
157 
158 | Context | Character Range |
159 |---------|-----------------|
160 | Desktop article | 60-75 characters |
161 | Mobile | 35-50 characters |
162 | Sidebar text | 30-45 characters |
163 | Wide monitors | Still cap at ~75ch |
164 
165 ---
166 
167 ## 5. Responsive Typography Principles
168 
169 ### The Problem
170 
171 ```
172 Fixed sizes don't scale well:
173 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Desktop size too big on mobile
174 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Mobile size too small on desktop
175 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Breakpoint jumps feel jarring
176 ```
177 
178 ### Fluid Typography (clamp)
179 
180 ```css
181 /* Syntax: clamp(MIN, PREFERRED, MAX) */
182 font-size: clamp(
183   MINIMUM_SIZE,
184   FLUID_CALCULATION,
185   MAXIMUM_SIZE
186 );
187 
188 /* FLUID_CALCULATION typically:
189    base + viewport-relative-unit */
190 ```
191 
192 ### Scaling Strategy
193 
194 | Element | Scaling Behavior |
195 |---------|-----------------|
196 | Body text | Slight scaling (1rem ‚Üí 1.125rem) |
197 | Subheadings | Moderate scaling |
198 | Headings | More dramatic scaling |
199 | Display text | Most dramatic scaling |
200 
201 ---
202 
203 ## 6. Weight and Emphasis Principles
204 
205 ### Semantic Weight Usage
206 
207 | Weight Range | Name | Use For |
208 |--------------|------|---------|
209 | 300-400 | Light/Normal | Body text, paragraphs |
210 | 500 | Medium | Subtle emphasis |
211 | 600 | Semibold | Subheadings, labels |
212 | 700 | Bold | Headings, strong emphasis |
213 | 800-900 | Heavy/Black | Display, hero text |
214 
215 ### Creating Contrast
216 
217 ```
218 Good contrast = skip at least 2 weight levels
219 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ 400 body + 700 heading = good
220 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ 400 body + 500 emphasis = subtle
221 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ 600 heading + 700 subheading = too similar
222 ```
223 
224 ### Avoid
225 
226 - ‚ùå Too many weights (max 3-4 per page)
227 - ‚ùå Adjacent weights for hierarchy (400/500)
228 - ‚ùå Heavy weights for long text
229 
230 ---
231 
232 ## 7. Letter Spacing (Tracking)
233 
234 ### Principles
235 
236 ```
237 Large text (headings): tighter tracking
238 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Letters are big, gaps feel larger
239 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Slight negative tracking looks better
240 
241 Small text (body): normal or slightly wider
242 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Improves readability at small sizes
243 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Never negative for body text
244 
245 ALL CAPS: always wider tracking
246 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Uppercase lacks ascenders/descenders
247 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Needs more space to feel right
248 ```
249 
250 ### Adjustment Guidelines
251 
252 | Context | Tracking Adjustment |
253 |---------|---------------------|
254 | Display/Hero | -2% to -4% |
255 | Headings | -1% to -2% |
256 | Body text | 0% (normal) |
257 | Small text | +1% to +2% |
258 | ALL CAPS | +5% to +10% |
259 
260 ---
261 
262 ## 8. Hierarchy Principles
263 
264 ### Visual Hierarchy Through Type
265 
266 ```
267 Ways to create hierarchy:
268 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ SIZE (most obvious)
269 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ WEIGHT (bold stands out)
270 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ COLOR (contrast levels)
271 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ SPACING (margins separate sections)
272 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ POSITION (top = important)
273 ```
274 
275 ### Typical Hierarchy
276 
277 | Level | Characteristics |
278 |-------|-----------------|
279 | Primary (H1) | Largest, boldest, most distinct |
280 | Secondary (H2) | Noticeably smaller but still bold |
281 | Tertiary (H3) | Medium size, may use weight only |
282 | Body | Standard size and weight |
283 | Caption/Meta | Smaller, often lighter color |
284 
285 ### Testing Hierarchy
286 
287 Ask: "Can I tell what's most important at a glance?"
288 
289 If squinting at the page, the hierarchy should still be clear.
290 
291 ---
292 
293 ## 9. Readability Psychology
294 
295 ### F-Pattern Reading
296 
297 ```
298 Users scan in F-pattern:
299 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Across the top (first line)
300 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Down the left side
301 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Across again (subheading)
302 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Continue down left
303 ```
304 
305 **Implication**: Key info on left and in headings
306 
307 ### Chunking for Comprehension
308 
309 - Short paragraphs (3-4 lines max)
310 - Clear subheadings
311 - Bullet points for lists
312 - White space between sections
313 
314 ### Cognitive Ease
315 
316 - Familiar fonts = easier reading
317 - High contrast = less strain
318 - Consistent patterns = predictable
319 
320 ---
321 
322 ## 10. Typography Selection Checklist
323 
324 Before finalizing typography:
325 
326 - [ ] **Asked user for font preferences?**
327 - [ ] **Considered brand/context?**
328 - [ ] **Selected appropriate scale ratio?**
329 - [ ] **Limited to 2-3 font families?**
330 - [ ] **Tested readability at all sizes?**
331 - [ ] **Checked line length (45-75ch)?**
332 - [ ] **Verified contrast for accessibility?**
333 - [ ] **Different from your last project?**
334 
335 ### Anti-Patterns
336 
337 - ‚ùå Same fonts every project
338 - ‚ùå Too many font families
339 - ‚ùå Ignoring readability for style
340 - ‚ùå Fixed sizes without responsiveness
341 - ‚ùå Decorative fonts for body text
342 
343 ---
344 
345 > **Remember**: Typography is about communication clarity. Choose based on content needs and audience, not personal preference.
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F82 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F83 path:skills/frontend-design/ux-psychology.md hash:92523c787e4abd1991d954f3b376682a091957ce19ba931c4b18faf75234f153 lines:541 ===
001 # UX Psychology Reference
002 
003 > Deep dive into UX laws, emotional design, trust building, and behavioral psychology.
004 
005 ---
006 
007 ## 1. Core UX Laws
008 
009 ### Hick's Law
010 
011 **Principle:** The time to make a decision increases logarithmically with the number of choices.
012 
013 ```
014 Decision Time = a + b √ó log‚ÇÇ(n + 1)
015 Where n = number of choices
016 ```
017 
018 **Application:**
019 - Navigation: Max 5-7 top-level items
020 - Forms: Break into steps (progressive disclosure)
021 - Options: Default selections when possible
022 - Filters: Prioritize most-used, hide advanced
023 
024 **Example:**
025 ```
026 ‚ùå Bad: 15 menu items in one nav
027 ‚úÖ Good: 5 main categories + "More"
028 
029 ‚ùå Bad: 20 form fields at once
030 ‚úÖ Good: 3-step wizard with 5-7 fields each
031 ```
032 
033 ---
034 
035 ### Fitts' Law
036 
037 **Principle:** Time to reach a target = function of distance and size.
038 
039 ```
040 MT = a + b √ó log‚ÇÇ(1 + D/W)
041 Where D = distance, W = width
042 ```
043 
044 **Application:**
045 - CTAs: Make primary buttons larger (min 44px height)
046 - Touch targets: 44√ó44px minimum on mobile
047 - Placement: Important actions near natural cursor position
048 - Corners: "Magic corners" (infinite edge = easy to hit)
049 
050 **Button Sizing:**
051 ```css
052 /* Size by importance */
053 .btn-primary { height: 48px; padding: 0 24px; }
054 .btn-secondary { height: 40px; padding: 0 16px; }
055 .btn-tertiary { height: 36px; padding: 0 12px; }
056 
057 /* Mobile touch targets */
058 @media (hover: none) {
059   .btn { min-height: 44px; min-width: 44px; }
060 }
061 ```
062 
063 ---
064 
065 ### Miller's Law
066 
067 **Principle:** Average person can hold 7¬±2 chunks in working memory.
068 
069 **Application:**
070 - Lists: Group into chunks of 5-7 items
071 - Navigation: Max 7 menu items
072 - Content: Break long content with headings
073 - Phone numbers: 555-123-4567 (chunked)
074 
075 **Chunking Example:**
076 ```
077 ‚ùå 5551234567
078 ‚úÖ 555-123-4567
079 
080 ‚ùå Long paragraph of text without breaks
081 ‚úÖ Short paragraphs
082    With bullet points
083    And subheadings
084 ```
085 
086 ---
087 
088 ### Von Restorff Effect (Isolation Effect)
089 
090 **Principle:** An item that stands out is more likely to be remembered.
091 
092 **Application:**
093 - CTA buttons: Distinct color from other elements
094 - Pricing: Highlight recommended plan
095 - Important info: Visual differentiation
096 - New features: Badge or callout
097 
098 **Example:**
099 ```css
100 /* All buttons gray, primary stands out */
101 .btn { background: #E5E7EB; }
102 .btn-primary { background: #3B82F6; }
103 
104 /* Recommended plan highlighted */
105 .pricing-card { border: 1px solid #E5E7EB; }
106 .pricing-card.popular {
107   border: 2px solid #3B82F6;
108   box-shadow: var(--shadow-lg);
109 }
110 ```
111 
112 ---
113 
114 ### Serial Position Effect
115 
116 **Principle:** Items at the beginning (primacy) and end (recency) of a list are remembered best.
117 
118 **Application:**
119 - Navigation: Most important items first and last
120 - Lists: Key info at top and bottom
121 - Forms: Most critical fields at start
122 - CTAs: Repeat at top and bottom of long pages
123 
124 **Example:**
125 ```
126 Navigation: Home | [key items] | Contact
127 
128 Long landing page:
129 - CTA at hero (top)
130 - Content sections
131 - CTA repeated at bottom
132 ```
133 
134 ---
135 
136 ## 2. Emotional Design (Don Norman)
137 
138 ### Three Levels of Processing
139 
140 ```
141 ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
142 ‚îÇ  VISCERAL (Lizard Brain)                                    ‚îÇ
143 ‚îÇ  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ                                      ‚îÇ
144 ‚îÇ  ‚Ä¢ Immediate, automatic reaction                            ‚îÇ
145 ‚îÇ  ‚Ä¢ First impressions (first 50ms)                          ‚îÇ
146 ‚îÇ  ‚Ä¢ Aesthetics: colors, shapes, imagery                      ‚îÇ
147 ‚îÇ  ‚Ä¢ "Wow, this looks beautiful!"                            ‚îÇ
148 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
149 ‚îÇ  BEHAVIORAL (Functional Brain)                              ‚îÇ
150 ‚îÇ  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ                              ‚îÇ
151 ‚îÇ  ‚Ä¢ Usability and function                                   ‚îÇ
152 ‚îÇ  ‚Ä¢ Pleasure from effective use                              ‚îÇ
153 ‚îÇ  ‚Ä¢ Performance, reliability, ease                           ‚îÇ
154 ‚îÇ  ‚Ä¢ "This works exactly how I expected!"                    ‚îÇ
155 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
156 ‚îÇ  REFLECTIVE (Conscious Brain)                               ‚îÇ
157 ‚îÇ  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ                              ‚îÇ
158 ‚îÇ  ‚Ä¢ Conscious thought and meaning                            ‚îÇ
159 ‚îÇ  ‚Ä¢ Personal identity and values                             ‚îÇ
160 ‚îÇ  ‚Ä¢ Long-term memory and loyalty                             ‚îÇ
161 ‚îÇ  ‚Ä¢ "This brand represents who I am"                        ‚îÇ
162 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
163 ```
164 
165 ### Designing for Each Level
166 
167 **Visceral:**
168 ```css
169 /* Beautiful first impression */
170 .hero {
171   background: linear-gradient(135deg, #0ea5e9 0%, #14b8a6 100%);
172   color: white;
173 }
174 
175 /* Pleasing microinteractions */
176 .button:hover {
177   transform: translateY(-2px);
178   box-shadow: var(--shadow-lg);
179 }
180 ```
181 
182 **Behavioral:**
183 ```javascript
184 // Instant feedback
185 button.onclick = () => {
186   button.disabled = true;
187   button.textContent = 'Saving...';
188 
189   save().then(() => {
190     showSuccess('Saved!');  // Immediate confirmation
191   });
192 };
193 ```
194 
195 **Reflective:**
196 ```html
197 <!-- Brand story and values -->
198 <section class="about">
199   <h2>Why We Exist</h2>
200   <p>We believe technology should empower, not complicate...</p>
201 </section>
202 
203 <!-- Social proof connecting to identity -->
204 <blockquote>
205   "This tool helped me become the designer I wanted to be."
206 </blockquote>
207 ```
208 
209 ---
210 
211 ## 3. Trust Building System
212 
213 ### Trust Signal Categories
214 
215 | Category | Elements | Implementation |
216 |----------|----------|----------------|
217 | **Security** | SSL, badges, encryption | Visible padlock, security logos on forms |
218 | **Social Proof** | Reviews, testimonials, logos | Star ratings, customer photos, brand logos |
219 | **Transparency** | Policies, pricing, contact | Clear links, no hidden fees, real address |
220 | **Professional** | Design quality, consistency | No broken elements, consistent branding |
221 | **Authority** | Certifications, awards, media | "As seen in...", industry certifications |
222 
223 ### Trust Signal Placement
224 
225 ```
226 ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
227 ‚îÇ  HEADER: Trust banner ("Free shipping | 30-day    ‚îÇ
228 ‚îÇ          returns | Secure checkout")               ‚îÇ
229 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
230 ‚îÇ  HERO: Social proof ("Trusted by 10,000+")        ‚îÇ
231 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
232 ‚îÇ  PRODUCT: Reviews visible, security badges         ‚îÇ
233 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
234 ‚îÇ  CHECKOUT: Payment icons, SSL badge, guarantee     ‚îÇ
235 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
236 ‚îÇ  FOOTER: Contact info, policies, certifications    ‚îÇ
237 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
238 ```
239 
240 ### Trust-Building CSS Patterns
241 
242 ```css
243 /* Trust badge styling */
244 .trust-badge {
245   display: flex;
246   align-items: center;
247   gap: 8px;
248   padding: 12px 16px;
249   background: #F0FDF4;  /* Light green = security */
250   border-radius: 2px; /* Sharp for trust = precision feel */
251   font-size: 14px;
252   color: #166534;
253 }
254 
255 /* Secure form indicator */
256 .secure-form::before {
257   content: 'üîí Secure form';
258   display: block;
259   font-size: 12px;
260   color: #166534;
261   margin-bottom: 8px;
262 }
263 
264 /* Testimonial card */
265 .testimonial {
266   display: flex;
267   gap: 16px;
268   padding: 24px;
269   background: white;
270   border-radius: 16px; /* Friendly = larger radius */
271   box-shadow: var(--shadow-sm);
272 }
273 
274 .testimonial-avatar {
275   width: 48px;
276   height: 48px;
277   border-radius: 50%;  /* Real photos > initials */
278 }
279 ```
280 
281 ---
282 
283 ## 4. Cognitive Load Management
284 
285 ### Three Types of Cognitive Load
286 
287 | Type | Definition | Designer's Role |
288 |------|------------|-----------------|
289 | **Intrinsic** | Inherent complexity of task | Break into smaller steps |
290 | **Extraneous** | Load from poor design | Eliminate this! |
291 | **Germane** | Effort for learning | Support and encourage |
292 
293 ### Reduction Strategies
294 
295 **1. Simplify (Reduce Extraneous)**
296 ```css
297 /* Visual noise ‚Üí Clean */
298 .card-busy {
299   border: 2px solid red;
300   background: linear-gradient(...);
301   box-shadow: 0 0 20px ...;
302   /* Too much! */
303 }
304 
305 .card-clean {
306   background: white;
307   border-radius: 16px;
308   box-shadow: 0 10px 30px -10px rgba(0,0,0,0.1);
309   /* Calm, focused */
310 }
311 ```
312 
313 **2. Chunk Information**
314 ```html
315 <!-- Overwhelming -->
316 <form>
317   <!-- 15 fields at once -->
318 </form>
319 
320 <!-- Chunked -->
321 <form>
322   <fieldset>
323     <legend>Step 1: Personal Info</legend>
324     <!-- 3-4 fields -->
325   </fieldset>
326   <fieldset>
327     <legend>Step 2: Shipping</legend>
328     <!-- 3-4 fields -->
329   </fieldset>
330 </form>
331 ```
332 
333 **3. Progressive Disclosure**
334 ```html
335 <!-- Hide complexity until needed -->
336 <div class="filters">
337   <div class="filters-basic">
338     <!-- Common filters visible -->
339   </div>
340   <button onclick="toggleAdvanced()">
341     Advanced Options ‚ñº
342   </button>
343   <div class="filters-advanced" hidden>
344     <!-- Complex filters hidden -->
345   </div>
346 </div>
347 ```
348 
349 **4. Use Familiar Patterns**
350 ```
351 ‚úÖ Standard navigation placement
352 ‚úÖ Expected icon meanings (üîç = search)
353 ‚úÖ Conventional form layouts
354 ‚úÖ Common gesture patterns (swipe, pinch)
355 ```
356 
357 **5. Offload Information**
358 ```html
359 <!-- Don't make users remember -->
360 <label>
361   Card Number
362   <input type="text" inputmode="numeric"
363          autocomplete="cc-number"
364          placeholder="1234 5678 9012 3456">
365 </label>
366 
367 <!-- Show what they entered -->
368 <div class="order-summary">
369   <p>Shipping to: <strong>John Doe, 123 Main St...</strong></p>
370   <a href="#">Edit</a>
371 </div>
372 ```
373 
374 ---
375 
376 ## 5. Persuasive Design (Ethical)
377 
378 ### Ethical Persuasion Techniques
379 
380 | Technique | Ethical Use | Dark Pattern (Avoid) |
381 |-----------|-------------|----------------------|
382 | **Scarcity** | Real stock levels | Fake countdown timers |
383 | **Social Proof** | Genuine reviews | Fake testimonials |
384 | **Authority** | Real credentials | Misleading badges |
385 | **Urgency** | Real deadlines | Manufactured FOMO |
386 | **Commitment** | Progress saving | Guilt-tripping |
387 
388 ### Nudge Patterns
389 
390 **Smart Defaults:**
391 ```html
392 <!-- Pre-select the recommended option -->
393 <input type="radio" name="plan" value="monthly">
394 <input type="radio" name="plan" value="annual" checked>
395   Annual (Save 20%)
396 ```
397 
398 **Anchoring:**
399 ```html
400 <!-- Show original price to frame discount -->
401 <div class="price">
402   <span class="original">$99</span>
403   <span class="current">$79</span>
404   <span class="savings">Save 20%</span>
405 </div>
406 ```
407 
408 **Social Proof:**
409 ```html
410 <!-- Real-time activity -->
411 <div class="activity">
412   <span class="avatar">üë§</span>
413   <span>Sarah from NYC just purchased</span>
414 </div>
415 
416 <!-- Aggregate proof -->
417 <p>Join 50,000+ designers who use our tool</p>
418 ```
419 
420 **Progress & Commitment:**
421 ```html
422 <!-- Show progress to encourage completion -->
423 <div class="progress">
424   <div class="progress-bar" style="width: 60%"></div>
425   <span>60% complete - almost there!</span>
426 </div>
427 ```
428 
429 ---
430 
431 ## 6. User Persona Quick Reference
432 
433 ### Gen Z (Born 1997-2012)
434 
435 ```
436 CHARACTERISTICS:
437 - Digital natives, mobile-first
438 - Value authenticity, diversity
439 - Short attention spans
440 - Visual learners
441 
442 DESIGN APPROACH:
443 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Colors: Vibrant, hypercolor, bold gradients
444 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Typography: Large, variable, experimental
445 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Layout: Vertical scroll, mobile-native
446 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Interactions: Fast, gamified, gesture-based
447 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Content: Short-form video, memes, stories
448 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Trust: Peer reviews > authority
449 ```
450 
451 ### Millennials (Born 1981-1996)
452 
453 ```
454 CHARACTERISTICS:
455 - Value experiences over things
456 - Research before buying
457 - Socially conscious
458 - Price-sensitive but quality-aware
459 
460 DESIGN APPROACH:
461 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Colors: Muted pastels, earth tones
462 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Typography: Clean, readable sans-serif
463 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Layout: Responsive, card-based
464 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Interactions: Smooth, purposeful animations
465 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Content: Value-driven, transparent
466 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Trust: Reviews, sustainability, values
467 ```
468 
469 ### Gen X (Born 1965-1980)
470 
471 ```
472 CHARACTERISTICS:
473 - Independent, self-reliant
474 - Value efficiency
475 - Skeptical of marketing
476 - Balanced tech comfort
477 
478 DESIGN APPROACH:
479 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Colors: Professional, trustworthy
480 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Typography: Familiar, conservative
481 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Layout: Clear hierarchy, traditional
482 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Interactions: Functional, not flashy
483 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Content: Direct, fact-based
484 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Trust: Expertise, track record
485 ```
486 
487 ### Baby Boomers (Born 1946-1964)
488 
489 ```
490 CHARACTERISTICS:
491 - Detail-oriented
492 - Loyal when trusted
493 - Value personal service
494 - Less tech-confident
495 
496 DESIGN APPROACH:
497 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Colors: High contrast, simple palette
498 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Typography: Large (18px+), high contrast
499 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Layout: Simple, linear, spacious
500 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Interactions: Minimal, clear feedback
501 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Content: Comprehensive, detailed
502 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Trust: Phone numbers, real people
503 ```
504 
505 ---
506 
507 ## 7. Emotion Color Mapping
508 
509 ```
510 ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
511 ‚îÇ  EMOTION          ‚îÇ  COLORS           ‚îÇ  USE       ‚îÇ
512 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îº‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îº‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
513 ‚îÇ  Trust            ‚îÇ  Blue, Green      ‚îÇ  Finance   ‚îÇ
514 ‚îÇ  Excitement       ‚îÇ  Red, Orange      ‚îÇ  Sales     ‚îÇ
515 ‚îÇ  Calm             ‚îÇ  Blue, Soft green ‚îÇ  Wellness  ‚îÇ
516 ‚îÇ  Luxury           ‚îÇ  Black, Gold      ‚îÇ  Premium   ‚îÇ
517 ‚îÇ  Creativity       ‚îÇ  Teal, Pink       ‚îÇ  Art       ‚îÇ
518 ‚îÇ  Energy           ‚îÇ  Yellow, Orange   ‚îÇ  Sports    ‚îÇ

521 ‚îÇ  Sophistication   ‚îÇ  Gray, Navy       ‚îÇ  Corporate ‚îÇ
522 ‚îÇ  Urgency          ‚îÇ  Red              ‚îÇ  Errors    ‚îÇ
523 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¥‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¥‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
524 ```
525 
526 ---
527 
528 ## 8. Psychology Checklist
529 
530 ### Before Launch
531 
532 - [ ] **Hick's Law:** No more than 7 choices in navigation
533 - [ ] **Fitts' Law:** Primary CTAs are large and reachable
534 - [ ] **Miller's Law:** Content is chunked appropriately
535 - [ ] **Von Restorff:** CTAs stand out from surroundings
536 - [ ] **Trust:** Security badges, reviews, policies visible
537 - [ ] **Emotional:** Design evokes intended feeling
538 - [ ] **Cognitive Load:** Interface is clean, not overwhelming
539 - [ ] **Familiar Patterns:** Standard conventions used
540 - [ ] **Feedback:** All actions have clear responses
541 - [ ] **Accessibility:** Inclusive for all users

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F84 path:skills/frontend-design/visual-effects.md hash:07568520407d298f50733028f92bf090d071a84a6ecd97950fba1384a0496a82 lines:383 ===
001 # Visual Effects Reference
002 
003 > Modern CSS effect principles and techniques - learn the concepts, create variations.
004 > **No fixed values to copy - understand the patterns.**
005 
006 ---
007 
008 ## 1. Glassmorphism Principles
009 
010 ### What Makes Glassmorphism Work
011 
012 ```
013 Key Properties:
014 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Semi-transparent background (not solid)
015 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Backdrop blur (frosted glass effect)
016 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Subtle border (for definition)
017 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Often: light shadow for depth
018 ```
019 
020 ### The Pattern (Customize Values)
021 
022 ```css
023 .glass {
024   /* Transparency: adjust opacity based on content readability */
025   background: rgba(R, G, B, OPACITY);
026   /* OPACITY: 0.1-0.3 for dark bg, 0.5-0.8 for light bg */
027 
028   /* Blur: higher = more frosted */
029   backdrop-filter: blur(AMOUNT);
030   /* AMOUNT: 8-12px subtle, 16-24px strong */
031 
032   /* Border: defines edges */
033   border: 1px solid rgba(255, 255, 255, OPACITY);
034   /* OPACITY: 0.1-0.3 typically */
035 
036   /* Radius: match your design system */
037   border-radius: YOUR_RADIUS;
038 }
039 ```
040 
041 ### When to Use Glassmorphism
042 - ‚úÖ Over colorful/image backgrounds
043 - ‚úÖ Modals, overlays, cards
044 - ‚úÖ Navigation bars with scrolling content behind
045 - ‚ùå Text-heavy content (readability issues)
046 - ‚ùå Simple solid backgrounds (pointless)
047 
048 ### When NOT to Use
049 - Low contrast situations
050 - Accessibility-critical content
051 - Performance-constrained devices
052 
053 ---
054 
055 ## 2. Neomorphism Principles
056 
057 ### What Makes Neomorphism Work
058 
059 ```
060 Key Concept: Soft, extruded elements using DUAL shadows
061 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Light shadow (from light source direction)
062 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Dark shadow (opposite direction)
063 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Background matches surrounding (same color)
064 ```
065 
066 ### The Pattern
067 
068 ```css
069 .neo-raised {
070   /* Background MUST match parent */
071   background: SAME_AS_PARENT;
072 
073   /* Two shadows: light direction + dark direction */
074   box-shadow:
075     OFFSET OFFSET BLUR rgba(light-color),
076     -OFFSET -OFFSET BLUR rgba(dark-color);
077 
078   /* OFFSET: typically 6-12px */
079   /* BLUR: typically 12-20px */
080 }
081 
082 .neo-pressed {
083   /* Inset creates "pushed in" effect */
084   box-shadow:
085     inset OFFSET OFFSET BLUR rgba(dark-color),
086     inset -OFFSET -OFFSET BLUR rgba(light-color);
087 }
088 ```
089 
090 ### Accessibility Warning
091 ‚ö†Ô∏è **Low contrast** - use sparingly, ensure clear boundaries
092 
093 ### When to Use
094 - Decorative elements
095 - Subtle interactive states
096 - Minimalist UI with flat colors
097 
098 ---
099 
100 ## 3. Shadow Hierarchy Principles
101 
102 ### Concept: Shadows Indicate Elevation
103 
104 ```
105 Higher elevation = larger shadow
106 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Level 0: No shadow (flat on surface)
107 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Level 1: Subtle shadow (slightly raised)
108 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Level 2: Medium shadow (cards, buttons)
109 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Level 3: Large shadow (modals, dropdowns)
110 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Level 4: Deep shadow (floating elements)
111 ```
112 
113 ### Shadow Properties to Adjust
114 
115 ```css
116 box-shadow: OFFSET-X OFFSET-Y BLUR SPREAD COLOR;
117 
118 /* Offset: direction of shadow */
119 /* Blur: softness (larger = softer) */
120 /* Spread: size expansion */
121 /* Color: typically black with low opacity */
122 ```
123 
124 ### Principles for Natural Shadows
125 
126 1. **Y-offset larger than X** (light comes from above)
127 2. **Low opacity** (5-15% for subtle, 15-25% for pronounced)
128 3. **Multiple layers** for realism (ambient + direct)
129 4. **Blur scales with offset** (larger offset = larger blur)
130 
131 ### Dark Mode Shadows
132 - Shadows less visible on dark backgrounds
133 - May need to increase opacity
134 - Or use glow/highlight instead
135 
136 ---
137 
138 ## 4. Gradient Principles
139 
140 ### Types and When to Use
141 
142 | Type | Pattern | Use Case |
143 |------|---------|----------|
144 | **Linear** | Color A ‚Üí Color B along line | Backgrounds, buttons, headers |
145 | **Radial** | Center ‚Üí outward | Spotlights, focal points |
146 | **Conic** | Around center | Pie charts, creative effects |
147 
148 ### Creating Harmonious Gradients
149 
150 ```
151 Good Gradient Rules:
152 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Use ADJACENT colors on wheel (analogous)
153 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Or same hue with different lightness
154 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Avoid complementary (can look harsh)
155 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Add middle stops for smoother transitions
156 ```
157 
158 ### Gradient Syntax Pattern
159 
160 ```css
161 .gradient {
162   background: linear-gradient(
163     DIRECTION,           /* angle or to-keyword */
164     COLOR-STOP-1,        /* color + optional position */
165     COLOR-STOP-2,
166     /* ... more stops */
167   );
168 }
169 
170 /* DIRECTION examples: */
171 /* 90deg, 135deg, to right, to bottom right */
172 ```
173 
174 ### Mesh Gradients
175 
176 ```
177 Multiple radial gradients overlapped:
178 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Each at different position
179 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Each with transparent falloff
180 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ **Mandatory for "Wow" factor in Hero sections**
181 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Creates organic, colorful effect (Search: "Aurora Gradient CSS")
182 ```
183 
184 ---
185 
186 ## 5. Border Effects Principles
187 
188 ### Gradient Borders
189 
190 ```
191 Technique: Pseudo-element with gradient background
192 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Element has padding = border width
193 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Pseudo-element fills with gradient
194 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Mask or clip creates border effect
195 ```
196 
197 ### Animated Borders
198 
199 ```
200 Technique: Rotating gradient or conic sweep
201 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Pseudo-element larger than content
202 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Animation rotates the gradient
203 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Overflow hidden clips to shape
204 ```
205 
206 ### Glow Borders
207 
208 ```css
209 /* Multiple box-shadows create glow */
210 box-shadow:
211   0 0 SMALL-BLUR COLOR,
212   0 0 MEDIUM-BLUR COLOR,
213   0 0 LARGE-BLUR COLOR;
214 
215 /* Each layer adds to the glow */
216 ```
217 
218 ---
219 
220 ## 6. Glow Effects Principles
221 
222 ### Text Glow
223 
224 ```css
225 text-shadow:
226   0 0 BLUR-1 COLOR,
227   0 0 BLUR-2 COLOR,
228   0 0 BLUR-3 COLOR;
229 
230 /* Multiple layers = stronger glow */
231 /* Larger blur = softer spread */
232 ```
233 
234 ### Element Glow
235 
236 ```css
237 box-shadow:
238   0 0 BLUR-1 COLOR,
239   0 0 BLUR-2 COLOR;
240 
241 /* Use color matching element for realistic glow */
242 /* Lower opacity for subtle, higher for neon */
243 ```
244 
245 ### Pulsing Glow Animation
246 
247 ```css
248 @keyframes glow-pulse {
249   0%, 100% { box-shadow: 0 0 SMALL-BLUR COLOR; }
250   50% { box-shadow: 0 0 LARGE-BLUR COLOR; }
251 }
252 
253 /* Easing and duration affect feel */
254 ```
255 
256 ---
257 
258 ## 7. Overlay Techniques
259 
260 ### Gradient Overlay on Images
261 
262 ```
263 Purpose: Improve text readability over images
264 Pattern: Gradient from transparent to opaque
265 Position: Where text will appear
266 ```
267 
268 ```css
269 .overlay::after {
270   content: '';
271   position: absolute;
272   inset: 0;
273   background: linear-gradient(
274     DIRECTION,
275     transparent PERCENTAGE,
276     rgba(0,0,0,OPACITY) 100%
277   );
278 }
279 ```
280 
281 ### Colored Overlay
282 
283 ```css
284 /* Blend mode or layered gradient */
285 background:
286   linear-gradient(YOUR-COLOR-WITH-OPACITY),
287   url('image.jpg');
288 ```
289 
290 ---
291 
292 ## 8. Modern CSS Techniques
293 
294 ### Container Queries (Concept)
295 
296 ```
297 Instead of viewport breakpoints:
298 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Component responds to ITS container
299 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Truly modular, reusable components
300 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Syntax: @container (condition) { }
301 ```
302 
303 ### :has() Selector (Concept)
304 
305 ```
306 Parent styling based on children:
307 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ "Parent that has X child"
308 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Enables previously impossible patterns
309 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Progressive enhancement approach
310 ```
311 
312 ### Scroll-Driven Animations (Concept)
313 
314 ```
315 Animation progress tied to scroll:
316 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Entry/exit animations on scroll
317 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Parallax effects
318 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Progress indicators
319 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ View-based or scroll-based timeline
320 ```
321 
322 ---
323 
324 ## 9. Performance Principles
325 
326 ### GPU-Accelerated Properties
327 
328 ```
329 CHEAP to animate (GPU):
330 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ transform (translate, scale, rotate)
331 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ opacity
332 
333 EXPENSIVE to animate (CPU):
334 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ width, height
335 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ top, left, right, bottom
336 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ margin, padding
337 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ box-shadow (recalculates)
338 ```
339 
340 ### will-change Usage
341 
342 ```css
343 /* Use sparingly, only for heavy animations */
344 .heavy-animation {
345   will-change: transform;
346 }
347 
348 /* Remove after animation if possible */
349 ```
350 
351 ### Reduced Motion
352 
353 ```css
354 @media (prefers-reduced-motion: reduce) {
355   /* Disable or minimize animations */
356   /* Respect user preference */
357 }
358 ```
359 
360 ---
361 
362 ## 10. Effect Selection Checklist
363 
364 Before applying any effect:
365 
366 - [ ] **Does it serve a purpose?** (not just decoration)
367 - [ ] **Is it appropriate for the context?** (brand, audience)
368 - [ ] **Have you varied from previous projects?** (avoid repetition)
369 - [ ] **Is it accessible?** (contrast, motion sensitivity)
370 - [ ] **Is it performant?** (especially on mobile)
371 - [ ] **Did you ask user preference?** (if style open-ended)
372 
373 ### Anti-Patterns
374 
375 - ‚ùå Glassmorphism on every element (kitsch)
376 - ‚ùå Dark + neon as default (lazy AI look)
377 - ‚ùå **Static/Flat designs with no depth (FAILED)**
378 - ‚ùå Effects that hurt readability
379 - ‚ùå Animations without purpose
380 
381 ---
382 
383 > **Remember**: Effects enhance meaning. Choose based on purpose and context, not because it "looks cool."

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F85 path:skills/game-development/2d-games/SKILL.md hash:f31d95e041d06f018620fc697f25a32ea115b4ec577d9f448f714eeeb606363d lines:119 ===
001 ---
002 name: 2d-games
003 description: 2D game development principles. Sprites, tilemaps, physics, camera.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Write, Edit, Glob, Grep
005 ---
006 
007 # 2D Game Development
008 
009 > Principles for 2D game systems.
010 
011 ---
012 
013 ## 1. Sprite Systems
014 
015 ### Sprite Organization
016 
017 | Component | Purpose |
018 |-----------|---------|
019 | **Atlas** | Combine textures, reduce draw calls |
020 | **Animation** | Frame sequences |
021 | **Pivot** | Rotation/scale origin |
022 | **Layering** | Z-order control |
023 
024 ### Animation Principles
025 
026 - Frame rate: 8-24 FPS typical
027 - Squash and stretch for impact
028 - Anticipation before action
029 - Follow-through after action
030 
031 ---
032 
033 ## 2. Tilemap Design
034 
035 ### Tile Considerations
036 
037 | Factor | Recommendation |
038 |--------|----------------|
039 | **Size** | 16x16, 32x32, 64x64 |
040 | **Auto-tiling** | Use for terrain |
041 | **Collision** | Simplified shapes |
042 
043 ### Layers
044 
045 | Layer | Content |
046 |-------|---------|
047 | Background | Non-interactive scenery |
048 | Terrain | Walkable ground |
049 | Props | Interactive objects |
050 | Foreground | Parallax overlay |
051 
052 ---
053 
054 ## 3. 2D Physics
055 
056 ### Collision Shapes
057 
058 | Shape | Use Case |
059 |-------|----------|
060 | Box | Rectangular objects |
061 | Circle | Balls, rounded |
062 | Capsule | Characters |
063 | Polygon | Complex shapes |
064 
065 ### Physics Considerations
066 
067 - Pixel-perfect vs physics-based
068 - Fixed timestep for consistency
069 - Layers for filtering
070 
071 ---
072 
073 ## 4. Camera Systems
074 
075 ### Camera Types
076 
077 | Type | Use |
078 |------|-----|
079 | **Follow** | Track player |
080 | **Look-ahead** | Anticipate movement |
081 | **Multi-target** | Two-player |
082 | **Room-based** | Metroidvania |
083 
084 ### Screen Shake
085 
086 - Short duration (50-200ms)
087 - Diminishing intensity
088 - Use sparingly
089 
090 ---
091 
092 ## 5. Genre Patterns
093 
094 ### Platformer
095 
096 - Coyote time (leniency after edge)
097 - Jump buffering
098 - Variable jump height
099 
100 ### Top-down
101 
102 - 8-directional or free movement
103 - Aim-based or auto-aim
104 - Consider rotation or not
105 
106 ---
107 
108 ## 6. Anti-Patterns
109 
110 | ‚ùå Don't | ‚úÖ Do |
111 |----------|-------|
112 | Separate textures | Use atlases |
113 | Complex collision shapes | Simplified collision |
114 | Jittery camera | Smooth following |
115 | Pixel-perfect on physics | Choose one approach |
116 
117 ---
118 
119 > **Remember:** 2D is about clarity. Every pixel should communicate.
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F85 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F86 path:skills/game-development/3d-games/SKILL.md hash:141bf1ca6af96066cffa91b2b37417b9d1cffec4fcc2a6ef1333ee976121f7dd lines:135 ===
001 ---
002 name: 3d-games
003 description: 3D game development principles. Rendering, shaders, physics, cameras.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Write, Edit, Glob, Grep
005 ---
006 
007 # 3D Game Development
008 
009 > Principles for 3D game systems.
010 
011 ---
012 
013 ## 1. Rendering Pipeline
014 
015 ### Stages
016 
017 ```
018 1. Vertex Processing ‚Üí Transform geometry
019 2. Rasterization ‚Üí Convert to pixels
020 3. Fragment Processing ‚Üí Color pixels
021 4. Output ‚Üí To screen
022 ```
023 
024 ### Optimization Principles
025 
026 | Technique | Purpose |
027 |-----------|---------|
028 | **Frustum culling** | Don't render off-screen |
029 | **Occlusion culling** | Don't render hidden |
030 | **LOD** | Less detail at distance |
031 | **Batching** | Combine draw calls |
032 
033 ---
034 
035 ## 2. Shader Principles
036 
037 ### Shader Types
038 
039 | Type | Purpose |
040 |------|---------|
041 | **Vertex** | Position, normals |
042 | **Fragment/Pixel** | Color, lighting |
043 | **Compute** | General computation |
044 
045 ### When to Write Custom Shaders
046 
047 - Special effects (water, fire, portals)
048 - Stylized rendering (toon, sketch)
049 - Performance optimization
050 - Unique visual identity
051 
052 ---
053 
054 ## 3. 3D Physics
055 
056 ### Collision Shapes
057 
058 | Shape | Use Case |
059 |-------|----------|
060 | **Box** | Buildings, crates |
061 | **Sphere** | Balls, quick checks |
062 | **Capsule** | Characters |
063 | **Mesh** | Terrain (expensive) |
064 
065 ### Principles
066 
067 - Simple colliders, complex visuals
068 - Layer-based filtering
069 - Raycasting for line-of-sight
070 
071 ---
072 
073 ## 4. Camera Systems
074 
075 ### Camera Types
076 
077 | Type | Use |
078 |------|-----|
079 | **Third-person** | Action, adventure |
080 | **First-person** | Immersive, FPS |
081 | **Isometric** | Strategy, RPG |
082 | **Orbital** | Inspection, editors |
083 
084 ### Camera Feel
085 
086 - Smooth following (lerp)
087 - Collision avoidance
088 - Look-ahead for movement
089 - FOV changes for speed
090 
091 ---
092 
093 ## 5. Lighting
094 
095 ### Light Types
096 
097 | Type | Use |
098 |------|-----|
099 | **Directional** | Sun, moon |
100 | **Point** | Lamps, torches |
101 | **Spot** | Flashlight, stage |
102 | **Ambient** | Base illumination |
103 
104 ### Performance Consideration
105 
106 - Real-time shadows are expensive
107 - Bake when possible
108 - Shadow cascades for large worlds
109 
110 ---
111 
112 ## 6. Level of Detail (LOD)
113 
114 ### LOD Strategy
115 
116 | Distance | Model |
117 |----------|-------|
118 | Near | Full detail |
119 | Medium | 50% triangles |
120 | Far | 25% or billboard |
121 
122 ---
123 
124 ## 7. Anti-Patterns
125 
126 | ‚ùå Don't | ‚úÖ Do |
127 |----------|-------|
128 | Mesh colliders everywhere | Simple shapes |
129 | Real-time shadows on mobile | Baked or blob shadows |
130 | One LOD for all distances | Distance-based LOD |
131 | Unoptimized shaders | Profile and simplify |
132 
133 ---
134 
135 > **Remember:** 3D is about illusion. Create the impression of detail, not the detail itself.
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F86 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F87 path:skills/game-development/game-art/SKILL.md hash:ab7029cb91c498c6469137f7b8b1575fdc7a97db3cc338c5cd2f0edc2ac2888a lines:185 ===
001 ---
002 name: game-art
003 description: Game art principles. Visual style selection, asset pipeline, animation workflow.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Glob, Grep
005 ---
006 
007 # Game Art Principles
008 
009 > Visual design thinking for games - style selection, asset pipelines, and art direction.
010 
011 ---
012 
013 ## 1. Art Style Selection
014 
015 ### Decision Tree
016 
017 ```
018 What feeling should the game evoke?
019 ‚îÇ
020 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Nostalgic / Retro
021 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Limited palette? ‚Üí Pixel Art
022 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Hand-drawn feel? ‚Üí Vector / Flash style
023 ‚îÇ
024 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Realistic / Immersive
025 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ High budget? ‚Üí PBR 3D
026 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Stylized realism? ‚Üí Hand-painted textures
027 ‚îÇ
028 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Approachable / Casual
029 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Clean shapes? ‚Üí Flat / Minimalist
030 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Soft feel? ‚Üí Gradient / Soft shadows
031 ‚îÇ
032 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Unique / Experimental
033     ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Define custom style guide
034 ```
035 
036 ### Style Comparison Matrix
037 
038 | Style | Production Speed | Skill Floor | Scalability | Best For |
039 |-------|------------------|-------------|-------------|----------|
040 | **Pixel Art** | Medium | Medium | Hard to hire | Indie, retro |
041 | **Vector/Flat** | Fast | Low | Easy | Mobile, casual |
042 | **Hand-painted** | Slow | High | Medium | Fantasy, stylized |
043 | **PBR 3D** | Slow | High | AAA pipeline | Realistic games |
044 | **Low-poly** | Fast | Medium | Easy | Indie 3D |
045 | **Cel-shaded** | Medium | Medium | Medium | Anime, cartoon |
046 
047 ---
048 
049 ## 2. Asset Pipeline Decisions
050 
051 ### 2D Pipeline
052 
053 | Phase | Tool Options | Output |
054 |-------|--------------|--------|
055 | **Concept** | Paper, Procreate, Photoshop | Reference sheet |
056 | **Creation** | Aseprite, Photoshop, Krita | Individual sprites |
057 | **Atlas** | TexturePacker, Aseprite | Spritesheet |
058 | **Animation** | Spine, DragonBones, Frame-by-frame | Animation data |
059 | **Integration** | Engine import | Game-ready assets |
060 
061 ### 3D Pipeline
062 
063 | Phase | Tool Options | Output |
064 |-------|--------------|--------|
065 | **Concept** | 2D art, Blockout | Reference |
066 | **Modeling** | Blender, Maya, 3ds Max | High-poly mesh |
067 | **Retopology** | Blender, ZBrush | Game-ready mesh |
068 | **UV/Texturing** | Substance Painter, Blender | Texture maps |
069 | **Rigging** | Blender, Maya | Skeletal rig |
070 | **Animation** | Blender, Maya, Mixamo | Animation clips |
071 | **Export** | FBX, glTF | Engine-ready |
072 
073 ---
074 
075 ## 3. Color Theory Decisions
076 
077 ### Palette Selection
078 
079 | Goal | Strategy | Example |
080 |------|----------|---------|
081 | **Harmony** | Complementary or analogous | Nature games |
082 | **Contrast** | High saturation differences | Action games |
083 | **Mood** | Warm/cool temperature | Horror, cozy |
084 | **Readability** | Value contrast over hue | Gameplay clarity |
085 
086 ### Color Principles
087 
088 - **Hierarchy:** Important elements should pop
089 - **Consistency:** Same object = same color family
090 - **Context:** Colors read differently on backgrounds
091 - **Accessibility:** Don't rely only on color
092 
093 ---
094 
095 ## 4. Animation Principles
096 
097 ### The 12 Principles (Applied to Games)
098 
099 | Principle | Game Application |
100 |-----------|------------------|
101 | **Squash & Stretch** | Jump arcs, impacts |
102 | **Anticipation** | Wind-up before attack |
103 | **Staging** | Clear silhouettes |
104 | **Follow-through** | Hair, capes after movement |
105 | **Slow in/out** | Easing on transitions |
106 | **Arcs** | Natural movement paths |
107 | **Secondary Action** | Breathing, blinking |
108 | **Timing** | Frame count = weight/speed |
109 | **Exaggeration** | Readable from distance |
110 | **Appeal** | Memorable design |
111 
112 ### Frame Count Guidelines
113 
114 | Action Type | Typical Frames | Feel |
115 |-------------|----------------|------|
116 | Idle breathing | 4-8 | Subtle |
117 | Walk cycle | 6-12 | Smooth |
118 | Run cycle | 4-8 | Energetic |
119 | Attack | 3-6 | Snappy |
120 | Death | 8-16 | Dramatic |
121 
122 ---
123 
124 ## 5. Resolution & Scale Decisions
125 
126 ### 2D Resolution by Platform
127 
128 | Platform | Base Resolution | Sprite Scale |
129 |----------|-----------------|--------------|
130 | Mobile | 1080p | 64-128px characters |
131 | Desktop | 1080p-4K | 128-256px characters |
132 | Pixel art | 320x180 to 640x360 | 16-32px characters |
133 
134 ### Consistency Rule
135 
136 Choose a base unit and stick to it:
137 - Pixel art: Work at 1x, scale up (never down)
138 - HD art: Define DPI, maintain ratio
139 - 3D: 1 unit = 1 meter (industry standard)
140 
141 ---
142 
143 ## 6. Asset Organization
144 
145 ### Naming Convention
146 
147 ```
148 [type]_[object]_[variant]_[state].[ext]
149 
150 Examples:
151 spr_player_idle_01.png
152 tex_stone_wall_normal.png
153 mesh_tree_oak_lod2.fbx
154 ```
155 
156 ### Folder Structure Principle
157 
158 ```
159 assets/
160 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ characters/
161 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ player/
162 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ enemies/
163 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ environment/
164 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ props/
165 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ tiles/
166 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ ui/
167 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ effects/
168 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ audio/
169 ```
170 
171 ---
172 
173 ## 7. Anti-Patterns
174 
175 | Don't | Do |
176 |-------|-----|
177 | Mix art styles randomly | Define and follow style guide |
178 | Work at final resolution only | Create at source resolution |
179 | Ignore silhouette readability | Test at gameplay distance |
180 | Over-detail background | Focus detail on player area |
181 | Skip color testing | Test on target display |
182 
183 ---
184 
185 > **Remember:** Art serves gameplay. If it doesn't help the player, it's decoration.
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F87 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F88 path:skills/game-development/game-audio/SKILL.md hash:5cfa7e0a750c202ce81dde7aef8ebbd6e9954ece42ce47ed1619163d217a48c3 lines:190 ===
001 ---
002 name: game-audio
003 description: Game audio principles. Sound design, music integration, adaptive audio systems.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Glob, Grep
005 ---
006 
007 # Game Audio Principles
008 
009 > Sound design and music integration for immersive game experiences.
010 
011 ---
012 
013 ## 1. Audio Category System
014 
015 ### Category Definitions
016 
017 | Category | Behavior | Examples |
018 |----------|----------|----------|
019 | **Music** | Looping, crossfade, ducking | BGM, combat music |
020 | **SFX** | One-shot, 3D positioned | Footsteps, impacts |
021 | **Ambient** | Looping, background layer | Wind, crowd, forest |
022 | **UI** | Immediate, non-3D | Button clicks, notifications |
023 | **Voice** | Priority, ducking trigger | Dialogue, announcer |
024 
025 ### Priority Hierarchy
026 
027 ```
028 When sounds compete for channels:
029 
030 1. Voice (highest - always audible)
031 2. Player SFX (feedback critical)
032 3. Enemy SFX (gameplay important)
033 4. Music (mood, but duckable)
034 5. Ambient (lowest - can drop)
035 ```
036 
037 ---
038 
039 ## 2. Sound Design Decisions
040 
041 ### SFX Creation Approach
042 
043 | Approach | When to Use | Trade-offs |
044 |----------|-------------|------------|
045 | **Recording** | Realistic needs | High quality, time intensive |
046 | **Synthesis** | Sci-fi, retro, UI | Unique, requires skill |
047 | **Library samples** | Fast production | Common sounds, licensing |
048 | **Layering** | Complex sounds | Best results, more work |
049 
050 ### Layering Structure
051 
052 | Layer | Purpose | Example: Gunshot |
053 |-------|---------|------------------|
054 | **Attack** | Initial transient | Click, snap |
055 | **Body** | Main character | Boom, blast |
056 | **Tail** | Decay, room | Reverb, echo |
057 | **Sweetener** | Special sauce | Shell casing, mechanical |
058 
059 ---
060 
061 ## 3. Music Integration
062 
063 ### Music State System
064 
065 ```
066 Game State ‚Üí Music Response
067 ‚îÇ
068 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Menu ‚Üí Calm, loopable theme
069 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Exploration ‚Üí Ambient, atmospheric
070 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Combat detected ‚Üí Transition to tension
071 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Combat engaged ‚Üí Full battle music
072 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Victory ‚Üí Stinger + calm transition
073 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Defeat ‚Üí Somber stinger
074 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Boss ‚Üí Unique, multi-phase track
075 ```
076 
077 ### Transition Techniques
078 
079 | Technique | Use When | Feel |
080 |-----------|----------|------|
081 | **Crossfade** | Smooth mood shift | Gradual |
082 | **Stinger** | Immediate event | Dramatic |
083 | **Stem mixing** | Dynamic intensity | Seamless |
084 | **Beat-synced** | Rhythmic gameplay | Musical |
085 | **Queue point** | Next natural break | Clean |
086 
087 ---
088 
089 ## 4. Adaptive Audio Decisions
090 
091 ### Intensity Parameters
092 
093 | Parameter | Affects | Example |
094 |-----------|---------|---------|
095 | **Threat level** | Music intensity | Enemy count |
096 | **Health** | Filter, reverb | Low health = muffled |
097 | **Speed** | Tempo, energy | Racing speed |
098 | **Environment** | Reverb, EQ | Cave vs outdoor |
099 | **Time of day** | Mood, volume | Night = quieter |
100 
101 ### Vertical vs Horizontal
102 
103 | System | What Changes | Best For |
104 |--------|--------------|----------|
105 | **Vertical (layers)** | Add/remove instrument layers | Intensity scaling |
106 | **Horizontal (segments)** | Different music sections | State changes |
107 | **Combined** | Both | AAA adaptive scores |
108 
109 ---
110 
111 ## 5. 3D Audio Decisions
112 
113 ### Spatialization
114 
115 | Element | 3D Positioned? | Reason |
116 |---------|----------------|--------|
117 | Player footsteps | No (or subtle) | Always audible |
118 | Enemy footsteps | Yes | Directional awareness |
119 | Gunfire | Yes | Combat awareness |
120 | Music | No | Mood, non-diegetic |
121 | Ambient zone | Yes (area) | Environmental |
122 | UI sounds | No | Interface feedback |
123 
124 ### Distance Behavior
125 
126 | Distance | Sound Behavior |
127 |----------|----------------|
128 | **Near** | Full volume, full frequency |
129 | **Medium** | Volume falloff, high-freq rolloff |
130 | **Far** | Low volume, low-pass filter |
131 | **Max** | Silent or ambient hint |
132 
133 ---
134 
135 ## 6. Platform Considerations
136 
137 ### Format Selection
138 
139 | Platform | Recommended Format | Reason |
140 |----------|-------------------|--------|
141 | PC | OGG Vorbis, WAV | Quality, no licensing |
142 | Console | Platform-specific | Certification |
143 | Mobile | MP3, AAC | Size, compatibility |
144 | Web | WebM/Opus, MP3 fallback | Browser support |
145 
146 ### Memory Budget
147 
148 | Game Type | Audio Budget | Strategy |
149 |-----------|--------------|----------|
150 | Mobile casual | 10-50 MB | Compressed, fewer variants |
151 | PC indie | 100-500 MB | Quality focus |
152 | AAA | 1+ GB | Full quality, many variants |
153 
154 ---
155 
156 ## 7. Mix Hierarchy
157 
158 ### Volume Balance Reference
159 
160 | Category | Relative Level | Notes |
161 |----------|----------------|-------|
162 | **Voice** | 0 dB (reference) | Always clear |
163 | **Player SFX** | -3 to -6 dB | Prominent but not harsh |
164 | **Music** | -6 to -12 dB | Foundation, ducks for voice |
165 | **Enemy SFX** | -6 to -9 dB | Important but not dominant |
166 | **Ambient** | -12 to -18 dB | Subtle background |
167 
168 ### Ducking Rules
169 
170 | When | Duck What | Amount |
171 |------|-----------|--------|
172 | Voice plays | Music, Ambient | -6 to -9 dB |
173 | Explosion | All except explosion | Brief duck |
174 | Menu open | Gameplay audio | -3 to -6 dB |
175 
176 ---
177 
178 ## 8. Anti-Patterns
179 
180 | Don't | Do |
181 |-------|-----|
182 | Play same sound repeatedly | Use variations (3-5 per sound) |
183 | Max volume everything | Use proper mix hierarchy |
184 | Ignore silence | Silence creates contrast |
185 | One music track loops forever | Provide variety, transitions |
186 | Skip audio in prototype | Placeholder audio matters |
187 
188 ---
189 
190 > **Remember:** 50% of the game experience is audio. A muted game loses half its soul.
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F88 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F89 path:skills/game-development/game-design/SKILL.md hash:93c4179046820a685506d81b066cbceeaa91b197cdb89ab7da1e04cac9062657 lines:129 ===
001 ---
002 name: game-design
003 description: Game design principles. GDD structure, balancing, player psychology, progression.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Glob, Grep
005 ---
006 
007 # Game Design Principles
008 
009 > Design thinking for engaging games.
010 
011 ---
012 
013 ## 1. Core Loop Design
014 
015 ### The 30-Second Test
016 
017 ```
018 Every game needs a fun 30-second loop:
019 1. ACTION ‚Üí Player does something
020 2. FEEDBACK ‚Üí Game responds
021 3. REWARD ‚Üí Player feels good
022 4. REPEAT
023 ```
024 
025 ### Loop Examples
026 
027 | Genre | Core Loop |
028 |-------|-----------|
029 | Platformer | Run ‚Üí Jump ‚Üí Land ‚Üí Collect |
030 | Shooter | Aim ‚Üí Shoot ‚Üí Kill ‚Üí Loot |
031 | Puzzle | Observe ‚Üí Think ‚Üí Solve ‚Üí Advance |
032 | RPG | Explore ‚Üí Fight ‚Üí Level ‚Üí Gear |
033 
034 ---
035 
036 ## 2. Game Design Document (GDD)
037 
038 ### Essential Sections
039 
040 | Section | Content |
041 |---------|---------|
042 | **Pitch** | One-sentence description |
043 | **Core Loop** | 30-second gameplay |
044 | **Mechanics** | How systems work |
045 | **Progression** | How player advances |
046 | **Art Style** | Visual direction |
047 | **Audio** | Sound direction |
048 
049 ### Principles
050 
051 - Keep it living (update regularly)
052 - Visuals help communicate
053 - Less is more (start small)
054 
055 ---
056 
057 ## 3. Player Psychology
058 
059 ### Motivation Types
060 
061 | Type | Driven By |
062 |------|-----------|
063 | **Achiever** | Goals, completion |
064 | **Explorer** | Discovery, secrets |
065 | **Socializer** | Interaction, community |
066 | **Killer** | Competition, dominance |
067 
068 ### Reward Schedules
069 
070 | Schedule | Effect | Use |
071 |----------|--------|-----|
072 | **Fixed** | Predictable | Milestone rewards |
073 | **Variable** | Addictive | Loot drops |
074 | **Ratio** | Effort-based | Grind games |
075 
076 ---
077 
078 ## 4. Difficulty Balancing
079 
080 ### Flow State
081 
082 ```
083 Too Hard ‚Üí Frustration ‚Üí Quit
084 Too Easy ‚Üí Boredom ‚Üí Quit
085 Just Right ‚Üí Flow ‚Üí Engagement
086 ```
087 
088 ### Balancing Strategies
089 
090 | Strategy | How |
091 |----------|-----|
092 | **Dynamic** | Adjust to player skill |
093 | **Selection** | Let player choose |
094 | **Accessibility** | Options for all |
095 
096 ---
097 
098 ## 5. Progression Design
099 
100 ### Progression Types
101 
102 | Type | Example |
103 |------|---------|
104 | **Skill** | Player gets better |
105 | **Power** | Character gets stronger |
106 | **Content** | New areas unlock |
107 | **Story** | Narrative advances |
108 
109 ### Pacing Principles
110 
111 - Early wins (hook quickly)
112 - Gradually increase challenge
113 - Rest beats between intensity
114 - Meaningful choices
115 
116 ---
117 
118 ## 6. Anti-Patterns
119 
120 | ‚ùå Don't | ‚úÖ Do |
121 |----------|-------|
122 | Design in isolation | Playtest constantly |
123 | Polish before fun | Prototype first |
124 | Force one way to play | Allow player expression |
125 | Punish excessively | Reward progress |
126 
127 ---
128 
129 > **Remember:** Fun is discovered through iteration, not designed on paper.
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F89 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F90 path:skills/game-development/mobile-games/SKILL.md hash:43db8fb50830a99fb14ace08cb29cc60cd7f51a240c5ae73dbe5b31da704f24f lines:108 ===
001 ---
002 name: mobile-games
003 description: Mobile game development principles. Touch input, battery, performance, app stores.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Write, Edit, Glob, Grep
005 ---
006 
007 # Mobile Game Development
008 
009 > Platform constraints and optimization principles.
010 
011 ---
012 
013 ## 1. Platform Considerations
014 
015 ### Key Constraints
016 
017 | Constraint | Strategy |
018 |------------|----------|
019 | **Touch input** | Large hit areas, gestures |
020 | **Battery** | Limit CPU/GPU usage |
021 | **Thermal** | Throttle when hot |
022 | **Screen size** | Responsive UI |
023 | **Interruptions** | Pause on background |
024 
025 ---
026 
027 ## 2. Touch Input Principles
028 
029 ### Touch vs Controller
030 
031 | Touch | Desktop/Console |
032 |-------|-----------------|
033 | Imprecise | Precise |
034 | Occludes screen | No occlusion |
035 | Limited buttons | Many buttons |
036 | Gestures available | Buttons/sticks |
037 
038 ### Best Practices
039 
040 - Minimum touch target: 44x44 points
041 - Visual feedback on touch
042 - Avoid precise timing requirements
043 - Support both portrait and landscape
044 
045 ---
046 
047 ## 3. Performance Targets
048 
049 ### Thermal Management
050 
051 | Action | Trigger |
052 |--------|---------|
053 | Reduce quality | Device warm |
054 | Limit FPS | Device hot |
055 | Pause effects | Critical temp |
056 
057 ### Battery Optimization
058 
059 - 30 FPS often sufficient
060 - Sleep when paused
061 - Minimize GPS/network
062 - Dark mode saves OLED battery
063 
064 ---
065 
066 ## 4. App Store Requirements
067 
068 ### iOS (App Store)
069 
070 | Requirement | Note |
071 |-------------|------|
072 | Privacy labels | Required |
073 | Account deletion | If account creation exists |
074 | Screenshots | For all device sizes |
075 
076 ### Android (Google Play)
077 
078 | Requirement | Note |
079 |-------------|------|
080 | Target API | Current year's SDK |
081 | 64-bit | Required |
082 | App bundles | Recommended |
083 
084 ---
085 
086 ## 5. Monetization Models
087 
088 | Model | Best For |
089 |-------|----------|
090 | **Premium** | Quality games, loyal audience |
091 | **Free + IAP** | Casual, progression-based |
092 | **Ads** | Hyper-casual, high volume |
093 | **Subscription** | Content updates, multiplayer |
094 
095 ---
096 
097 ## 6. Anti-Patterns
098 
099 | ‚ùå Don't | ‚úÖ Do |
100 |----------|-------|
101 | Desktop controls on mobile | Design for touch |
102 | Ignore battery drain | Monitor thermals |
103 | Force landscape | Support player preference |
104 | Always-on network | Cache and sync |
105 
106 ---
107 
108 > **Remember:** Mobile is the most constrained platform. Respect battery and attention.
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F90 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F91 path:skills/game-development/multiplayer/SKILL.md hash:79ee8d6f2e04a993b6cdf5eb251590051427cc4e09aa3a7f67f1ab8e61e205f5 lines:132 ===
001 ---
002 name: multiplayer
003 description: Multiplayer game development principles. Architecture, networking, synchronization.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Write, Edit, Glob, Grep, Bash
005 ---
006 
007 # Multiplayer Game Development
008 
009 > Networking architecture and synchronization principles.
010 
011 ---
012 
013 ## 1. Architecture Selection
014 
015 ### Decision Tree
016 
017 ```
018 What type of multiplayer?
019 ‚îÇ
020 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Competitive / Real-time
021 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Dedicated Server (authoritative)
022 ‚îÇ
023 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Cooperative / Casual
024 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Host-based (one player is server)
025 ‚îÇ
026 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Turn-based
027 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Client-server (simple)
028 ‚îÇ
029 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Massive (MMO)
030     ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Distributed servers
031 ```
032 
033 ### Comparison
034 
035 | Architecture | Latency | Cost | Security |
036 |--------------|---------|------|----------|
037 | **Dedicated** | Low | High | Strong |
038 | **P2P** | Variable | Low | Weak |
039 | **Host-based** | Medium | Low | Medium |
040 
041 ---
042 
043 ## 2. Synchronization Principles
044 
045 ### State vs Input
046 
047 | Approach | Sync What | Best For |
048 |----------|-----------|----------|
049 | **State Sync** | Game state | Simple, few objects |
050 | **Input Sync** | Player inputs | Action games |
051 | **Hybrid** | Both | Most games |
052 
053 ### Lag Compensation
054 
055 | Technique | Purpose |
056 |-----------|---------|
057 | **Prediction** | Client predicts server |
058 | **Interpolation** | Smooth remote players |
059 | **Reconciliation** | Fix mispredictions |
060 | **Lag compensation** | Rewind for hit detection |
061 
062 ---
063 
064 ## 3. Network Optimization
065 
066 ### Bandwidth Reduction
067 
068 | Technique | Savings |
069 |-----------|---------|
070 | **Delta compression** | Send only changes |
071 | **Quantization** | Reduce precision |
072 | **Priority** | Important data first |
073 | **Area of interest** | Only nearby entities |
074 
075 ### Update Rates
076 
077 | Type | Rate |
078 |------|------|
079 | Position | 20-60 Hz |
080 | Health | On change |
081 | Inventory | On change |
082 | Chat | On send |
083 
084 ---
085 
086 ## 4. Security Principles
087 
088 ### Server Authority
089 
090 ```
091 Client: "I hit the enemy"
092 Server: Validate ‚Üí did projectile actually hit?
093          ‚Üí was player in valid state?
094          ‚Üí was timing possible?
095 ```
096 
097 ### Anti-Cheat
098 
099 | Cheat | Prevention |
100 |-------|------------|
101 | Speed hack | Server validates movement |
102 | Aimbot | Server validates sight line |
103 | Item dupe | Server owns inventory |
104 | Wall hack | Don't send hidden data |
105 
106 ---
107 
108 ## 5. Matchmaking
109 
110 ### Considerations
111 
112 | Factor | Impact |
113 |--------|--------|
114 | **Skill** | Fair matches |
115 | **Latency** | Playable connection |
116 | **Wait time** | Player patience |
117 | **Party size** | Group play |
118 
119 ---
120 
121 ## 6. Anti-Patterns
122 
123 | ‚ùå Don't | ‚úÖ Do |
124 |----------|-------|
125 | Trust the client | Server is authority |
126 | Send everything | Send only necessary |
127 | Ignore latency | Design for 100-200ms |
128 | Sync exact positions | Interpolate/predict |
129 
130 ---
131 
132 > **Remember:** Never trust the client. The server is the source of truth.
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F91 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F92 path:skills/game-development/pc-games/SKILL.md hash:739b244b02659ec53ca719bbdf8ac2684dbeeafc5d5ddac124ffa6407f10f5df lines:144 ===
001 ---
002 name: pc-games
003 description: PC and console game development principles. Engine selection, platform features, optimization strategies.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Write, Edit, Glob, Grep

006 
007 # PC/Console Game Development
008 
009 > Engine selection and platform-specific principles.
010 
011 ---
012 
013 ## 1. Engine Selection
014 
015 ### Decision Tree
016 
017 ```
018 What are you building?
019 ‚îÇ
020 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ 2D Game
021 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Open source important? ‚Üí Godot
022 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Large team/assets? ‚Üí Unity
023 ‚îÇ
024 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ 3D Game
025 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ AAA visual quality? ‚Üí Unreal
026 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Cross-platform priority? ‚Üí Unity
027 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Indie/open source? ‚Üí Godot 4
028 ‚îÇ
029 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Specific Needs
030     ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ DOTS performance? ‚Üí Unity
031     ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Nanite/Lumen? ‚Üí Unreal
032     ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Lightweight? ‚Üí Godot
033 ```
034 
035 ### Comparison
036 
037 | Factor | Unity 6 | Godot 4 | Unreal 5 |
038 |--------|---------|---------|----------|
039 | 2D | Good | Excellent | Limited |
040 | 3D | Good | Good | Excellent |
041 | Learning | Medium | Easy | Hard |
042 | Cost | Revenue share | Free | 5% after $1M |
043 | Team | Any | Solo-Medium | Medium-Large |
044 
045 ---
046 
047 ## 2. Platform Features
048 
049 ### Steam Integration
050 
051 | Feature | Purpose |
052 |---------|---------|
053 | Achievements | Player goals |
054 | Cloud Saves | Cross-device progress |
055 | Leaderboards | Competition |
056 | Workshop | User mods |
057 | Rich Presence | Show in-game status |
058 
059 ### Console Requirements
060 
061 | Platform | Certification |
062 |----------|--------------|
063 | PlayStation | TRC compliance |
064 | Xbox | XR compliance |
065 | Nintendo | Lotcheck |
066 
067 ---
068 
069 ## 3. Controller Support
070 
071 ### Input Abstraction
072 
073 ```
074 Map ACTIONS, not buttons:
075 - "confirm" ‚Üí A (Xbox), Cross (PS), B (Nintendo)
076 - "cancel" ‚Üí B (Xbox), Circle (PS), A (Nintendo)
077 ```
078 
079 ### Haptic Feedback
080 
081 | Intensity | Use |
082 |-----------|-----|
083 | Light | UI feedback |
084 | Medium | Impacts |
085 | Heavy | Major events |
086 
087 ---
088 
089 ## 4. Performance Optimization
090 
091 ### Profiling First
092 
093 | Engine | Tool |
094 |--------|------|
095 | Unity | Profiler Window |
096 | Godot | Debugger ‚Üí Profiler |
097 | Unreal | Unreal Insights |
098 
099 ### Common Bottlenecks
100 
101 | Bottleneck | Solution |
102 |------------|----------|
103 | Draw calls | Batching, atlases |
104 | GC spikes | Object pooling |
105 | Physics | Simpler colliders |
106 | Shaders | LOD shaders |
107 
108 ---
109 
110 ## 5. Engine-Specific Principles
111 
112 ### Unity 6
113 
114 - DOTS for performance-critical systems
115 - Burst compiler for hot paths
116 - Addressables for asset streaming
117 
118 ### Godot 4
119 
120 - GDScript for rapid iteration
121 - C# for complex logic
122 - Signals for decoupling
123 
124 ### Unreal 5
125 
126 - Blueprint for designers
127 - C++ for performance
128 - Nanite for high-poly environments
129 - Lumen for dynamic lighting
130 
131 ---
132 
133 ## 6. Anti-Patterns
134 
135 | ‚ùå Don't | ‚úÖ Do |
136 |----------|-------|
137 | Choose engine by hype | Choose by project needs |
138 | Ignore platform guidelines | Study certification requirements |
139 | Hardcode input buttons | Abstract to actions |
140 | Skip profiling | Profile early and often |
141 
142 ---
143 
144 > **Remember:** Engine is a tool. Master the principles, then adapt to any engine.

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F93 path:skills/game-development/SKILL.md hash:994e2de3a8fd7dcd5caa8f08ddcb663d0d27cf161ddd5f74f88a441c0905189d lines:167 ===
001 ---
002 name: game-development
003 description: Game development orchestrator. Routes to platform-specific skills based on project needs.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Write, Edit, Glob, Grep, Bash
005 ---
006 
007 # Game Development
008 
009 > **Orchestrator skill** that provides core principles and routes to specialized sub-skills.
010 
011 ---
012 
013 ## When to Use This Skill
014 
015 You are working on a game development project. This skill teaches the PRINCIPLES of game development and directs you to the right sub-skill based on context.
016 
017 ---
018 
019 ## Sub-Skill Routing
020 
021 ### Platform Selection
022 
023 | If the game targets... | Use Sub-Skill |
024 |------------------------|---------------|
025 | Web browsers (HTML5, WebGL) | `game-development/web-games` |
026 | Mobile (iOS, Android) | `game-development/mobile-games` |
027 | PC (Steam, Desktop) | `game-development/pc-games` |
028 | VR/AR headsets | `game-development/vr-ar` |
029 
030 ### Dimension Selection
031 
032 | If the game is... | Use Sub-Skill |
033 |-------------------|---------------|
034 | 2D (sprites, tilemaps) | `game-development/2d-games` |
035 | 3D (meshes, shaders) | `game-development/3d-games` |
036 
037 ### Specialty Areas
038 
039 | If you need... | Use Sub-Skill |
040 |----------------|---------------|
041 | GDD, balancing, player psychology | `game-development/game-design` |
042 | Multiplayer, networking | `game-development/multiplayer` |
043 | Visual style, asset pipeline, animation | `game-development/game-art` |
044 | Sound design, music, adaptive audio | `game-development/game-audio` |
045 
046 ---
047 
048 ## Core Principles (All Platforms)
049 
050 ### 1. The Game Loop
051 
052 Every game, regardless of platform, follows this pattern:
053 
054 ```
055 INPUT  ‚Üí Read player actions
056 UPDATE ‚Üí Process game logic (fixed timestep)
057 RENDER ‚Üí Draw the frame (interpolated)
058 ```
059 
060 **Fixed Timestep Rule:**
061 - Physics/logic: Fixed rate (e.g., 50Hz)
062 - Rendering: As fast as possible
063 - Interpolate between states for smooth visuals
064 
065 ---
066 
067 ### 2. Pattern Selection Matrix
068 
069 | Pattern | Use When | Example |
070 |---------|----------|---------|
071 | **State Machine** | 3-5 discrete states | Player: Idle‚ÜíWalk‚ÜíJump |
072 | **Object Pooling** | Frequent spawn/destroy | Bullets, particles |
073 | **Observer/Events** | Cross-system communication | Health‚ÜíUI updates |
074 | **ECS** | Thousands of similar entities | RTS units, particles |
075 | **Command** | Undo, replay, networking | Input recording |
076 | **Behavior Tree** | Complex AI decisions | Enemy AI |
077 
078 **Decision Rule:** Start with State Machine. Add ECS only when performance demands.
079 
080 ---
081 
082 ### 3. Input Abstraction
083 
084 Abstract input into ACTIONS, not raw keys:
085 
086 ```
087 "jump"  ‚Üí Space, Gamepad A, Touch tap
088 "move"  ‚Üí WASD, Left stick, Virtual joystick
089 ```
090 
091 **Why:** Enables multi-platform, rebindable controls.
092 
093 ---
094 
095 ### 4. Performance Budget (60 FPS = 16.67ms)
096 
097 | System | Budget |
098 |--------|--------|
099 | Input | 1ms |
100 | Physics | 3ms |
101 | AI | 2ms |
102 | Game Logic | 4ms |
103 | Rendering | 5ms |
104 | Buffer | 1.67ms |
105 
106 **Optimization Priority:**
107 1. Algorithm (O(n¬≤) ‚Üí O(n log n))
108 2. Batching (reduce draw calls)
109 3. Pooling (avoid GC spikes)
110 4. LOD (detail by distance)
111 5. Culling (skip invisible)
112 
113 ---
114 
115 ### 5. AI Selection by Complexity
116 
117 | AI Type | Complexity | Use When |
118 |---------|------------|----------|
119 | **FSM** | Simple | 3-5 states, predictable behavior |
120 | **Behavior Tree** | Medium | Modular, designer-friendly |
121 | **GOAP** | High | Emergent, planning-based |
122 | **Utility AI** | High | Scoring-based decisions |
123 
124 ---
125 
126 ### 6. Collision Strategy
127 
128 | Type | Best For |
129 |------|----------|
130 | **AABB** | Rectangles, fast checks |
131 | **Circle** | Round objects, cheap |
132 | **Spatial Hash** | Many similar-sized objects |
133 | **Quadtree** | Large worlds, varying sizes |
134 
135 ---
136 
137 ## Anti-Patterns (Universal)
138 
139 | Don't | Do |
140 |-------|-----|
141 | Update everything every frame | Use events, dirty flags |
142 | Create objects in hot loops | Object pooling |
143 | Cache nothing | Cache references |
144 | Optimize without profiling | Profile first |
145 | Mix input with logic | Abstract input layer |
146 
147 ---
148 
149 ## Routing Examples
150 
151 ### Example 1: "I want to make a browser-based 2D platformer"
152 ‚Üí Start with `game-development/web-games` for framework selection
153 ‚Üí Then `game-development/2d-games` for sprite/tilemap patterns
154 ‚Üí Reference `game-development/game-design` for level design
155 
156 ### Example 2: "Mobile puzzle game for iOS and Android"
157 ‚Üí Start with `game-development/mobile-games` for touch input and stores
158 ‚Üí Use `game-development/game-design` for puzzle balancing
159 
160 ### Example 3: "Multiplayer VR shooter"
161 ‚Üí `game-development/vr-ar` for comfort and immersion
162 ‚Üí `game-development/3d-games` for rendering
163 ‚Üí `game-development/multiplayer` for networking
164 
165 ---
166 
167 > **Remember:** Great games come from iteration, not perfection. Prototype fast, then polish.
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F93 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F94 path:skills/game-development/vr-ar/SKILL.md hash:59ddbdecc4fa17e74c4747f5f02bd69edb8bffcd1cdc2866dd6a053e19bc139e lines:123 ===

006 
007 # VR/AR Development
008 
009 > Immersive experience principles.
010 
011 ---
012 
013 ## 1. Platform Selection
014 
015 ### VR Platforms
016 
017 | Platform | Use Case |
018 |----------|----------|
019 | **Quest** | Standalone, wireless |
020 | **PCVR** | High fidelity |
021 | **PSVR** | Console market |
022 | **WebXR** | Browser-based |
023 
024 ### AR Platforms
025 
026 | Platform | Use Case |
027 |----------|----------|
028 | **ARKit** | iOS devices |
029 | **ARCore** | Android devices |
030 | **WebXR** | Browser AR |
031 | **HoloLens** | Enterprise |
032 
033 ---
034 
035 ## 2. Comfort Principles
036 
037 ### Motion Sickness Prevention
038 
039 | Cause | Solution |
040 |-------|----------|
041 | **Locomotion** | Teleport, snap turn |
042 | **Low FPS** | Maintain 90 FPS |
043 | **Camera shake** | Avoid or minimize |
044 | **Rapid acceleration** | Gradual movement |
045 
046 ### Comfort Settings
047 
048 - Vignette during movement
049 - Snap vs smooth turning
050 - Seated vs standing modes
051 - Height calibration
052 
053 ---
054 
055 ## 3. Performance Requirements
056 
057 ### Target Metrics
058 
059 | Platform | FPS | Resolution |
060 |----------|-----|------------|
061 | Quest 2 | 72-90 | 1832x1920 |
062 | Quest 3 | 90-120 | 2064x2208 |
063 | PCVR | 90 | 2160x2160+ |
064 | PSVR2 | 90-120 | 2000x2040 |
065 
066 ### Frame Budget
067 
068 - VR requires consistent frame times
069 - Single dropped frame = visible judder
070 - 90 FPS = 11.11ms budget
071 
072 ---
073 
074 ## 4. Interaction Principles
075 
076 ### Controller Interaction
077 
078 | Type | Use |
079 |------|-----|
080 | **Point + click** | UI, distant objects |
081 | **Grab** | Manipulation |
082 | **Gesture** | Magic, special actions |
083 | **Physical** | Throwing, swinging |
084 
085 ### Hand Tracking
086 
087 - More immersive but less precise
088 - Good for: social, casual
089 - Challenging for: action, precision
090 
091 ---
092 
093 ## 5. Spatial Design
094 
095 ### World Scale
096 
097 - 1 unit = 1 meter (critical)
098 - Objects must feel right size
099 - Test with real measurements
100 
101 ### Depth Cues
102 
103 | Cue | Importance |
104 |-----|------------|
105 | Stereo | Primary depth |
106 | Motion parallax | Secondary |
107 | Shadows | Grounding |
108 | Occlusion | Layering |
109 
110 ---
111 
112 ## 6. Anti-Patterns
113 
114 | ‚ùå Don't | ‚úÖ Do |
115 |----------|-------|
116 | Move camera without player | Player controls camera |
117 | Drop below 90 FPS | Maintain frame rate |
118 | Use tiny UI text | Large, readable text |
119 | Ignore arm length | Scale to player reach |
120 
121 ---
122 
123 > **Remember:** Comfort is not optional. Sick players don't play.
