001 ---
002 name: web-games
003 description: Web browser game development principles. Framework selection, WebGPU, optimization, PWA.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Write, Edit, Glob, Grep
005 ---
006 
007 # Web Browser Game Development
008 
009 > Framework selection and browser-specific principles.
010 
011 ---
012 
013 ## 1. Framework Selection
014 
015 ### Decision Tree
016 
017 ```
018 What type of game?
019 ‚îÇ
020 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ 2D Game
021 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Full game engine features? ‚Üí Phaser
022 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Raw rendering power? ‚Üí PixiJS
023 ‚îÇ
024 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ 3D Game
025 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Full engine (physics, XR)? ‚Üí Babylon.js
026 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Rendering focused? ‚Üí Three.js
027 ‚îÇ
028 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Hybrid / Canvas
029     ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Custom ‚Üí Raw Canvas/WebGL
030 ```
031 
032 ### Comparison (2025)
033 
034 | Framework | Type | Best For |
035 |-----------|------|----------|
036 | **Phaser 4** | 2D | Full game features |
037 | **PixiJS 8** | 2D | Rendering, UI |
038 | **Three.js** | 3D | Visualizations, lightweight |
039 | **Babylon.js 7** | 3D | Full engine, XR |
040 
041 ---
042 
043 ## 2. WebGPU Adoption
044 
045 ### Browser Support (2025)
046 
047 | Browser | Support |
048 |---------|---------|
049 | Chrome | ‚úÖ Since v113 |
050 | Edge | ‚úÖ Since v113 |
051 | Firefox | ‚úÖ Since v131 |
052 | Safari | ‚úÖ Since 18.0 |
053 | **Total** | **~73%** global |
054 
055 ### Decision
056 
057 - **New projects**: Use WebGPU with WebGL fallback
058 - **Legacy support**: Start with WebGL
059 - **Feature detection**: Check `navigator.gpu`
060 
061 ---
062 
063 ## 3. Performance Principles
064 
065 ### Browser Constraints
066 
067 | Constraint | Strategy |
068 |------------|----------|
069 | No local file access | Asset bundling, CDN |
070 | Tab throttling | Pause when hidden |
071 | Mobile data limits | Compress assets |
072 | Audio autoplay | Require user interaction |
073 
074 ### Optimization Priority
075 
076 1. **Asset compression** - KTX2, Draco, WebP
077 2. **Lazy loading** - Load on demand
078 3. **Object pooling** - Avoid GC
079 4. **Draw call batching** - Reduce state changes
080 5. **Web Workers** - Offload heavy computation
081 
082 ---
083 
084 ## 4. Asset Strategy
085 
086 ### Compression Formats
087 
088 | Type | Format |
089 |------|--------|
090 | Textures | KTX2 + Basis Universal |
091 | Audio | WebM/Opus (fallback: MP3) |
092 | 3D Models | glTF + Draco/Meshopt |
093 
094 ### Loading Strategy
095 
096 | Phase | Load |
097 |-------|------|
098 | Startup | Core assets, <2MB |
099 | Gameplay | Stream on demand |
100 | Background | Prefetch next level |
101 
102 ---
103 
104 ## 5. PWA for Games
105 
106 ### Benefits
107 
108 - Offline play
109 - Install to home screen
110 - Full screen mode
111 - Push notifications
112 
113 ### Requirements
114 
115 - Service worker for caching
116 - Web app manifest
117 - HTTPS
118 
119 ---
120 
121 ## 6. Audio Handling
122 
123 ### Browser Requirements
124 
125 - Audio context requires user interaction
126 - Create AudioContext on first click/tap
127 - Resume context if suspended
128 
129 ### Best Practices
130 
131 - Use Web Audio API
132 - Pool audio sources
133 - Preload common sounds
134 - Compress with WebM/Opus
135 
136 ---
137 
138 ## 7. Anti-Patterns
139 
140 | ‚ùå Don't | ‚úÖ Do |
141 |----------|-------|
142 | Load all assets upfront | Progressive loading |
143 | Ignore tab visibility | Pause when hidden |
144 | Block on audio load | Lazy load audio |
145 | Skip compression | Compress everything |
146 | Assume fast connection | Handle slow networks |
147 
148 ---
149 
150 > **Remember:** Browser is the most accessible platform. Respect its constraints.

022

046

086 - [ ] Person schema for author
087 - [ ] FAQPage schema
088 - [ ] Fast loading (< 2.5s)
089 - [ ] Clean HTML structure

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F97 path:skills/i18n-localization/SKILL.md hash:1509cf8dc323307ffec7288f185414226862a400c3ef2617c62fdd77ee4cb8f9 lines:154 ===
001 ---
002 name: i18n-localization
003 description: Internationalization and localization patterns. Detecting hardcoded strings, managing translations, locale files, RTL support.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Glob, Grep
005 ---
006 
007 # i18n & Localization
008 
009 > Internationalization (i18n) and Localization (L10n) best practices.
010 
011 ---
012 
013 ## 1. Core Concepts
014 
015 | Term | Meaning |
016 |------|---------|
017 | **i18n** | Internationalization - making app translatable |
018 | **L10n** | Localization - actual translations |
019 | **Locale** | Language + Region (en-US, tr-TR) |
020 | **RTL** | Right-to-left languages (Arabic, Hebrew) |
021 
022 ---
023 
024 ## 2. When to Use i18n
025 
026 | Project Type | i18n Needed? |
027 |--------------|--------------|
028 | Public web app | ‚úÖ Yes |
029 | SaaS product | ‚úÖ Yes |
030 | Internal tool | ‚ö†Ô∏è Maybe |
031 | Single-region app | ‚ö†Ô∏è Consider future |
032 | Personal project | ‚ùå Optional |
033 
034 ---
035 
036 ## 3. Implementation Patterns
037 
038 ### React (react-i18next)
039 
040 ```tsx
041 import { useTranslation } from 'react-i18next';
042 
043 function Welcome() {
044   const { t } = useTranslation();
045   return <h1>{t('welcome.title')}</h1>;
046 }
047 ```
048 
049 ### Next.js (next-intl)
050 
051 ```tsx
052 import { useTranslations } from 'next-intl';
053 
054 export default function Page() {
055   const t = useTranslations('Home');
056   return <h1>{t('title')}</h1>;
057 }
058 ```
059 
060 ### Python (gettext)
061 
062 ```python
063 from gettext import gettext as _
064 
065 print(_("Welcome to our app"))
066 ```
067 
068 ---
069 
070 ## 4. File Structure
071 
072 ```
073 locales/
074 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ en/
075 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ common.json
076 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ auth.json
077 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ errors.json
078 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ tr/
079 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ common.json
080 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ auth.json
081 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ errors.json
082 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ ar/          # RTL
083     ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ ...
084 ```
085 
086 ---
087 
088 ## 5. Best Practices
089 
090 ### DO ‚úÖ
091 
092 - Use translation keys, not raw text
093 - Namespace translations by feature
094 - Support pluralization
095 - Handle date/number formats per locale
096 - Plan for RTL from the start
097 - Use ICU message format for complex strings
098 
099 ### DON'T ‚ùå
100 
101 - Hardcode strings in components
102 - Concatenate translated strings
103 - Assume text length (German is 30% longer)
104 - Forget about RTL layout
105 - Mix languages in same file
106 
107 ---
108 
109 ## 6. Common Issues
110 
111 | Issue | Solution |
112 |-------|----------|
113 | Missing translation | Fallback to default language |
114 | Hardcoded strings | Use linter/checker script |
115 | Date format | Use Intl.DateTimeFormat |
116 | Number format | Use Intl.NumberFormat |
117 | Pluralization | Use ICU message format |
118 
119 ---
120 
121 ## 7. RTL Support
122 
123 ```css
124 /* CSS Logical Properties */
125 .container {
126   margin-inline-start: 1rem;  /* Not margin-left */
127   padding-inline-end: 1rem;   /* Not padding-right */
128 }
129 
130 [dir="rtl"] .icon {
131   transform: scaleX(-1);
132 }
133 ```
134 
135 ---
136 
137 ## 8. Checklist
138 
139 Before shipping:
140 
141 - [ ] All user-facing strings use translation keys
142 - [ ] Locale files exist for all supported languages
143 - [ ] Date/number formatting uses Intl API
144 - [ ] RTL layout tested (if applicable)
145 - [ ] Fallback language configured
146 - [ ] No hardcoded strings in components
147 
148 ---
149 
150 ## Script
151 
152 | Script | Purpose | Command |
153 |--------|---------|---------|
154 | `scripts/i18n_checker.py` | Detect hardcoded strings & missing translations | `python scripts/i18n_checker.py <project_path>` |

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F98 path:skills/intelligent-routing/SKILL.md hash:b0da558d5cbd5c44de0e9af8db8d9301a3b6e5595594d2fc0b2341deaefaf908 lines:335 ===
001 ---
002 name: intelligent-routing
003 description: Automatic agent selection and intelligent task routing. Analyzes user requests and automatically selects the best specialist agent(s) without requiring explicit user mentions.
004 version: 1.0.0
005 ---
006 
007 # Intelligent Agent Routing
008 
009 **Purpose**: Automatically analyze user requests and route them to the most appropriate specialist agent(s) without requiring explicit user mentions.
010 
011 ## Core Principle
012 
013 > **The AI should act as an intelligent Project Manager**, analyzing each request and automatically selecting the best specialist(s) for the job.
014 
015 ## How It Works
016 
017 ### 1. Request Analysis
018 
019 Before responding to ANY user request, perform automatic analysis:
020 
021 ```mermaid
022 graph TD
023     A[User Request: Add login] --> B[ANALYZE]
024     B --> C[Keywords]
025     B --> D[Domains]
026     B --> E[Complexity]
027     C --> F[SELECT AGENT]
028     D --> F
029     E --> F
030     F --> G[security-auditor + backend-specialist]
031     G --> H[AUTO-INVOKE with context]
032 ```
033 
034 ### 2. Agent Selection Matrix
035 
036 **Use this matrix to automatically select agents:**
037 
038 | User Intent         | Keywords                                   | Selected Agent(s)                           | Auto-invoke? |
039 | ------------------- | ------------------------------------------ | ------------------------------------------- | ------------ |
040 | **Authentication**  | "login", "auth", "signup", "password"      | `security-auditor` + `backend-specialist`   | ‚úÖ YES       |
041 | **UI Component**    | "button", "card", "layout", "style"        | `frontend-specialist`                       | ‚úÖ YES       |
042 | **Mobile UI**       | "screen", "navigation", "touch", "gesture" | `mobile-developer`                          | ‚úÖ YES       |
043 | **API Endpoint**    | "endpoint", "route", "API", "POST", "GET"  | `backend-specialist`                        | ‚úÖ YES       |
044 | **Database**        | "schema", "migration", "query", "table"    | `database-architect` + `backend-specialist` | ‚úÖ YES       |
045 | **Bug Fix**         | "error", "bug", "not working", "broken"    | `debugger`                                  | ‚úÖ YES       |
046 | **Test**            | "test", "coverage", "unit", "e2e"          | `test-engineer`                             | ‚úÖ YES       |
047 | **Deployment**      | "deploy", "production", "CI/CD", "docker"  | `devops-engineer`                           | ‚úÖ YES       |
048 | **Security Review** | "security", "vulnerability", "exploit"     | `security-auditor` + `penetration-tester`   | ‚úÖ YES       |
049 | **Performance**     | "slow", "optimize", "performance", "speed" | `performance-optimizer`                     | ‚úÖ YES       |
050 | **Product Def**     | "requirements", "user story", "backlog", "MVP" | `product-owner`                             | ‚úÖ YES       |
051 | **New Feature**     | "build", "create", "implement", "new app"  | `orchestrator` ‚Üí multi-agent                | ‚ö†Ô∏è ASK FIRST |
052 | **Complex Task**    | Multiple domains detected                  | `orchestrator` ‚Üí multi-agent                | ‚ö†Ô∏è ASK FIRST |
053 
054 ### 3. Automatic Routing Protocol
055 
056 ## TIER 0 - Automatic Analysis (ALWAYS ACTIVE)
057 
058 Before responding to ANY request:
059 
060 ```javascript
061 // Pseudo-code for decision tree
062 function analyzeRequest(userMessage) {
063     // 1. Classify request type
064     const requestType = classifyRequest(userMessage);
065 
066     // 2. Detect domains
067     const domains = detectDomains(userMessage);
068 
069     // 3. Determine complexity
070     const complexity = assessComplexity(domains);
071 
072     // 4. Select agent(s)
073     if (complexity === "SIMPLE" && domains.length === 1) {
074         return selectSingleAgent(domains[0]);
075     } else if (complexity === "MODERATE" && domains.length <= 2) {
076         return selectMultipleAgents(domains);
077     } else {
078         return "orchestrator"; // Complex task
079     }
080 }
081 ```
082 
083 ## 4. Response Format
084 
085 **When auto-selecting an agent, inform the user concisely:**
086 
087 ```markdown
088 ü§ñ **Applying knowledge of `@security-auditor` + `@backend-specialist`...**
089 
090 [Proceed with specialized response]
091 ```
092 
093 **Benefits:**
094 
095 - ‚úÖ User sees which expertise is being applied
096 - ‚úÖ Transparent decision-making
097 - ‚úÖ Still automatic (no /commands needed)
098 
099 ## Domain Detection Rules
100 
101 ### Single-Domain Tasks (Auto-invoke Single Agent)
102 
103 | Domain          | Patterns                                   | Agent                   |
104 | --------------- | ------------------------------------------ | ----------------------- |
105 | **Security**    | auth, login, jwt, password, hash, token    | `security-auditor`      |
106 | **Frontend**    | component, react, vue, css, html, tailwind | `frontend-specialist`   |
107 | **Backend**     | api, server, express, fastapi, node        | `backend-specialist`    |
108 | **Mobile**      | react native, flutter, ios, android, expo  | `mobile-developer`      |
109 | **Database**    | prisma, sql, mongodb, schema, migration    | `database-architect`    |
110 | **Testing**     | test, jest, vitest, playwright, cypress    | `test-engineer`         |
111 | **DevOps**      | docker, kubernetes, ci/cd, pm2, nginx      | `devops-engineer`       |
112 | **Debug**       | error, bug, crash, not working, issue      | `debugger`              |
113 | **Performance** | slow, lag, optimize, cache, performance    | `performance-optimizer` |
114 | **SEO**         | seo, meta, analytics, sitemap, robots      | `seo-specialist`        |
115 | **Game**        | unity, godot, phaser, game, multiplayer    | `game-developer`        |
116 
117 ### Multi-Domain Tasks (Auto-invoke Orchestrator)
118 
119 If request matches **2+ domains from different categories**, automatically use `orchestrator`:
120 
121 ```text
122 Example: "Create a secure login system with dark mode UI"
123 ‚Üí Detected: Security + Frontend
124 ‚Üí Auto-invoke: orchestrator
125 ‚Üí Orchestrator will handle: security-auditor, frontend-specialist, test-engineer
126 ```
127 
128 ## Complexity Assessment
129 
130 ### SIMPLE (Direct agent invocation)
131 
132 - Single file edit
133 - Clear, specific task
134 - One domain only
135 - Example: "Fix the login button style"
136 
137 **Action**: Auto-invoke respective agent
138 
139 ### MODERATE (2-3 agents)
140 
141 - 2-3 files affected
142 - Clear requirements
143 - 2 domains max
144 - Example: "Add API endpoint for user profile"
145 
146 **Action**: Auto-invoke relevant agents sequentially
147 
148 ### COMPLEX (Orchestrator required)
149 
150 - Multiple files/domains
151 - Architectural decisions needed
152 - Unclear requirements
153 - Example: "Build a social media app"
154 
155 **Action**: Auto-invoke `orchestrator` ‚Üí will ask Socratic questions
156 
157 ## Implementation Rules
158 
159 ### Rule 1: Silent Analysis
160 
161 #### DO NOT announce "I'm analyzing your request..."
162 
163 - ‚úÖ Analyze silently
164 - ‚úÖ Inform which agent is being applied
165 - ‚ùå Avoid verbose meta-commentary
166 
167 ### Rule 2: Inform Agent Selection
168 
169 **DO inform which expertise is being applied:**
170 
171 ```markdown
172 ü§ñ **Applying knowledge of `@frontend-specialist`...**
173 
174 I will create the component with the following characteristics:
175 [Continue with specialized response]
176 ```
177 
178 ### Rule 3: Seamless Experience
179 
180 **The user should not notice a difference from talking to the right specialist directly.**
181 
182 ### Rule 4: Override Capability
183 
184 **User can still explicitly mention agents:**
185 
186 ```text
187 User: "Use @backend-specialist to review this"
188 ‚Üí Override auto-selection
189 ‚Üí Use explicitly mentioned agent
190 ```
191 
192 ## Edge Cases
193 
194 ### Case 1: Generic Question
195 
196 ```text
197 User: "How does React work?"
198 ‚Üí Type: QUESTION
199 ‚Üí No agent needed
200 ‚Üí Respond directly with explanation
201 ```
202 
203 ### Case 2: Extremely Vague Request
204 
205 ```text
206 User: "Make it better"
207 ‚Üí Complexity: UNCLEAR
208 ‚Üí Action: Ask clarifying questions first
209 ‚Üí Then route to appropriate agent
210 ```
211 
212 ### Case 3: Contradictory Patterns
213 
214 ```text
215 User: "Add mobile support to the web app"
216 ‚Üí Conflict: mobile vs web
217 ‚Üí Action: Ask: "Do you want responsive web or native mobile app?"
218 ‚Üí Then route accordingly
219 ```
220 
221 ## Integration with Existing Workflows
222 
223 ### With /orchestrate Command
224 
225 - **User types `/orchestrate`**: Explicit orchestration mode
226 - **AI detects complex task**: Auto-invoke orchestrator (same result)
227 
228 **Difference**: User doesn't need to know the command exists.
229 
230 ### With Socratic Gate
231 
232 - **Auto-routing does NOT bypass Socratic Gate**
233 - If task is unclear, still ask questions first
234 - Then route to appropriate agent
235 
236 ### With GEMINI.md Rules
237 
238 - **Priority**: GEMINI.md rules > intelligent-routing
239 - If GEMINI.md specifies explicit routing, follow it
240 - Intelligent routing is the DEFAULT when no explicit rule exists
241 
242 ## Testing the System
243 
244 ### Test Cases
245 
246 #### Test 1: Simple Frontend Task
247 
248 ```text
249 User: "Create a dark mode toggle button"
250 Expected: Auto-invoke frontend-specialist
251 Verify: Response shows "Using @frontend-specialist"
252 ```
253 
254 #### Test 2: Security Task
255 
256 ```text
257 User: "Review the authentication flow for vulnerabilities"
258 Expected: Auto-invoke security-auditor
259 Verify: Security-focused analysis
260 ```
261 
262 #### Test 3: Complex Multi-Domain
263 
264 ```text
265 User: "Build a chat application with real-time notifications"
266 Expected: Auto-invoke orchestrator
267 Verify: Multiple agents coordinated (backend, frontend, test)
268 ```
269 
270 #### Test 4: Bug Fix
271 
272 ```text
273 User: "Login is not working, getting 401 error"
274 Expected: Auto-invoke debugger
275 Verify: Systematic debugging approach
276 ```
277 
278 ## Performance Considerations
279 
280 ### Token Usage
281 
282 - Analysis adds ~50-100 tokens per request
283 - Tradeoff: Better accuracy vs slight overhead
284 - Overall SAVES tokens by reducing back-and-forth
285 
286 ### Response Time
287 
288 - Analysis is instant (pattern matching)
289 - No additional API calls required
290 - Agent selection happens before first response
291 
292 ## User Education
293 
294 ### Optional: First-Time Explanation
295 
296 If this is the first interaction in a project:
297 
298 ```markdown
299 üí° **Tip**: I am configured with automatic specialist agent selection.
300 I will always choose the most suitable specialist for your task. You can
301 still mention agents explicitly with `@agent-name` if you prefer.
302 ```
303 
304 ## Debugging Agent Selection
305 
306 ### Enable Debug Mode (for development)
307 
308 Add to GEMINI.md temporarily:
309 
310 ```markdown
311 ## DEBUG: Intelligent Routing
312 
313 Show selection reasoning:
314 
315 - Detected domains: [list]
316 - Selected agent: [name]
317 - Reasoning: [why]
318 ```
319 
320 ## Summary
321 
322 **intelligent-routing skill enables:**
323 
324 ‚úÖ Zero-command operation (no need for `/orchestrate`)
325 ‚úÖ Automatic specialist selection based on request analysis
326 ‚úÖ Transparent communication of which expertise is being applied
327 ‚úÖ Seamless integration with existing workflows
328 ‚úÖ Override capability for explicit agent mentions
329 ‚úÖ Fallback to orchestrator for complex tasks
330 
331 **Result**: User gets specialist-level responses without needing to know the system architecture.
332

334 
335 **Next Steps**: Integrate this skill into GEMINI.md TIER 0 rules.

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F99 path:skills/lint-and-validate/SKILL.md hash:00497ead822be9f5dc871ab48dfba38a19f1a04cc77e5fdee77898a2a7e2e88f lines:45 ===
001 ---
002 name: lint-and-validate
003 description: Automatic quality control, linting, and static analysis procedures. Use after every code modification to ensure syntax correctness and project standards. Triggers onKeywords: lint, format, check, validate, types, static analysis.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Glob, Grep, Bash
005 ---
006 
007 # Lint and Validate Skill
008 
009 > **MANDATORY:** Run appropriate validation tools after EVERY code change. Do not finish a task until the code is error-free.
010 
011 ### Procedures by Ecosystem
012 
013 #### Node.js / TypeScript
014 1. **Lint/Fix:** `npm run lint` or `npx eslint "path" --fix`
015 2. **Types:** `npx tsc --noEmit`
016 3. **Security:** `npm audit --audit-level=high`
017 
018 #### Python
019 1. **Linter (Ruff):** `ruff check "path" --fix` (Fast & Modern)
020 2. **Security (Bandit):** `bandit -r "path" -ll`
021 3. **Types (MyPy):** `mypy "path"`
022 
023 ## The Quality Loop
024 1. **Write/Edit Code**
025 2. **Run Audit:** `npm run lint && npx tsc --noEmit`
026 3. **Analyze Report:** Check the "FINAL AUDIT REPORT" section.
027 4. **Fix & Repeat:** Submitting code with "FINAL AUDIT" failures is NOT allowed.
028 
029 ## Error Handling
030 - If `lint` fails: Fix the style or syntax issues immediately.
031 - If `tsc` fails: Correct type mismatches before proceeding.
032 - If no tool is configured: Check the project root for `.eslintrc`, `tsconfig.json`, `pyproject.toml` and suggest creating one.
033 
034 ---
035 **Strict Rule:** No code should be committed or reported as "done" without passing these checks.
036 
037 ---
038 
039 ## Scripts
040 
041 | Script | Purpose | Command |
042 |--------|---------|---------|
043 | `scripts/lint_runner.py` | Unified lint check | `python scripts/lint_runner.py <project_path>` |
044 | `scripts/type_coverage.py` | Type coverage analysis | `python scripts/type_coverage.py <project_path>` |
045

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F100 path:skills/mcp-builder/SKILL.md hash:d13eb1291ed76e0375b43d434e4676e4802264501a48ddeddcc961324133567a lines:176 ===
001 ---
002 name: mcp-builder

004 allowed-tools: Read, Write, Edit, Glob, Grep
005 ---
006 
007 # MCP Builder
008 
009 > Principles for building MCP servers.
010 
011 ---
012 
013 ## 1. MCP Overview
014 
015 ### What is MCP?
016 
017 Model Context Protocol - standard for connecting AI systems with external tools and data sources.
018 
019 ### Core Concepts
020 
021 | Concept | Purpose |
022 |---------|---------|
023 | **Tools** | Functions AI can call |
024 | **Resources** | Data AI can read |
025 | **Prompts** | Pre-defined prompt templates |
026 
027 ---
028 
029 ## 2. Server Architecture
030 
031 ### Project Structure
032 
033 ```
034 my-mcp-server/
035 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ src/
036 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ index.ts      # Main entry
037 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ package.json
038 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ tsconfig.json
039 ```
040 
041 ### Transport Types
042 
043 | Type | Use |
044 |------|-----|
045 | **Stdio** | Local, CLI-based |
046 | **SSE** | Web-based, streaming |
047 | **WebSocket** | Real-time, bidirectional |
048 
049 ---
050 
051 ## 3. Tool Design Principles
052 
053 ### Good Tool Design
054 
055 | Principle | Description |
056 |-----------|-------------|
057 | Clear name | Action-oriented (get_weather, create_user) |
058 | Single purpose | One thing well |
059 | Validated input | Schema with types and descriptions |
060 | Structured output | Predictable response format |
061 
062 ### Input Schema Design
063 
064 | Field | Required? |
065 |-------|-----------|
066 | Type | Yes - object |
067 | Properties | Define each param |
068 | Required | List mandatory params |
069 | Description | Human-readable |
070 
071 ---
072 
073 ## 4. Resource Patterns
074 
075 ### Resource Types
076 
077 | Type | Use |
078 |------|-----|
079 | Static | Fixed data (config, docs) |
080 | Dynamic | Generated on request |
081 | Template | URI with parameters |
082 
083 ### URI Patterns
084 
085 | Pattern | Example |
086 |---------|---------|
087 | Fixed | `docs://readme` |
088 | Parameterized | `users://{userId}` |
089 | Collection | `files://project/*` |
090 
091 ---
092 
093 ## 5. Error Handling
094 
095 ### Error Types
096 
097 | Situation | Response |
098 |-----------|----------|
099 | Invalid params | Validation error message |
100 | Not found | Clear "not found" |
101 | Server error | Generic error, log details |
102 
103 ### Best Practices
104 
105 - Return structured errors
106 - Don't expose internal details
107 - Log for debugging
108 - Provide actionable messages
109 
110 ---
111 
112 ## 6. Multimodal Handling
113 
114 ### Supported Types
115 
116 | Type | Encoding |
117 |------|----------|
118 | Text | Plain text |
119 | Images | Base64 + MIME type |
120 | Files | Base64 + MIME type |
121 
122 ---
123 
124 ## 7. Security Principles
125 
126 ### Input Validation
127 
128 - Validate all tool inputs
129 - Sanitize user-provided data
130 - Limit resource access
131 
132 ### API Keys
133 
134 - Use environment variables
135 - Don't log secrets
136 - Validate permissions
137 
138 ---
139 
140 ## 8. Configuration
141 
142 ### Claude Desktop Config
143 
144 | Field | Purpose |
145 |-------|---------|
146 | command | Executable to run |
147 | args | Command arguments |
148 | env | Environment variables |
149 
150 ---
151 
152 ## 9. Testing
153 
154 ### Test Categories
155 
156 | Type | Focus |
157 |------|-------|
158 | Unit | Tool logic |
159 | Integration | Full server |
160 | Contract | Schema validation |
161 
162 ---
163 
164 ## 10. Best Practices Checklist
165 
166 - [ ] Clear, action-oriented tool names
167 - [ ] Complete input schemas with descriptions
168 - [ ] Structured JSON output
169 - [ ] Error handling for all cases
170 - [ ] Input validation
171 - [ ] Environment-based configuration
172 - [ ] Logging for debugging
173 
174 ---
175 
176 > **Remember:** MCP tools should be simple, focused, and well-documented. The AI relies on descriptions to use them correctly.

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F101 path:skills/mobile-design/decision-trees.md hash:ed7e218bdd40a6d6614974acf4d54772bc6384536d747ac7e4f378870388b0d3 lines:516 ===
001 # Mobile Decision Trees
002 
003 > Framework selection, state management, storage strategy, and context-based decisions.
004 > **These are THINKING guides, not copy-paste answers.**
005 
006 ---
007 
008 ## 1. Framework Selection
009 
010 ### Master Decision Tree
011 
012 ```
013 WHAT ARE YOU BUILDING?
014         ‚îÇ
015         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Need OTA updates without app store review?
016         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
017         ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Yes ‚Üí React Native + Expo
018         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Expo Go for development
019         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ EAS Update for production OTA
020         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ         ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Best for: rapid iteration, web teams
021         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
022         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ No ‚Üí Continue ‚ñº
023         ‚îÇ
024         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Need pixel-perfect custom UI across platforms?
025         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
026         ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Yes ‚Üí Flutter
027         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Custom rendering engine
028         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Single UI for iOS + Android
029         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ         ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Best for: branded, visual apps
030         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
031         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ No ‚Üí Continue ‚ñº
032         ‚îÇ
033         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Heavy native features (ARKit, HealthKit, specific sensors)?
034         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
035         ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ iOS only ‚Üí SwiftUI / UIKit
036         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ              ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Maximum native capability
037         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
038         ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Android only ‚Üí Kotlin + Jetpack Compose
039         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ                  ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Maximum native capability
040         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
041         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Both ‚Üí Consider native with shared logic
042         ‚îÇ              ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Kotlin Multiplatform for shared
043         ‚îÇ
044         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Existing web team + TypeScript codebase?
045         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
046         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Yes ‚Üí React Native
047         ‚îÇ             ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Familiar paradigm for React devs
048         ‚îÇ             ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Share code with web (limited)
049         ‚îÇ             ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Large ecosystem
050         ‚îÇ
051         ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Enterprise with existing Flutter team?
052             ‚îÇ
053             ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Yes ‚Üí Flutter
054                       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Leverage existing expertise
055 ```
056 
057 ### Framework Comparison
058 
059 | Factor | React Native | Flutter | Native (Swift/Kotlin) |
060 |--------|-------------|---------|----------------------|
061 | **OTA Updates** | ‚úÖ Expo | ‚ùå No | ‚ùå No |
062 | **Learning Curve** | Low (React devs) | Medium | Higher |
063 | **Performance** | Good | Excellent | Best |
064 | **UI Consistency** | Platform-native | Identical | Platform-native |
065 | **Bundle Size** | Medium | Larger | Smallest |
066 | **Native Access** | Via bridges | Via channels | Direct |
067 | **Hot Reload** | ‚úÖ | ‚úÖ | ‚úÖ (Xcode 15+) |
068 
069 ### When to Choose Native
070 
071 ```
072 CHOOSE NATIVE WHEN:
073 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Maximum performance required (games, 3D)
074 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Deep OS integration needed
075 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Platform-specific features are core
076 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Team has native expertise
077 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ App store presence is primary
078 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Long-term maintenance priority
079 
080 AVOID NATIVE WHEN:
081 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Limited budget/time
082 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Need rapid iteration
083 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Identical UI on both platforms
084 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Team is web-focused
085 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Cross-platform is priority
086 ```
087 
088 ---
089 
090 ## 2. State Management Selection
091 
092 ### React Native State Decision
093 
094 ```
095 WHAT'S YOUR STATE COMPLEXITY?
096         ‚îÇ
097         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Simple app, few screens, minimal shared state
098         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
099         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Zustand (or just useState/Context)
100         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Minimal boilerplate
101         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Easy to understand
102         ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Scales OK to medium
103         ‚îÇ
104         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Primarily server data (API-driven)
105         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
106         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ TanStack Query (React Query) + Zustand
107         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Query for server state
108         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Zustand for UI state
109         ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Excellent caching, refetching
110         ‚îÇ
111         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Complex app with many features
112         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
113         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Redux Toolkit + RTK Query
114         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Predicable, debuggable
115         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ RTK Query for API
116         ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Good for large teams
117         ‚îÇ
118         ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Atomic, granular state needs
119             ‚îÇ
120             ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Jotai
121                 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Atom-based (like Recoil)
122                 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Minimizes re-renders
123                 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Good for derived state
124 ```
125 
126 ### Flutter State Decision
127 
128 ```
129 WHAT'S YOUR STATE COMPLEXITY?
130         ‚îÇ
131         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Simple app, learning Flutter
132         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
133         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Provider (or setState)
134         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Official, simple
135         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Built into Flutter
136         ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Good for small apps
137         ‚îÇ
138         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Modern, type-safe, testable
139         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
140         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Riverpod 2.0
141         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Compile-time safety
142         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Code generation
143         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Excellent for medium-large apps
144         ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Recommended for new projects
145         ‚îÇ
146         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Enterprise, strict patterns needed
147         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
148         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ BLoC
149         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Event ‚Üí State pattern
150         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Very testable
151         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ More boilerplate
152         ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Good for large teams
153         ‚îÇ
154         ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Quick prototyping
155             ‚îÇ
156             ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ GetX (with caution)
157                 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Fast to implement
158                 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Less strict patterns
159                 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Can become messy at scale
160 ```
161 
162 ### State Management Anti-Patterns
163 
164 ```
165 ‚ùå DON'T:
166 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Use global state for everything
167 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Mix state management approaches
168 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Store server state in local state
169 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Skip state normalization
170 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Overuse Context (re-render heavy)
171 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Put navigation state in app state
172 
173 ‚úÖ DO:
174 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Server state ‚Üí Query library
175 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ UI state ‚Üí Minimal, local first
176 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Lift state only when needed
177 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Choose ONE approach per project
178 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Keep state close to where it's used
179 ```
180 
181 ---
182 
183 ## 3. Navigation Pattern Selection
184 
185 ```
186 HOW MANY TOP-LEVEL DESTINATIONS?
187         ‚îÇ
188         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ 2 destinations
189         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Consider: Top tabs or simple stack
190         ‚îÇ
191         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ 3-5 destinations (equal importance)
192         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ ‚úÖ Tab Bar / Bottom Navigation
193         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Most common pattern
194         ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Easy discovery
195         ‚îÇ
196         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ 5+ destinations
197         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
198         ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ All important ‚Üí Drawer Navigation
199         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ                   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Hidden but many options
200         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
201         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Some less important ‚Üí Tab bar + drawer hybrid
202         ‚îÇ
203         ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Single linear flow?
204             ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Stack Navigation only
205                 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Onboarding, checkout, etc.
206 ```
207 
208 ### Navigation by App Type
209 
210 | App Type | Pattern | Reason |
211 |----------|---------|--------|
212 | Social (Instagram) | Tab bar | Frequent switching |
213 | E-commerce | Tab bar + stack | Categories as tabs |
214 | Email (Gmail) | Drawer + list-detail | Many folders |
215 | Settings | Stack only | Deep drill-down |
216 | Onboarding | Stack wizard | Linear flow |
217 | Messaging | Tab (chats) + stack | Threads |
218 
219 ---
220 
221 ## 4. Storage Strategy Selection
222 
223 ```
224 WHAT TYPE OF DATA?
225         ‚îÇ
226         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Sensitive (tokens, passwords, keys)
227         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
228         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ ‚úÖ Secure Storage
229         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ iOS: Keychain
230         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Android: EncryptedSharedPreferences
231         ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ RN: expo-secure-store / react-native-keychain
232         ‚îÇ
233         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ User preferences (settings, theme)
234         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
235         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ ‚úÖ Key-Value Storage
236         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ iOS: UserDefaults
237         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Android: SharedPreferences
238         ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ RN: AsyncStorage / MMKV
239         ‚îÇ
240         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Structured data (entities, relationships)
241         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
242         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ ‚úÖ Database
243         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ SQLite (expo-sqlite, sqflite)
244         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Realm (NoSQL, reactive)
245         ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ WatermelonDB (large datasets)
246         ‚îÇ
247         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Large files (images, documents)
248         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
249         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ ‚úÖ File System
250         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ iOS: Documents / Caches directory
251         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Android: Internal/External storage
252         ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ RN: react-native-fs / expo-file-system
253         ‚îÇ
254         ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Cached API data
255             ‚îÇ
256             ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ ‚úÖ Query Library Cache
257                 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ TanStack Query (RN)
258                 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Riverpod async (Flutter)
259                 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Automatic invalidation
260 ```
261 
262 ### Storage Comparison
263 
264 | Storage | Speed | Security | Capacity | Use Case |
265 |---------|-------|----------|----------|----------|
266 | Secure Storage | Medium | üîí High | Small | Tokens, secrets |
267 | Key-Value | Fast | Low | Medium | Settings |
268 | SQLite | Fast | Low | Large | Structured data |
269 | File System | Medium | Low | Very Large | Media, documents |
270 | Query Cache | Fast | Low | Medium | API responses |
271 
272 ---
273 
274 ## 5. Offline Strategy Selection
275 
276 ```
277 HOW CRITICAL IS OFFLINE?
278         ‚îÇ
279         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Nice to have (works when possible)
280         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
281         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Cache last data + show stale
282         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Simple implementation
283         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ TanStack Query with staleTime
284         ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Show "last updated" timestamp
285         ‚îÇ
286         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Essential (core functionality offline)
287         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
288         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Offline-first architecture
289         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Local database as source of truth
290         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Sync to server when online
291         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Conflict resolution strategy
292         ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Queue actions for later sync
293         ‚îÇ
294         ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Real-time critical (collaboration, chat)
295             ‚îÇ
296             ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ WebSocket + local queue
297                 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Optimistic updates
298                 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Eventual consistency
299                 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Complex conflict handling
300 ```
301 
302 ### Offline Implementation Patterns
303 
304 ```
305 1. CACHE-FIRST (Simple)
306    Request ‚Üí Check cache ‚Üí If stale, fetch ‚Üí Update cache
307 
308 2. STALE-WHILE-REVALIDATE
309    Request ‚Üí Return cached ‚Üí Fetch update ‚Üí Update UI
310 
311 3. OFFLINE-FIRST (Complex)
312    Action ‚Üí Write to local DB ‚Üí Queue sync ‚Üí Sync when online
313 
314 4. SYNC ENGINE
315    Use: Firebase, Realm Sync, Supabase realtime
316    Handles conflict resolution automatically
317 ```
318 
319 ---
320 
321 ## 6. Authentication Pattern Selection
322 
323 ```
324 WHAT AUTH TYPE NEEDED?
325         ‚îÇ
326         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Simple email/password
327         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
328         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Token-based (JWT)
329         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Store refresh token securely
330         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Access token in memory
331         ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Silent refresh flow
332         ‚îÇ
333         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Social login (Google, Apple, etc.)
334         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
335         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ OAuth 2.0 + PKCE
336         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Use platform SDKs
337         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Deep link callback
338         ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Apple Sign-In required for iOS
339         ‚îÇ
340         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Enterprise/SSO
341         ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ
342         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ OIDC / SAML
343         ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Web view or system browser
344         ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Handle redirect properly
345         ‚îÇ
346         ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Biometric (FaceID, fingerprint)
347             ‚îÇ
348             ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Local auth + secure token
349                 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Biometrics unlock stored token
350                 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Not a replacement for server auth
351                 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Fallback to PIN/password
352 ```
353 
354 ### Auth Token Storage
355 
356 ```
357 ‚ùå NEVER store tokens in:
358 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ AsyncStorage (plain text)
359 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Redux/state (not persisted correctly)
360 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Local storage equivalent
361 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Logs or debug output
362 
363 ‚úÖ ALWAYS store tokens in:
364 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ iOS: Keychain
365 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Android: EncryptedSharedPreferences
366 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Expo: SecureStore
367 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Biometric-protected if available
368 ```
369 
370 ---
371 
372 ## 7. Project Type Templates
373 
374 ### E-Commerce App
375 
376 ```
377 RECOMMENDED STACK:
378 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Framework: React Native + Expo (OTA for pricing)
379 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Navigation: Tab bar (Home, Search, Cart, Account)
380 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ State: TanStack Query (products) + Zustand (cart)
381 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Storage: SecureStore (auth) + SQLite (cart cache)
382 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Offline: Cache products, queue cart actions
383 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Auth: Email/password + Social + Apple Pay
384 
385 KEY DECISIONS:
386 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Product images: Lazy load, cache aggressively
387 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Cart: Sync across devices via API
388 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Checkout: Secure, minimal steps
389 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Deep links: Product shares, marketing
390 ```
391 
392 ### Social/Content App
393 
394 ```
395 RECOMMENDED STACK:
396 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Framework: React Native or Flutter
397 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Navigation: Tab bar (Feed, Search, Create, Notifications, Profile)
398 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ State: TanStack Query (feed) + Zustand (UI)
399 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Storage: SQLite (feed cache, drafts)
400 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Offline: Cache feed, queue posts
401 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Auth: Social login primary, Apple required
402 
403 KEY DECISIONS:
404 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Feed: Infinite scroll, memoized items
405 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Media: Upload queuing, background upload
406 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Push: Deep link to content
407 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Real-time: WebSocket for notifications
408 ```
409 
410 ### Productivity/SaaS App
411 
412 ```
413 RECOMMENDED STACK:
414 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Framework: Flutter (consistent UI) or RN
415 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Navigation: Drawer or Tab bar
416 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ State: Riverpod/BLoC or Redux Toolkit
417 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Storage: SQLite (offline), SecureStore (auth)
418 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Offline: Full offline editing, sync
419 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Auth: SSO/OIDC for enterprise
420 
421 KEY DECISIONS:
422 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Data sync: Conflict resolution strategy
423 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Collaborative: Real-time or eventual?
424 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Files: Large file handling
425 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Enterprise: MDM, compliance
426 ```
427 
428 ---
429 
430 ## 8. Decision Checklist
431 
432 ### Before Starting ANY Project
433 
434 - [ ] Target platforms defined (iOS/Android/both)?
435 - [ ] Framework selected based on criteria?
436 - [ ] State management approach chosen?
437 - [ ] Navigation pattern selected?
438 - [ ] Storage strategy for each data type?
439 - [ ] Offline requirements defined?
440 - [ ] Auth flow designed?
441 - [ ] Deep linking planned from start?
442 
443 ### Questions to Ask User
444 
445 ```
446 If project details are vague, ASK:
447 
448 1. "Will this need OTA updates without app store review?"
449    ‚Üí Affects framework choice (Expo = yes)
450 
451 2. "Do iOS and Android need identical UI?"
452    ‚Üí Affects framework (Flutter = identical)
453 
454 3. "What's the offline requirement?"
455    ‚Üí Affects architecture complexity
456 
457 4. "Is there an existing backend/auth system?"
458    ‚Üí Affects auth and API approach
459 
460 5. "What devices? Phone only, or tablet?"
461    ‚Üí Affects navigation and layout
462 
463 6. "Enterprise or consumer?"
464    ‚Üí Affects auth (SSO), security, compliance
465 ```
466 
467 ---
468 
469 ## 9. Anti-Pattern Decisions
470 
471 ### ‚ùå Decision Anti-Patterns
472 
473 | Anti-Pattern | Why It's Bad | Better Approach |
474 |--------------|--------------|-----------------|
475 | **Redux for simple app** | Massive overkill | Zustand or context |
476 | **Native for MVP** | Slow development | Cross-platform MVP |
477 | **Drawer for 3 sections** | Hidden navigation | Tab bar |
478 | **AsyncStorage for tokens** | Insecure | SecureStore |
479 | **No offline consideration** | Broken on subway | Plan from start |
480 | **Same stack for all projects** | Doesn't fit context | Evaluate per project |
481 
482 ---
483 
484 ## 10. Quick Reference
485 
486 ### Framework Quick Pick
487 
488 ```
489 OTA needed?           ‚Üí React Native + Expo
490 Identical UI?         ‚Üí Flutter
491 Maximum performance?  ‚Üí Native
492 Web team?            ‚Üí React Native
493 Quick prototype?     ‚Üí Expo
494 ```
495 
496 ### State Quick Pick
497 
498 ```
499 Simple app?          ‚Üí Zustand / Provider
500 Server-heavy?        ‚Üí TanStack Query / Riverpod
501 Enterprise?          ‚Üí Redux / BLoC
502 Atomic state?        ‚Üí Jotai
503 ```
504 
505 ### Storage Quick Pick
506 
507 ```
508 Secrets?             ‚Üí SecureStore / Keychain
509 Settings?            ‚Üí AsyncStorage / UserDefaults
510 Structured data?     ‚Üí SQLite
511 API cache?           ‚Üí Query library
512 ```
513 
514 ---
515 
516 > **Remember:** These trees are guides for THINKING, not rules to follow blindly. Every project has unique constraints. ASK clarifying questions when requirements are vague, and choose based on actual needs, not defaults.

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F102 path:skills/mobile-design/mobile-backend.md hash:b46b4c0d122de115ed85a8ea814c898cebecb6338f58008b8ce23f28d136dcb2 lines:491 ===
001 # Mobile Backend Patterns
002 
003 > **This file covers backend/API patterns SPECIFIC to mobile clients.**
004 > Generic backend patterns are in `nodejs-best-practices` and `api-patterns`.
005 > **Mobile backend is NOT the same as web backend. Different constraints, different patterns.**
006 
007 ---
008 
009 ## üß† MOBILE BACKEND MINDSET
010 
011 ```
012 Mobile clients are DIFFERENT from web clients:
013 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Unreliable network (2G, subway, elevator)
014 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Battery constraints (minimize wake-ups)
015 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Limited storage (can't cache everything)
016 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Interrupted sessions (calls, notifications)
017 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Diverse devices (old phones to flagships)
018 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Binary updates are slow (App Store review)
019 ```
020 
021 **Your backend must compensate for ALL of these.**
022 
023 ---
024 
025 ## üö´ AI MOBILE BACKEND ANTI-PATTERNS
026 
027 ### These are common AI mistakes when building mobile backends:
028 
029 | ‚ùå AI Default | Why It's Wrong | ‚úÖ Mobile-Correct |
030 |---------------|----------------|-------------------|
031 | Same API for web and mobile | Mobile needs compact responses | Separate mobile endpoints OR field selection |
032 | Full object responses | Wastes bandwidth, battery | Partial responses, pagination |
033 | No offline consideration | App crashes without network | Offline-first design, sync queues |
034 | WebSocket for everything | Battery drain | Push notifications + polling fallback |
035 | No app versioning | Can't force updates, breaking changes | Version headers, minimum version check |
036 | Generic error messages | Users can't fix issues | Mobile-specific error codes + recovery actions |
037 | Session-based auth | Mobile apps restart | Token-based with refresh |
038 | Ignore device info | Can't debug issues | Device ID, app version in headers |
039 
040 ---
041 
042 ## 1. Push Notifications
043 
044 ### Platform Architecture
045 
046 ```
047 ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
048 ‚îÇ                    YOUR BACKEND                                  ‚îÇ
049 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î§
050 ‚îÇ                         ‚îÇ                                        ‚îÇ
051 ‚îÇ              ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¥‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê                            ‚îÇ
052 ‚îÇ              ‚ñº                     ‚ñº                            ‚îÇ
053 ‚îÇ    ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê   ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê                    ‚îÇ
054 ‚îÇ    ‚îÇ   FCM (Google)  ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ  APNs (Apple)   ‚îÇ                    ‚îÇ
055 ‚îÇ    ‚îÇ   Firebase      ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ  Direct or FCM  ‚îÇ                    ‚îÇ
056 ‚îÇ    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚î¨‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò                    ‚îÇ
057 ‚îÇ             ‚îÇ                     ‚îÇ                              ‚îÇ
058 ‚îÇ             ‚ñº                     ‚ñº                              ‚îÇ
059 ‚îÇ    ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê   ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê                    ‚îÇ
060 ‚îÇ    ‚îÇ Android Device  ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ   iOS Device    ‚îÇ                    ‚îÇ
061 ‚îÇ    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò                    ‚îÇ
062 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
063 ```
064 
065 ### Push Types
066 
067 | Type | Use Case | User Sees |
068 |------|----------|-----------|
069 | **Display** | New message, order update | Notification banner |
070 | **Silent** | Background sync, content update | Nothing (background) |
071 | **Data** | Custom handling by app | Depends on app logic |
072 
073 ### Anti-Patterns
074 
075 | ‚ùå NEVER | ‚úÖ ALWAYS |
076 |----------|----------|
077 | Send sensitive data in push | Push says "New message", app fetches content |
078 | Overload with pushes | Batch, dedupe, respect quiet hours |
079 | Same message to all | Segment by user preference, timezone |
080 | Ignore failed tokens | Clean up invalid tokens regularly |
081 | Skip APNs for iOS | FCM alone doesn't guarantee iOS delivery |
082 
083 ### Token Management
084 
085 ```
086 TOKEN LIFECYCLE:
087 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ App registers ‚Üí Get token ‚Üí Send to backend
088 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Token can change ‚Üí App must re-register on start
089 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Token expires ‚Üí Clean from database
090 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ User uninstalls ‚Üí Token becomes invalid (detect via error)
091 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Multiple devices ‚Üí Store multiple tokens per user
092 ```
093 
094 ---
095 
096 ## 2. Offline Sync & Conflict Resolution
097 
098 ### Sync Strategy Selection
099 
100 ```
101 WHAT TYPE OF DATA?
102         ‚îÇ
103         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Read-only (news, catalog)
104         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Simple cache + TTL
105         ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ ETag/Last-Modified for invalidation
106         ‚îÇ
107         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ User-owned (notes, todos)
108         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Last-write-wins (simple)
109         ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Or timestamp-based merge
110         ‚îÇ
111         ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Collaborative (shared docs)
112         ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ CRDT or OT required
113         ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Consider Firebase/Supabase
114         ‚îÇ
115         ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Critical (payments, inventory)
116             ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Server is source of truth
117                 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Optimistic UI + server confirmation
118 ```
119 
120 ### Conflict Resolution Strategies
121 
122 | Strategy | How It Works | Best For |
123 |----------|--------------|----------|
124 | **Last-write-wins** | Latest timestamp overwrites | Simple data, single user |
125 | **Server-wins** | Server always authoritative | Critical transactions |
126 | **Client-wins** | Offline changes prioritized | Offline-heavy apps |
127 | **Merge** | Combine changes field-by-field | Documents, rich content |
128 | **CRDT** | Mathematically conflict-free | Real-time collaboration |
129 
130 ### Sync Queue Pattern
131 
132 ```
133 CLIENT SIDE:
134 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ User makes change ‚Üí Write to local DB
135 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Add to sync queue ‚Üí { action, data, timestamp, retries }
136 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Network available ‚Üí Process queue FIFO
137 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Success ‚Üí Remove from queue
138 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Failure ‚Üí Retry with backoff (max 5 retries)
139 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Conflict ‚Üí Apply resolution strategy
140 
141 SERVER SIDE:
142 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Accept change with client timestamp
143 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Compare with server version
144 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Apply conflict resolution
145 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Return merged state
146 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Client updates local with server response
147 ```
148 
149 ---
150 
151 ## 3. Mobile API Optimization
152 
153 ### Response Size Reduction
154 
155 | Technique | Savings | Implementation |
156 |-----------|---------|----------------|
157 | **Field selection** | 30-70% | `?fields=id,name,thumbnail` |
158 | **Compression** | 60-80% | gzip/brotli (automatic) |
159 | **Pagination** | Varies | Cursor-based for mobile |
160 | **Image variants** | 50-90% | `/image?w=200&q=80` |
161 | **Delta sync** | 80-95% | Only changed records since timestamp |
162 
163 ### Pagination: Cursor vs Offset
164 
165 ```
166 OFFSET (Bad for mobile):
167 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Page 1: OFFSET 0 LIMIT 20
168 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Page 2: OFFSET 20 LIMIT 20
169 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Problem: New item added ‚Üí duplicates!
170 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Problem: Large offset = slow query
171 
172 CURSOR (Good for mobile):
173 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ First: ?limit=20
174 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Next: ?limit=20&after=cursor_abc123
175 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Cursor = encoded (id + sort values)
176 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ No duplicates on data changes
177 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Consistent performance
178 ```
179 
180 ### Batch Requests
181 
182 ```
183 Instead of:
184 GET /users/1
185 GET /users/2
186 GET /users/3
187 (3 round trips, 3x latency)
188 
189 Use:
190 POST /batch
191 { requests: [
192     { method: "GET", path: "/users/1" },
193     { method: "GET", path: "/users/2" },
194     { method: "GET", path: "/users/3" }
195 ]}
196 (1 round trip)
197 ```
198 
199 ---
200 
201 ## 4. App Versioning
202 
203 ### Version Check Endpoint
204 
205 ```
206 GET /api/app-config
207 Headers:
208   X-App-Version: 2.1.0
209   X-Platform: ios
210   X-Device-ID: abc123
211 
212 Response:
213 {
214   "minimum_version": "2.0.0",
215   "latest_version": "2.3.0",
216   "force_update": false,
217   "update_url": "https://apps.apple.com/...",
218   "feature_flags": {
219     "new_player": true,
220     "dark_mode": true
221   },
222   "maintenance": false,
223   "maintenance_message": null
224 }
225 ```
226 
227 ### Version Comparison Logic
228 
229 ```
230 CLIENT VERSION vs MINIMUM VERSION:
231 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ client >= minimum ‚Üí Continue normally
232 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ client < minimum ‚Üí Show force update screen
233 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Block app usage until updated
234 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ client < latest ‚Üí Show optional update prompt
235 
236 FEATURE FLAGS:
237 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Enable/disable features without app update
238 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ A/B testing by version/device
239 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Gradual rollout (10% ‚Üí 50% ‚Üí 100%)
240 ```
241 
242 ---
243 
244 ## 5. Authentication for Mobile
245 
246 ### Token Strategy
247 
248 ```
249 ACCESS TOKEN:
250 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Short-lived (15 min - 1 hour)
251 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Stored in memory (not persistent)
252 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Used for API requests
253 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Refresh when expired
254 
255 REFRESH TOKEN:
256 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Long-lived (30-90 days)
257 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Stored in SecureStore/Keychain
258 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Used only to get new access token
259 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Rotate on each use (security)
260 
261 DEVICE TOKEN:
262 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Identifies this device
263 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Allows "log out all devices"
264 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Stored alongside refresh token
265 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Server tracks active devices
266 ```
267 
268 ### Silent Re-authentication
269 
270 ```
271 REQUEST FLOW:
272 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Make request with access token
273 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ 401 Unauthorized?
274 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Have refresh token?
275 ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Yes ‚Üí Call /auth/refresh
276 ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Success ‚Üí Retry original request
277 ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Failure ‚Üí Force logout
278 ‚îÇ   ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ No ‚Üí Force logout
279 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Token just expired (not invalid)
280 ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Auto-refresh, user doesn't notice
281 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Success ‚Üí Continue
282 ```
283 
284 ---
285 
286 ## 6. Error Handling for Mobile
287 
288 ### Mobile-Specific Error Format
289 
290 ```json
291 {
292   "error": {
293     "code": "PAYMENT_DECLINED",
294     "message": "Your payment was declined",
295     "user_message": "Please check your card details or try another payment method",
296     "action": {
297       "type": "navigate",
298       "destination": "payment_methods"
299     },
300     "retry": {
301       "allowed": true,
302       "after_seconds": 5
303     }
304   }
305 }
306 ```
307 
308 ### Error Categories
309 
310 | Code Range | Category | Mobile Handling |
311 |------------|----------|-----------------|
312 | 400-499 | Client error | Show message, user action needed |
313 | 401 | Auth expired | Silent refresh or re-login |
314 | 403 | Forbidden | Show upgrade/permission screen |
315 | 404 | Not found | Remove from local cache |
316 | 409 | Conflict | Show sync conflict UI |
317 | 429 | Rate limit | Retry after header, backoff |
318 | 500-599 | Server error | Retry with backoff, show "try later" |
319 | Network | No connection | Use cached data, queue for sync |
320 
321 ---
322 
323 ## 7. Media & Binary Handling
324 
325 ### Image Optimization
326 
327 ```
328 CLIENT REQUEST:
329 GET /images/{id}?w=400&h=300&q=80&format=webp
330 
331 SERVER RESPONSE:
332 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Resize on-the-fly OR use CDN
333 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ WebP for Android (smaller)
334 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ HEIC for iOS 14+ (if supported)
335 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ JPEG fallback
336 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Cache-Control: max-age=31536000
337 ```
338 
339 ### Chunked Upload (Large Files)
340 
341 ```
342 UPLOAD FLOW:
343 1. POST /uploads/init
344    { filename, size, mime_type }
345    ‚Üí { upload_id, chunk_size }
346 
347 2. PUT /uploads/{upload_id}/chunks/{n}
348    ‚Üí Upload each chunk (1-5 MB)
349    ‚Üí Can resume if interrupted
350 
351 3. POST /uploads/{upload_id}/complete
352    ‚Üí Server assembles chunks
353    ‚Üí Return final file URL
354 ```
355 
356 ### Streaming Audio/Video
357 
358 ```
359 REQUIREMENTS:
360 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ HLS (HTTP Live Streaming) for iOS
361 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ DASH or HLS for Android
362 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Multiple quality levels (adaptive bitrate)
363 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Range request support (seeking)
364 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Offline download chunks
365 
366 ENDPOINTS:
367 GET /media/{id}/manifest.m3u8  ‚Üí HLS manifest
368 GET /media/{id}/segment_{n}.ts ‚Üí Video segment
369 GET /media/{id}/download       ‚Üí Full file for offline
370 ```
371 
372 ---
373 
374 ## 8. Security for Mobile
375 
376 ### Device Attestation
377 
378 ```
379 VERIFY REAL DEVICE (not emulator/bot):
380 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ iOS: DeviceCheck API
381 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Server verifies with Apple
382 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Android: Play Integrity API (replaces SafetyNet)
383 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Server verifies with Google
384 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Fail closed: Reject if attestation fails
385 ```
386 
387 ### Request Signing
388 
389 ```
390 CLIENT:
391 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Create signature = HMAC(timestamp + path + body, secret)
392 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Send: X-Signature: {signature}
393 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Send: X-Timestamp: {timestamp}
394 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Send: X-Device-ID: {device_id}
395 
396 SERVER:
397 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Validate timestamp (within 5 minutes)
398 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Recreate signature with same inputs
399 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Compare signatures
400 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Reject if mismatch (tampering detected)
401 ```
402 
403 ### Rate Limiting
404 
405 ```
406 MOBILE-SPECIFIC LIMITS:
407 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Per device (X-Device-ID)
408 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Per user (after auth)
409 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Per endpoint (stricter for sensitive)
410 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Sliding window preferred
411 
412 HEADERS:
413 X-RateLimit-Limit: 100
414 X-RateLimit-Remaining: 95
415 X-RateLimit-Reset: 1609459200
416 Retry-After: 60 (when 429)
417 ```
418 
419 ---
420 
421 ## 9. Monitoring & Analytics
422 
423 ### Required Headers from Mobile
424 
425 ```
426 Every mobile request should include:
427 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ X-App-Version: 2.1.0
428 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ X-Platform: ios | android
429 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ X-OS-Version: 17.0
430 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ X-Device-Model: iPhone15,2
431 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ X-Device-ID: uuid (persistent)
432 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ X-Request-ID: uuid (per request, for tracing)
433 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Accept-Language: tr-TR
434 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ X-Timezone: Europe/Istanbul
435 ```
436 
437 ### What to Log
438 
439 ```
440 FOR EACH REQUEST:
441 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ All headers above
442 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Endpoint, method, status
443 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Response time
444 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Error details (if any)
445 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ User ID (if authenticated)
446 
447 ALERTS:
448 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Error rate > 5% per version
449 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ P95 latency > 2 seconds
450 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Specific version crash spike
451 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Auth failure spike (attack?)
452 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Push delivery failure spike
453 ```

473 - [ ] Silent re-auth flow?
474 - [ ] Multi-device logout?

480 - [ ] Silent vs display push defined?
481 - [ ] Sensitive data NOT in push payload?
482

485 - [ ] Feature flags configured?
486 - [ ] Force update mechanism?
487 - [ ] Monitoring headers required?

491 > **Remember:** Mobile backend must be resilient to bad networks, respect battery life, and handle interrupted sessions gracefully. The client cannot be trusted, but it also cannot be hung up‚Äîprovide offline capabilities and clear error recovery paths.

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F103 path:skills/mobile-design/mobile-color-system.md hash:9e6e302b1a03179811cbe15b8cba70eca5c6dbd42396d9efbc331d704c9b86b1 lines:420 ===
001 # Mobile Color System Reference
002 
003 > OLED optimization, dark mode, battery-aware colors, and outdoor visibility.
004 > **Color on mobile isn't just aesthetics‚Äîit's battery life and usability.**
005 
006 ---
007 
008 ## 1. Mobile Color Fundamentals
009 
010 ### Why Mobile Color is Different
011 
012 ```
013 DESKTOP:                           MOBILE:
014 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ LCD screens (backlit)          ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ OLED common (self-emissive)
015 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Controlled lighting            ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Outdoor, bright sun
016 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Stable power                   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Battery matters
017 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Personal preference            ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ System-wide dark mode
018 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Static viewing                 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Variable angles, motion
019 ```
020 
021 ### Mobile Color Priorities
022 
023 | Priority | Why |
024 |----------|-----|
025 | **1. Readability** | Outdoor, variable lighting |
026 | **2. Battery efficiency** | OLED = dark mode saves power |
027 | **3. System integration** | Dark/light mode support |
028 | **4. Semantics** | Error, success, warning colors |
029 | **5. Brand** | After functional requirements |
030 
031 ---
032 
033 ## 2. OLED Considerations
034 
035 ### How OLED Differs
036 
037 ```
038 LCD (Liquid Crystal Display):
039 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Backlight always on
040 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Black = backlight through dark filter
041 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Energy use = constant
042 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Dark mode = no battery savings
043 
044 OLED (Organic LED):
045 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Each pixel emits own light
046 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Black = pixel OFF (zero power)
047 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Energy use = brighter pixels use more
048 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Dark mode = significant battery savings
049 ```
050 
051 ### Battery Savings with OLED
052 
053 ```
054 Color energy consumption (relative):
055 
056 #000000 (True Black)  ‚ñà‚ñà‚ñà‚ñà‚ñë‚ñë‚ñë‚ñë‚ñë‚ñë  0%
057 #1A1A1A (Near Black)  ‚ñà‚ñà‚ñà‚ñà‚ñà‚ñë‚ñë‚ñë‚ñë‚ñë  ~15%
058 #333333 (Dark Gray)   ‚ñà‚ñà‚ñà‚ñà‚ñà‚ñà‚ñë‚ñë‚ñë‚ñë  ~30%
059 #666666 (Medium Gray) ‚ñà‚ñà‚ñà‚ñà‚ñà‚ñà‚ñà‚ñë‚ñë‚ñë  ~50%
060 #FFFFFF (White)       ‚ñà‚ñà‚ñà‚ñà‚ñà‚ñà‚ñà‚ñà‚ñà‚ñà  100%
061 
062 Saturated colors also use significant power:
063 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Blue pixels: Most efficient
064 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Green pixels: Medium
065 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Red pixels: Least efficient
066 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Desaturated colors save more
067 ```
068 
069 ### True Black vs Near Black
070 
071 ```
072 #000000 (True Black):
073 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Maximum battery savings
074 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Can cause "black smear" on scroll
075 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Sharp contrast (may be harsh)
076 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Used by Apple in pure dark mode
077 
078 #121212 or #1A1A1A (Near Black):
079 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Still good battery savings
080 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Smoother scrolling (no smear)
081 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Slightly softer on eyes
082 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Material Design recommendation
083 
084 RECOMMENDATION: #000000 for backgrounds, #0D0D0D-#1A1A1A for surfaces
085 ```
086 
087 ---
088 
089 ## 3. Dark Mode Design
090 
091 ### Dark Mode Benefits
092 
093 ```
094 Users enable dark mode for:
095 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Battery savings (OLED)
096 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Reduced eye strain (low light)
097 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Personal preference
098 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ AMOLED aesthetic
099 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Accessibility (light sensitivity)
100 ```
101 
102 ### Dark Mode Color Strategy
103 
104 ```
105 LIGHT MODE                      DARK MODE
106 ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ                      ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
107 Background: #FFFFFF      ‚Üí      #000000 or #121212
108 Surface:    #F5F5F5      ‚Üí      #1E1E1E
109 Surface 2:  #EEEEEE      ‚Üí      #2C2C2C
110 
111 Primary:    #1976D2      ‚Üí      #90CAF9 (lighter)
112 Text:       #212121      ‚Üí      #E0E0E0 (not pure white)
113 Secondary:  #757575      ‚Üí      #9E9E9E
114 
115 Elevation in dark mode:
116 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Higher = slightly lighter surface
117 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ 0dp ‚Üí  0% overlay
118 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ 4dp ‚Üí  9% overlay
119 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ 8dp ‚Üí  12% overlay
120 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Creates depth without shadows
121 ```
122 
123 ### Text Colors in Dark Mode
124 
125 | Role | Light Mode | Dark Mode |
126 |------|------------|-----------|
127 | Primary | #000000 (Black) | #E8E8E8 (Not pure white) |
128 | Secondary | #666666 | #B0B0B0 |
129 | Disabled | #9E9E9E | #6E6E6E |
130 | Links | #1976D2 | #8AB4F8 |
131 
132 ### Color Inversion Rules
133 
134 ```
135 DON'T just invert colors:
136 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Saturated colors become eye-burning
137 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Semantic colors lose meaning
138 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Brand colors may break
139 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Contrast ratios change unpredictably
140 
141 DO create intentional dark palette:
142 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Desaturate primary colors
143 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Use lighter tints for emphasis
144 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Maintain semantic color meanings
145 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Check contrast ratios independently
146 ```
147 
148 ---
149 
150 ## 4. Outdoor Visibility
151 
152 ### The Sunlight Problem
153 
154 ```
155 Screen visibility outdoors:
156 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Bright sun washes out low contrast
157 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Glare reduces readability
158 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Polarized sunglasses affect
159 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Users shield screen with hand
160 
161 Affected elements:
162 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Light gray text on white
163 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Subtle color differences
164 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Low opacity overlays
165 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Pastel colors
166 ```
167 
168 ### High Contrast Strategies
169 
170 ```
171 For outdoor visibility:
172 
173 MINIMUM CONTRAST RATIOS:
174 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Normal text: 4.5:1 (WCAG AA)
175 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Large text: 3:1 (WCAG AA)
176 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Recommended: 7:1+ (AAA)
177 
178 AVOID:
179 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ #999 on #FFF (fails AA)
180 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ #BBB on #FFF (fails)
181 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Pale colors on light backgrounds
182 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Subtle gradients for critical info
183 
184 DO:
185 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Use system semantic colors
186 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Test in bright environment
187 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Provide high contrast mode
188 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Use solid colors for critical UI
189 ```
190 
191 ---
192 
193 ## 5. Semantic Colors
194 
195 ### Consistent Meaning
196 
197 | Semantic | Meaning | iOS Default | Android Default |
198 |----------|---------|-------------|-----------------|
199 | Error | Problems, destruction | #FF3B30 | #B3261E |
200 | Success | Completion, positive | #34C759 | #4CAF50 |
201 | Warning | Attention, caution | #FF9500 | #FFC107 |
202 | Info | Information | #007AFF | #2196F3 |
203 
204 ### Semantic Color Rules
205 
206 ```
207 NEVER use semantic colors for:
208 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Branding (confuses meaning)
209 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Decoration (reduces impact)
210 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Arbitrary styling
211 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Status indicators (use icons too)
212 
213 ALWAYS:
214 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Pair with icons (colorblind users)
215 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Maintain across light/dark modes
216 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Keep consistent throughout app
217 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Follow platform conventions
218 ```
219 
220 ### Error State Colors
221 
222 ```
223 Error states need:
224 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Red-ish color (semantic)
225 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ High contrast against background
226 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Icon reinforcement
227 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Clear text explanation
228 
229 iOS:
230 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Light: #FF3B30
231 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Dark: #FF453A
232 
233 Android:
234 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Light: #B3261E
235 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Dark: #F2B8B5 (on error container)
236 ```
237 
238 ---
239 
240 ## 6. Dynamic Color (Android)
241 
242 ### Material You
243 
244 ```
245 Android 12+ Dynamic Color:
246 
247 User's wallpaper ‚Üí Color extraction ‚Üí App theme
248 
249 Your app automatically gets:
250 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Primary (from wallpaper dominant)
251 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Secondary (complementary)
252 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Tertiary (accent)
253 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Surface colors (neutral, derived)
254 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ On-colors (text on each)
255 ```
256 
257 ### Supporting Dynamic Color
258 
259 ```kotlin
260 // Jetpack Compose
261 MaterialTheme(
262     colorScheme = dynamicColorScheme()
263         ?: staticColorScheme() // Fallback for older Android
264 )
265 
266 // React Native
267 // Limited support - consider react-native-material-you
268 ```
269 
270 ### Fallback Colors
271 
272 ```
273 When dynamic color unavailable:
274 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Android < 12
275 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ User disabled
276 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Non-supporting launchers
277 
278 Provide static color scheme:
279 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Define your brand colors
280 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Test in both modes
281 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Match dynamic color roles
282 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Support light + dark
283 ```
284 
285 ---
286 
287 ## 7. Color Accessibility
288 
289 ### Colorblind Considerations
290 
291 ```
292 ~8% of men, ~0.5% of women are colorblind
293 
294 Types:
295 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Protanopia (red weakness)
296 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Deuteranopia (green weakness)
297 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Tritanopia (blue weakness)
298 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Monochromacy (rare, no color)
299 
300 Design rules:
301 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Never rely on color alone
302 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Use patterns, icons, text
303 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Test with simulation tools
304 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Avoid red/green distinctions only
305 ```
306 
307 ### Contrast Testing Tools
308 
309 ```
310 Use these to verify:
311 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Built-in accessibility inspector (Xcode)
312 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Accessibility Scanner (Android)
313 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Contrast ratio calculators
314 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Colorblind simulation
315 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Test on actual devices in sunlight
316 ```
317 
318 ### Sufficient Contrast
319 
320 ```
321 WCAG Guidelines:
322 
323 AA (Minimum)
324 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Normal text: 4.5:1
325 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Large text (18pt+): 3:1
326 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ UI components: 3:1
327 
328 AAA (Enhanced)
329 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Normal text: 7:1
330 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Large text: 4.5:1
331 
332 Mobile recommendation: Meet AA, aim for AAA
333 ```
334 
335 ---
336 
337 ## 8. Color Anti-Patterns
338 
339 ### ‚ùå Common Mistakes
340 
341 | Mistake | Problem | Fix |
342 |---------|---------|-----|
343 | **Light gray on white** | Invisible outdoors | Min 4.5:1 contrast |
344 | **Pure white in dark mode** | Eye strain | Use #E0E0E0-#F0F0F0 |
345 | **Same saturation dark mode** | Garish, glowing | Desaturate colors |
346 | **Red/green only indicator** | Colorblind users can't see | Add icons |
347 | **Semantic colors for brand** | Confusing meaning | Use neutral for brand |
348 | **Ignoring system dark mode** | Jarring experience | Support both modes |
349 
350 ### ‚ùå AI Color Mistakes
351 
352 ```
353 AI tends to:
354 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Use same colors for light/dark
355 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Ignore OLED battery implications
356 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Skip contrast calculations
357 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Default to purple/violet (BANNED)
358 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Use low contrast "aesthetic" grays
359 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Not test in outdoor conditions
360 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Forget colorblind users
361 
362 RULE: Design for the worst case.
363 Test in bright sunlight, with colorblindness simulation.
364 ```
365 
366 ---
367 
368 ## 9. Color System Checklist
369 
370 ### Before Choosing Colors
371 
372 - [ ] Light and dark mode variants defined?
373 - [ ] Contrast ratios checked (4.5:1+)?
374 - [ ] OLED battery considered (dark mode)?
375 - [ ] Semantic colors follow conventions?
376 - [ ] Colorblind-safe (not color-only indicators)?
377 
378 ### Before Release
379 
380 - [ ] Tested in bright sunlight?
381 - [ ] Tested dark mode on OLED device?
382 - [ ] System dark mode respected?
383 - [ ] Dynamic color supported (Android)?
384 - [ ] Error/success/warning consistent?
385 - [ ] All text meets contrast requirements?
386 
387 ---
388 
389 ## 10. Quick Reference
390 
391 ### Dark Mode Backgrounds
392 
393 ```
394 True black (OLED max savings): #000000
395 Near black (Material):         #121212
396 Surface 1:                     #1E1E1E
397 Surface 2:                     #2C2C2C
398 Surface 3:                     #3C3C3C
399 ```
400 
401 ### Text on Dark
402 
403 ```
404 Primary:   #E0E0E0 to #ECECEC
405 Secondary: #A0A0A0 to #B0B0B0
406 Disabled:  #606060 to #707070
407 ```
408 
409 ### Contrast Ratios
410 
411 ```
412 Small text:  4.5:1 (minimum)
413 Large text:  3:1 (minimum)
414 UI elements: 3:1 (minimum)
415 Ideal:       7:1 (AAA)
416 ```
417 
418 ---
419 
420 > **Remember:** Color on mobile must work in the worst conditions‚Äîbright sun, tired eyes, colorblindness, low battery. Pretty colors that fail these tests are useless colors.

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F104 path:skills/mobile-design/mobile-debugging.md hash:647fed510688212d3025c3f1ab06aae44dc5c19d245521de400d2575699e8008 lines:122 ===
001 # Mobile Debugging Guide
002 
003 > **Stop console.log() debugging!**
004 > Mobile apps have complex native layers. Text logs are not enough.
005 > **This file teaches effective mobile debugging strategies.**
006 
007 ---
008 
009 ## üß† MOBILE DEBUGGING MINDSET
010 
011 ```
012 Web Debugging:      Mobile Debugging:
013 ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê    ‚îå‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îê
014 ‚îÇ  Browser     ‚îÇ    ‚îÇ  JS Bridge   ‚îÇ
015 ‚îÇ  DevTools    ‚îÇ    ‚îÇ  Native UI   ‚îÇ
016 ‚îÇ  Network Tab ‚îÇ    ‚îÇ  GPU/Memory  ‚îÇ
017 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò    ‚îÇ  Threads     ‚îÇ
018                     ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îò
019 ```
020 
021 **Key Differences:**
022 1.  **Native Layer:** JS code works, but app crashes? It's likely native (Java/Obj-C).
023 2.  **Deployment:** You can't just "refresh". State gets lost or stuck.
024 3.  **Network:** SSL Pinning, proxy settings are harder.
025 4.  **Device Logs:** `adb logcat` and `Console.app` are your truth.
026 
027 ---
028 
029 ## üö´ AI DEBUGGING ANTI-PATTERNS
030 
031 | ‚ùå Default | ‚úÖ Mobile-Correct |
032 |------------|-------------------|
033 | "Add console.logs" | Use Flipper / Reactotron |
034 | "Check network tab" | Use Charles Proxy / Proxyman |
035 | "It works on simulator" | **Test on Real Device** (HW specific bugs) |
036 | "Reinstall node_modules" | **Clean Native Build** (Gradle/Pod cache) |
037 | Ignored native logs | Read `logcat` / Xcode logs |
038 
039 ---
040 
041 ## 1. The Toolset
042 
043 ### ‚ö° React Native & Expo
044 
045 | Tool | Purpose | Best For |
046 |------|---------|----------|
047 | **Reactotron** | State/API/Redux | JS side debugging |
048 | **Flipper** | Layout/Network/db | Native + JS bridge |
049 | **Expo Tools** | Element inspector | Quick UI checks |
050 
051 ### üõ†Ô∏è Native Layer (The Deep Dive)
052 
053 | Tool | Platform | Command | Why Use? |
054 |------|----------|---------|----------|
055 | **Logcat** | Android | `adb logcat` | Native crashes, ANRs |
056 | **Console** | iOS | via Xcode | Native exceptions, memory |
057 | **Layout Insp.** | Android | Android Studio | UI hierarchy bugs |
058 | **View Insp.** | iOS | Xcode | UI hierarchy bugs |
059 
060 ---
061 
062 ## 2. Common Debugging Workflows
063 
064 ### üïµÔ∏è "The App Just Crashed" (Red Screen vs Crash to Home)
065 
066 **Scenario A: Red Screen (JS Error)**
067 - **Cause:** Undefined is not an object, import error.
068 - **Fix:** Read the stack trace on screen. It's usually clear.
069 
070 **Scenario B: Crash to Home Screen (Native Crash)**
071 - **Cause:** Native module failure, memory OOM, permission usage without declaration.
072 - **Tools:**
073     - **Android:** `adb logcat *:E` (Filter for Errors)
074     - **iOS:** Open Xcode ‚Üí Window ‚Üí Devices ‚Üí View Device Logs
075 
076 > **üí° Pro Tip:** If app crashes immediately on launch, it's almost 100% a native configuration issue (Info.plist, AndroidManifest.xml).
077 
078 ### üåê "API Request Failed" (Network)
079 
080 **Web:** Open Chrome DevTools ‚Üí Network.
081 **Mobile:** *You usually can't see this easily.*
082 
083 **Solution 1: Reactotron/Flipper**
084 - View network requests in the monitoring app.
085 
086 **Solution 2: Proxy (Charles/Proxyman)**
087 - **Hard but powerful.** See ALL traffic even from native SDKs.
088 - Requires installing SSL cert on device.
089 
090 ### üê¢ "The UI is Laggy" (Performance)
091 
092 **Don't guess.** measure.
093 - **React Native:** Performance Monitor (Shake menu).
094 - **Android:** "Profile GPU Rendering" in Developer Options.
095 - **Issues:**
096     - **JS FPS drop:** Heavy calculation in JS thread.
097     - **UI FPS drop:** Too many views, intricate hierarchy, heavy images.
098 
099 ---
100 
101 ## 3. Platform-Specific Nightmares
102 
103 ### Android
104 - **Gradle Sync Fail:** Usually Java version mismatch or duplicate classes.
105 - **Emulator Network:** Emulator `localhost` is `10.0.2.2`, NOT `127.0.0.1`.
106 - **Cached Builds:** `./gradlew clean` is your best friend.
107 
108 ### iOS
109 - **Pod Issues:** `pod deintegrate && pod install`.
110 - **Signing Errors:** Check Team ID and Bundle Identifier.
111 - **Cache:** Xcode ‚Üí Product ‚Üí Clean Build Folder.
112 
113 ---
114 
115 ## üìù DEBUGGING CHECKLIST
116 
117 - [ ] **Is it a JS or Native crash?** (Red screen or home screen?)
118 - [ ] **Did you clean build?** (Native caches are aggressive)
119 - [ ] **Are you on a real device?** (Simulators hide concurrency bugs)
120 - [ ] **Did you check the native logs?** (Not just terminal output)
121 
122 > **Remember:** If JavaScript looks perfect but the app fails, look closer at the Native side.
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F104 ===
