=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F115 path:skills/nodejs-best-practices/SKILL.md hash:e6d0dea6b638c8674370bba370377b2812dfc84268700e55e08f7babb685c17d lines:333 ===
001 ---
002 name: nodejs-best-practices
003 description: Node.js development principles and decision-making. Framework selection, async patterns, security, and architecture. Teaches thinking, not copying.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Write, Edit, Glob, Grep
005 ---
006 
007 # Node.js Best Practices
008 
009 > Principles and decision-making for Node.js development in 2025.
010 > **Learn to THINK, not memorize code patterns.**
011 
012 ---
013 
014 ## ‚ö†Ô∏è How to Use This Skill
015 
016 This skill teaches **decision-making principles**, not fixed code to copy.
017 
018 - ASK user for preferences when unclear
019 - Choose framework/pattern based on CONTEXT
020 - Don't default to same solution every time
021 
022 ---
023 
024 ## 1. Framework Selection (2025)
025 
026 ### Decision Tree
027 
028 ```
029 What are you building?
030 ‚îÇ
031 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Edge/Serverless (Cloudflare, Vercel)
032 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Hono (zero-dependency, ultra-fast cold starts)
033 ‚îÇ
034 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ High Performance API
035 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Fastify (2-3x faster than Express)
036 ‚îÇ
037 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Enterprise/Team familiarity
038 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ NestJS (structured, DI, decorators)
039 ‚îÇ
040 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Legacy/Stable/Maximum ecosystem
041 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Express (mature, most middleware)
042 ‚îÇ
043 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Full-stack with frontend
044     ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Next.js API Routes or tRPC
045 ```
046 
047 ### Comparison Principles
048 
049 | Factor | Hono | Fastify | Express |
050 |--------|------|---------|---------|
051 | **Best for** | Edge, serverless | Performance | Legacy, learning |
052 | **Cold start** | Fastest | Fast | Moderate |
053 | **Ecosystem** | Growing | Good | Largest |
054 | **TypeScript** | Native | Excellent | Good |
055 | **Learning curve** | Low | Medium | Low |
056 
057 ### Selection Questions to Ask:
058 1. What's the deployment target?
059 2. Is cold start time critical?
060 3. Does team have existing experience?
061 4. Is there legacy code to maintain?
062 
063 ---
064 
065 ## 2. Runtime Considerations (2025)
066 
067 ### Native TypeScript
068 
069 ```
070 Node.js 22+: --experimental-strip-types
071 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Run .ts files directly
072 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ No build step needed for simple projects
073 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Consider for: scripts, simple APIs
074 ```
075 
076 ### Module System Decision
077 
078 ```
079 ESM (import/export)
080 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Modern standard
081 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Better tree-shaking
082 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Async module loading
083 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Use for: new projects
084 
085 CommonJS (require)
086 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Legacy compatibility
087 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ More npm packages support
088 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Use for: existing codebases, some edge cases
089 ```
090 
091 ### Runtime Selection
092 
093 | Runtime | Best For |
094 |---------|----------|
095 | **Node.js** | General purpose, largest ecosystem |
096 | **Bun** | Performance, built-in bundler |
097 | **Deno** | Security-first, built-in TypeScript |
098 
099 ---
100 
101 ## 3. Architecture Principles
102 
103 ### Layered Structure Concept
104 
105 ```
106 Request Flow:
107 ‚îÇ
108 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Controller/Route Layer
109 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Handles HTTP specifics
110 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Input validation at boundary
111 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Calls service layer
112 ‚îÇ
113 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Service Layer
114 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Business logic
115 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Framework-agnostic
116 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Calls repository layer
117 ‚îÇ
118 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Repository Layer
119     ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Data access only
120     ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Database queries
121     ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ ORM interactions
122 ```
123 
124 ### Why This Matters:
125 - **Testability**: Mock layers independently
126 - **Flexibility**: Swap database without touching business logic
127 - **Clarity**: Each layer has single responsibility
128 
129 ### When to Simplify:
130 - Small scripts ‚Üí Single file OK
131 - Prototypes ‚Üí Less structure acceptable
132 - Always ask: "Will this grow?"
133 
134 ---
135 
136 ## 4. Error Handling Principles
137 
138 ### Centralized Error Handling
139 
140 ```
141 Pattern:
142 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Create custom error classes
143 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Throw from any layer
144 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Catch at top level (middleware)
145 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Format consistent response
146 ```
147 
148 ### Error Response Philosophy
149 
150 ```
151 Client gets:
152 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Appropriate HTTP status
153 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Error code for programmatic handling
154 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ User-friendly message
155 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ NO internal details (security!)
156 
157 Logs get:
158 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Full stack trace
159 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Request context
160 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ User ID (if applicable)
161 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Timestamp
162 ```
163 
164 ### Status Code Selection
165 
166 | Situation | Status | When |
167 |-----------|--------|------|
168 | Bad input | 400 | Client sent invalid data |
169 | No auth | 401 | Missing or invalid credentials |
170 | No permission | 403 | Valid auth, but not allowed |
171 | Not found | 404 | Resource doesn't exist |
172 | Conflict | 409 | Duplicate or state conflict |
173 | Validation | 422 | Schema valid but business rules fail |
174 | Server error | 500 | Our fault, log everything |
175 
176 ---
177 
178 ## 5. Async Patterns Principles
179 
180 ### When to Use Each
181 
182 | Pattern | Use When |
183 |---------|----------|
184 | `async/await` | Sequential async operations |
185 | `Promise.all` | Parallel independent operations |
186 | `Promise.allSettled` | Parallel where some can fail |
187 | `Promise.race` | Timeout or first response wins |
188 
189 ### Event Loop Awareness
190 
191 ```
192 I/O-bound (async helps):
193 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Database queries
194 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ HTTP requests
195 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ File system
196 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Network operations
197 
198 CPU-bound (async doesn't help):
199 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Crypto operations
200 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Image processing
201 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Complex calculations
202 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ ‚Üí Use worker threads or offload
203 ```
204 
205 ### Avoiding Event Loop Blocking
206 
207 - Never use sync methods in production (fs.readFileSync, etc.)
208 - Offload CPU-intensive work
209 - Use streaming for large data
210 
211 ---
212 
213 ## 6. Validation Principles
214 
215 ### Validate at Boundaries
216 
217 ```
218 Where to validate:
219 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ API entry point (request body/params)
220 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Before database operations
221 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ External data (API responses, file uploads)
222 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Environment variables (startup)
223 ```
224 
225 ### Validation Library Selection
226 
227 | Library | Best For |
228 |---------|----------|
229 | **Zod** | TypeScript first, inference |
230 | **Valibot** | Smaller bundle (tree-shakeable) |
231 | **ArkType** | Performance critical |
232 | **Yup** | Existing React Form usage |
233 
234 ### Validation Philosophy
235 
236 - Fail fast: Validate early
237 - Be specific: Clear error messages
238 - Don't trust: Even "internal" data
239 
240 ---
241 
242 ## 7. Security Principles
243 
244 ### Security Checklist (Not Code)
245 
246 - [ ] **Input validation**: All inputs validated
247 - [ ] **Parameterized queries**: No string concatenation for SQL
248 - [ ] **Password hashing**: bcrypt or argon2
249 - [ ] **JWT verification**: Always verify signature and expiry
250 - [ ] **Rate limiting**: Protect from abuse
251 - [ ] **Security headers**: Helmet.js or equivalent
252 - [ ] **HTTPS**: Everywhere in production
253 - [ ] **CORS**: Properly configured
254 - [ ] **Secrets**: Environment variables only
255 - [ ] **Dependencies**: Regularly audited
256 
257 ### Security Mindset
258 
259 ```
260 Trust nothing:
261 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Query params ‚Üí validate
262 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Request body ‚Üí validate
263 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Headers ‚Üí verify
264 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Cookies ‚Üí validate
265 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ File uploads ‚Üí scan
266 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ External APIs ‚Üí validate response
267 ```
268 
269 ---
270 
271 ## 8. Testing Principles
272 
273 ### Test Strategy Selection
274 
275 | Type | Purpose | Tools |
276 |------|---------|-------|
277 | **Unit** | Business logic | node:test, Vitest |
278 | **Integration** | API endpoints | Supertest |
279 | **E2E** | Full flows | Playwright |
280 
281 ### What to Test (Priorities)
282 
283 1. **Critical paths**: Auth, payments, core business
284 2. **Edge cases**: Empty inputs, boundaries
285 3. **Error handling**: What happens when things fail?
286 4. **Not worth testing**: Framework code, trivial getters
287 
288 ### Built-in Test Runner (Node.js 22+)
289 
290 ```
291 node --test src/**/*.test.ts
292 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ No external dependency
293 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Good coverage reporting
294 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Watch mode available
295 ```
296 
297 ---
298 
299 ## 10. Anti-Patterns to Avoid
300 
301 ### ‚ùå DON'T:
302 - Use Express for new edge projects (use Hono)
303 - Use sync methods in production code
304 - Put business logic in controllers
305 - Skip input validation
306 - Hardcode secrets
307 - Trust external data without validation
308 - Block event loop with CPU work
309 
310 ### ‚úÖ DO:
311 - Choose framework based on context
312 - Ask user for preferences when unclear
313 - Use layered architecture for growing projects
314 - Validate all inputs
315 - Use environment variables for secrets
316 - Profile before optimizing
317 
318 ---
319 
320 ## 11. Decision Checklist
321 
322 Before implementing:
323 
324 - [ ] **Asked user about stack preference?**
325 - [ ] **Chosen framework for THIS context?** (not just default)
326 - [ ] **Considered deployment target?**
327 - [ ] **Planned error handling strategy?**
328 - [ ] **Identified validation points?**
329 - [ ] **Considered security requirements?**
330 
331 ---
332 
333 > **Remember**: Node.js best practices are about decision-making, not memorizing patterns. Every project deserves fresh consideration based on its requirements.

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F116 path:skills/parallel-agents/SKILL.md hash:a623844590ef73ae76a77a7b4ea77aa40b173cc098a4a3ccb0edb50f34401819 lines:175 ===
001 ---

006 
007 # Native Parallel Agents
008 
009 > Orchestration through Antigravity's built-in Agent Tool
010 
011 ## Overview
012 
013 This skill enables coordinating multiple specialized agents through Antigravity's native agent system. Unlike external scripts, this approach keeps all orchestration within Antigravity's control.
014 
015 ## When to Use Orchestration
016 
017 ‚úÖ **Good for:**
018 - Complex tasks requiring multiple expertise domains
019 - Code analysis from security, performance, and quality perspectives
020 - Comprehensive reviews (architecture + security + testing)
021 - Feature implementation needing backend + frontend + database work
022 
023 ‚ùå **Not for:**
024 - Simple, single-domain tasks
025 - Quick fixes or small changes
026 - Tasks where one agent suffices
027 
028 ---
029 
030 ## Native Agent Invocation
031 
032 ### Single Agent
033 ```
034 Use the security-auditor agent to review authentication
035 ```
036 
037 ### Sequential Chain
038 ```
039 First, use the explorer-agent to discover project structure.
040 Then, use the backend-specialist to review API endpoints.
041 Finally, use the test-engineer to identify test gaps.
042 ```
043 
044 ### With Context Passing
045 ```
046 Use the frontend-specialist to analyze React components.
047 Based on those findings, have the test-engineer generate component tests.
048 ```
049 
050 ### Resume Previous Work
051 ```
052 Resume agent [agentId] and continue with additional requirements.
053 ```
054 
055 ---
056 
057 ## Orchestration Patterns
058 
059 ### Pattern 1: Comprehensive Analysis
060 ```
061 Agents: explorer-agent ‚Üí [domain-agents] ‚Üí synthesis
062 
063 1. explorer-agent: Map codebase structure
064 2. security-auditor: Security posture
065 3. backend-specialist: API quality
066 4. frontend-specialist: UI/UX patterns
067 5. test-engineer: Test coverage
068 6. Synthesize all findings
069 ```
070 
071 ### Pattern 2: Feature Review
072 ```
073 Agents: affected-domain-agents ‚Üí test-engineer
074 
075 1. Identify affected domains (backend? frontend? both?)
076 2. Invoke relevant domain agents
077 3. test-engineer verifies changes
078 4. Synthesize recommendations
079 ```
080 
081 ### Pattern 3: Security Audit
082 ```
083 Agents: security-auditor ‚Üí penetration-tester ‚Üí synthesis
084 
085 1. security-auditor: Configuration and code review
086 2. penetration-tester: Active vulnerability testing
087 3. Synthesize with prioritized remediation
088 ```
089 
090 ---
091 
092 ## Available Agents
093 
094 | Agent | Expertise | Trigger Phrases |
095 |-------|-----------|-----------------|
096 | `orchestrator` | Coordination | "comprehensive", "multi-perspective" |
097 | `security-auditor` | Security | "security", "auth", "vulnerabilities" |
098 | `penetration-tester` | Security Testing | "pentest", "red team", "exploit" |
099 | `backend-specialist` | Backend | "API", "server", "Node.js", "Express" |
100 | `frontend-specialist` | Frontend | "React", "UI", "components", "Next.js" |
101 | `test-engineer` | Testing | "tests", "coverage", "TDD" |
102 | `devops-engineer` | DevOps | "deploy", "CI/CD", "infrastructure" |
103 | `database-architect` | Database | "schema", "Prisma", "migrations" |
104 | `mobile-developer` | Mobile | "React Native", "Flutter", "mobile" |
105 | `api-designer` | API Design | "REST", "GraphQL", "OpenAPI" |
106 | `debugger` | Debugging | "bug", "error", "not working" |
107 | `explorer-agent` | Discovery | "explore", "map", "structure" |
108 | `documentation-writer` | Documentation | "write docs", "create README", "generate API docs" |
109 | `performance-optimizer` | Performance | "slow", "optimize", "profiling" |
110 | `project-planner` | Planning | "plan", "roadmap", "milestones" |
111 | `seo-specialist` | SEO | "SEO", "meta tags", "search ranking" |
112 | `game-developer` | Game Development | "game", "Unity", "Godot", "Phaser" |
113 
114 ---
115 
116 ## Antigravity Built-in Agents
117 
118 These work alongside custom agents:
119 
120 | Agent | Model | Purpose |
121 |-------|-------|---------|
122 | **Explore** | Haiku | Fast read-only codebase search |
123 | **Plan** | Sonnet | Research during plan mode |
124 | **General-purpose** | Sonnet | Complex multi-step modifications |
125 
126 Use **Explore** for quick searches, **custom agents** for domain expertise.
127 
128 ---
129 
130 ## Synthesis Protocol
131 
132 After all agents complete, synthesize:
133 
134 ```markdown
135 ## Orchestration Synthesis
136 
137 ### Task Summary
138 [What was accomplished]
139 
140 ### Agent Contributions
141 | Agent | Finding |
142 |-------|---------|
143 | security-auditor | Found X |
144 | backend-specialist | Identified Y |
145 
146 ### Consolidated Recommendations
147 1. **Critical**: [Issue from Agent A]
148 2. **Important**: [Issue from Agent B]
149 3. **Nice-to-have**: [Enhancement from Agent C]
150 
151 ### Action Items
152 - [ ] Fix critical security issue
153 - [ ] Refactor API endpoint
154 - [ ] Add missing tests
155 ```
156 
157 ---
158 
159 ## Best Practices
160 
161 1. **Available agents** - 17 specialized agents can be orchestrated
162 2. **Logical order** - Discovery ‚Üí Analysis ‚Üí Implementation ‚Üí Testing
163 3. **Share context** - Pass relevant findings to subsequent agents
164 4. **Single synthesis** - One unified report, not separate outputs
165 5. **Verify changes** - Always include test-engineer for code modifications
166 
167 ---
168 
169 ## Key Benefits
170 
171 - ‚úÖ **Single session** - All agents share context
172 - ‚úÖ **AI-controlled** - Claude orchestrates autonomously
173 - ‚úÖ **Native integration** - Works with built-in Explore, Plan agents
174 - ‚úÖ **Resume support** - Can continue previous agent work
175 - ‚úÖ **Context passing** - Findings flow between agents

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F117 path:skills/performance-profiling/SKILL.md hash:5e58efdd8fd951cf89910c65317b7b7bcc5bf8fde9317e32f4a751fa208d8ff2 lines:143 ===
001 ---
002 name: performance-profiling
003 description: Performance profiling principles. Measurement, analysis, and optimization techniques.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Glob, Grep, Bash
005 ---
006 
007 # Performance Profiling
008 
009 > Measure, analyze, optimize - in that order.
010 
011 ## üîß Runtime Scripts
012 
013 **Execute these for automated profiling:**
014 
015 | Script | Purpose | Usage |
016 |--------|---------|-------|
017 | `scripts/lighthouse_audit.py` | Lighthouse performance audit | `python scripts/lighthouse_audit.py https://example.com` |
018 
019 ---
020 
021 ## 1. Core Web Vitals
022 
023 ### Targets
024 
025 | Metric | Good | Poor | Measures |
026 |--------|------|------|----------|
027 | **LCP** | < 2.5s | > 4.0s | Loading |
028 | **INP** | < 200ms | > 500ms | Interactivity |
029 | **CLS** | < 0.1 | > 0.25 | Stability |
030 
031 ### When to Measure
032 
033 | Stage | Tool |
034 |-------|------|
035 | Development | Local Lighthouse |
036 | CI/CD | Lighthouse CI |
037 | Production | RUM (Real User Monitoring) |
038 
039 ---
040 
041 ## 2. Profiling Workflow
042 
043 ### The 4-Step Process
044 
045 ```
046 1. BASELINE ‚Üí Measure current state
047 2. IDENTIFY ‚Üí Find the bottleneck
048 3. FIX ‚Üí Make targeted change
049 4. VALIDATE ‚Üí Confirm improvement
050 ```
051 
052 ### Profiling Tool Selection
053 
054 | Problem | Tool |
055 |---------|------|
056 | Page load | Lighthouse |
057 | Bundle size | Bundle analyzer |
058 | Runtime | DevTools Performance |
059 | Memory | DevTools Memory |
060 | Network | DevTools Network |
061 
062 ---
063 
064 ## 3. Bundle Analysis
065 
066 ### What to Look For
067 
068 | Issue | Indicator |
069 |-------|-----------|
070 | Large dependencies | Top of bundle |
071 | Duplicate code | Multiple chunks |
072 | Unused code | Low coverage |
073 | Missing splits | Single large chunk |
074 
075 ### Optimization Actions
076 
077 | Finding | Action |
078 |---------|--------|
079 | Big library | Import specific modules |
080 | Duplicate deps | Dedupe, update versions |
081 | Route in main | Code split |
082 | Unused exports | Tree shake |
083 
084 ---
085 
086 ## 4. Runtime Profiling
087 
088 ### Performance Tab Analysis
089 
090 | Pattern | Meaning |
091 |---------|---------|
092 | Long tasks (>50ms) | UI blocking |
093 | Many small tasks | Possible batching opportunity |
094 | Layout/paint | Rendering bottleneck |
095 | Script | JavaScript execution |
096 
097 ### Memory Tab Analysis
098 
099 | Pattern | Meaning |
100 |---------|---------|
101 | Growing heap | Possible leak |
102 | Large retained | Check references |
103 | Detached DOM | Not cleaned up |
104 
105 ---
106 
107 ## 5. Common Bottlenecks
108 
109 ### By Symptom
110 
111 | Symptom | Likely Cause |
112 |---------|--------------|
113 | Slow initial load | Large JS, render blocking |
114 | Slow interactions | Heavy event handlers |
115 | Jank during scroll | Layout thrashing |
116 | Growing memory | Leaks, retained refs |
117 
118 ---
119 
120 ## 6. Quick Win Priorities
121 
122 | Priority | Action | Impact |
123 |----------|--------|--------|
124 | 1 | Enable compression | High |
125 | 2 | Lazy load images | High |
126 | 3 | Code split routes | High |
127 | 4 | Cache static assets | Medium |
128 | 5 | Optimize images | Medium |
129 
130 ---
131 
132 ## 7. Anti-Patterns
133 
134 | ‚ùå Don't | ‚úÖ Do |
135 |----------|-------|
136 | Guess at problems | Profile first |
137 | Micro-optimize | Fix biggest issue |
138 | Optimize early | Optimize when needed |
139 | Ignore real users | Use RUM data |
140 
141 ---
142 
143 > **Remember:** The fastest code is code that doesn't run. Remove before optimizing.

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F118 path:skills/plan-writing/SKILL.md hash:93cd02ab3c431913845d0dd2bed7649cb4636785314cec4cfdb3f4a403f97f68 lines:152 ===
001 ---
002 name: plan-writing
003 description: Structured task planning with clear breakdowns, dependencies, and verification criteria. Use when implementing features, refactoring, or any multi-step work.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Glob, Grep
005 ---
006 
007 # Plan Writing
008 
009 > Source: obra/superpowers
010 
011 ## Overview
012 This skill provides a framework for breaking down work into clear, actionable tasks with verification criteria.
013 
014 ## Task Breakdown Principles
015 
016 ### 1. Small, Focused Tasks
017 - Each task should take 2-5 minutes
018 - One clear outcome per task
019 - Independently verifiable
020 
021 ### 2. Clear Verification
022 - How do you know it's done?
023 - What can you check/test?
024 - What's the expected output?
025 
026 ### 3. Logical Ordering
027 - Dependencies identified
028 - Parallel work where possible
029 - Critical path highlighted
030 - **Phase X: Verification is always LAST**
031 
032 ### 4. Dynamic Naming in Project Root
033 - Plan files are saved as `{task-slug}.md` in the PROJECT ROOT
034 - Name derived from task (e.g., "add auth" ‚Üí `auth-feature.md`)
035 - **NEVER** inside `.claude/`, `docs/`, or temp folders
036 
037 ## Planning Principles (NOT Templates!)
038 
039 > üî¥ **NO fixed templates. Each plan is UNIQUE to the task.**
040 
041 ### Principle 1: Keep It SHORT
042 
043 | ‚ùå Wrong | ‚úÖ Right |
044 |----------|----------|
045 | 50 tasks with sub-sub-tasks | 5-10 clear tasks max |
046 | Every micro-step listed | Only actionable items |
047 | Verbose descriptions | One-line per task |
048 
049 > **Rule:** If plan is longer than 1 page, it's too long. Simplify.
050 
051 ---
052 
053 ### Principle 2: Be SPECIFIC, Not Generic
054 
055 | ‚ùå Wrong | ‚úÖ Right |
056 |----------|----------|
057 | "Set up project" | "Run `npx create-next-app`" |
058 | "Add authentication" | "Install next-auth, create `/api/auth/[...nextauth].ts`" |
059 | "Style the UI" | "Add Tailwind classes to `Header.tsx`" |
060 
061 > **Rule:** Each task should have a clear, verifiable outcome.
062 
063 ---
064 
065 ### Principle 3: Dynamic Content Based on Project Type
066 
067 **For NEW PROJECT:**
068 - What tech stack? (decide first)
069 - What's the MVP? (minimal features)
070 - What's the file structure?
071 
072 **For FEATURE ADDITION:**
073 - Which files are affected?
074 - What dependencies needed?
075 - How to verify it works?
076 
077 **For BUG FIX:**
078 - What's the root cause?
079 - What file/line to change?
080 - How to test the fix?
081 
082 ---
083 
084 ### Principle 4: Scripts Are Project-Specific
085 
086 > üî¥ **DO NOT copy-paste script commands. Choose based on project type.**
087 
088 | Project Type | Relevant Scripts |
089 |--------------|------------------|
090 | Frontend/React | `ux_audit.py`, `accessibility_checker.py` |
091 | Backend/API | `api_validator.py`, `security_scan.py` |
092 | Mobile | `mobile_audit.py` |
093 | Database | `schema_validator.py` |
094 | Full-stack | Mix of above based on what you touched |
095 
096 **Wrong:** Adding all scripts to every plan
097 **Right:** Only scripts relevant to THIS task
098 
099 ---
100 
101 ### Principle 5: Verification is Simple
102 
103 | ‚ùå Wrong | ‚úÖ Right |
104 |----------|----------|
105 | "Verify the component works correctly" | "Run `npm run dev`, click button, see toast" |
106 | "Test the API" | "curl localhost:3000/api/users returns 200" |
107 | "Check styles" | "Open browser, verify dark mode toggle works" |
108 
109 ---
110 
111 ## Plan Structure (Flexible, Not Fixed!)
112 
113 ```
114 # [Task Name]
115 
116 ## Goal
117 One sentence: What are we building/fixing?
118 
119 ## Tasks
120 - [ ] Task 1: [Specific action] ‚Üí Verify: [How to check]
121 - [ ] Task 2: [Specific action] ‚Üí Verify: [How to check]
122 - [ ] Task 3: [Specific action] ‚Üí Verify: [How to check]
123 
124 ## Done When
125 - [ ] [Main success criteria]
126 ```
127 
128 > **That's it.** No phases, no sub-sections unless truly needed.
129 > Keep it minimal. Add complexity only when required.
130 
131 ## Notes
132 [Any important considerations]
133 ```
134 
135 ---
136 
137 ## Best Practices (Quick Reference)
138 
139 1. **Start with goal** - What are we building/fixing?
140 2. **Max 10 tasks** - If more, break into multiple plans
141 3. **Each task verifiable** - Clear "done" criteria
142 4. **Project-specific** - No copy-paste templates
143 5. **Update as you go** - Mark `[x]` when complete
144 
145 ---
146 
147 ## When to Use
148 
149 - New project from scratch
150 - Adding a feature
151 - Fixing a bug (if complex)
152 - Refactoring multiple files
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F118 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F119 path:skills/powershell-windows/SKILL.md hash:e902ee8d16b3fe50d8c53d7612fbfce4c97526ec4d069e7738e14bc9ae3acacb lines:167 ===
001 ---
002 name: powershell-windows
003 description: PowerShell Windows patterns. Critical pitfalls, operator syntax, error handling.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Write, Edit, Glob, Grep, Bash
005 ---
006 
007 # PowerShell Windows Patterns
008 
009 > Critical patterns and pitfalls for Windows PowerShell.
010 
011 ---
012 
013 ## 1. Operator Syntax Rules
014 
015 ### CRITICAL: Parentheses Required
016 
017 | ‚ùå Wrong | ‚úÖ Correct |
018 |----------|-----------|
019 | `if (Test-Path "a" -or Test-Path "b")` | `if ((Test-Path "a") -or (Test-Path "b"))` |
020 | `if (Get-Item $x -and $y -eq 5)` | `if ((Get-Item $x) -and ($y -eq 5))` |
021 
022 **Rule:** Each cmdlet call MUST be in parentheses when using logical operators.
023 
024 ---
025 
026 ## 2. Unicode/Emoji Restriction
027 
028 ### CRITICAL: No Unicode in Scripts
029 
030 | Purpose | ‚ùå Don't Use | ‚úÖ Use |
031 |---------|-------------|--------|
032 | Success | ‚úÖ ‚úì | [OK] [+] |
033 | Error | ‚ùå ‚úó üî¥ | [!] [X] |
034 | Warning | ‚ö†Ô∏è üü° | [*] [WARN] |
035 | Info | ‚ÑπÔ∏è üîµ | [i] [INFO] |
036 | Progress | ‚è≥ | [...] |
037 
038 **Rule:** Use ASCII characters only in PowerShell scripts.
039 
040 ---
041 
042 ## 3. Null Check Patterns
043 
044 ### Always Check Before Access
045 
046 | ‚ùå Wrong | ‚úÖ Correct |
047 |----------|-----------|
048 | `$array.Count -gt 0` | `$array -and $array.Count -gt 0` |
049 | `$text.Length` | `if ($text) { $text.Length }` |
050 
051 ---
052 
053 ## 4. String Interpolation
054 
055 ### Complex Expressions
056 
057 | ‚ùå Wrong | ‚úÖ Correct |
058 |----------|-----------|
059 | `"Value: $($obj.prop.sub)"` | Store in variable first |
060 
061 **Pattern:**
062 ```
063 $value = $obj.prop.sub
064 Write-Output "Value: $value"
065 ```
066 
067 ---
068 
069 ## 5. Error Handling
070 
071 ### ErrorActionPreference
072 
073 | Value | Use |
074 |-------|-----|
075 | Stop | Development (fail fast) |
076 | Continue | Production scripts |
077 | SilentlyContinue | When errors expected |
078 
079 ### Try/Catch Pattern
080 
081 - Don't return inside try block
082 - Use finally for cleanup
083 - Return after try/catch
084 
085 ---
086 
087 ## 6. File Paths
088 
089 ### Windows Path Rules
090 
091 | Pattern | Use |
092 |---------|-----|
093 | Literal path | `C:\Users\User\file.txt` |
094 | Variable path | `Join-Path $env:USERPROFILE "file.txt"` |
095 | Relative | `Join-Path $ScriptDir "data"` |
096 
097 **Rule:** Use Join-Path for cross-platform safety.
098 
099 ---
100 
101 ## 7. Array Operations
102 
103 ### Correct Patterns
104 
105 | Operation | Syntax |
106 |-----------|--------|
107 | Empty array | `$array = @()` |
108 | Add item | `$array += $item` |
109 | ArrayList add | `$list.Add($item) | Out-Null` |
110 
111 ---
112 
113 ## 8. JSON Operations
114 
115 ### CRITICAL: Depth Parameter
116 
117 | ‚ùå Wrong | ‚úÖ Correct |
118 |----------|-----------|
119 | `ConvertTo-Json` | `ConvertTo-Json -Depth 10` |
120 
121 **Rule:** Always specify `-Depth` for nested objects.
122 
123 ### File Operations
124 
125 | Operation | Pattern |
126 |-----------|---------|
127 | Read | `Get-Content "file.json" -Raw | ConvertFrom-Json` |
128 | Write | `$data | ConvertTo-Json -Depth 10 | Out-File "file.json" -Encoding UTF8` |
129 
130 ---
131 
132 ## 9. Common Errors
133 
134 | Error Message | Cause | Fix |
135 |---------------|-------|-----|
136 | "parameter 'or'" | Missing parentheses | Wrap cmdlets in () |
137 | "Unexpected token" | Unicode character | Use ASCII only |
138 | "Cannot find property" | Null object | Check null first |
139 | "Cannot convert" | Type mismatch | Use .ToString() |
140 
141 ---
142 
143 ## 10. Script Template
144 
145 ```powershell
146 # Strict mode
147 Set-StrictMode -Version Latest
148 $ErrorActionPreference = "Continue"
149 
150 # Paths
151 $ScriptDir = Split-Path -Parent $MyInvocation.MyCommand.Path
152 
153 # Main
154 try {
155     # Logic here
156     Write-Output "[OK] Done"
157     exit 0
158 }
159 catch {
160     Write-Warning "Error: $_"
161     exit 1
162 }
163 ```
164 
165 ---
166 
167 > **Remember:** PowerShell has unique syntax rules. Parentheses, ASCII-only, and null checks are non-negotiable.
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F119 ===

001 ---

006 
007 # Python Patterns
008 
009 > Python development principles and decision-making for 2025.
010 > **Learn to THINK, not memorize patterns.**
011 
012 ---
013 
014 ## ‚ö†Ô∏è How to Use This Skill
015 
016 This skill teaches **decision-making principles**, not fixed code to copy.
017 
018 - ASK user for framework preference when unclear
019 - Choose async vs sync based on CONTEXT
020 - Don't default to same framework every time
021 
022 ---
023 
024 ## 1. Framework Selection (2025)
025 
026 ### Decision Tree
027 
028 ```
029 What are you building?
030 ‚îÇ
031 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ API-first / Microservices
032 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ FastAPI (async, modern, fast)
033 ‚îÇ
034 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Full-stack web / CMS / Admin
035 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Django (batteries-included)
036 ‚îÇ
037 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Simple / Script / Learning
038 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Flask (minimal, flexible)
039 ‚îÇ
040 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ AI/ML API serving
041 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ FastAPI (Pydantic, async, uvicorn)
042 ‚îÇ
043 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Background workers
044     ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Celery + any framework
045 ```
046 
047 ### Comparison Principles
048 
049 | Factor | FastAPI | Django | Flask |
050 |--------|---------|--------|-------|
051 | **Best for** | APIs, microservices | Full-stack, CMS | Simple, learning |
052 | **Async** | Native | Django 5.0+ | Via extensions |
053 | **Admin** | Manual | Built-in | Via extensions |
054 | **ORM** | Choose your own | Django ORM | Choose your own |
055 | **Learning curve** | Low | Medium | Low |
056 
057 ### Selection Questions to Ask:
058 1. Is this API-only or full-stack?
059 2. Need admin interface?
060 3. Team familiar with async?
061 4. Existing infrastructure?
062 
063 ---
064 
065 ## 2. Async vs Sync Decision
066 
067 ### When to Use Async
068 
069 ```
070 async def is better when:
071 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ I/O-bound operations (database, HTTP, file)
072 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Many concurrent connections
073 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Real-time features
074 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Microservices communication
075 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ FastAPI/Starlette/Django ASGI
076 
077 def (sync) is better when:
078 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ CPU-bound operations
079 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Simple scripts
080 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Legacy codebase
081 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Team unfamiliar with async
082 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Blocking libraries (no async version)
083 ```
084 
085 ### The Golden Rule
086 
087 ```
088 I/O-bound ‚Üí async (waiting for external)
089 CPU-bound ‚Üí sync + multiprocessing (computing)
090 
091 Don't:
092 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Mix sync and async carelessly
093 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Use sync libraries in async code
094 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Force async for CPU work
095 ```
096 
097 ### Async Library Selection
098 
099 | Need | Async Library |
100 |------|---------------|
101 | HTTP client | httpx |
102 | PostgreSQL | asyncpg |
103 | Redis | aioredis / redis-py async |
104 | File I/O | aiofiles |
105 | Database ORM | SQLAlchemy 2.0 async, Tortoise |
106 
107 ---
108 
109 ## 3. Type Hints Strategy
110 
111 ### When to Type
112 
113 ```
114 Always type:
115 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Function parameters
116 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Return types
117 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Class attributes
118 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Public APIs
119 
120 Can skip:
121 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Local variables (let inference work)
122 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ One-off scripts
123 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Tests (usually)
124 ```
125 
126 ### Common Type Patterns
127 
128 ```python
129 # These are patterns, understand them:
130 
131 # Optional ‚Üí might be None
132 from typing import Optional
133 def find_user(id: int) -> Optional[User]: ...
134 
135 # Union ‚Üí one of multiple types
136 def process(data: str | dict) -> None: ...
137 
138 # Generic collections
139 def get_items() -> list[Item]: ...
140 def get_mapping() -> dict[str, int]: ...
141 
142 # Callable
143 from typing import Callable
144 def apply(fn: Callable[[int], str]) -> str: ...
145 ```
146 
147 ### Pydantic for Validation
148 
149 ```
150 When to use Pydantic:
151 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ API request/response models
152 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Configuration/settings
153 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Data validation
154 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Serialization
155 
156 Benefits:
157 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Runtime validation
158 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Auto-generated JSON schema
159 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Works with FastAPI natively
160 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Clear error messages
161 ```
162 
163 ---
164 
165 ## 4. Project Structure Principles
166 
167 ### Structure Selection
168 
169 ```
170 Small project / Script:
171 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ main.py
172 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ utils.py
173 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ requirements.txt
174 
175 Medium API:
176 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ app/
177 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ __init__.py
178 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ main.py
179 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ models/
180 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ routes/
181 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ services/
182 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ schemas/
183 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ tests/
184 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ pyproject.toml
185 
186 Large application:
187 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ src/
188 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ myapp/
189 ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ core/
190 ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ api/
191 ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ services/
192 ‚îÇ       ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ models/
193 ‚îÇ       ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ ...
194 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ tests/
195 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ pyproject.toml
196 ```
197 
198 ### FastAPI Structure Principles
199 
200 ```
201 Organize by feature or layer:
202 
203 By layer:
204 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ routes/ (API endpoints)
205 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ services/ (business logic)
206 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ models/ (database models)
207 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ schemas/ (Pydantic models)
208 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ dependencies/ (shared deps)
209 
210 By feature:
211 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ users/
212 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ routes.py
213 ‚îÇ   ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ service.py
214 ‚îÇ   ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ schemas.py
215 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ products/
216     ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ ...
217 ```
218 
219 ---
220 
221 ## 5. Django Principles (2025)
222 
223 ### Django Async (Django 5.0+)
224 
225 ```
226 Django supports async:
227 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Async views
228 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Async middleware
229 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Async ORM (limited)
230 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ ASGI deployment
231 
232 When to use async in Django:
233 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ External API calls
234 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ WebSocket (Channels)
235 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ High-concurrency views
236 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Background task triggering
237 ```
238 
239 ### Django Best Practices
240 
241 ```
242 Model design:
243 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Fat models, thin views
244 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Use managers for common queries
245 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Abstract base classes for shared fields
246 
247 Views:
248 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Class-based for complex CRUD
249 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Function-based for simple endpoints
250 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Use viewsets with DRF
251 
252 Queries:
253 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ select_related() for FKs
254 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ prefetch_related() for M2M
255 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Avoid N+1 queries
256 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Use .only() for specific fields
257 ```
258 
259 ---
260 
261 ## 6. FastAPI Principles
262 
263 ### async def vs def in FastAPI
264 
265 ```
266 Use async def when:
267 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Using async database drivers
268 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Making async HTTP calls
269 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ I/O-bound operations
270 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Want to handle concurrency
271 
272 Use def when:
273 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Blocking operations
274 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Sync database drivers
275 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ CPU-bound work
276 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ FastAPI runs in threadpool automatically
277 ```
278 
279 ### Dependency Injection
280 
281 ```
282 Use dependencies for:
283 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Database sessions
284 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Current user / Auth
285 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Configuration
286 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Shared resources
287 
288 Benefits:
289 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Testability (mock dependencies)
290 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Clean separation
291 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Automatic cleanup (yield)
292 ```
293 
294 ### Pydantic v2 Integration
295 
296 ```python
297 # FastAPI + Pydantic are tightly integrated:
298 
299 # Request validation
300 @app.post("/users")
301 async def create(user: UserCreate) -> UserResponse:
302     # user is already validated
303     ...
304 
305 # Response serialization
306 # Return type becomes response schema
307 ```
308 
309 ---
310 
311 ## 7. Background Tasks
312 
313 ### Selection Guide
314 
315 | Solution | Best For |
316 |----------|----------|
317 | **BackgroundTasks** | Simple, in-process tasks |
318 | **Celery** | Distributed, complex workflows |
319 | **ARQ** | Async, Redis-based |
320 | **RQ** | Simple Redis queue |
321 | **Dramatiq** | Actor-based, simpler than Celery |
322 
323 ### When to Use Each
324 
325 ```
326 FastAPI BackgroundTasks:
327 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Quick operations
328 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ No persistence needed
329 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Fire-and-forget
330 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Same process
331 
332 Celery/ARQ:
333 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Long-running tasks
334 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Need retry logic
335 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Distributed workers
336 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Persistent queue
337 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Complex workflows
338 ```
339 
340 ---
341 
342 ## 8. Error Handling Principles
343 
344 ### Exception Strategy
345 
346 ```
347 In FastAPI:
348 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Create custom exception classes
349 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Register exception handlers
350 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Return consistent error format
351 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Log without exposing internals
352 
353 Pattern:
354 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Raise domain exceptions in services
355 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Catch and transform in handlers
356 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Client gets clean error response
357 ```
358 
359 ### Error Response Philosophy
360 
361 ```
362 Include:
363 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Error code (programmatic)
364 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Message (human readable)
365 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Details (field-level when applicable)
366 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ NOT stack traces (security)
367 ```
368 
369 ---
370 
371 ## 9. Testing Principles
372 
373 ### Testing Strategy
374 
375 | Type | Purpose | Tools |
376 |------|---------|-------|
377 | **Unit** | Business logic | pytest |
378 | **Integration** | API endpoints | pytest + httpx/TestClient |
379 | **E2E** | Full workflows | pytest + DB |
380 
381 ### Async Testing
382 
383 ```python
384 # Use pytest-asyncio for async tests
385 
386 import pytest
387 from httpx import AsyncClient
388 
389 @pytest.mark.asyncio
390 async def test_endpoint():
391     async with AsyncClient(app=app, base_url="http://test") as client:
392         response = await client.get("/users")
393         assert response.status_code == 200
394 ```
395 
396 ### Fixtures Strategy
397 
398 ```
399 Common fixtures:
400 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ db_session ‚Üí Database connection
401 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ client ‚Üí Test client
402 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ authenticated_user ‚Üí User with token
403 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ sample_data ‚Üí Test data setup
404 ```
405 
406 ---
407 
408 ## 10. Decision Checklist
409 
410 Before implementing:
411 
412 - [ ] **Asked user about framework preference?**
413 - [ ] **Chosen framework for THIS context?** (not just default)
414 - [ ] **Decided async vs sync?**
415 - [ ] **Planned type hint strategy?**
416 - [ ] **Defined project structure?**
417 - [ ] **Planned error handling?**
418 - [ ] **Considered background tasks?**
419 
420 ---
421 
422 ## 11. Anti-Patterns to Avoid
423 
424 ### ‚ùå DON'T:
425 - Default to Django for simple APIs (FastAPI may be better)
426 - Use sync libraries in async code
427 - Skip type hints for public APIs
428 - Put business logic in routes/views
429 - Ignore N+1 queries
430 - Mix async and sync carelessly
431 
432 ### ‚úÖ DO:
433 - Choose framework based on context
434 - Ask about async requirements
435 - Use Pydantic for validation
436 - Separate concerns (routes ‚Üí services ‚Üí repos)
437 - Test critical paths
438 
439 ---
440 
441 > **Remember**: Python patterns are about decision-making for YOUR specific context. Don't copy code‚Äîthink about what serves your application best.
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F120 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F121 path:skills/react-patterns/SKILL.md hash:b10579e408d1a03dca9f23c62648c8b669e8a18a9f119a48860b9aa44f397b81 lines:198 ===
001 ---
002 name: react-patterns
003 description: Modern React patterns and principles. Hooks, composition, performance, TypeScript best practices.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Write, Edit, Glob, Grep
005 ---
006 
007 # React Patterns
008 
009 > Principles for building production-ready React applications.
010 
011 ---
012 
013 ## 1. Component Design Principles
014 
015 ### Component Types
016 
017 | Type | Use | State |
018 |------|-----|-------|
019 | **Server** | Data fetching, static | None |
020 | **Client** | Interactivity | useState, effects |
021 | **Presentational** | UI display | Props only |
022 | **Container** | Logic/state | Heavy state |
023 
024 ### Design Rules
025 
026 - One responsibility per component
027 - Props down, events up
028 - Composition over inheritance
029 - Prefer small, focused components
030 
031 ---
032 
033 ## 2. Hook Patterns
034 
035 ### When to Extract Hooks
036 
037 | Pattern | Extract When |
038 |---------|-------------|
039 | **useLocalStorage** | Same storage logic needed |
040 | **useDebounce** | Multiple debounced values |
041 | **useFetch** | Repeated fetch patterns |
042 | **useForm** | Complex form state |
043 
044 ### Hook Rules
045 
046 - Hooks at top level only
047 - Same order every render
048 - Custom hooks start with "use"
049 - Clean up effects on unmount
050 
051 ---
052 
053 ## 3. State Management Selection
054 
055 | Complexity | Solution |
056 |------------|----------|
057 | Simple | useState, useReducer |
058 | Shared local | Context |
059 | Server state | React Query, SWR |
060 | Complex global | Zustand, Redux Toolkit |
061 
062 ### State Placement
063 
064 | Scope | Where |
065 |-------|-------|
066 | Single component | useState |
067 | Parent-child | Lift state up |
068 | Subtree | Context |
069 | App-wide | Global store |
070 
071 ---
072 
073 ## 4. React 19 Patterns
074 
075 ### New Hooks
076 
077 | Hook | Purpose |
078 |------|---------|
079 | **useActionState** | Form submission state |
080 | **useOptimistic** | Optimistic UI updates |
081 | **use** | Read resources in render |
082 
083 ### Compiler Benefits
084 
085 - Automatic memoization
086 - Less manual useMemo/useCallback
087 - Focus on pure components
088 
089 ---
090 
091 ## 5. Composition Patterns
092 
093 ### Compound Components
094 
095 - Parent provides context
096 - Children consume context
097 - Flexible slot-based composition
098 - Example: Tabs, Accordion, Dropdown
099 
100 ### Render Props vs Hooks
101 
102 | Use Case | Prefer |
103 |----------|--------|
104 | Reusable logic | Custom hook |
105 | Render flexibility | Render props |
106 | Cross-cutting | Higher-order component |
107 
108 ---
109 
110 ## 6. Performance Principles
111 
112 ### When to Optimize
113 
114 | Signal | Action |
115 |--------|--------|
116 | Slow renders | Profile first |
117 | Large lists | Virtualize |
118 | Expensive calc | useMemo |
119 | Stable callbacks | useCallback |
120 
121 ### Optimization Order
122 
123 1. Check if actually slow
124 2. Profile with DevTools
125 3. Identify bottleneck
126 4. Apply targeted fix
127 
128 ---
129 
130 ## 7. Error Handling
131 
132 ### Error Boundary Usage
133 
134 | Scope | Placement |
135 |-------|-----------|
136 | App-wide | Root level |
137 | Feature | Route/feature level |
138 | Component | Around risky component |
139 
140 ### Error Recovery
141 
142 - Show fallback UI
143 - Log error
144 - Offer retry option
145 - Preserve user data
146 
147 ---
148 
149 ## 8. TypeScript Patterns
150 
151 ### Props Typing
152 
153 | Pattern | Use |
154 |---------|-----|
155 | Interface | Component props |
156 | Type | Unions, complex |
157 | Generic | Reusable components |
158 
159 ### Common Types
160 
161 | Need | Type |
162 |------|------|
163 | Children | ReactNode |
164 | Event handler | MouseEventHandler |
165 | Ref | RefObject<Element> |
166 
167 ---
168 
169 ## 9. Testing Principles
170 
171 | Level | Focus |
172 |-------|-------|
173 | Unit | Pure functions, hooks |
174 | Integration | Component behavior |
175 | E2E | User flows |
176 
177 ### Test Priorities
178 
179 - User-visible behavior
180 - Edge cases
181 - Error states
182 - Accessibility
183 
184 ---
185 
186 ## 10. Anti-Patterns
187 
188 | ‚ùå Don't | ‚úÖ Do |
189 |----------|-------|
190 | Prop drilling deep | Use context |
191 | Giant components | Split smaller |
192 | useEffect for everything | Server components |
193 | Premature optimization | Profile first |
194 | Index as key | Stable unique ID |
195 
196 ---
197 
198 > **Remember:** React is about composition. Build small, combine thoughtfully.

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F122 path:skills/red-team-tactics/SKILL.md hash:7cc6a5c25dc015f9a5d7035f1612f40716bd33a0b11659726397322d7d836587 lines:199 ===
001 ---
002 name: red-team-tactics
003 description: Red team tactics principles based on MITRE ATT&CK. Attack phases, detection evasion, reporting.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Glob, Grep
005 ---
006 
007 # Red Team Tactics
008 
009 > Adversary simulation principles based on MITRE ATT&CK framework.
010 
011 ---
012 
013 ## 1. MITRE ATT&CK Phases
014 
015 ### Attack Lifecycle
016 
017 ```
018 RECONNAISSANCE ‚Üí INITIAL ACCESS ‚Üí EXECUTION ‚Üí PERSISTENCE
019        ‚Üì              ‚Üì              ‚Üì            ‚Üì
020    PRIVILEGE ESC ‚Üí DEFENSE EVASION ‚Üí CRED ACCESS ‚Üí DISCOVERY
021        ‚Üì              ‚Üì              ‚Üì            ‚Üì
022 LATERAL MOVEMENT ‚Üí COLLECTION ‚Üí C2 ‚Üí EXFILTRATION ‚Üí IMPACT
023 ```
024 
025 ### Phase Objectives
026 
027 | Phase | Objective |
028 |-------|-----------|
029 | **Recon** | Map attack surface |
030 | **Initial Access** | Get first foothold |
031 | **Execution** | Run code on target |
032 | **Persistence** | Survive reboots |
033 | **Privilege Escalation** | Get admin/root |
034 | **Defense Evasion** | Avoid detection |
035 | **Credential Access** | Harvest credentials |
036 | **Discovery** | Map internal network |
037 | **Lateral Movement** | Spread to other systems |
038 | **Collection** | Gather target data |
039 | **C2** | Maintain command channel |
040 | **Exfiltration** | Extract data |
041 
042 ---
043 
044 ## 2. Reconnaissance Principles
045 
046 ### Passive vs Active
047 
048 | Type | Trade-off |
049 |------|-----------|
050 | **Passive** | No target contact, limited info |
051 | **Active** | Direct contact, more detection risk |
052 
053 ### Information Targets
054 
055 | Category | Value |
056 |----------|-------|
057 | Technology stack | Attack vector selection |
058 | Employee info | Social engineering |
059 | Network ranges | Scanning scope |
060 | Third parties | Supply chain attack |
061 
062 ---
063 
064 ## 3. Initial Access Vectors
065 
066 ### Selection Criteria
067 
068 | Vector | When to Use |
069 |--------|-------------|
070 | **Phishing** | Human target, email access |
071 | **Public exploits** | Vulnerable services exposed |
072 | **Valid credentials** | Leaked or cracked |
073 | **Supply chain** | Third-party access |
074 
075 ---
076 
077 ## 4. Privilege Escalation Principles
078 
079 ### Windows Targets
080 
081 | Check | Opportunity |
082 |-------|-------------|
083 | Unquoted service paths | Write to path |
084 | Weak service permissions | Modify service |
085 | Token privileges | Abuse SeDebug, etc. |
086 | Stored credentials | Harvest |
087 
088 ### Linux Targets
089 
090 | Check | Opportunity |
091 |-------|-------------|
092 | SUID binaries | Execute as owner |
093 | Sudo misconfiguration | Command execution |
094 | Kernel vulnerabilities | Kernel exploits |
095 | Cron jobs | Writable scripts |
096 
097 ---
098 
099 ## 5. Defense Evasion Principles
100 
101 ### Key Techniques
102 
103 | Technique | Purpose |
104 |-----------|---------|
105 | LOLBins | Use legitimate tools |
106 | Obfuscation | Hide malicious code |
107 | Timestomping | Hide file modifications |
108 | Log clearing | Remove evidence |
109 
110 ### Operational Security
111 
112 - Work during business hours
113 - Mimic legitimate traffic patterns
114 - Use encrypted channels
115 - Blend with normal behavior
116 
117 ---
118 
119 ## 6. Lateral Movement Principles
120 
121 ### Credential Types
122 
123 | Type | Use |
124 |------|-----|
125 | Password | Standard auth |
126 | Hash | Pass-the-hash |
127 | Ticket | Pass-the-ticket |
128 | Certificate | Certificate auth |
129 
130 ### Movement Paths
131 
132 - Admin shares
133 - Remote services (RDP, SSH, WinRM)
134 - Exploitation of internal services
135 
136 ---
137 
138 ## 7. Active Directory Attacks
139 
140 ### Attack Categories
141 
142 | Attack | Target |
143 |--------|--------|
144 | Kerberoasting | Service account passwords |
145 | AS-REP Roasting | Accounts without pre-auth |
146 | DCSync | Domain credentials |
147 | Golden Ticket | Persistent domain access |
148 
149 ---
150 
151 ## 8. Reporting Principles
152 
153 ### Attack Narrative
154 
155 Document the full attack chain:
156 1. How initial access was gained
157 2. What techniques were used
158 3. What objectives were achieved
159 4. Where detection failed
160 
161 ### Detection Gaps
162 
163 For each successful technique:
164 - What should have detected it?
165 - Why didn't detection work?
166 - How to improve detection
167 
168 ---
169 
170 ## 9. Ethical Boundaries
171 
172 ### Always
173 
174 - Stay within scope
175 - Minimize impact
176 - Report immediately if real threat found
177 - Document all actions
178 
179 ### Never
180 
181 - Destroy production data
182 - Cause denial of service (unless scoped)
183 - Access beyond proof of concept
184 - Retain sensitive data
185 
186 ---
187 
188 ## 10. Anti-Patterns
189 
190 | ‚ùå Don't | ‚úÖ Do |
191 |----------|-------|
192 | Rush to exploitation | Follow methodology |
193 | Cause damage | Minimize impact |
194 | Skip reporting | Document everything |
195 | Ignore scope | Stay within boundaries |
196 
197 ---
198 
199 > **Remember:** Red team simulates attackers to improve defenses, not to cause harm.
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F122 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F124 path:skills/server-management/SKILL.md hash:60277deafa8e97df1d8ec571eab94e752dba768e70aee6d994c87a25a4a09521 lines:161 ===
001 ---
002 name: server-management
003 description: Server management principles and decision-making. Process management, monitoring strategy, and scaling decisions. Teaches thinking, not commands.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Write, Edit, Glob, Grep, Bash
005 ---
006 
007 # Server Management
008 
009 > Server management principles for production operations.
010 > **Learn to THINK, not memorize commands.**
011 
012 ---
013 
014 ## 1. Process Management Principles
015 
016 ### Tool Selection
017 
018 | Scenario | Tool |
019 |----------|------|
020 | **Node.js app** | PM2 (clustering, reload) |
021 | **Any app** | systemd (Linux native) |
022 | **Containers** | Docker/Podman |
023 | **Orchestration** | Kubernetes, Docker Swarm |
024 
025 ### Process Management Goals
026 
027 | Goal | What It Means |
028 |------|---------------|
029 | **Restart on crash** | Auto-recovery |
030 | **Zero-downtime reload** | No service interruption |
031 | **Clustering** | Use all CPU cores |
032 | **Persistence** | Survive server reboot |
033 
034 ---
035 
036 ## 2. Monitoring Principles
037 
038 ### What to Monitor
039 
040 | Category | Key Metrics |
041 |----------|-------------|
042 | **Availability** | Uptime, health checks |
043 | **Performance** | Response time, throughput |
044 | **Errors** | Error rate, types |
045 | **Resources** | CPU, memory, disk |
046 
047 ### Alert Severity Strategy
048 
049 | Level | Response |
050 |-------|----------|
051 | **Critical** | Immediate action |
052 | **Warning** | Investigate soon |
053 | **Info** | Review daily |
054 
055 ### Monitoring Tool Selection
056 
057 | Need | Options |
058 |------|---------|
059 | Simple/Free | PM2 metrics, htop |
060 | Full observability | Grafana, Datadog |
061 | Error tracking | Sentry |
062 | Uptime | UptimeRobot, Pingdom |
063 
064 ---
065 
066 ## 3. Log Management Principles
067 
068 ### Log Strategy
069 
070 | Log Type | Purpose |
071 |----------|---------|
072 | **Application logs** | Debug, audit |
073 | **Access logs** | Traffic analysis |
074 | **Error logs** | Issue detection |
075 
076 ### Log Principles
077 
078 1. **Rotate logs** to prevent disk fill
079 2. **Structured logging** (JSON) for parsing
080 3. **Appropriate levels** (error/warn/info/debug)
081 4. **No sensitive data** in logs
082 
083 ---
084 
085 ## 4. Scaling Decisions
086 
087 ### When to Scale
088 
089 | Symptom | Solution |
090 |---------|----------|
091 | High CPU | Add instances (horizontal) |
092 | High memory | Increase RAM or fix leak |
093 | Slow response | Profile first, then scale |
094 | Traffic spikes | Auto-scaling |
095 
096 ### Scaling Strategy
097 
098 | Type | When to Use |
099 |------|-------------|
100 | **Vertical** | Quick fix, single instance |
101 | **Horizontal** | Sustainable, distributed |
102 | **Auto** | Variable traffic |
103 
104 ---
105 
106 ## 5. Health Check Principles
107 
108 ### What Constitutes Healthy
109 
110 | Check | Meaning |
111 |-------|---------|
112 | **HTTP 200** | Service responding |
113 | **Database connected** | Data accessible |
114 | **Dependencies OK** | External services reachable |
115 | **Resources OK** | CPU/memory not exhausted |
116 
117 ### Health Check Implementation
118 
119 - Simple: Just return 200
120 - Deep: Check all dependencies
121 - Choose based on load balancer needs
122 
123 ---
124 
125 ## 6. Security Principles
126 
127 | Area | Principle |
128 |------|-----------|
129 | **Access** | SSH keys only, no passwords |
130 | **Firewall** | Only needed ports open |
131 | **Updates** | Regular security patches |
132 | **Secrets** | Environment vars, not files |
133 | **Audit** | Log access and changes |
134 
135 ---
136 
137 ## 7. Troubleshooting Priority
138 
139 When something's wrong:
140 
141 1. **Check if running** (process status)
142 2. **Check logs** (error messages)
143 3. **Check resources** (disk, memory, CPU)
144 4. **Check network** (ports, DNS)
145 5. **Check dependencies** (database, APIs)
146 
147 ---
148 
149 ## 8. Anti-Patterns
150 
151 | ‚ùå Don't | ‚úÖ Do |
152 |----------|-------|
153 | Run as root | Use non-root user |
154 | Ignore logs | Set up log rotation |
155 | Skip monitoring | Monitor from day one |
156 | Manual restarts | Auto-restart config |
157 | No backups | Regular backup schedule |
158 
159 ---
160 
161 > **Remember:** A well-managed server is boring. That's the goal.

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F125 path:skills/systematic-debugging/SKILL.md hash:53b60eed01a42d11ad7acdb7d1f732fefcb6b226d133fa9fbeb96f5c7d0238e3 lines:109 ===
001 ---
002 name: systematic-debugging
003 description: 4-phase systematic debugging methodology with root cause analysis and evidence-based verification. Use when debugging complex issues.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Glob, Grep
005 ---
006 
007 # Systematic Debugging
008 
009 > Source: obra/superpowers
010 
011 ## Overview
012 This skill provides a structured approach to debugging that prevents random guessing and ensures problems are properly understood before solving.
013 
014 ## 4-Phase Debugging Process
015 
016 ### Phase 1: Reproduce
017 Before fixing, reliably reproduce the issue.
018 
019 ```markdown
020 ## Reproduction Steps
021 1. [Exact step to reproduce]
022 2. [Next step]
023 3. [Expected vs actual result]
024 
025 ## Reproduction Rate
026 - [ ] Always (100%)
027 - [ ] Often (50-90%)
028 - [ ] Sometimes (10-50%)
029 - [ ] Rare (<10%)
030 ```
031 
032 ### Phase 2: Isolate
033 Narrow down the source.
034 
035 ```markdown
036 ## Isolation Questions
037 - When did this start happening?
038 - What changed recently?
039 - Does it happen in all environments?
040 - Can we reproduce with minimal code?
041 - What's the smallest change that triggers it?
042 ```
043 
044 ### Phase 3: Understand
045 Find the root cause, not just symptoms.
046 
047 ```markdown
048 ## Root Cause Analysis
049 ### The 5 Whys
050 1. Why: [First observation]
051 2. Why: [Deeper reason]
052 3. Why: [Still deeper]
053 4. Why: [Getting closer]
054 5. Why: [Root cause]
055 ```
056 
057 ### Phase 4: Fix & Verify
058 Fix and verify it's truly fixed.
059 
060 ```markdown
061 ## Fix Verification
062 - [ ] Bug no longer reproduces
063 - [ ] Related functionality still works
064 - [ ] No new issues introduced
065 - [ ] Test added to prevent regression
066 ```
067 
068 ## Debugging Checklist
069 
070 ```markdown
071 ## Before Starting
072 - [ ] Can reproduce consistently
073 - [ ] Have minimal reproduction case
074 - [ ] Understand expected behavior
075 
076 ## During Investigation
077 - [ ] Check recent changes (git log)
078 - [ ] Check logs for errors
079 - [ ] Add logging if needed
080 - [ ] Use debugger/breakpoints
081 
082 ## After Fix
083 - [ ] Root cause documented
084 - [ ] Fix verified
085 - [ ] Regression test added
086 - [ ] Similar code checked
087 ```
088 
089 ## Common Debugging Commands
090 
091 ```bash
092 # Recent changes
093 git log --oneline -20
094 git diff HEAD~5
095 
096 # Search for pattern
097 grep -r "errorPattern" --include="*.ts"
098 
099 # Check logs
100 pm2 logs app-name --err --lines 100
101 ```
102 
103 ## Anti-Patterns
104 
105 ‚ùå **Random changes** - "Maybe if I change this..."
106 ‚ùå **Ignoring evidence** - "That can't be the cause"
107 ‚ùå **Assuming** - "It must be X" without proof
108 ‚ùå **Not reproducing first** - Fixing blindly
109 ‚ùå **Stopping at symptoms** - Not finding root cause
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F125 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F126 path:skills/tailwind-patterns/SKILL.md hash:bc64b47c56a44183441f3c908457dd4dcaaf1dfe4dc2c508b83f56ecdb017667 lines:269 ===
001 ---
002 name: tailwind-patterns
003 description: Tailwind CSS v4 principles. CSS-first configuration, container queries, modern patterns, design token architecture.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Write, Edit, Glob, Grep
005 ---
006 
007 # Tailwind CSS Patterns (v4 - 2025)
008 
009 > Modern utility-first CSS with CSS-native configuration.
010 
011 ---
012 
013 ## 1. Tailwind v4 Architecture
014 
015 ### What Changed from v3
016 
017 | v3 (Legacy) | v4 (Current) |
018 |-------------|--------------|
019 | `tailwind.config.js` | CSS-based `@theme` directive |
020 | PostCSS plugin | Oxide engine (10x faster) |
021 | JIT mode | Native, always-on |
022 | Plugin system | CSS-native features |
023 | `@apply` directive | Still works, discouraged |
024 
025 ### v4 Core Concepts
026 
027 | Concept | Description |
028 |---------|-------------|
029 | **CSS-first** | Configuration in CSS, not JavaScript |
030 | **Oxide Engine** | Rust-based compiler, much faster |
031 | **Native Nesting** | CSS nesting without PostCSS |
032 | **CSS Variables** | All tokens exposed as `--*` vars |
033 
034 ---
035 
036 ## 2. CSS-Based Configuration
037 
038 ### Theme Definition
039 
040 ```
041 @theme {
042   /* Colors - use semantic names */
043   --color-primary: oklch(0.7 0.15 250);
044   --color-surface: oklch(0.98 0 0);
045   --color-surface-dark: oklch(0.15 0 0);
046 
047   /* Spacing scale */
048   --spacing-xs: 0.25rem;
049   --spacing-sm: 0.5rem;
050   --spacing-md: 1rem;
051   --spacing-lg: 2rem;
052 
053   /* Typography */
054   --font-sans: 'Inter', system-ui, sans-serif;
055   --font-mono: 'JetBrains Mono', monospace;
056 }
057 ```
058 
059 ### When to Extend vs Override
060 
061 | Action | Use When |
062 |--------|----------|
063 | **Extend** | Adding new values alongside defaults |
064 | **Override** | Replacing default scale entirely |
065 | **Semantic tokens** | Project-specific naming (primary, surface) |
066 
067 ---
068 
069 ## 3. Container Queries (v4 Native)
070 
071 ### Breakpoint vs Container
072 
073 | Type | Responds To |
074 |------|-------------|
075 | **Breakpoint** (`md:`) | Viewport width |
076 | **Container** (`@container`) | Parent element width |
077 
078 ### Container Query Usage
079 
080 | Pattern | Classes |
081 |---------|---------|
082 | Define container | `@container` on parent |
083 | Container breakpoint | `@sm:`, `@md:`, `@lg:` on children |
084 | Named containers | `@container/card` for specificity |
085 
086 ### When to Use
087 
088 | Scenario | Use |
089 |----------|-----|
090 | Page-level layouts | Viewport breakpoints |
091 | Component-level responsive | Container queries |
092 | Reusable components | Container queries (context-independent) |
093 
094 ---
095 
096 ## 4. Responsive Design
097 
098 ### Breakpoint System
099 
100 | Prefix | Min Width | Target |
101 |--------|-----------|--------|
102 | (none) | 0px | Mobile-first base |
103 | `sm:` | 640px | Large phone / small tablet |
104 | `md:` | 768px | Tablet |
105 | `lg:` | 1024px | Laptop |
106 | `xl:` | 1280px | Desktop |
107 | `2xl:` | 1536px | Large desktop |
108 
109 ### Mobile-First Principle
110 
111 1. Write mobile styles first (no prefix)
112 2. Add larger screen overrides with prefixes
113 3. Example: `w-full md:w-1/2 lg:w-1/3`
114 
115 ---
116 
117 ## 5. Dark Mode
118 
119 ### Configuration Strategies
120 
121 | Method | Behavior | Use When |
122 |--------|----------|----------|
123 | `class` | `.dark` class toggles | Manual theme switcher |
124 | `media` | Follows system preference | No user control |
125 | `selector` | Custom selector (v4) | Complex theming |
126 
127 ### Dark Mode Pattern
128 
129 | Element | Light | Dark |
130 |---------|-------|------|
131 | Background | `bg-white` | `dark:bg-zinc-900` |
132 | Text | `text-zinc-900` | `dark:text-zinc-100` |
133 | Borders | `border-zinc-200` | `dark:border-zinc-700` |
134 
135 ---
136 
137 ## 6. Modern Layout Patterns
138 
139 ### Flexbox Patterns
140 
141 | Pattern | Classes |
142 |---------|---------|
143 | Center (both axes) | `flex items-center justify-center` |
144 | Vertical stack | `flex flex-col gap-4` |
145 | Horizontal row | `flex gap-4` |
146 | Space between | `flex justify-between items-center` |
147 | Wrap grid | `flex flex-wrap gap-4` |
148 
149 ### Grid Patterns
150 
151 | Pattern | Classes |
152 |---------|---------|
153 | Auto-fit responsive | `grid grid-cols-[repeat(auto-fit,minmax(250px,1fr))]` |
154 | Asymmetric (Bento) | `grid grid-cols-3 grid-rows-2` with spans |
155 | Sidebar layout | `grid grid-cols-[auto_1fr]` |
156 
157 > **Note:** Prefer asymmetric/Bento layouts over symmetric 3-column grids.
158 
159 ---
160 
161 ## 7. Modern Color System
162 
163 ### OKLCH vs RGB/HSL
164 
165 | Format | Advantage |
166 |--------|-----------|
167 | **OKLCH** | Perceptually uniform, better for design |
168 | **HSL** | Intuitive hue/saturation |
169 | **RGB** | Legacy compatibility |
170 
171 ### Color Token Architecture
172 
173 | Layer | Example | Purpose |
174 |-------|---------|---------|
175 | **Primitive** | `--blue-500` | Raw color values |
176 | **Semantic** | `--color-primary` | Purpose-based naming |
177 | **Component** | `--button-bg` | Component-specific |
178 
179 ---
180 
181 ## 8. Typography System
182 
183 ### Font Stack Pattern
184 
185 | Type | Recommended |
186 |------|-------------|
187 | Sans | `'Inter', 'SF Pro', system-ui, sans-serif` |
188 | Mono | `'JetBrains Mono', 'Fira Code', monospace` |
189 | Display | `'Outfit', 'Poppins', sans-serif` |
190 
191 ### Type Scale
192 
193 | Class | Size | Use |
194 |-------|------|-----|
195 | `text-xs` | 0.75rem | Labels, captions |
196 | `text-sm` | 0.875rem | Secondary text |
197 | `text-base` | 1rem | Body text |
198 | `text-lg` | 1.125rem | Lead text |
199 | `text-xl`+ | 1.25rem+ | Headings |
200 
201 ---
202 
203 ## 9. Animation & Transitions
204 
205 ### Built-in Animations
206 
207 | Class | Effect |
208 |-------|--------|
209 | `animate-spin` | Continuous rotation |
210 | `animate-ping` | Attention pulse |
211 | `animate-pulse` | Subtle opacity pulse |
212 | `animate-bounce` | Bouncing effect |
213 
214 ### Transition Patterns
215 
216 | Pattern | Classes |
217 |---------|---------|
218 | All properties | `transition-all duration-200` |
219 | Specific | `transition-colors duration-150` |
220 | With easing | `ease-out` or `ease-in-out` |
221 | Hover effect | `hover:scale-105 transition-transform` |
222 
223 ---
224 
225 ## 10. Component Extraction
226 
227 ### When to Extract
228 
229 | Signal | Action |
230 |--------|--------|
231 | Same class combo 3+ times | Extract component |
232 | Complex state variants | Extract component |
233 | Design system element | Extract + document |
234 
235 ### Extraction Methods
236 
237 | Method | Use When |
238 |--------|----------|
239 | **React/Vue component** | Dynamic, JS needed |
240 | **@apply in CSS** | Static, no JS needed |
241 | **Design tokens** | Reusable values |
242 
243 ---
244 
245 ## 11. Anti-Patterns
246 
247 | Don't | Do |
248 |-------|-----|
249 | Arbitrary values everywhere | Use design system scale |
250 | `!important` | Fix specificity properly |
251 | Inline `style=` | Use utilities |
252 | Duplicate long class lists | Extract component |
253 | Mix v3 config with v4 | Migrate fully to CSS-first |
254 | Use `@apply` heavily | Prefer components |
255 
256 ---
257 
258 ## 12. Performance Principles
259 
260 | Principle | Implementation |
261 |-----------|----------------|
262 | **Purge unused** | Automatic in v4 |
263 | **Avoid dynamism** | No template string classes |
264 | **Use Oxide** | Default in v4, 10x faster |
265 | **Cache builds** | CI/CD caching |
266 
267 ---
268 
269 > **Remember:** Tailwind v4 is CSS-first. Embrace CSS variables, container queries, and native features. The config file is now optional.

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F127 path:skills/tdd-workflow/SKILL.md hash:b8fceb81c0967e5beadb7a89e80bc6b199c5c203fb34de50514ba9742d530157 lines:149 ===
001 ---
002 name: tdd-workflow
003 description: Test-Driven Development workflow principles. RED-GREEN-REFACTOR cycle.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Write, Edit, Glob, Grep, Bash
005 ---
006 
007 # TDD Workflow
008 
009 > Write tests first, code second.
010 
011 ---
012 
013 ## 1. The TDD Cycle
014 
015 ```
016 üî¥ RED ‚Üí Write failing test
017     ‚Üì
018 üü¢ GREEN ‚Üí Write minimal code to pass
019     ‚Üì
020 üîµ REFACTOR ‚Üí Improve code quality
021     ‚Üì
022    Repeat...
023 ```
024 
025 ---
026 
027 ## 2. The Three Laws of TDD
028 
029 1. Write production code only to make a failing test pass
030 2. Write only enough test to demonstrate failure
031 3. Write only enough code to make the test pass
032 
033 ---
034 
035 ## 3. RED Phase Principles
036 
037 ### What to Write
038 
039 | Focus | Example |
040 |-------|---------|
041 | Behavior | "should add two numbers" |
042 | Edge cases | "should handle empty input" |
043 | Error states | "should throw for invalid data" |
044 
045 ### RED Phase Rules
046 
047 - Test must fail first
048 - Test name describes expected behavior
049 - One assertion per test (ideally)
050 
051 ---
052 
053 ## 4. GREEN Phase Principles
054 
055 ### Minimum Code
056 
057 | Principle | Meaning |
058 |-----------|---------|
059 | **YAGNI** | You Aren't Gonna Need It |
060 | **Simplest thing** | Write the minimum to pass |
061 | **No optimization** | Just make it work |
062 
063 ### GREEN Phase Rules
064 
065 - Don't write unneeded code
066 - Don't optimize yet
067 - Pass the test, nothing more
068 
069 ---
070 
071 ## 5. REFACTOR Phase Principles
072 
073 ### What to Improve
074 
075 | Area | Action |
076 |------|--------|
077 | Duplication | Extract common code |
078 | Naming | Make intent clear |
079 | Structure | Improve organization |
080 | Complexity | Simplify logic |
081 
082 ### REFACTOR Rules
083 
084 - All tests must stay green
085 - Small incremental changes
086 - Commit after each refactor
087 
088 ---
089 
090 ## 6. AAA Pattern
091 
092 Every test follows:
093 
094 | Step | Purpose |
095 |------|---------|
096 | **Arrange** | Set up test data |
097 | **Act** | Execute code under test |
098 | **Assert** | Verify expected outcome |
099 
100 ---
101 
102 ## 7. When to Use TDD
103 
104 | Scenario | TDD Value |
105 |----------|-----------|
106 | New feature | High |
107 | Bug fix | High (write test first) |
108 | Complex logic | High |
109 | Exploratory | Low (spike, then TDD) |
110 | UI layout | Low |
111 
112 ---
113 
114 ## 8. Test Prioritization
115 
116 | Priority | Test Type |
117 |----------|-----------|
118 | 1 | Happy path |
119 | 2 | Error cases |
120 | 3 | Edge cases |
121 | 4 | Performance |
122 
123 ---
124 
125 ## 9. Anti-Patterns
126 
127 | ‚ùå Don't | ‚úÖ Do |
128 |----------|-------|
129 | Skip the RED phase | Watch test fail first |
130 | Write tests after | Write tests before |
131 | Over-engineer initial | Keep it simple |
132 | Multiple asserts | One behavior per test |
133 | Test implementation | Test behavior |
134 
135 ---
136 
137 ## 10. AI-Augmented TDD
138 
139 ### Multi-Agent Pattern
140 
141 | Agent | Role |
142 |-------|------|
143 | Agent A | Write failing tests (RED) |
144 | Agent B | Implement to pass (GREEN) |
145 | Agent C | Optimize (REFACTOR) |
146 
147 ---
148 
149 > **Remember:** The test is the specification. If you can't write a test, you don't understand the requirement.
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F127 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F128 path:skills/testing-patterns/SKILL.md hash:f229085ad979d04c004b01865ad8fc4dcd732f4a917b56af59f600e0a3a26e8d lines:178 ===
001 ---
002 name: testing-patterns
003 description: Testing patterns and principles. Unit, integration, mocking strategies.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Write, Edit, Glob, Grep, Bash
005 ---
006 
007 # Testing Patterns
008 
009 > Principles for reliable test suites.
010 
011 ---
012 
013 ## 1. Testing Pyramid
014 
015 ```
016         /\          E2E (Few)
017        /  \         Critical flows
018       /----\
019      /      \       Integration (Some)
020     /--------\      API, DB queries
021    /          \
022   /------------\    Unit (Many)
023                     Functions, classes
024 ```
025 
026 ---
027 
028 ## 2. AAA Pattern
029 
030 | Step | Purpose |
031 |------|---------|
032 | **Arrange** | Set up test data |
033 | **Act** | Execute code under test |
034 | **Assert** | Verify outcome |
035 
036 ---
037 
038 ## 3. Test Type Selection
039 
040 ### When to Use Each
041 
042 | Type | Best For | Speed |
043 |------|----------|-------|
044 | **Unit** | Pure functions, logic | Fast (<50ms) |
045 | **Integration** | API, DB, services | Medium |
046 | **E2E** | Critical user flows | Slow |
047 
048 ---
049 
050 ## 4. Unit Test Principles
051 
052 ### Good Unit Tests
053 
054 | Principle | Meaning |
055 |-----------|---------|
056 | Fast | < 100ms each |
057 | Isolated | No external deps |
058 | Repeatable | Same result always |
059 | Self-checking | No manual verification |
060 | Timely | Written with code |
061 
062 ### What to Unit Test
063 
064 | Test | Don't Test |
065 |------|------------|
066 | Business logic | Framework code |
067 | Edge cases | Third-party libs |
068 | Error handling | Simple getters |
069 
070 ---
071 
072 ## 5. Integration Test Principles
073 
074 ### What to Test
075 
076 | Area | Focus |
077 |------|-------|
078 | API endpoints | Request/response |
079 | Database | Queries, transactions |
080 | External services | Contracts |
081 
082 ### Setup/Teardown
083 
084 | Phase | Action |
085 |-------|--------|
086 | Before All | Connect resources |
087 | Before Each | Reset state |
088 | After Each | Clean up |
089 | After All | Disconnect |
090 
091 ---
092 
093 ## 6. Mocking Principles
094 
095 ### When to Mock
096 
097 | Mock | Don't Mock |
098 |------|------------|
099 | External APIs | The code under test |
100 | Database (unit) | Simple dependencies |
101 | Time/random | Pure functions |
102 | Network | In-memory stores |
103 
104 ### Mock Types
105 
106 | Type | Use |
107 |------|-----|
108 | Stub | Return fixed values |
109 | Spy | Track calls |
110 | Mock | Set expectations |
111 | Fake | Simplified implementation |
112 
113 ---
114 
115 ## 7. Test Organization
116 
117 ### Naming
118 
119 | Pattern | Example |
120 |---------|---------|
121 | Should behavior | "should return error when..." |
122 | When condition | "when user not found..." |
123 | Given-when-then | "given X, when Y, then Z" |
124 
125 ### Grouping
126 
127 | Level | Use |
128 |-------|-----|
129 | describe | Group related tests |
130 | it/test | Individual case |
131 | beforeEach | Common setup |
132 
133 ---
134 
135 ## 8. Test Data
136 
137 ### Strategies
138 
139 | Approach | Use |
140 |----------|-----|
141 | Factories | Generate test data |
142 | Fixtures | Predefined datasets |
143 | Builders | Fluent object creation |
144 
145 ### Principles
146 
147 - Use realistic data
148 - Randomize non-essential values (faker)
149 - Share common fixtures
150 - Keep data minimal
151 
152 ---
153 
154 ## 9. Best Practices
155 
156 | Practice | Why |
157 |----------|-----|
158 | One assert per test | Clear failure reason |
159 | Independent tests | No order dependency |
160 | Fast tests | Run frequently |
161 | Descriptive names | Self-documenting |
162 | Clean up | Avoid side effects |
163 
164 ---
165 
166 ## 10. Anti-Patterns
167 
168 | ‚ùå Don't | ‚úÖ Do |
169 |----------|-------|
170 | Test implementation | Test behavior |
171 | Duplicate test code | Use factories |
172 | Complex test setup | Simplify or split |
173 | Ignore flaky tests | Fix root cause |
174 | Skip cleanup | Reset state |
175 
176 ---
177 
178 > **Remember:** Tests are documentation. If someone can't understand what the code does from the tests, rewrite them.

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F129 path:skills/ui-ux-pro-max/SKILL.md hash:8eda31a15ece36f551e8fe42fdfaea16fa346e6cc0d1c4573282002e2670753f lines:292 ===
001 ---
002 name: ui-ux-pro-max
003 description: UI/UX design intelligence. 50 styles, 21 palettes, 50 font pairings, 20 charts, 9 stacks.
004 ---
005 # ui-ux-pro-max
006 
007 Comprehensive design guide for web and mobile applications. Contains 67 styles, 96 color palettes, 56 font pairings, 98 UX guidelines, and 25 chart types across 13 technology stacks. Searchable database with priority-based recommendations.
008 
009 ## Prerequisites
010 
011 Check if Python is installed:
012 
013 ```bash
014 python3 --version || python --version
015 ```
016 
017 If Python is not installed, install it based on user's OS:
018 
019 **macOS:**
020 ```bash
021 brew install python3
022 ```
023 
024 **Ubuntu/Debian:**
025 ```bash
026 sudo apt update && sudo apt install python3
027 ```
028 
029 **Windows:**
030 ```powershell
031 winget install Python.Python.3.12
032 ```
033 
034 ---
035 
036 ## How to Use This Skill
037 
038 When user requests UI/UX work (design, build, create, implement, review, fix, improve), follow this workflow:
039 
040 ### Step 1: Analyze User Requirements
041 
042 Extract key information from user request:
043 - **Product type**: SaaS, e-commerce, portfolio, dashboard, landing page, etc.
044 - **Style keywords**: minimal, playful, professional, elegant, dark mode, etc.
045 - **Industry**: healthcare, fintech, gaming, education, etc.
046 - **Stack**: React, Vue, Next.js, or default to `html-tailwind`
047 
048 ### Step 2: Generate Design System (REQUIRED)
049 
050 **Always start with `--design-system`** to get comprehensive recommendations with reasoning:
051 
052 ```bash
053 python3 skills/ui-ux-pro-max/scripts/search.py "<product_type> <industry> <keywords>" --design-system [-p "Project Name"]
054 ```
055 
056 This command:
057 1. Searches 5 domains in parallel (product, style, color, landing, typography)
058 2. Applies reasoning rules from `ui-reasoning.csv` to select best matches
059 3. Returns complete design system: pattern, style, colors, typography, effects
060 4. Includes anti-patterns to avoid
061 
062 **Example:**
063 ```bash
064 python3 skills/ui-ux-pro-max/scripts/search.py "beauty spa wellness service" --design-system -p "Serenity Spa"
065 ```
066 
067 ### Step 2b: Persist Design System (Master + Overrides Pattern)
068 
069 To save the design system for hierarchical retrieval across sessions, add `--persist`:
070 
071 ```bash
072 python3 skills/ui-ux-pro-max/scripts/search.py "<query>" --design-system --persist -p "Project Name"
073 ```
074 
075 This creates:
076 - `design-system/MASTER.md` ‚Äî Global Source of Truth with all design rules
077 - `design-system/pages/` ‚Äî Folder for page-specific overrides
078 
079 **With page-specific override:**
080 ```bash
081 python3 skills/ui-ux-pro-max/scripts/search.py "<query>" --design-system --persist -p "Project Name" --page "dashboard"
082 ```
083 
084 This also creates:
085 - `design-system/pages/dashboard.md` ‚Äî Page-specific deviations from Master
086 
087 **How hierarchical retrieval works:**
088 1. When building a specific page (e.g., "Checkout"), first check `design-system/pages/checkout.md`
089 2. If the page file exists, its rules **override** the Master file
090 3. If not, use `design-system/MASTER.md` exclusively
091 
092 ### Step 3: Supplement with Detailed Searches (as needed)
093 
094 After getting the design system, use domain searches to get additional details:
095 
096 ```bash
097 python3 skills/ui-ux-pro-max/scripts/search.py "<keyword>" --domain <domain> [-n <max_results>]
098 ```
099 
100 **When to use detailed searches:**
101 
102 | Need | Domain | Example |
103 |------|--------|---------|
104 | More style options | `style` | `--domain style "glassmorphism dark"` |
105 | Chart recommendations | `chart` | `--domain chart "real-time dashboard"` |
106 | UX best practices | `ux` | `--domain ux "animation accessibility"` |
107 | Alternative fonts | `typography` | `--domain typography "elegant luxury"` |
108 | Landing structure | `landing` | `--domain landing "hero social-proof"` |
109 
110 ### Step 4: Stack Guidelines (Default: html-tailwind)
111 
112 Get implementation-specific best practices. If user doesn't specify a stack, **default to `html-tailwind`**.
113 
114 ```bash
115 python3 skills/ui-ux-pro-max/scripts/search.py "<keyword>" --stack html-tailwind
116 ```
117 
118 Available stacks: `html-tailwind`, `react`, `nextjs`, `vue`, `svelte`, `swiftui`, `react-native`, `flutter`, `shadcn`, `jetpack-compose`
119 
120 ---
121 
122 ## Search Reference
123 
124 ### Available Domains
125 
126 | Domain | Use For | Example Keywords |
127 |--------|---------|------------------|
128 | `product` | Product type recommendations | SaaS, e-commerce, portfolio, healthcare, beauty, service |
129 | `style` | UI styles, colors, effects | glassmorphism, minimalism, dark mode, brutalism |
130 | `typography` | Font pairings, Google Fonts | elegant, playful, professional, modern |
131 | `color` | Color palettes by product type | saas, ecommerce, healthcare, beauty, fintech, service |
132 | `landing` | Page structure, CTA strategies | hero, hero-centric, testimonial, pricing, social-proof |
133 | `chart` | Chart types, library recommendations | trend, comparison, timeline, funnel, pie |
134 | `ux` | Best practices, anti-patterns | animation, accessibility, z-index, loading |
135 | `react` | React/Next.js performance | waterfall, bundle, suspense, memo, rerender, cache |
136 | `web` | Web interface guidelines | aria, focus, keyboard, semantic, virtualize |
137 | `prompt` | AI prompts, CSS keywords | (style name) |
138 
139 ### Available Stacks
140 
141 | Stack | Focus |
142 |-------|-------|
143 | `html-tailwind` | Tailwind utilities, responsive, a11y (DEFAULT) |
144 | `react` | State, hooks, performance, patterns |
145 | `nextjs` | SSR, routing, images, API routes |
146 | `vue` | Composition API, Pinia, Vue Router |
147 | `svelte` | Runes, stores, SvelteKit |
148 | `swiftui` | Views, State, Navigation, Animation |
149 | `react-native` | Components, Navigation, Lists |
150 | `flutter` | Widgets, State, Layout, Theming |
151 | `shadcn` | shadcn/ui components, theming, forms, patterns |
152 | `jetpack-compose` | Composables, Modifiers, State Hoisting, Recomposition |
153 
154 ---
155

157 
158 **User request:** "L√†m landing page cho d·ªãch v·ª• chƒÉm s√≥c da chuy√™n nghi·ªáp"

161 - Product type: Beauty/Spa service

197
