199 # ASCII box (default) - best for terminal display
200 python3 skills/ui-ux-pro-max/scripts/search.py "fintech crypto" --design-system

204 ```
205

207 
208 ## Tips for Better Results
209 
210 1. **Be specific with keywords** - "healthcare SaaS dashboard" > "app"
211 2. **Search multiple times** - Different keywords reveal different insights
212 3. **Combine domains** - Style + Typography + Color = Complete design system
213 4. **Always check UX** - Search "animation", "z-index", "accessibility" for common issues
214 5. **Use stack flag** - Get implementation-specific best practices
215 6. **Iterate** - If first search doesn't match, try different keywords
216 
217 ---
218 
219 ## Common Rules for Professional UI
220 
221 These are frequently overlooked issues that make UI look unprofessional:
222 
223 ### Icons & Visual Elements
224 
225 | Rule | Do | Don't |
226 |------|----|----- |
227 | **No emoji icons** | Use SVG icons (Heroicons, Lucide, Simple Icons) | Use emojis like üé® üöÄ ‚öôÔ∏è as UI icons |
228 | **Stable hover states** | Use color/opacity transitions on hover | Use scale transforms that shift layout |
229 | **Correct brand logos** | Research official SVG from Simple Icons | Guess or use incorrect logo paths |
230 | **Consistent icon sizing** | Use fixed viewBox (24x24) with w-6 h-6 | Mix different icon sizes randomly |
231 
232 ### Interaction & Cursor
233 
234 | Rule | Do | Don't |
235 |------|----|----- |
236 | **Cursor pointer** | Add `cursor-pointer` to all clickable/hoverable cards | Leave default cursor on interactive elements |
237 | **Hover feedback** | Provide visual feedback (color, shadow, border) | No indication element is interactive |
238 | **Smooth transitions** | Use `transition-colors duration-200` | Instant state changes or too slow (>500ms) |
239 
240 ### Light/Dark Mode Contrast
241 
242 | Rule | Do | Don't |
243 |------|----|----- |
244 | **Glass card light mode** | Use `bg-white/80` or higher opacity | Use `bg-white/10` (too transparent) |
245 | **Text contrast light** | Use `#0F172A` (slate-900) for text | Use `#94A3B8` (slate-400) for body text |
246 | **Muted text light** | Use `#475569` (slate-600) minimum | Use gray-400 or lighter |
247 | **Border visibility** | Use `border-gray-200` in light mode | Use `border-white/10` (invisible) |
248 
249 ### Layout & Spacing
250 
251 | Rule | Do | Don't |
252 |------|----|----- |
253 | **Floating navbar** | Add `top-4 left-4 right-4` spacing | Stick navbar to `top-0 left-0 right-0` |
254 | **Content padding** | Account for fixed navbar height | Let content hide behind fixed elements |
255 | **Consistent max-width** | Use same `max-w-6xl` or `max-w-7xl` | Mix different container widths |
256 
257 ---
258 
259 ## Pre-Delivery Checklist
260 
261 Before delivering UI code, verify these items:
262 
263 ### Visual Quality
264 - [ ] No emojis used as icons (use SVG instead)
265 - [ ] All icons from consistent icon set (Heroicons/Lucide)
266 - [ ] Brand logos are correct (verified from Simple Icons)
267 - [ ] Hover states don't cause layout shift
268 - [ ] Use theme colors directly (bg-primary) not var() wrapper
269 
270 ### Interaction
271 - [ ] All clickable elements have `cursor-pointer`
272 - [ ] Hover states provide clear visual feedback
273 - [ ] Transitions are smooth (150-300ms)
274 - [ ] Focus states visible for keyboard navigation
275 
276 ### Light/Dark Mode
277 - [ ] Light mode text has sufficient contrast (4.5:1 minimum)
278 - [ ] Glass/transparent elements visible in light mode
279 - [ ] Borders visible in both modes
280 - [ ] Test both modes before delivery
281 
282 ### Layout
283 - [ ] Floating elements have proper spacing from edges
284 - [ ] No content hidden behind fixed navbars
285 - [ ] Responsive at 375px, 768px, 1024px, 1440px
286 - [ ] No horizontal scroll on mobile
287 
288 ### Accessibility
289 - [ ] All images have alt text
290 - [ ] Form inputs have labels
291 - [ ] Color is not the only indicator
292 - [ ] `prefers-reduced-motion` respected
=== FILE_CAPSULE_END FID:F129 ===

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F130 path:skills/vulnerability-scanner/checklists.md hash:fcad8d2be67a2ef31a223f2fba9e1ed13188fcc15857a584a8fb5b55d9813e42 lines:121 ===
001 # Security Checklists
002 
003 > Quick reference checklists for security audits. Use alongside vulnerability-scanner principles.
004 
005 ---
006 
007 ## OWASP Top 10 Audit Checklist
008 
009 ### A01: Broken Access Control
010 - [ ] Authorization on all protected routes
011 - [ ] Deny by default
012 - [ ] Rate limiting implemented
013 - [ ] CORS properly configured
014 
015 ### A02: Cryptographic Failures
016 - [ ] Passwords hashed (bcrypt/argon2, cost 12+)
017 - [ ] Sensitive data encrypted at rest
018 - [ ] TLS 1.2+ for all connections
019 - [ ] No secrets in code/logs
020 
021 ### A03: Injection
022 - [ ] Parameterized queries
023 - [ ] Input validation on all user data
024 - [ ] Output encoding for XSS
025 - [ ] No eval() or dynamic code execution
026 
027 ### A04: Insecure Design
028 - [ ] Threat modeling done
029 - [ ] Security requirements defined
030 - [ ] Business logic validated
031 
032 ### A05: Security Misconfiguration
033 - [ ] Unnecessary features disabled
034 - [ ] Error messages sanitized
035 - [ ] Security headers configured
036 - [ ] Default credentials changed
037 
038 ### A06: Vulnerable Components
039 - [ ] Dependencies up to date
040 - [ ] No known vulnerabilities
041 - [ ] Unused dependencies removed
042 
043 ### A07: Authentication Failures
044 - [ ] MFA available
045 - [ ] Session invalidation on logout
046 - [ ] Session timeout implemented
047 - [ ] Brute force protection
048 
049 ### A08: Integrity Failures
050 - [ ] Dependency integrity verified
051 - [ ] CI/CD pipeline secured
052 - [ ] Update mechanism secured
053 
054 ### A09: Logging Failures
055 - [ ] Security events logged
056 - [ ] Logs protected
057 - [ ] No sensitive data in logs
058 - [ ] Alerting configured
059 
060 ### A10: SSRF
061 - [ ] URL validation implemented
062 - [ ] Allow-list for external calls
063 - [ ] Network segmentation
064 
065 ---
066 
067 ## Authentication Checklist
068 
069 - [ ] Strong password policy
070 - [ ] Account lockout
071 - [ ] Secure password reset
072 - [ ] Session management
073 - [ ] Token expiration
074 - [ ] Logout invalidation
075 
076 ---
077 
078 ## API Security Checklist
079 
080 - [ ] Authentication required
081 - [ ] Authorization per endpoint
082 - [ ] Input validation
083 - [ ] Rate limiting
084 - [ ] Output sanitization
085 - [ ] Error handling
086 
087 ---
088 
089 ## Data Protection Checklist
090 
091 - [ ] Encryption at rest
092 - [ ] Encryption in transit
093 - [ ] Key management
094 - [ ] Data minimization
095 - [ ] Secure deletion
096 
097 ---
098 
099 ## Security Headers
100 
101 | Header | Purpose |
102 |--------|---------|
103 | **Content-Security-Policy** | XSS prevention |
104 | **X-Content-Type-Options** | MIME sniffing |
105 | **X-Frame-Options** | Clickjacking |
106 | **Strict-Transport-Security** | Force HTTPS |
107 | **Referrer-Policy** | Referrer control |
108 
109 ---
110 
111 ## Quick Audit Commands
112 
113 | Check | What to Look For |
114 |-------|------------------|
115 | Secrets in code | password, api_key, secret |
116 | Dangerous patterns | eval, innerHTML, SQL concat |
117 | Dependency issues | npm audit, snyk |
118 
119 ---
120 
121 > **Usage:** Copy relevant checklists into your PLAN.md or security report.

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F131 path:skills/vulnerability-scanner/SKILL.md hash:8dfe6febffb085d2b7bf7ba68aba5734a7c696b1235a5d60c97394a818705eba lines:276 ===
001 ---
002 name: vulnerability-scanner
003 description: Advanced vulnerability analysis principles. OWASP 2025, Supply Chain Security, attack surface mapping, risk prioritization.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Glob, Grep, Bash
005 ---
006 
007 # Vulnerability Scanner
008 
009 > Think like an attacker, defend like an expert. 2025 threat landscape awareness.
010 
011 ## üîß Runtime Scripts
012 
013 **Execute for automated validation:**
014 
015 | Script | Purpose | Usage |
016 |--------|---------|-------|
017 | `scripts/security_scan.py` | Validate security principles applied | `python scripts/security_scan.py <project_path>` |
018 
019 ## üìã Reference Files
020 
021 | File | Purpose |
022 |------|---------|
023 | [checklists.md](checklists.md) | OWASP Top 10, Auth, API, Data protection checklists |
024 
025 ---
026 
027 ## 1. Security Expert Mindset
028 
029 ### Core Principles
030 
031 | Principle | Application |
032 |-----------|-------------|
033 | **Assume Breach** | Design as if attacker already inside |
034 | **Zero Trust** | Never trust, always verify |
035 | **Defense in Depth** | Multiple layers, no single point |
036 | **Least Privilege** | Minimum required access only |
037 | **Fail Secure** | On error, deny access |
038 
039 ### Threat Modeling Questions
040 
041 Before scanning, ask:
042 1. What are we protecting? (Assets)
043 2. Who would attack? (Threat actors)
044 3. How would they attack? (Attack vectors)
045 4. What's the impact? (Business risk)
046 
047 ---
048 
049 ## 2. OWASP Top 10:2025
050 
051 ### Risk Categories
052 
053 | Rank | Category | Think About |
054 |------|----------|-------------|
055 | **A01** | Broken Access Control | Who can access what? IDOR, SSRF |
056 | **A02** | Security Misconfiguration | Defaults, headers, exposed services |
057 | **A03** | Software Supply Chain üÜï | Dependencies, CI/CD, build integrity |
058 | **A04** | Cryptographic Failures | Weak crypto, exposed secrets |
059 | **A05** | Injection | User input ‚Üí system commands |
060 | **A06** | Insecure Design | Flawed architecture |
061 | **A07** | Authentication Failures | Session, credential management |
062 | **A08** | Integrity Failures | Unsigned updates, tampered data |
063 | **A09** | Logging & Alerting | Blind spots, no monitoring |
064 | **A10** | Exceptional Conditions üÜï | Error handling, fail-open states |
065 
066 ### 2025 Key Changes
067 
068 ```
069 2021 ‚Üí 2025 Shifts:
070 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ SSRF merged into A01 (Access Control)
071 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ A02 elevated (Cloud/Container configs)
072 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ A03 NEW: Supply Chain (major focus)
073 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ A10 NEW: Exceptional Conditions
074 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Focus shift: Root causes > Symptoms
075 ```
076 
077 ---
078 
079 ## 3. Supply Chain Security (A03)
080 
081 ### Attack Surface
082 
083 | Vector | Risk | Question to Ask |
084 |--------|------|-----------------|
085 | **Dependencies** | Malicious packages | Do we audit new deps? |
086 | **Lock files** | Integrity attacks | Are they committed? |
087 | **Build pipeline** | CI/CD compromise | Who can modify? |
088 | **Registry** | Typosquatting | Verified sources? |
089 
090 ### Defense Principles
091 
092 - Verify package integrity (checksums)
093 - Pin versions, audit updates
094 - Use private registries for critical deps
095 - Sign and verify artifacts
096 
097 ---
098 
099 ## 4. Attack Surface Mapping
100 
101 ### What to Map
102 
103 | Category | Elements |
104 |----------|----------|
105 | **Entry Points** | APIs, forms, file uploads |
106 | **Data Flows** | Input ‚Üí Process ‚Üí Output |
107 | **Trust Boundaries** | Where auth/authz checked |
108 | **Assets** | Secrets, PII, business data |
109 
110 ### Prioritization Matrix
111 
112 ```
113 Risk = Likelihood √ó Impact
114 
115 High Impact + High Likelihood ‚Üí CRITICAL
116 High Impact + Low Likelihood  ‚Üí HIGH
117 Low Impact + High Likelihood  ‚Üí MEDIUM
118 Low Impact + Low Likelihood   ‚Üí LOW
119 ```
120 
121 ---
122 
123 ## 5. Risk Prioritization
124 
125 ### CVSS + Context
126 
127 | Factor | Weight | Question |
128 |--------|--------|----------|
129 | **CVSS Score** | Base severity | How severe is the vuln? |
130 | **EPSS Score** | Exploit likelihood | Is it being exploited? |
131 | **Asset Value** | Business context | What's at risk? |
132 | **Exposure** | Attack surface | Internet-facing? |
133 
134 ### Prioritization Decision Tree
135 
136 ```
137 Is it actively exploited (EPSS >0.5)?
138 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ YES ‚Üí CRITICAL: Immediate action
139 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ NO ‚Üí Check CVSS
140          ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ CVSS ‚â•9.0 ‚Üí HIGH
141          ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ CVSS 7.0-8.9 ‚Üí Consider asset value
142          ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ CVSS <7.0 ‚Üí Schedule for later
143 ```
144 
145 ---
146 
147 ## 6. Exceptional Conditions (A10 - New)
148 
149 ### Fail-Open vs Fail-Closed
150 
151 | Scenario | Fail-Open (BAD) | Fail-Closed (GOOD) |
152 |----------|-----------------|---------------------|
153 | Auth error | Allow access | Deny access |
154 | Parsing fails | Accept input | Reject input |
155 | Timeout | Retry forever | Limit + abort |
156 
157 ### What to Check
158 
159 - Exception handlers that catch-all and ignore
160 - Missing error handling on security operations
161 - Race conditions in auth/authz
162 - Resource exhaustion scenarios
163 
164 ---
165 
166 ## 7. Scanning Methodology
167 
168 ### Phase-Based Approach
169 
170 ```
171 1. RECONNAISSANCE
172    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Understand the target
173        ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Technology stack
174        ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Entry points
175        ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Data flows
176 
177 2. DISCOVERY
178    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Identify potential issues
179        ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Configuration review
180        ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Dependency analysis
181        ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Code pattern search
182 
183 3. ANALYSIS
184    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Validate and prioritize
185        ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ False positive elimination
186        ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Risk scoring
187        ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Attack chain mapping
188 
189 4. REPORTING
190    ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Actionable findings
191        ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Clear reproduction steps
192        ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ Business impact
193        ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ Remediation guidance
194 ```
195 
196 ---
197 
198 ## 8. Code Pattern Analysis
199 
200 ### High-Risk Patterns
201 
202 | Pattern | Risk | Look For |
203 |---------|------|----------|
204 | **String concat in queries** | Injection | `"SELECT * FROM " + user_input` |
205 | **Dynamic code execution** | RCE | `eval()`, `exec()`, `Function()` |
206 | **Unsafe deserialization** | RCE | `pickle.loads()`, `unserialize()` |
207 | **Path manipulation** | Traversal | User input in file paths |
208 | **Disabled security** | Various | `verify=False`, `--insecure` |
209 
210 ### Secret Patterns
211 
212 | Type | Indicators |
213 |------|-----------|
214 | API Keys | `api_key`, `apikey`, high entropy |
215 | Tokens | `token`, `bearer`, `jwt` |
216 | Credentials | `password`, `secret`, `key` |
217 | Cloud | `AWS_`, `AZURE_`, `GCP_` prefixes |
218 
219 ---
220 
221 ## 9. Cloud Security Considerations
222 
223 ### Shared Responsibility
224 
225 | Layer | You Own | Provider Owns |
226 |-------|---------|---------------|
227 | Data | ‚úÖ | ‚ùå |
228 | Application | ‚úÖ | ‚ùå |
229 | OS/Runtime | Depends | Depends |
230 | Infrastructure | ‚ùå | ‚úÖ |
231 
232 ### Cloud-Specific Checks
233 
234 - IAM: Least privilege applied?
235 - Storage: Public buckets?
236 - Network: Security groups tightened?
237 - Secrets: Using secrets manager?
238 
239 ---
240 
241 ## 10. Anti-Patterns
242 
243 | ‚ùå Don't | ‚úÖ Do |
244 |----------|-------|
245 | Scan without understanding | Map attack surface first |
246 | Alert on every CVE | Prioritize by exploitability + asset |
247 | Ignore false positives | Maintain verified baseline |
248 | Fix symptoms only | Address root causes |
249 | Scan once before deploy | Continuous scanning |
250 | Trust third-party deps blindly | Verify integrity, audit code |
251 
252 ---
253 
254 ## 11. Reporting Principles
255 
256 ### Finding Structure
257 
258 Each finding should answer:
259 1. **What?** - Clear vulnerability description
260 2. **Where?** - Exact location (file, line, endpoint)
261 3. **Why?** - Root cause explanation
262 4. **Impact?** - Business consequence
263 5. **How to fix?** - Specific remediation
264 
265 ### Severity Classification
266 
267 | Severity | Criteria |
268 |----------|----------|
269 | **Critical** | RCE, auth bypass, mass data exposure |
270 | **High** | Data exposure, privilege escalation |
271 | **Medium** | Limited scope, requires conditions |
272 | **Low** | Informational, best practice |
273 
274 ---
275 
276 > **Remember:** Vulnerability scanning finds issues. Expert thinking prioritizes what matters. Always ask: "What would an attacker do with this?"

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F132 path:skills/webapp-testing/SKILL.md hash:aa05117912ef52addc31bdf601e8610c45badec923fc68bbc0d849b42695959a lines:187 ===
001 ---
002 name: webapp-testing
003 description: Web application testing principles. E2E, Playwright, deep audit strategies.
004 allowed-tools: Read, Write, Edit, Glob, Grep, Bash
005 ---
006 
007 # Web App Testing
008 
009 > Discover and test everything. Leave no route untested.
010 
011 ## üîß Runtime Scripts
012 
013 **Execute these for automated browser testing:**
014 
015 | Script | Purpose | Usage |
016 |--------|---------|-------|
017 | `scripts/playwright_runner.py` | Basic browser test | `python scripts/playwright_runner.py https://example.com` |
018 | | With screenshot | `python scripts/playwright_runner.py <url> --screenshot` |
019 | | Accessibility check | `python scripts/playwright_runner.py <url> --a11y` |
020 
021 **Requires:** `pip install playwright && playwright install chromium`
022 
023 ---
024 
025 ## 1. Deep Audit Approach
026 
027 ### Discovery First
028 
029 | Target | How to Find |
030 |--------|-------------|
031 | Routes | Scan app/, pages/, router files |
032 | API endpoints | Grep for HTTP methods |
033 | Components | Find component directories |
034 | Features | Read documentation |
035 
036 ### Systematic Testing
037 
038 1. **Map** - List all routes/APIs
039 2. **Scan** - Verify they respond
040 3. **Test** - Cover critical paths
041 
042 ---
043 
044 ## 2. Testing Pyramid for Web
045 
046 ```
047         /\          E2E (Few)
048        /  \         Critical user flows
049       /----\
050      /      \       Integration (Some)
051     /--------\      API, data flow
052    /          \
053   /------------\    Component (Many)
054                     Individual UI pieces
055 ```
056 
057 ---
058 
059 ## 3. E2E Test Principles
060 
061 ### What to Test
062 
063 | Priority | Tests |
064 |----------|-------|
065 | 1 | Happy path user flows |
066 | 2 | Authentication flows |
067 | 3 | Critical business actions |
068 | 4 | Error handling |
069 
070 ### E2E Best Practices
071 
072 | Practice | Why |
073 |----------|-----|
074 | Use data-testid | Stable selectors |
075 | Wait for elements | Avoid flaky tests |
076 | Clean state | Independent tests |
077 | Avoid implementation details | Test user behavior |
078 
079 ---
080 
081 ## 4. Playwright Principles
082 
083 ### Core Concepts
084 
085 | Concept | Use |
086 |---------|-----|
087 | Page Object Model | Encapsulate page logic |
088 | Fixtures | Reusable test setup |
089 | Assertions | Built-in auto-wait |
090 | Trace Viewer | Debug failures |
091 
092 ### Configuration
093 
094 | Setting | Recommendation |
095 |---------|----------------|
096 | Retries | 2 on CI |
097 | Trace | on-first-retry |
098 | Screenshots | on-failure |
099 | Video | retain-on-failure |
100 
101 ---
102 
103 ## 5. Visual Testing
104 
105 ### When to Use
106 
107 | Scenario | Value |
108 |----------|-------|
109 | Design system | High |
110 | Marketing pages | High |
111 | Component library | Medium |
112 | Dynamic content | Lower |
113 
114 ### Strategy
115 
116 - Baseline screenshots
117 - Compare on changes
118 - Review visual diffs
119 - Update intentional changes
120 
121 ---
122 
123 ## 6. API Testing Principles
124 
125 ### Coverage Areas
126 
127 | Area | Tests |
128 |------|-------|
129 | Status codes | 200, 400, 404, 500 |
130 | Response shape | Matches schema |
131 | Error messages | User-friendly |
132 | Edge cases | Empty, large, special chars |
133 
134 ---
135 
136 ## 7. Test Organization
137 
138 ### File Structure
139 
140 ```
141 tests/
142 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ e2e/           # Full user flows
143 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ integration/   # API, data
144 ‚îú‚îÄ‚îÄ component/     # UI units
145 ‚îî‚îÄ‚îÄ fixtures/      # Shared data
146 ```
147 
148 ### Naming Convention
149 
150 | Pattern | Example |
151 |---------|---------|
152 | Feature-based | `login.spec.ts` |
153 | Descriptive | `user-can-checkout.spec.ts` |
154 
155 ---
156 
157 ## 8. CI Integration
158 
159 ### Pipeline Steps
160 
161 1. Install dependencies
162 2. Install browsers
163 3. Run tests
164 4. Upload artifacts (traces, screenshots)
165 
166 ### Parallelization
167 
168 | Strategy | Use |
169 |----------|-----|
170 | Per file | Playwright default |
171 | Sharding | Large suites |
172 | Workers | Multiple browsers |
173 
174 ---
175 
176 ## 9. Anti-Patterns
177 
178 | ‚ùå Don't | ‚úÖ Do |
179 |----------|-------|
180 | Test implementation | Test behavior |
181 | Hardcode waits | Use auto-wait |
182 | Skip cleanup | Isolate tests |
183 | Ignore flaky tests | Fix root cause |
184 
185 ---
186 
187 > **Remember:** E2E tests are expensive. Use them for critical paths only.

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F133 path:workflows/brainstorm.md hash:737f1abb5c3b36afe88f24a85418be5dc3895f9855b766e425cc9c839a2eaf96 lines:113 ===
001 ---
002 description: Structured brainstorming for projects and features. Explores multiple options before implementation.
003 ---
004 
005 # /brainstorm - Structured Idea Exploration
006 
007 $ARGUMENTS
008 
009 ---
010 
011 ## Purpose
012 
013 This command activates BRAINSTORM mode for structured idea exploration. Use when you need to explore options before committing to an implementation.
014 
015 ---
016 
017 ## Behavior
018 
019 When `/brainstorm` is triggered:
020 
021 1. **Understand the goal**
022    - What problem are we solving?
023    - Who is the user?
024    - What constraints exist?
025 
026 2. **Generate options**
027    - Provide at least 3 different approaches
028    - Each with pros and cons
029    - Consider unconventional solutions
030 
031 3. **Compare and recommend**
032    - Summarize tradeoffs
033    - Give a recommendation with reasoning
034 
035 ---
036 
037 ## Output Format
038 
039 ```markdown
040 ## üß† Brainstorm: [Topic]
041 
042 ### Context
043 [Brief problem statement]
044 
045 ---
046 
047 ### Option A: [Name]
048 [Description]
049 
050 ‚úÖ **Pros:**
051 - [benefit 1]
052 - [benefit 2]
053 
054 ‚ùå **Cons:**
055 - [drawback 1]
056 
057 üìä **Effort:** Low | Medium | High
058 
059 ---
060 
061 ### Option B: [Name]
062 [Description]
063 
064 ‚úÖ **Pros:**
065 - [benefit 1]
066 
067 ‚ùå **Cons:**
068 - [drawback 1]
069 - [drawback 2]
070 
071 üìä **Effort:** Low | Medium | High
072 
073 ---
074 
075 ### Option C: [Name]
076 [Description]
077 
078 ‚úÖ **Pros:**
079 - [benefit 1]
080 
081 ‚ùå **Cons:**
082 - [drawback 1]
083 
084 üìä **Effort:** Low | Medium | High
085 
086 ---
087 
088 ## üí° Recommendation
089 
090 **Option [X]** because [reasoning].
091 
092 What direction would you like to explore?
093 ```
094 
095 ---
096 
097 ## Examples
098 
099 ```
100 /brainstorm authentication system
101 /brainstorm state management for complex form
102 /brainstorm database schema for social app
103 /brainstorm caching strategy
104 ```
105 
106 ---
107 
108 ## Key Principles
109 
110 - **No code** - this is about ideas, not implementation
111 - **Visual when helpful** - use diagrams for architecture
112 - **Honest tradeoffs** - don't hide complexity
113 - **Defer to user** - present options, let them decide

011 ## Task
012 
013 This command starts a new application creation process.
014 
015 ### Steps:
016

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F135 path:workflows/debug.md hash:96af930583709686f4f8a29d07012e89eb69825259e8bddd42043485a1fe8c83 lines:103 ===
001 ---
002 description: Debugging command. Activates DEBUG mode for systematic problem investigation.
003 ---
004 
005 # /debug - Systematic Problem Investigation
006 
007 $ARGUMENTS
008 
009 ---
010 
011 ## Purpose
012 
013 This command activates DEBUG mode for systematic investigation of issues, errors, or unexpected behavior.
014 
015 ---
016 
017 ## Behavior
018 
019 When `/debug` is triggered:
020 
021 1. **Gather information**
022    - Error message
023    - Reproduction steps
024    - Expected vs actual behavior
025    - Recent changes
026 
027 2. **Form hypotheses**
028    - List possible causes
029    - Order by likelihood
030 
031 3. **Investigate systematically**
032    - Test each hypothesis
033    - Check logs, data flow
034    - Use elimination method
035 
036 4. **Fix and prevent**
037    - Apply fix
038    - Explain root cause
039    - Add prevention measures
040 
041 ---
042 
043 ## Output Format
044 
045 ```markdown
046 ## üîç Debug: [Issue]
047 
048 ### 1. Symptom
049 [What's happening]
050 
051 ### 2. Information Gathered
052 - Error: `[error message]`
053 - File: `[filepath]`
054 - Line: [line number]
055 
056 ### 3. Hypotheses
057 1. ‚ùì [Most likely cause]
058 2. ‚ùì [Second possibility]
059 3. ‚ùì [Less likely cause]
060 
061 ### 4. Investigation
062 
063 **Testing hypothesis 1:**
064 [What I checked] ‚Üí [Result]
065 
066 **Testing hypothesis 2:**
067 [What I checked] ‚Üí [Result]
068 
069 ### 5. Root Cause
070 üéØ **[Explanation of why this happened]**
071 
072 ### 6. Fix
073 ```[language]
074 // Before
075 [broken code]
076 
077 // After
078 [fixed code]
079 ```
080 
081 ### 7. Prevention
082 üõ°Ô∏è [How to prevent this in the future]
083 ```
084 
085 ---
086 
087 ## Examples
088 
089 ```
090 /debug login not working
091 /debug API returns 500
092 /debug form doesn't submit
093 /debug data not saving
094 ```
095 
096 ---
097 
098 ## Key Principles
099 
100 - **Ask before assuming** - get full error context
101 - **Test hypotheses** - don't guess randomly
102 - **Explain why** - not just what to fix
103 - **Prevent recurrence** - add tests, validation

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F137 path:workflows/enhance.md hash:0e91e5e0b5d145624e0713f6c57b050f4b8206f4b08f82c0ba85cb97bbcbff4f lines:63 ===
001 ---
002 description: Add or update features in existing application. Used for iterative development.
003 ---
004 
005 # /enhance - Update Application
006 
007 $ARGUMENTS
008 
009 ---
010 
011 ## Task
012 
013 This command adds features or makes updates to existing application.
014 
015 ### Steps:
016 
017 1. **Understand Current State**
018    - Load project state with `python .agent/scripts/session_manager.py info`
019    - Understand existing features, tech stack
020 
021 2. **Plan Changes**
022    - Determine what will be added/changed
023    - Detect affected files
024    - Check dependencies
025 
026 3. **Present Plan to User** (for major changes)
027    ```
028    "To add admin panel:
029    - I'll create 15 new files
030    - Update 8 files
031    - Takes ~10 minutes
032 
033    Should I start?"
034    ```
035 
036 4. **Apply**
037    - Call relevant agents
038    - Make changes
039    - Test
040 
041 5. **Update Preview**
042    - Hot reload or restart
043 
044 ---
045 
046 ## Usage Examples
047 
048 ```
049 /enhance add dark mode
050 /enhance build admin panel
051 /enhance integrate payment system
052 /enhance add search feature
053 /enhance edit profile page
054 /enhance make responsive
055 ```
056 
057 ---
058 
059 ## Caution
060 
061 - Get approval for major changes
062 - Warn on conflicting requests (e.g., "use Firebase" when project uses PostgreSQL)
063 - Commit each change with git

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F138 path:workflows/orchestrate.md hash:6976e2a35a7146454b7882f143ce1a60dc6fb74d1b223cbd6b0508b5eadf51ed lines:237 ===
001 ---
002 description: Coordinate multiple agents for complex tasks. Use for multi-perspective analysis, comprehensive reviews, or tasks requiring different domain expertise.
003 ---
004 
005 # Multi-Agent Orchestration
006 
007 You are now in **ORCHESTRATION MODE**. Your task: coordinate specialized agents to solve this complex problem.
008 
009 ## Task to Orchestrate
010 $ARGUMENTS
011 
012 ---
013 
014 ## üî¥ CRITICAL: Minimum Agent Requirement
015 
016 > ‚ö†Ô∏è **ORCHESTRATION = MINIMUM 3 DIFFERENT AGENTS**
017 >
018 > If you use fewer than 3 agents, you are NOT orchestrating - you're just delegating.
019 >
020 > **Validation before completion:**
021 > - Count invoked agents
022 > - If `agent_count < 3` ‚Üí STOP and invoke more agents
023 > - Single agent = FAILURE of orchestration
024 
025 ### Agent Selection Matrix
026 
027 | Task Type | REQUIRED Agents (minimum) |
028 |-----------|---------------------------|
029 | **Web App** | frontend-specialist, backend-specialist, test-engineer |
030 | **API** | backend-specialist, security-auditor, test-engineer |
031 | **UI/Design** | frontend-specialist, seo-specialist, performance-optimizer |
032 | **Database** | database-architect, backend-specialist, security-auditor |
033 | **Full Stack** | project-planner, frontend-specialist, backend-specialist, devops-engineer |
034 | **Debug** | debugger, explorer-agent, test-engineer |
035 | **Security** | security-auditor, penetration-tester, devops-engineer |
036 
037 ---
038 
039 ## Pre-Flight: Mode Check
040 
041 | Current Mode | Task Type | Action |
042 |--------------|-----------|--------|
043 | **plan** | Any | ‚úÖ Proceed with planning-first approach |
044 | **edit** | Simple execution | ‚úÖ Proceed directly |
045 | **edit** | Complex/multi-file | ‚ö†Ô∏è Ask: "This task requires planning. Switch to plan mode?" |
046 | **ask** | Any | ‚ö†Ô∏è Ask: "Ready to orchestrate. Switch to edit or plan mode?" |
047 
048 ---
049 
050 ## üî¥ STRICT 2-PHASE ORCHESTRATION
051 
052 ### PHASE 1: PLANNING (Sequential - NO parallel agents)
053 
054 | Step | Agent | Action |
055 |------|-------|--------|
056 | 1 | `project-planner` | Create docs/PLAN.md |
057 | 2 | (optional) `explorer-agent` | Codebase discovery if needed |
058 
059 > üî¥ **NO OTHER AGENTS during planning!** Only project-planner and explorer-agent.
060 
061 ### ‚è∏Ô∏è CHECKPOINT: User Approval
062 
063 ```
064 After PLAN.md is complete, ASK:
065 
066 "‚úÖ Plan olu≈üturuldu: docs/PLAN.md
067 
068 Onaylƒ±yor musunuz? (Y/N)
069 - Y: Implementation ba≈ülatƒ±lƒ±r
070 - N: Planƒ± d√ºzeltirim"
071 ```
072 
073 > üî¥ **DO NOT proceed to Phase 2 without explicit user approval!**
074 
075 ### PHASE 2: IMPLEMENTATION (Parallel agents after approval)
076 
077 | Parallel Group | Agents |
078 |----------------|--------|
079 | Foundation | `database-architect`, `security-auditor` |
080 | Core | `backend-specialist`, `frontend-specialist` |
081 | Polish | `test-engineer`, `devops-engineer` |
082 
083 > ‚úÖ After user approval, invoke multiple agents in PARALLEL.
084 
085 ## Available Agents (17 total)
086 
087 | Agent | Domain | Use When |
088 |-------|--------|----------|
089 | `project-planner` | Planning | Task breakdown, PLAN.md |
090 | `explorer-agent` | Discovery | Codebase mapping |
091 | `frontend-specialist` | UI/UX | React, Vue, CSS, HTML |
092 | `backend-specialist` | Server | API, Node.js, Python |
093 | `database-architect` | Data | SQL, NoSQL, Schema |
094 | `security-auditor` | Security | Vulnerabilities, Auth |
095 | `penetration-tester` | Security | Active testing |
096 | `test-engineer` | Testing | Unit, E2E, Coverage |
097 | `devops-engineer` | Ops | CI/CD, Docker, Deploy |
098 | `mobile-developer` | Mobile | React Native, Flutter |
099 | `performance-optimizer` | Speed | Lighthouse, Profiling |
100 | `seo-specialist` | SEO | Meta, Schema, Rankings |
101 | `documentation-writer` | Docs | README, API docs |
102 | `debugger` | Debug | Error analysis |
103 | `game-developer` | Games | Unity, Godot |
104 | `orchestrator` | Meta | Coordination |
105 
106 ---
107 
108 ## Orchestration Protocol
109 
110 ### Step 1: Analyze Task Domains
111 Identify ALL domains this task touches:
112 ```
113 ‚ñ° Security     ‚Üí security-auditor, penetration-tester
114 ‚ñ° Backend/API  ‚Üí backend-specialist
115 ‚ñ° Frontend/UI  ‚Üí frontend-specialist
116 ‚ñ° Database     ‚Üí database-architect
117 ‚ñ° Testing      ‚Üí test-engineer
118 ‚ñ° DevOps       ‚Üí devops-engineer
119 ‚ñ° Mobile       ‚Üí mobile-developer
120 ‚ñ° Performance  ‚Üí performance-optimizer
121 ‚ñ° SEO          ‚Üí seo-specialist
122 ‚ñ° Planning     ‚Üí project-planner
123 ```
124 
125 ### Step 2: Phase Detection
126 
127 | If Plan Exists | Action |
128 |----------------|--------|
129 | NO `docs/PLAN.md` | ‚Üí Go to PHASE 1 (planning only) |
130 | YES `docs/PLAN.md` + user approved | ‚Üí Go to PHASE 2 (implementation) |
131 
132 ### Step 3: Execute Based on Phase
133 
134 **PHASE 1 (Planning):**
135 ```
136 Use the project-planner agent to create PLAN.md
137 ‚Üí STOP after plan is created
138 ‚Üí ASK user for approval
139 ```
140 
141 **PHASE 2 (Implementation - after approval):**
142 ```
143 Invoke agents in PARALLEL:
144 Use the frontend-specialist agent to [task]
145 Use the backend-specialist agent to [task]
146 Use the test-engineer agent to [task]
147 ```
148 
149 **üî¥ CRITICAL: Context Passing (MANDATORY)**
150 
151 When invoking ANY subagent, you MUST include:
152 
153 1. **Original User Request:** Full text of what user asked
154 2. **Decisions Made:** All user answers to Socratic questions
155 3. **Previous Agent Work:** Summary of what previous agents did
156 4. **Current Plan State:** If plan files exist in workspace, include them
157 
158 **Example with FULL context:**
159 ```
160 Use the project-planner agent to create PLAN.md:
161 
162 **CONTEXT:**
163 - User Request: "√ñƒürenciler i√ßin sosyal platform, mock data ile"
164 - Decisions: Tech=Vue 3, Layout=Grid Widget, Auth=Mock, Design=Gen√ß Dinamik
165 - Previous Work: Orchestrator asked 6 questions, user chose all options
166 - Current Plan: playful-roaming-dream.md exists in workspace with initial structure
167 
168 **TASK:** Create detailed PLAN.md based on ABOVE decisions. Do NOT infer from folder name.
169 ```
170 
171 > ‚ö†Ô∏è **VIOLATION:** Invoking subagent without full context = subagent will make wrong assumptions!
172 
173 
174 ### Step 4: Verification (MANDATORY)
175 The LAST agent must run appropriate verification scripts:
176 ```bash
177 python .agent/skills/vulnerability-scanner/scripts/security_scan.py .
178 python .agent/skills/lint-and-validate/scripts/lint_runner.py .
179 ```
180 
181 ### Step 5: Synthesize Results
182 Combine all agent outputs into unified report.
183 
184 ---
185 
186 ## Output Format
187 
188 ```markdown
189 ## üéº Orchestration Report
190 
191 ### Task
192 [Original task summary]
193 
194 ### Mode
195 [Current Antigravity Agent mode: plan/edit/ask]
196 
197 ### Agents Invoked (MINIMUM 3)
198 | # | Agent | Focus Area | Status |
199 |---|-------|------------|--------|
200 | 1 | project-planner | Task breakdown | ‚úÖ |
201 | 2 | frontend-specialist | UI implementation | ‚úÖ |
202 | 3 | test-engineer | Verification scripts | ‚úÖ |
203 
204 ### Verification Scripts Executed
205 - [x] security_scan.py ‚Üí Pass/Fail
206 - [x] lint_runner.py ‚Üí Pass/Fail
207 
208 ### Key Findings
209 1. **[Agent 1]**: Finding
210 2. **[Agent 2]**: Finding
211 3. **[Agent 3]**: Finding
212 
213 ### Deliverables
214 - [ ] PLAN.md created
215 - [ ] Code implemented
216 - [ ] Tests passing
217 - [ ] Scripts verified
218 
219 ### Summary
220 [One paragraph synthesis of all agent work]
221 ```
222 
223 ---
224 
225 ## üî¥ EXIT GATE
226 
227 Before completing orchestration, verify:
228 
229 1. ‚úÖ **Agent Count:** `invoked_agents >= 3`
230 2. ‚úÖ **Scripts Executed:** At least `security_scan.py` ran
231 3. ‚úÖ **Report Generated:** Orchestration Report with all agents listed
232 
233 > **If any check fails ‚Üí DO NOT mark orchestration complete. Invoke more agents or run scripts.**
234 
235 ---
236 
237 **Begin orchestration now. Select 3+ agents, execute sequentially, run verification scripts, synthesize results.**

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F139 path:workflows/plan.md hash:9961d158fbc5ae3b67145e58e4306d65d6385437c764aacaaf67a2b74c985aaf lines:89 ===
001 ---
002 description: Create project plan using project-planner agent. No code writing - only plan file generation.
003 ---
004 
005 # /plan - Project Planning Mode
006 
007 $ARGUMENTS
008 
009 ---
010 
011 ## üî¥ CRITICAL RULES
012 
013 1. **NO CODE WRITING** - This command creates plan file only
014 2. **Use project-planner agent** - NOT Antigravity Agent's native Plan mode
015 3. **Socratic Gate** - Ask clarifying questions before planning
016 4. **Dynamic Naming** - Plan file named based on task
017 
018 ---
019 
020 ## Task
021 
022 Use the `project-planner` agent with this context:
023 
024 ```
025 CONTEXT:
026 - User Request: $ARGUMENTS
027 - Mode: PLANNING ONLY (no code)
028 - Output: docs/PLAN-{task-slug}.md (dynamic naming)
029 
030 NAMING RULES:
031 1. Extract 2-3 key words from request
032 2. Lowercase, hyphen-separated
033 3. Max 30 characters
034 4. Example: "e-commerce cart" ‚Üí PLAN-ecommerce-cart.md
035 
036 RULES:
037 1. Follow project-planner.md Phase -1 (Context Check)
038 2. Follow project-planner.md Phase 0 (Socratic Gate)
039 3. Create PLAN-{slug}.md with task breakdown
040 4. DO NOT write any code files
041 5. REPORT the exact file name created
042 ```
043 
044 ---
045 
046 ## Expected Output
047 
048 | Deliverable | Location |
049 |-------------|----------|
050 | Project Plan | `docs/PLAN-{task-slug}.md` |
051 | Task Breakdown | Inside plan file |
052 | Agent Assignments | Inside plan file |
053 | Verification Checklist | Phase X in plan file |
054 
055 ---
056 
057 ## After Planning
058 
059 Tell user:
060 ```
061 [OK] Plan created: docs/PLAN-{slug}.md
062 
063 Next steps:
064 - Review the plan
065 - Run `/create` to start implementation
066 - Or modify plan manually
067 ```
068 
069 ---
070 
071 ## Naming Examples
072 
073 | Request | Plan File |
074 |---------|-----------|
075 | `/plan e-commerce site with cart` | `docs/PLAN-ecommerce-cart.md` |
076 | `/plan mobile app for fitness` | `docs/PLAN-fitness-app.md` |
077 | `/plan add dark mode feature` | `docs/PLAN-dark-mode.md` |
078 | `/plan fix authentication bug` | `docs/PLAN-auth-fix.md` |
079 | `/plan SaaS dashboard` | `docs/PLAN-saas-dashboard.md` |
080 
081 ---
082 
083 ## Usage
084 
085 ```
086 /plan e-commerce site with cart
087 /plan mobile app for fitness tracking
088 /plan SaaS dashboard with analytics
089 ```

072 ## Technical

074 Auto preview uses `auto_preview.py` script:
075 
076 ```bash
077 python .agent/scripts/auto_preview.py start [port]
078 python .agent/scripts/auto_preview.py stop
079 python .agent/scripts/auto_preview.py status
080 ```

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F142 path:workflows/test.md hash:420414646890deadc487ee12e89fb831084aa825de7aefab0b4414fc8ee9ddd8 lines:144 ===
001 ---
002 description: Test generation and test running command. Creates and executes tests for code.
003 ---
004 
005 # /test - Test Generation and Execution
006 
007 $ARGUMENTS
008 
009 ---
010 
011 ## Purpose
012 
013 This command generates tests, runs existing tests, or checks test coverage.
014 
015 ---
016 
017 ## Sub-commands
018 
019 ```
020 /test                - Run all tests
021 /test [file/feature] - Generate tests for specific target
022 /test coverage       - Show test coverage report
023 /test watch          - Run tests in watch mode
024 ```
025 
026 ---
027 
028 ## Behavior
029 
030 ### Generate Tests
031 
032 When asked to test a file or feature:
033 
034 1. **Analyze the code**
035    - Identify functions and methods
036    - Find edge cases
037    - Detect dependencies to mock
038 
039 2. **Generate test cases**
040    - Happy path tests
041    - Error cases
042    - Edge cases
043    - Integration tests (if needed)
044 
045 3. **Write tests**
046    - Use project's test framework (Jest, Vitest, etc.)
047    - Follow existing test patterns
048    - Mock external dependencies
049 
050 ---
051 
052 ## Output Format
053 
054 ### For Test Generation
055 
056 ```markdown
057 ## üß™ Tests: [Target]
058 
059 ### Test Plan
060 | Test Case | Type | Coverage |
061 |-----------|------|----------|
062 | Should create user | Unit | Happy path |
063 | Should reject invalid email | Unit | Validation |
064 | Should handle db error | Unit | Error case |
065 
066 ### Generated Tests
067 
068 `tests/[file].test.ts`
069 
070 [Code block with tests]
071 
072 ---
073 
074 Run with: `npm test`
075 ```
076 
077 ### For Test Execution
078 
079 ```
080 üß™ Running tests...
081 
082 ‚úÖ auth.test.ts (5 passed)
083 ‚úÖ user.test.ts (8 passed)
084 ‚ùå order.test.ts (2 passed, 1 failed)
085 
086 Failed:
087   ‚úó should calculate total with discount
088     Expected: 90
089     Received: 100
090 
091 Total: 15 tests (14 passed, 1 failed)
092 ```
093 
094 ---
095 
096 ## Examples
097 
098 ```
099 /test src/services/auth.service.ts
100 /test user registration flow
101 /test coverage
102 /test fix failed tests
103 ```
104 
105 ---
106 
107 ## Test Patterns
108 
109 ### Unit Test Structure
110 
111 ```typescript
112 describe('AuthService', () => {
113   describe('login', () => {
114     it('should return token for valid credentials', async () => {
115       // Arrange
116       const credentials = { email: 'test@test.com', password: 'pass123' };
117 
118       // Act
119       const result = await authService.login(credentials);
120 
121       // Assert
122       expect(result.token).toBeDefined();
123     });
124 
125     it('should throw for invalid password', async () => {
126       // Arrange
127       const credentials = { email: 'test@test.com', password: 'wrong' };
128 
129       // Act & Assert
130       await expect(authService.login(credentials)).rejects.toThrow('Invalid credentials');
131     });
132   });
133 });
134 ```
135 
136 ---
137 
138 ## Key Principles
139 
140 - **Test behavior not implementation**
141 - **One assertion per test** (when practical)
142 - **Descriptive test names**
143 - **Arrange-Act-Assert pattern**
144 - **Mock external dependencies**

=== FILE_CAPSULE_BEGIN FID:F143 path:workflows/ui-ux-pro-max.md hash:5a56e002ee6f73789fdc76982b051a6af77d6639dea5418409bd2bad4a7c8683 lines:296 ===
001 ---
002 description: Plan and implement UI
003 ---
004 
005 ---
006 description: AI-powered design intelligence with 50+ styles, 95+ color palettes, and automated design system generation
007 ---
008 
009 # ui-ux-pro-max
010 
011 Comprehensive design guide for web and mobile applications. Contains 50+ styles, 97 color palettes, 57 font pairings, 99 UX guidelines, and 25 chart types across 9 technology stacks. Searchable database with priority-based recommendations.
012 
013 ## Prerequisites
014 
015 Check if Python is installed:
016 
017 ```bash
018 python3 --version || python --version
019 ```
020 
021 If Python is not installed, install it based on user's OS:
022 
023 **macOS:**
024 ```bash
025 brew install python3
026 ```
027 
028 **Ubuntu/Debian:**
029 ```bash
030 sudo apt update && sudo apt install python3
031 ```
032 
033 **Windows:**
034 ```powershell
035 winget install Python.Python.3.12
036 ```
037 
038 ---
039 
040 ## How to Use This Workflow
041 
042 When user requests UI/UX work (design, build, create, implement, review, fix, improve), follow this workflow:
043 
044 ### Step 1: Analyze User Requirements
045 
046 Extract key information from user request:
047 - **Product type**: SaaS, e-commerce, portfolio, dashboard, landing page, etc.
048 - **Style keywords**: minimal, playful, professional, elegant, dark mode, etc.
049 - **Industry**: healthcare, fintech, gaming, education, etc.
050 - **Stack**: React, Vue, Next.js, or default to `html-tailwind`
051 
052 ### Step 2: Generate Design System (REQUIRED)
053 
054 **Always start with `--design-system`** to get comprehensive recommendations with reasoning:
055 
056 ```bash
057 python3 .agent/.shared/ui-ux-pro-max/scripts/search.py "<product_type> <industry> <keywords>" --design-system [-p "Project Name"]
058 ```
059 
060 This command:
061 1. Searches 5 domains in parallel (product, style, color, landing, typography)
062 2. Applies reasoning rules from `ui-reasoning.csv` to select best matches
063 3. Returns complete design system: pattern, style, colors, typography, effects
064 4. Includes anti-patterns to avoid
065 
066 **Example:**
067 ```bash
068 python3 .agent/.shared/ui-ux-pro-max/scripts/search.py "beauty spa wellness service" --design-system -p "Serenity Spa"
069 ```
070 
071 ### Step 2b: Persist Design System (Master + Overrides Pattern)
072 
073 To save the design system for hierarchical retrieval across sessions, add `--persist`:
074 
075 ```bash
076 python3 .agent/.shared/ui-ux-pro-max/scripts/search.py "<query>" --design-system --persist -p "Project Name"
077 ```
078 
079 This creates:
080 - `design-system/MASTER.md` ‚Äî Global Source of Truth with all design rules
081 - `design-system/pages/` ‚Äî Folder for page-specific overrides
082 
083 **With page-specific override:**
084 ```bash
085 python3 .agent/.shared/ui-ux-pro-max/scripts/search.py "<query>" --design-system --persist -p "Project Name" --page "dashboard"
086 ```
087 
088 This also creates:
089 - `design-system/pages/dashboard.md` ‚Äî Page-specific deviations from Master
090 
091 **How hierarchical retrieval works:**
092 1. When building a specific page (e.g., "Checkout"), first check `design-system/pages/checkout.md`
093 2. If the page file exists, its rules **override** the Master file
094 3. If not, use `design-system/MASTER.md` exclusively
095 
096 ### Step 3: Supplement with Detailed Searches (as needed)
097 
098 After getting the design system, use domain searches to get additional details:
099 
100 ```bash
101 python3 .agent/.shared/ui-ux-pro-max/scripts/search.py "<keyword>" --domain <domain> [-n <max_results>]
102 ```
103 
104 **When to use detailed searches:**
105 
106 | Need | Domain | Example |
107 |------|--------|---------|
108 | More style options | `style` | `--domain style "glassmorphism dark"` |
109 | Chart recommendations | `chart` | `--domain chart "real-time dashboard"` |
110 | UX best practices | `ux` | `--domain ux "animation accessibility"` |
111 | Alternative fonts | `typography` | `--domain typography "elegant luxury"` |
112 | Landing structure | `landing` | `--domain landing "hero social-proof"` |
113 
114 ### Step 4: Stack Guidelines (Default: html-tailwind)
115 
116 Get implementation-specific best practices. If user doesn't specify a stack, **default to `html-tailwind`**.
117 
118 ```bash
119 python3 .agent/.shared/ui-ux-pro-max/scripts/search.py "<keyword>" --stack html-tailwind
120 ```
121 
122 Available stacks: `html-tailwind`, `react`, `nextjs`, `vue`, `svelte`, `swiftui`, `react-native`, `flutter`, `shadcn`, `jetpack-compose`
123 , `jetpack-compose`
124 ---
125 
126 ## Search Reference
127 
128 ### Available Domains
129 
130 | Domain | Use For | Example Keywords |
131 |--------|---------|------------------|
132 | `product` | Product type recommendations | SaaS, e-commerce, portfolio, healthcare, beauty, service |
133 | `style` | UI styles, colors, effects | glassmorphism, minimalism, dark mode, brutalism |
134 | `typography` | Font pairings, Google Fonts | elegant, playful, professional, modern |
135 | `color` | Color palettes by product type | saas, ecommerce, healthcare, beauty, fintech, service |
136 | `landing` | Page structure, CTA strategies | hero, hero-centric, testimonial, pricing, social-proof |
137 | `chart` | Chart types, library recommendations | trend, comparison, timeline, funnel, pie |
138 | `ux` | Best practices, anti-patterns | animation, accessibility, z-index, loading |
139 | `react` | React/Next.js performance | waterfall, bundle, suspense, memo, rerender, cache |
140 | `web` | Web interface guidelines | aria, focus, keyboard, semantic, virtualize |
141 | `prompt` | AI prompts, CSS keywords | (style name) |
142 
143 ### Available Stacks
144 
145 | Stack | Focus |
146 |-------|-------|
147 | `html-tailwind` | Tailwind utilities, responsive, a11y (DEFAULT) |
148 | `react` | State, hooks, performance, patterns |
149 | `nextjs` | SSR, routing, images, API routes |
150 | `vue` | Composition API, Pinia, Vue Router |
151 | `svelte` | Runes, stores, SvelteKit |
152 | `swiftui` | Views, State, Navigation, Animation |
153 | `react-native` | Components, Navigation, Lists |
154 | `flutter` | Widgets, State, Layout, Theming |
155 | `shadcn` | shadcn/ui components, theming, forms, patterns |
156 | `jetpack-compose` | Composables, Modifiers, State Hoisting, Recomposition |

212 ## Tips for Better Results
213 
214 1. **Be specific with keywords** - "healthcare SaaS dashboard" > "app"
215 2. **Search multiple times** - Different keywords reveal different insights
216 3. **Combine domains** - Style + Typography + Color = Complete design system
217 4. **Always check UX** - Search "animation", "z-index", "accessibility" for common issues
218 5. **Use stack flag** - Get implementation-specific best practices
219 6. **Iterate** - If first search doesn't match, try different keywords
220

222 
223 ## Common Rules for Professional UI
224 
225 These are frequently overlooked issues that make UI look unprofessional:
226 
227 ### Icons & Visual Elements
228 
229 | Rule | Do | Don't |
230 |------|----|----- |
231 | **No emoji icons** | Use SVG icons (Heroicons, Lucide, Simple Icons) | Use emojis like üé® üöÄ ‚öôÔ∏è as UI icons |
232 | **Stable hover states** | Use color/opacity transitions on hover | Use scale transforms that shift layout |
233 | **Correct brand logos** | Research official SVG from Simple Icons | Guess or use incorrect logo paths |
234 | **Consistent icon sizing** | Use fixed viewBox (24x24) with w-6 h-6 | Mix different icon sizes randomly |
235 
236 ### Interaction & Cursor
237 
238 | Rule | Do | Don't |
239 |------|----|----- |
240 | **Cursor pointer** | Add `cursor-pointer` to all clickable/hoverable cards | Leave default cursor on interactive elements |
241 | **Hover feedback** | Provide visual feedback (color, shadow, border) | No indication element is interactive |
242 | **Smooth transitions** | Use `transition-colors duration-200` | Instant state changes or too slow (>500ms) |
243 
244 ### Light/Dark Mode Contrast
245 
246 | Rule | Do | Don't |
247 |------|----|----- |
248 | **Glass card light mode** | Use `bg-white/80` or higher opacity | Use `bg-white/10` (too transparent) |
249 | **Text contrast light** | Use `#0F172A` (slate-900) for text | Use `#94A3B8` (slate-400) for body text |
250 | **Muted text light** | Use `#475569` (slate-600) minimum | Use gray-400 or lighter |
251 | **Border visibility** | Use `border-gray-200` in light mode | Use `border-white/10` (invisible) |
252 
253 ### Layout & Spacing
254 
255 | Rule | Do | Don't |
256 |------|----|----- |
257 | **Floating navbar** | Add `top-4 left-4 right-4` spacing | Stick navbar to `top-0 left-0 right-0` |
258 | **Content padding** | Account for fixed navbar height | Let content hide behind fixed elements |
259 | **Consistent max-width** | Use same `max-w-6xl` or `max-w-7xl` | Mix different container widths |
260 
261 ---
262 
263 ## Pre-Delivery Checklist
264 
265 Before delivering UI code, verify these items:
266 
267 ### Visual Quality
268 - [ ] No emojis used as icons (use SVG instead)
269 - [ ] All icons from consistent icon set (Heroicons/Lucide)
270 - [ ] Brand logos are correct (verified from Simple Icons)
271 - [ ] Hover states don't cause layout shift
272 - [ ] Use theme colors directly (bg-primary) not var() wrapper
273 
274 ### Interaction
275 - [ ] All clickable elements have `cursor-pointer`
276 - [ ] Hover states provide clear visual feedback
277 - [ ] Transitions are smooth (150-300ms)
278 - [ ] Focus states visible for keyboard navigation
279 
280 ### Light/Dark Mode
281 - [ ] Light mode text has sufficient contrast (4.5:1 minimum)
282 - [ ] Glass/transparent elements visible in light mode
283 - [ ] Borders visible in both modes
284 - [ ] Test both modes before delivery
285 
286 ### Layout
287 - [ ] Floating elements have proper spacing from edges
288 - [ ] No content hidden behind fixed navbars
289 - [ ] Responsive at 375px, 768px, 1024px, 1440px
290 - [ ] No horizontal scroll on mobile
291 
292 ### Accessibility
293 - [ ] All images have alt text
294 - [ ] Form inputs have labels
295 - [ ] Color is not the only indicator
296 - [ ] `prefers-reduced-motion` respected
